Title: Online Safety Act 2023
Date: 2024-08-23
Publisher: Statute Law Database
Identifier: http://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2023/50

## Online Safety Act 2023

      B e it enacted  by the King’s most Excellent Majesty, by and with the
advice and consent of the Lords Spiritual and Temporal, and Commons, in this
present Parliament assembled, and by the authority of the same, as follows:—

### Introduction

#### Introduction

1

1.1

This Act provides for a new regulatory framework which has the general purpose
of making the use of internet services regulated by this Act safer for
individuals in the United Kingdom.

1.2

To achieve that purpose, this Act (among other things)—

1.2.a

imposes duties which, in broad terms, require providers of services regulated
by this Act to identify, mitigate and manage the risks of harm (including
risks which particularly affect individuals with a certain characteristic)
from—

1.2.a.i

illegal content and activity, and

1.2.a.ii

content and activity that is harmful to children, and

1.2.b

confers new functions and powers on the regulator, OFCOM.

1.3

Duties imposed on providers by this Act seek to secure (among other things)
that services regulated by this Act are—

1.3.a

safe by design, and

1.3.b

designed and operated in such a way that—

1.3.b.i

a higher standard of protection is provided for children than for adults,

1.3.b.ii

users’ rights to freedom of expression and privacy are protected, and

1.3.b.iii

transparency and accountability are provided in relation to those services.

#### Overview of Act

2

2.1

Parts 2 to 9 and 11 and 12 of this Act contain provision about the regulation
by OFCOM of certain internet services.

2.2

Part 2 contains key definitions, including the definition of a user-to-user
service, a search service, a Part 3 service and a regulated service.

2.3

Part 3 imposes duties of care on providers of user-to-user services and search
services and requires OFCOM to issue codes of practice about those duties.

2.4

Part 4 imposes further duties on providers of user-to-user services and search
services.

2.5

Part 5 imposes duties on providers of internet services (including user-to-
user services and search services) that publish certain pornographic content.

2.6

Part 6, which imposes requirements to pay fees to OFCOM, applies to providers
of internet services to which the duties in Part 3, 4 or 5 apply (“regulated
services”).

2.7

Part 7 is about OFCOM’s powers and duties in relation to regulated services
(including powers to obtain information and enforcement powers).

2.8

Part 8 is about appeals and complaints relating to regulated services.

2.9

Part 9 is about the Secretary of State’s functions in relation to regulated
services.

2.10

Part 10 contains communications offences.

2.11

Parts 11 and 12 contain supplementary provisions including an index of terms
defined in this Act (see section 237).

### Key definitions

#### “User-to-user service” and “search service”

3

3.1

In this Act “ user-to-user service ” means an internet service by means of
which content that is generated directly on the service by a user of the
service, or uploaded to or shared on the service by a user of the service, may
be encountered by another user, or other users, of the service.

3.2

For the purposes of subsection  (1) —

3.2.a

it does not matter if content is actually shared with another user or users as
long as a service has a functionality that allows such sharing;

3.2.b

it does not matter what proportion of content on a service is content
described in that subsection.

3.3

For the meaning of “content” and “encounter”, see section 236.

3.4

In this Act “ search service ” means an internet service that is, or includes,
a search engine (see section 229).

3.5

Subsections  (6)  and  (7)  have effect to determine whether an internet
service that—

3.5.a

is of a kind described in subsection  (1) , and

3.5.b

includes a search engine,

is a user-to-user service or a search service for the purposes of this Act.

3.6

It is a search service if the only content described in subsection (1) that is
enabled by the service is content of any of the following kinds—

3.6.a

content mentioned in paragraph  1 ,  2  or  3  of Schedule 1 (emails, SMS and
MMS messages, one-to-one live aural communications) and related identifying
content;

3.6.b

content arising in connection with any of the activities described in
paragraph  4(1)  of Schedule 1 (comments etc on provider content);

3.6.c

content present on a part of the service in relation to which the conditions
in paragraph  7(2)  of Schedule 1 are met (internal business service
conditions).

3.7

Otherwise, it is a user-to-user service.

#### “Regulated service”, “Part 3 service” etc

4

4.1

This section applies for the purposes of this Act.

4.2

A user-to-user service is a “regulated user-to-user service”, and a search
service is a “regulated search service”, if the service—

4.2.a

has links with the United Kingdom (see subsections  (5)  and  (6) ), and

4.2.b

is not—

4.2.b.i

a service of a description that is exempt as provided for by Schedule 1, or

4.2.b.ii

a service of a kind described in Schedule 2 (services combining user-generated
content or search content not regulated by this Act with pornographic content
that is regulated).

4.3

“ Part 3 service ” means a regulated user-to-user service or a regulated
search service.

4.4

“ Regulated service ” means—

4.4.a

a regulated user-to-user service,

4.4.b

a regulated search service, or

4.4.c

an internet service, other than a regulated user-to-user service or a
regulated search service, that is within section 80 (2)  (including a service
of a kind described in Schedule 2).

4.5

For the purposes of subsection  (2) , a user-to-user service or a search
service “has links with the United Kingdom” if—

4.5.a

the service has a significant number of United Kingdom users, or

4.5.b

United Kingdom users form one of the target markets for the service (or the
only target market).

4.6

For the purposes of subsection  (2) , a user-to-user service or a search
service also “has links with the United Kingdom” if—

4.6.a

the service is capable of being used in the United Kingdom by individuals, and

4.6.b

there are reasonable grounds to believe that there is a material risk of
significant harm to individuals in the United Kingdom presented by—

4.6.b.i

in the case of a user-to-user service, user-generated content present on the
service or (if the service includes a search engine) search content of the
service;

4.6.b.ii

in the case of a search service, search content of the service.

4.7

A regulated user-to-user service that includes a public search engine is
referred to in this Act as a “combined service”.

“ Public search engine ” means a search engine other than one in relation to
which the conditions in paragraph  7(2)  of Schedule 1 (internal business
service conditions) are met.

4.8

In this section—

      “ search content ” has the same meaning as in Part 3 (see section 57);
“ user-generated content ” has the meaning given by section 55 (see
subsections  (3)  and  (4)  of that section).

#### Disapplication of Act to certain parts of services

5

5.1

This Act does not apply in relation to a part of a Part 3 service if the
conditions in paragraph  7(2)  of Schedule 1 (internal business service
conditions) are met in relation to that part.

5.2

This Act does not apply in relation to a part of a regulated search service
if—

5.2.a

the only user-generated content enabled by that part of the service is content
of any of the following kinds—

5.2.a.i

content mentioned in paragraph  1 ,  2  or  3  of Schedule 1 (emails, SMS and
MMS messages, one-to-one live aural communications) and related identifying
content;

5.2.a.ii

content arising in connection with any of the activities described in
paragraph  4(1)  of Schedule 1 (comments etc on provider content); and

5.2.b

no regulated provider pornographic content is published or displayed on that
part of the service.

5.3

In this section—

      “ regulated provider pornographic content ” and “ published or displayed
” have the same meaning as in Part 5 (see section 79);           “ user-
generated content ” has the meaning given by section 55 (see subsections  (3)
and  (4)  of that section).

### Providers of regulated user-to-user services and regulated search services: duties of care

#### Introduction

##### Overview of Part 3

6

6.1

This Part imposes duties of care on providers of regulated user-to-user
services and regulated search services and requires OFCOM to issue codes of
practice relating to some of those duties.

6.2

Chapter 2 imposes duties of care on providers of regulated user-to-user
services in relation to content and activity on their services.

6.3

Chapter 3 imposes duties of care on providers of regulated search services in
relation to content and activity on their services.

6.4

Chapter 4 imposes duties on providers of regulated user-to-user services and
regulated search services to assess whether a service is likely to be accessed
by children.

6.5

Chapter 5 imposes duties on providers of certain regulated user-to-user
services and regulated search services relating to fraudulent advertising.

6.6

Chapter 6 requires OFCOM to issue codes of practice relating to particular
duties and explains what effects the codes of practice have.

6.7

Chapter 7 is about the interpretation of this Part, and it includes
definitions of the following key terms—

      “content that is harmful to children”, “primary priority content that is
harmful to children” and “ priority content that is harmful to children ” (see
sections 60 to 62);           “illegal content”, “priority offence”,
“terrorism content”, “CSEA content” and “ priority illegal content ” (see
section 59);           “ search content ” (see section 57).

#### Providers of user-to-user services: duties of care

##### User-to-user services: which duties apply, and scope of duties

###### Providers of user-to-user services: duties of care

7

7.1

Subsections  (2)  to  (6)  apply to determine which of the duties set out in
this Chapter (and, in the case of combined services, Chapter 3) must be
complied with by providers of regulated user-to-user services.

7.2

All providers of regulated user-to-user services must comply with the
following duties in relation to each such service which they provide—

7.2.a

the duties about illegal content risk assessments set out in section 9,

7.2.b

the duties about illegal content set out in section 10 (2)  to  (8) ,

7.2.c

the duty about content reporting set out in section 20,

7.2.d

the duties about complaints procedures set out in section 21,

7.2.e

the duties about freedom of expression and privacy set out in section 22 (2)
and  (3) , and

7.2.f

the duties about record-keeping and review set out in section 23 (2)  to  (6)
.

7.3

Additional duties must be complied with by providers of particular kinds of
regulated user-to-user services, as follows.

7.4

All providers of regulated user-to-user services that are likely to be
accessed by children must comply with the following duties in relation to each
such service which they provide—

7.4.a

the duties about children’s risk assessments set out in section 11, and

7.4.b

the duties to protect children’s online safety set out in section 12 (2)  to
(13) .

7.5

All providers of Category 1 services must comply with the following duties in
relation to each such service which they provide—

7.5.a

the duty about illegal content risk assessments set out in section 10 (9) ,

7.5.b

the duty about children’s risk assessments set out in section 12 (14) ,

7.5.c

the duties about assessments related to adult user empowerment set out in
section 14,

7.5.d

the duties to empower adult users set out in section 15,

7.5.e

the duties to protect content of democratic importance set out in section 17,

7.5.f

the duties to protect news publisher content set out in section 18,

7.5.g

the duties to protect journalistic content set out in section 19,

7.5.h

the duties about freedom of expression and privacy set out in section 22 (4) ,
(6)  and  (7) , and

7.5.i

the duties about record-keeping set out in section 23 (9)  and  (10) .

7.6

All providers of combined services must comply with the following duties in
relation to the search engine of each such service which they provide—

7.6.a

if the service is not a Category 2A service and is not likely to be accessed
by children, the duties set out in Chapter 3 referred to in section 24 (2) ;

7.6.b

if the service is not a Category 2A service and is likely to be accessed by
children, the duties set out in Chapter 3 referred to in section 24 (2)  and
(4) ;

7.6.c

if the service is a Category 2A service not likely to be accessed by children,
the duties set out in Chapter 3 referred to in section 24 (2)  and  (5) ;

7.6.d

if the service is a Category 2A service likely to be accessed by children, the
duties set out in Chapter 3 referred to in section 24 (2) ,  (4)  and  (5) .

7.7

For the meaning of “likely to be accessed by children”, see section 37.

7.8

For the meaning of “Category 1 service”, see section 95 (register of
categories of services).

###### Scope of duties of care

8

8.1

A duty set out in this Chapter which must be complied with in relation to a
user-to-user service that includes regulated provider pornographic content
does not extend to—

8.1.a

the regulated provider pornographic content, or

8.1.b

the design, operation or use of the service so far as relating to that
content.

See Part 5 for the duties which relate to regulated provider pornographic
content, and the meaning of that term.

8.2

A duty set out in this Chapter which must be complied with in relation to a
combined service does not extend to—

8.2.a

the search content of the service,

8.2.b

any other content that, following a search request, may be encountered as a
result of subsequent interactions with internet services, or

8.2.c

anything relating to the design, operation or use of the search engine.

8.3

A duty set out in this Chapter which must be complied with in relation to a
user-to-user service extends only to—

8.3.a

the design, operation and use of the service in the United Kingdom, and

8.3.b

in the case of a duty that is expressed to apply in relation to users of a
service, the design, operation and use of the service as it affects United
Kingdom users of the service.

##### Illegal content duties for user-to-user services

###### Illegal content risk assessment duties

9

9.1

This section sets out the duties about risk assessments which apply in
relation to all regulated user-to-user services.

9.2

A duty to carry out a suitable and sufficient illegal content risk assessment
at a time set out in, or as provided by, Schedule 3.

9.3

A duty to take appropriate steps to keep an illegal content risk assessment up
to date, including when OFCOM make any significant change to a risk profile
that relates to services of the kind in question.

9.4

Before making any significant change to any aspect of a service’s design or
operation, a duty to carry out a further suitable and sufficient illegal
content risk assessment relating to the impacts of that proposed change.

9.5

An “illegal content risk assessment” of a service of a particular kind means
an assessment of the following matters, taking into account the risk profile
that relates to services of that kind—

9.5.a

the user base;

9.5.b

the level of risk of individuals who are users of the service encountering the
following by means of the service—

9.5.b.i

each kind of priority illegal content (with each kind separately assessed),
and

9.5.b.ii

other illegal content,

taking into account (in particular) algorithms used by the service, and how
easily, quickly and widely content may be disseminated by means of the
service;

9.5.c

the level of risk of the service being used for the commission or facilitation
of a priority offence;

9.5.d

the level of risk of harm to individuals presented by illegal content of
different kinds or by the use of the service for the commission or
facilitation of a priority offence;

9.5.e

the level of risk of functionalities of the service facilitating the presence
or dissemination of illegal content or the use of the service for the
commission or facilitation of a priority offence, identifying and assessing
those functionalities that present higher levels of risk;

9.5.f

the different ways in which the service is used, and the impact of such use on
the level of risk of harm that might be suffered by individuals;

9.5.g

the nature, and severity, of the harm that might be suffered by individuals
from the matters identified in accordance with paragraphs  (b)  to  (f) ;

9.5.h

how the design and operation of the service (including the business model,
governance, use of proactive technology, measures to promote users’ media
literacy and safe use of the service, and other systems and processes) may
reduce or increase the risks identified.

9.6

In this section references to risk profiles are to the risk profiles for the
time being published under section 98 which relate to the risk of harm to
individuals presented by illegal content.

9.7

See also—

9.7.a

section 23 (2)  and  (10)  (records of risk assessments), and

9.7.b

Schedule 3 (timing of providers’ assessments).

###### Safety duties about illegal content

10

10.1

This section sets out the duties about illegal content which apply in relation
to regulated user-to-user services (as indicated by the headings).

######### All services

10.2

A duty, in relation to a service, to take or use proportionate measures
relating to the design or operation of the service to—

10.2.a

prevent individuals from encountering priority illegal content by means of the
service,

10.2.b

effectively mitigate and manage the risk of the service being used for the
commission or facilitation of a priority offence, as identified in the most
recent illegal content risk assessment of the service, and

10.2.c

effectively mitigate and manage the risks of harm to individuals, as
identified in the most recent illegal content risk assessment of the service
(see section 9(5)(g)).

10.3

A duty to operate a service using proportionate systems and processes designed
to—

10.3.a

minimise the length of time for which any priority illegal content is present;

10.3.b

where the provider is alerted by a person to the presence of any illegal
content, or becomes aware of it in any other way, swiftly take down such
content.

10.4

The duties set out in subsections  (2)  and  (3)  apply across all areas of a
service, including the way it is designed, operated and used as well as
content present on the service, and (among other things) require the provider
of a service to take or use measures in the following areas, if it is
proportionate to do so—

10.4.a

regulatory compliance and risk management arrangements,

10.4.b

design of functionalities, algorithms and other features,

10.4.c

policies on terms of use,

10.4.d

policies on user access to the service or to particular content present on the
service, including blocking users from accessing the service or particular
content,

10.4.e

content moderation, including taking down content,

10.4.f

functionalities allowing users to control the content they encounter,

10.4.g

user support measures, and

10.4.h

staff policies and practices.

10.5

A duty to include provisions in the terms of service specifying how
individuals are to be protected from illegal content, addressing each
paragraph of subsection  (3) , and (in relation to paragraph (a)) separately
addressing terrorism content, CSEA content (see section 59 and Schedule 6) and
other priority illegal content.

10.6

A duty to apply the provisions of the terms of service referred to in
subsection  (5)  consistently.

10.7

A duty to include provisions in the terms of service giving information about
any proactive technology used by a service for the purpose of compliance with
a duty set out in subsection  (2)  or  (3)  (including the kind of technology,
when it is used, and how it works).

10.8

A duty to ensure that the provisions of the terms of service referred to in
subsections  (5)  and  (7)  are clear and accessible.

######### Additional duty for Category 1 services

10.9

A duty to summarise in the terms of service the findings of the most recent
illegal content risk assessment of a service (including as to levels of risk
and as to nature, and severity, of potential harm to individuals).

######### Interpretation

10.10

In determining what is proportionate for the purposes of this section, the
following factors, in particular, are relevant—

10.10.a

all the findings of the most recent illegal content risk assessment (including
as to levels of risk and as to nature, and severity, of potential harm to
individuals), and

10.10.b

the size and capacity of the provider of a service.

10.11

In this section “ illegal content risk assessment ” has the meaning given by
section 9.

10.12

See also, in relation to duties set out in this section, section 22 (duties
about freedom of expression and privacy).

##### User-to-user services likely to be accessed by children

###### Children’s risk assessment duties

11

11.1

This section sets out the duties about risk assessments which apply in
relation to regulated user-to-user services that are likely to be accessed by
children (in addition to the duties about risk assessments set out in section
9 and, in the case of services likely to be accessed by children which are
Category 1 services, the duties about assessments set out in section 14).

11.2

A duty to carry out a suitable and sufficient children’s risk assessment at a
time set out in, or as provided by, Schedule 3.

11.3

A duty to take appropriate steps to keep a children’s risk assessment up to
date, including when OFCOM make any significant change to a risk profile that
relates to services of the kind in question.

11.4

Before making any significant change to any aspect of a service’s design or
operation, a duty to carry out a further suitable and sufficient children’s
risk assessment relating to the impacts of that proposed change.

11.5

Where a children’s risk assessment of a service identifies the presence of
non-designated content that is harmful to children, a duty to notify OFCOM of—

11.5.a

the kinds of such content identified, and

11.5.b

the incidence of those kinds of content on the service.

11.6

A “children’s risk assessment” of a service of a particular kind means an
assessment of the following matters, taking into account the risk profile that
relates to services of that kind—

11.6.a

the user base, including the number of users who are children in different age
groups;

11.6.b

the level of risk of children who are users of the service encountering the
following by means of the service—

11.6.b.i

each kind of primary priority content that is harmful to children (with each
kind separately assessed),

11.6.b.ii

each kind of priority content that is harmful to children (with each kind
separately assessed), and

11.6.b.iii

non-designated content that is harmful to children,

giving separate consideration to children in different age groups, and taking
into account (in particular) algorithms used by the service and how easily,
quickly and widely content may be disseminated by means of the service;

11.6.c

the level of risk of harm to children presented by different kinds of content
that is harmful to children, giving separate consideration to children in
different age groups;

11.6.d

the level of risk of harm to children presented by content that is harmful to
children which particularly affects individuals with a certain characteristic
or members of a certain group;

11.6.e

the extent to which the design of the service, in particular its
functionalities, affects the level of risk of harm that might be suffered by
children, identifying and assessing those functionalities that present higher
levels of risk, including functionalities—

11.6.e.i

enabling adults to search for other users of the service (including children),
or

11.6.e.ii

enabling adults to contact other users (including children) by means of the
service;

11.6.f

the different ways in which the service is used, including functionalities or
other features of the service that affect how much children use the service
(for example a feature that enables content to play automatically), and the
impact of such use on the level of risk of harm that might be suffered by
children;

11.6.g

the nature, and severity, of the harm that might be suffered by children from
the matters identified in accordance with paragraphs  (b)  to  (f) , giving
separate consideration to children in different age groups;

11.6.h

how the design and operation of the service (including the business model,
governance, use of proactive technology, measures to promote users’ media
literacy and safe use of the service, and other systems and processes) may
reduce or increase the risks identified.

11.7

In this section references to risk profiles are to the risk profiles for the
time being published under section 98 which relate to the risk of harm to
children presented by content that is harmful to children.

11.8

See also—

11.8.a

section 23 (2)  and  (10)  (records of risk assessments), and

11.8.b

Schedule 3 (timing of providers’ assessments).

###### Safety duties protecting children

12

12.1

This section sets out the duties to protect children’s online safety which
apply in relation to regulated user-to-user services that are likely to be
accessed by children (as indicated by the headings).

######### All services

12.2

A duty, in relation to a service, to take or use proportionate measures
relating to the design or operation of the service to effectively—

12.2.a

mitigate and manage the risks of harm to children in different age groups, as
identified in the most recent children’s risk assessment of the service (see
section 11 (6)(g) ), and

12.2.b

mitigate the impact of harm to children in different age groups presented by
content that is harmful to children present on the service.

12.3

A duty to operate a service using proportionate systems and processes designed
to—

12.3.a

prevent children of any age from encountering, by means of the service,
primary priority content that is harmful to children;

12.3.b

protect children in age groups judged to be at risk of harm from other content
that is harmful to children (or from a particular kind of such content) from
encountering it by means of the service.

12.4

The duty set out in subsection  (3)(a)  requires a provider to use age
verification or age estimation (or both) to prevent children of any age from
encountering primary priority content that is harmful to children which the
provider identifies on the service.

12.5

That requirement applies to a provider in relation to a particular kind of
primary priority content that is harmful to children in every case except
where—

12.5.a

a term of service indicates (in whatever words) that the presence of that kind
of primary priority content that is harmful to children is prohibited on the
service, and

12.5.b

that policy applies in relation to all users of the service.

12.6

If a provider is required by subsection  (4)  to use age verification or age
estimation for the purpose of compliance with the duty set out in subsection
(3)(a), the age verification or age estimation must be of such a kind, and
used in such a way, that it is highly effective at correctly determining
whether or not a particular user is a child.

12.7

Age verification or age estimation to identify who is or is not a child user
or which age group a child user is in are examples of measures which (if not
required by subsection  (4) ) may be taken or used (among others) for the
purpose of compliance with a duty set out in subsection (2) or (3).

12.8

The duties set out in subsections  (2)  and  (3)  apply across all areas of a
service, including the way it is designed, operated and used as well as
content present on the service, and (among other things) require the provider
of a service to take or use measures in the following areas, if it is
proportionate to do so—

12.8.a

regulatory compliance and risk management arrangements,

12.8.b

design of functionalities, algorithms and other features,

12.8.c

policies on terms of use,

12.8.d

policies on user access to the service or to particular content present on the
service, including blocking users from accessing the service or particular
content,

12.8.e

content moderation, including taking down content,

12.8.f

functionalities allowing for control over content that is encountered,
especially by children,

12.8.g

user support measures, and

12.8.h

staff policies and practices.

12.9

A duty to include provisions in the terms of service specifying—

12.9.a

how children of any age are to be prevented from encountering primary priority
content that is harmful to children (with each kind of primary priority
content separately covered);

12.9.b

how children in age groups judged to be at risk of harm from priority content
that is harmful to children (or from a particular kind of such content) are to
be protected from encountering it, where they are not prevented from doing so
(with each kind of priority content separately covered);

12.9.c

how children in age groups judged to be at risk of harm from non-designated
content that is harmful to children (or from a particular kind of such
content) are to be protected from encountering it, where they are not
prevented from doing so.

12.10

A duty to apply the provisions of the terms of service referred to in
subsection  (9)  consistently.

12.11

If a provider takes or uses a measure designed to prevent access to the whole
of the service or a part of the service by children under a certain age, a
duty to—

12.11.a

include provisions in the terms of service specifying details about the
operation of the measure, and

12.11.b

apply those provisions consistently.

12.12

A duty to include provisions in the terms of service giving information about
any proactive technology used by a service for the purpose of compliance with
a duty set out in subsection  (2)  or  (3)  (including the kind of technology,
when it is used, and how it works).

12.13

A duty to ensure that the provisions of the terms of service referred to in
subsections  (9) ,  (11)  and  (12)  are clear and accessible.

######### Additional duty for Category 1 services

12.14

A duty to summarise in the terms of service the findings of the most recent
children’s risk assessment of a service (including as to levels of risk and as
to nature, and severity, of potential harm to children).

###### Safety duties protecting children: interpretation

13

13.1

In determining what is proportionate for the purposes of section 12, the
following factors, in particular, are relevant—

13.1.a

all the findings of the most recent children’s risk assessment (including as
to levels of risk and as to nature, and severity, of potential harm to
children), and

13.1.b

the size and capacity of the provider of a service.

13.2

So far as a duty set out in section 12 relates to non-designated content that
is harmful to children, the duty is to be taken to extend only to addressing
risks of harm from the kinds of such content that have been identified in the
most recent children’s risk assessment (if any have been identified).

13.3

References in section 12 (3)(b)  and  (9)(b)  and  (c)  to children in age
groups judged to be at risk of harm from content that is harmful to children
are references to children in age groups judged to be at risk of such harm as
assessed by the provider of a service in the most recent children’s risk
assessment of the service.

13.4

The duties set out in section 12 (3)  and  (9)  are to be taken to extend only
to content that is harmful to children where the risk of harm is presented by
the nature of the content (rather than the fact of its dissemination).

13.5

The duties set out in section 12 extend only to such parts of a service as it
is possible for children to access.

13.6

For the purposes of subsection  (5) , a provider is only entitled to conclude
that it is not possible for children to access a service, or a part of it, if
age verification or age estimation is used on the service with the result that
children are not normally able to access the service or that part of it.

13.7

In section 12 and this section “ children’s risk assessment ” has the meaning
given by section 11.

13.8

See also, in relation to duties set out in section 12, section 22 (duties
about freedom of expression and privacy).

##### Category 1 services

###### Assessment duties: user empowerment

14

14.1

This section sets out the duties about assessments related to adult user
empowerment which apply in relation to Category 1 services (in addition to the
duties about risk assessments set out in section 9 and, in the case of
Category 1 services likely to be accessed by children, section 11).

14.2

A duty to carry out a suitable and sufficient assessment for the purposes of
section 15(2) at a time set out in, or as provided by, Schedule 3.

14.3

A duty to take appropriate steps to keep such an assessment up to date.

14.4

Before making any significant change to any aspect of a service’s design or
operation, a duty to carry out a further suitable and sufficient assessment
for the purposes of section 15(2) relating to the impacts of that proposed
change.

14.5

An assessment of a service “ for the purposes of section 15(2) ” means an
assessment of the following matters—

14.5.a

the user base;

14.5.b

the incidence of relevant content on the service;

14.5.c

the likelihood of adult users of the service encountering, by means of the
service, each kind of relevant content (with each kind separately assessed),
taking into account (in particular) algorithms used by the service, and how
easily, quickly and widely content may be disseminated by means of the
service;

14.5.d

the likelihood of adult users with a certain characteristic or who are members
of a certain group encountering relevant content which particularly affects
them;

14.5.e

the likelihood of functionalities of the service facilitating the presence or
dissemination of relevant content, identifying and assessing those
functionalities more likely to do so;

14.5.f

the different ways in which the service is used, and the impact of such use on
the likelihood of adult users encountering relevant content;

14.5.g

how the design and operation of the service (including the business model,
governance, use of proactive technology, measures to strengthen adult users’
control over their interaction with user-generated content, and other systems
and processes) may reduce or increase the likelihood of adult users
encountering relevant content.

14.6

In this section “ relevant content ” means content to which section 15(2)
applies (content to which user empowerment duties set out in that provision
apply).

14.7

See also—

14.7.a

section 23 (9)  and  (10)  (records of assessments), and

14.7.b

Schedule 3 (timing of providers’ assessments).

###### User empowerment duties

15

15.1

This section sets out the duties to empower adult users which apply in
relation to Category 1 services.

15.2

A duty to include in a service, to the extent that it is proportionate to do
so, features which adult users may use or apply if they wish to increase their
control over content to which this subsection applies.

15.3

The features referred to in subsection  (2)  are those which, if used or
applied by a user, result in the use by the service of systems or processes
designed to effectively—

15.3.a

reduce the likelihood of the user encountering content to which subsection
(2)  applies present on the service, or

15.3.b

alert the user to content present on the service that is a particular kind of
content to which subsection  (2)  applies.

15.4

A duty to ensure that all features included in a service in compliance with
the duty set out in subsection  (2)  (“control features”) are made available
to all adult users and are easy to access.

15.5

A duty to operate a service using a system or process which seeks to ensure
that all registered adult users are offered the earliest possible opportunity,
in relation to each control feature included in the service, to take a step
indicating to the provider that—

15.5.a

the user wishes to retain the default setting for the feature (whether that is
that the feature is in use or applied, or is not in use or applied), or

15.5.b

the user wishes to change the default setting for the feature.

15.6

The duty set out in subsection  (5) —

15.6.a

continues to apply in relation to a user and a control feature for so long as
the user has not yet taken a step mentioned in that subsection in relation to
the feature;

15.6.b

no longer applies in relation to a user once the user has taken such a step in
relation to every control feature included in the service.

15.7

A duty to include clear and accessible provisions in the terms of service
specifying which control features are offered and how users may take advantage
of them.

15.8

A duty to summarise in the terms of service the findings of the most recent
assessment of a service under section 14 (assessments related to the duty set
out in subsection (2)).

15.9

A duty to include in a service features which adult users may use or apply if
they wish to filter out non-verified users.

15.10

The features referred to in subsection  (9)  are those which, if used or
applied by a user, result in the use by the service of systems or processes
designed to effectively—

15.10.a

prevent non-verified users from interacting with content which that user
generates, uploads or shares on the service, and

15.10.b

reduce the likelihood of that user encountering content which non-verified
users generate, upload or share on the service.

###### User empowerment duties: interpretation

16

16.1

In determining what is proportionate for the purposes of section 15 (2) , the
following factors, in particular, are relevant—

16.1.a

all the findings of the most recent assessment under section 14, and

16.1.b

the size and capacity of the provider of the service.

16.2

Section 15 (2)  applies to content that—

16.2.a

is regulated user-generated content in relation to the service in question,
and

16.2.b

is within subsection  (3) ,  (4)  or  (5) .

16.3

Content is within this subsection if it encourages, promotes or provides
instructions for—

16.3.a

suicide or an act of deliberate self-injury, or

16.3.b

an eating disorder or behaviours associated with an eating disorder.

16.4

Content is within this subsection if it is abusive and the abuse targets any
of the following characteristics—

16.4.a

race,

16.4.b

religion,

16.4.c

sex,

16.4.d

sexual orientation,

16.4.e

disability, or

16.4.f

gender reassignment.

16.5

Content is within this subsection if it incites hatred against people—

16.5.a

of a particular race, religion, sex or sexual orientation,

16.5.b

who have a disability, or

16.5.c

who have the characteristic of gender reassignment.

16.6

The duty set out in section 15 (5)  applies in relation to all registered
adult users, not just those who begin to use a service after that duty begins
to apply.

16.7

In section 15 and this section—

      “ disability ” means any physical or mental impairment;           “
injury ” includes poisoning;           “ non-verified user ” means a user who—
is an individual, whether in the United Kingdom or outside it, and
has not verified their identity to the provider of a service;
“ race ” includes colour, nationality, and ethnic or national origins.

16.8

In section 15 and this section—

16.8.a

references to features include references to functionalities and settings, and

16.8.b

references to religion include references to a lack of religion.

16.9

For the purposes of section 15 and this section, a person has the
characteristic of gender reassignment if the person is proposing to undergo,
is undergoing or has undergone a process (or part of a process) for the
purpose of reassigning the person’s sex by changing physiological or other
attributes of sex, and the reference to gender reassignment in subsection  (4)
is to be construed accordingly.

16.10

See also, in relation to duties set out in section 15, section 22 (duties
about freedom of expression and privacy).

###### Duties to protect content of democratic importance

17

17.1

This section sets out the duties to protect content of democratic importance
which apply in relation to Category 1 services.

17.2

A duty to operate a service using proportionate systems and processes designed
to ensure that the importance of the free expression of content of democratic
importance is taken into account when making decisions about—

17.2.a

how to treat such content (especially decisions about whether to take it down
or restrict users’ access to it), and

17.2.b

whether to take action against a user generating, uploading or sharing such
content.

17.3

A duty to ensure that the systems and processes mentioned in subsection  (2)
apply in the same way to a wide diversity of political opinion.

17.4

A duty to include provisions in the terms of service specifying the policies
and processes that are designed to take account of the principle mentioned in
subsection  (2) , including, in particular, how that principle is applied to
decisions mentioned in that subsection.

17.5

A duty to ensure that—

17.5.a

the provisions of the terms of service referred to in subsection  (4)  are
clear and accessible, and

17.5.b

those provisions are applied consistently.

17.6

In determining what is proportionate for the purposes of subsection (2), the
size and capacity of the provider of a service, in particular, is relevant.

17.7

For the purposes of this section content is “ content of democratic importance
”, in relation to a user-to-user service, if—

17.7.a

the content is—

17.7.a.i

news publisher content in relation to that service, or

17.7.a.ii

regulated user-generated content in relation to that service; and

17.7.b

the content is or appears to be specifically intended to contribute to
democratic political debate in the United Kingdom or a part or area of the
United Kingdom.

17.8

In this section, the reference to “taking action” against a user is to giving
a warning to a user, or suspending or banning a user from using a service, or
in any way restricting a user’s ability to use a service.

17.9

For the meaning of “news publisher content” and “regulated user-generated
content”, see section 55.

###### Duties to protect news publisher content

18

18.1

This section sets out the duties to protect news publisher content which apply
in relation to Category 1 services.

18.2

Subject to subsections  (4) ,  (5)  and  (8) , a duty, in relation to a
service, to take the steps set out in subsection  (3)  before—

18.2.a

taking action in relation to content present on the service that is news
publisher content, or

18.2.b

taking action against a user who is a recognised news publisher.

18.3

The steps referred to in subsection (2) are—

18.3.a

to give the recognised news publisher in question a notification which—

18.3.a.i

specifies the action that the provider is considering taking,

18.3.a.ii

gives reasons for that proposed action by reference to each relevant provision
of the terms of service,

18.3.a.iii

where the proposed action relates to news publisher content that is also
journalistic content, explains how the provider took the importance of the
free expression of journalistic content into account when deciding on the
proposed action, and

18.3.a.iv

specifies a reasonable period within which the recognised news publisher may
make representations,

18.3.b

to consider any representations that are made, and

18.3.c

to notify the recognised news publisher of the decision and the reasons for it
(addressing any representations made).

18.4

If a provider of a service reasonably considers that the provider would incur
criminal or civil liability in relation to news publisher content present on
the service if it were not taken down swiftly, the provider may take down that
content without having taken the steps set out in subsection  (3) .

18.5

A provider of a service may also take down news publisher content present on
the service without having taken the steps set out in subsection  (3)  if that
content amounts to a relevant offence (see section 59 and also subsection (10)
of this section).

18.6

Subject to subsection  (8) , if a provider takes action in relation to news
publisher content or against a recognised news publisher without having taken
the steps set out in subsection  (3) , a duty to take the steps set out in
subsection  (7) .

18.7

The steps referred to in subsection  (6)  are—

18.7.a

to swiftly notify the recognised news publisher in question of the action
taken, giving the provider’s justification for not having first taken the
steps set out in subsection (3),

18.7.b

to specify a reasonable period within which the recognised news publisher may
request that the action is reversed, and

18.7.c

if a request is made as mentioned in paragraph (b)—

18.7.c.i

to consider the request and whether the steps set out in subsection (3) should
have been taken prior to the action being taken,

18.7.c.ii

if the provider concludes that those steps should have been taken, to swiftly
reverse the action, and

18.7.c.iii

to notify the recognised news publisher of the decision and the reasons for it
(addressing any reasons accompanying the request for reversal of the action).

18.8

If a recognised news publisher has been banned from using a service (and the
ban is still in force), the provider of the service may take action in
relation to news publisher content present on the service which was generated
or originally published or broadcast by the recognised news publisher without
complying with the duties set out in this section.

18.9

For the purposes of this section, a provider is not to be regarded as taking
action in relation to news publisher content in the following circumstances—

18.9.a

a provider takes action in relation to content which is not news publisher
content, that action affects related news publisher content, the grounds for
the action only relate to the content which is not news publisher content, and
it is not technically feasible for the action only to relate to the content
which is not news publisher content;

18.9.b

a provider takes action against a user, and that action affects news publisher
content that has been uploaded to or shared on the service by the user.

18.10

Section 192 (providers’ judgements about the status of content) applies in
relation to judgements by providers about whether news publisher content
amounts to a relevant offence as it applies in relation to judgements about
whether content is illegal content.

18.11

Any provision of the terms of service has effect subject to this section.

18.12

In this section—

18.12.a

references to “news publisher content” are to content that is news publisher
content in relation to the service in question;

18.12.b

references to “taking action” against a person are to giving a warning to a
person, or suspending or banning a person from using a service, or in any way
restricting a person’s ability to use a service.

18.13

In this section references to “ taking action ” in relation to content are to—

18.13.a

taking down content,

18.13.b

restricting users’ access to content, or

18.13.c

adding warning labels to content, except warning labels normally encountered
only by child users,

and also include references to taking any other action in relation to content
on the grounds that it is content of a kind which is the subject of a relevant
term of service (but not otherwise).

18.14

A “ relevant term of service ” means a term of service which indicates to
users (in whatever words) that the presence of a particular kind of content,
from the time it is generated, uploaded or shared on the service, is not
tolerated on the service or is tolerated but liable to result in the provider
treating it in a way that makes it less likely that other users will encounter
it.

18.15

Taking any step set out in subsection (3) or  (7)  does not count as “ taking
action ” for the purposes of this section.

18.16

See—

      section 19 for the meaning of “journalistic content”;           section
55 for the meaning of “news publisher content”;           section 56 for the
meaning of “recognised news publisher”.

###### Duties to protect journalistic content

19

19.1

This section sets out the duties to protect journalistic content which apply
in relation to Category 1 services.

######### The duties

19.2

A duty to operate a service using proportionate systems and processes designed
to ensure that the importance of the free expression of journalistic content
is taken into account when making decisions about—

19.2.a

how to treat such content (especially decisions about whether to take it down
or restrict users’ access to it), and

19.2.b

whether to take action against a user generating, uploading or sharing such
content.

19.3

A duty, in relation to a decision by a provider to take down content or to
restrict access to it, to make a dedicated and expedited complaints procedure
available to a person who considers the content to be journalistic content and
who is—

19.3.a

the user who generated, uploaded or shared the content on the service, or

19.3.b

the creator of the content (see subsections  (14)  and  (15) ).

19.4

A duty to make a dedicated and expedited complaints procedure available to
users of a service in relation to a decision by the provider of the service to
take action against a user because of content generated, uploaded or shared by
the user which the user considers to be journalistic content.

19.5

A duty to ensure that—

19.5.a

if a complaint about a decision mentioned in subsection  (3)  is upheld, the
content is swiftly reinstated on the service;

19.5.b

if a complaint about a decision mentioned in subsection  (4)  is upheld, the
action against the user is swiftly reversed.

19.6

Subsections (3) and (4) do not require a provider to make a dedicated and
expedited complaints procedure available to a recognised news publisher in
relation to a decision if the provider has taken the steps set out in section
18(3) in relation to that decision.

19.7

A duty to include provisions in the terms of service specifying—

19.7.a

by what methods content present on the service is to be identified as
journalistic content;

19.7.b

how the importance of the free expression of journalistic content is to be
taken into account when making decisions mentioned in subsection  (2) ;

19.7.c

the policies and processes for handling complaints in relation to content
which is, or is considered to be, journalistic content.

19.8

A duty to ensure that—

19.8.a

the provisions of the terms of service referred to in subsection  (7)  are
clear and accessible, and

19.8.b

those provisions are applied consistently.

######### Interpretation

19.9

In determining what is proportionate for the purposes of subsection (2), the
size and capacity of the provider of a service, in particular, is relevant.

19.10

For the purposes of this Part content is “ journalistic content ”, in relation
to a user-to-user service, if—

19.10.a

the content is—

19.10.a.i

news publisher content in relation to that service, or

19.10.a.ii

regulated user-generated content in relation to that service;

19.10.b

the content is generated for the purposes of journalism; and

19.10.c

the content is UK-linked.

19.11

For the purposes of this section content is “UK-linked” if—

19.11.a

United Kingdom users of the service form one of the target markets for the
content (or the only target market), or

19.11.b

the content is or is likely to be of interest to a significant number of
United Kingdom users.

19.12

In this section references to “taking action” against a user are to giving a
warning to a user, or suspending or banning a user from using a service, or in
any way restricting a user’s ability to use a service.

19.13

In this section the reference to the “ creator ” of content is to be read in
accordance with subsections  (14)  and  (15) .

19.14

The creator of news publisher content is the recognised news publisher in
question.

19.15

The creator of content other than news publisher content is—

19.15.a

an individual who—

19.15.a.i

created the content, and

19.15.a.ii

is in the United Kingdom; or

19.15.b

an entity which—

19.15.b.i

created the content, and

19.15.b.ii

is incorporated or formed under the law of any part of the United Kingdom.

19.16

For the meaning of “news publisher content”, “regulated user-generated
content” and “recognised news publisher”, see sections 55 and 56.

##### Duties about content reporting and complaints procedures

###### Duty about content reporting

20

20.1

This section sets out the duty about content reporting which applies in
relation to all regulated user-to-user services.

20.2

A duty to operate a service using systems and processes that allow users and
affected persons to easily report content which they consider to be content of
a kind specified below (with the duty extending to different kinds of content
depending on the kind of service, as indicated by the headings).

######### All services

20.3

Illegal content.

######### Services likely to be accessed by children

20.4

Content that is harmful to children, present on a part of a service that it is
possible for children to access.

######### Interpretation

20.5

In this section “ affected person ” means a person, other than a user of the
service in question, who is in the United Kingdom and who is—

20.5.a

the subject of the content,

20.5.b

a member of a class or group of people with a certain characteristic targeted
by the content,

20.5.c

a parent of, or other adult with responsibility for, a child who is a user of
the service or is the subject of the content, or

20.5.d

an adult providing assistance in using the service to another adult who
requires such assistance, where that other adult is a user of the service or
is the subject of the content.

20.6

For the purposes of subsection  (4) , a provider is only entitled to conclude
that it is not possible for children to access a service, or a part of it, if
age verification or age estimation is used on the service with the result that
children are not normally able to access the service or that part of it.

20.7

See also—

20.7.a

section 22 (duties about freedom of expression and privacy), and

20.7.b

section 72 (5)(a)  (reporting of content that terms of service allow to be
taken down or restricted).

###### Duties about complaints procedures

21

21.1

This section sets out the duties about complaints procedures which apply in
relation to all regulated user-to-user services.

21.2

A duty to operate a complaints procedure in relation to a service that—

21.2.a

allows for relevant kinds of complaint to be made (as set out under the
headings below),

21.2.b

provides for appropriate action to be taken by the provider of the service in
response to complaints of a relevant kind, and

21.2.c

is easy to access, easy to use (including by children) and transparent.

21.3

A duty to include in the terms of service provisions which are easily
accessible (including to children) specifying the policies and processes that
govern the handling and resolution of complaints of a relevant kind.

######### All services

21.4

The following kinds of complaint are relevant for all services—

21.4.a

complaints by users and affected persons about content present on a service
which they consider to be illegal content;

21.4.b

complaints by users and affected persons if they consider that the provider is
not complying with a duty set out in—

21.4.b.i

section 10 (illegal content),

21.4.b.ii

section 20 (content reporting), or

21.4.b.iii

section 22 (2)  or  (3)  (freedom of expression and privacy);

21.4.c

complaints by a user who has generated, uploaded or shared content on a
service if that content is taken down on the basis that it is illegal content;

21.4.d

complaints by a user of a service if the provider has given a warning to the
user, suspended or banned the user from using the service, or in any other way
restricted the user’s ability to use the service, as a result of content
generated, uploaded or shared by the user which the provider considers to be
illegal content;

21.4.e

complaints by a user who has generated, uploaded or shared content on a
service if—

21.4.e.i

the use of proactive technology on the service results in that content being
taken down or access to it being restricted, or given a lower priority or
otherwise becoming less likely to be encountered by other users, and

21.4.e.ii

the user considers that the proactive technology has been used in a way not
contemplated by, or in breach of, the terms of service (for example, by
affecting content not of a kind specified in the terms of service as a kind of
content in relation to which the technology would operate).

######### Services likely to be accessed by children

21.5

The following kinds of complaint are relevant for services that are likely to
be accessed by children—

21.5.a

complaints by users and affected persons about content, present on a part of a
service that it is possible for children to access, which they consider to be
content that is harmful to children;

21.5.b

complaints by users and affected persons if they consider that the provider is
not complying with a duty set out in section 12 (children’s online safety);

21.5.c

complaints by a user who has generated, uploaded or shared content on a
service if that content is taken down, or access to it is restricted, on the
basis that it is content that is harmful to children;

21.5.d

complaints by a user of a service if the provider has given a warning to the
user, suspended or banned the user from using the service, or in any other way
restricted the user’s ability to use the service, as a result of content
generated, uploaded or shared by the user which the provider considers to be
content that is harmful to children;

21.5.e

complaints by a user who is unable to access content because measures used to
comply with a duty set out in section 12 (2)  or  (3)  have resulted in an
incorrect assessment of the user’s age.

######### Category 1 services

21.6

The relevant kind of complaint for Category 1 services is complaints by users
and affected persons if they consider that the provider is not complying with
a duty set out in—

21.6.a

section 15 (user empowerment),

21.6.b

section 17 (content of democratic importance),

21.6.c

section 18 (news publisher content),

21.6.d

section 19 (journalistic content), or

21.6.e

section 22 (4) ,  (6)  or  (7)  (freedom of expression and privacy).

######### Interpretation

21.7

In this section “ affected person ” has the meaning given by section 20.

21.8

For the purposes of subsection  (5)(a) , a provider is only entitled to
conclude that it is not possible for children to access a service, or a part
of it, if age verification or age estimation is used on the service with the
result that children are not normally able to access the service or that part
of it.

21.9

See also—

21.9.a

section 22 (duties about freedom of expression and privacy), and

21.9.b

section 72 (6)  (complaints procedure relating to content that terms of
service allow to be taken down or restricted).

##### Cross-cutting duties

###### Duties about freedom of expression and privacy

22

22.1

This section sets out the duties about freedom of expression and privacy which
apply in relation to regulated user-to-user services (as indicated by the
headings).

######### All services

22.2

When deciding on, and implementing, safety measures and policies, a duty to
have particular regard to the importance of protecting users’ right to freedom
of expression within the law.

22.3

When deciding on, and implementing, safety measures and policies, a duty to
have particular regard to the importance of protecting users from a breach of
any statutory provision or rule of law concerning privacy that is relevant to
the use or operation of a user-to-user service (including, but not limited to,
any such provision or rule concerning the processing of personal data).

######### Additional duties for Category 1 services

22.4

A duty—

22.4.a

when deciding on safety measures and policies, to carry out an assessment of
the impact that such measures or policies would have on—

22.4.a.i

users’ right to freedom of expression within the law, and

22.4.a.ii

the privacy of users; and

22.4.b

to carry out an assessment of the impact of adopted safety measures and
policies on the matters mentioned in paragraph  (a)(i)  and  (ii) .

22.5

An impact assessment relating to a service must include a section which
considers the impact of the safety measures and policies on the availability
and treatment on the service of content which is news publisher content or
journalistic content in relation to the service.

22.6

A duty to—

22.6.a

keep an impact assessment up to date, and

22.6.b

publish impact assessments.

22.7

A duty to specify in a publicly available statement the positive steps that
the provider has taken in response to an impact assessment to—

22.7.a

protect users’ right to freedom of expression within the law, and

22.7.b

protect the privacy of users.

######### Interpretation

22.8

In this section—

      “ impact assessment ” means an impact assessment under subsection  (4) ;
“ safety measures and policies ” means measures and policies designed to
secure compliance with any of the duties set out in—         section 10
(illegal content),           section 12 (children’s online safety),
section 15 (user empowerment),           section 20 (content reporting), or
section 21 (complaints procedures).

22.9

Any reference in this section to the privacy of users or steps taken to
protect the privacy of users is to be construed in accordance with subsection
(3) .

22.10

See—

      section 19 for the meaning of “journalistic content”;           section
55 for the meaning of “news publisher content”.

###### Record-keeping and review duties

23

23.1

This section sets out the record-keeping and review duties which apply in
relation to regulated user-to-user services (as indicated by the headings).

######### All services

23.2

A duty to make and keep a written record, in an easily understandable form, of
all aspects of every risk assessment under section 9 or 11, including details
about how the assessment was carried out and its findings.

23.3

A duty to make and keep a written record of any measures taken or in use to
comply with a relevant duty which—

23.3.a

are described in a code of practice and recommended for the purpose of
compliance with the duty in question, and

23.3.b

apply in relation to the provider and the service in question.

In this section such measures are referred to as “ applicable measures in a
code of practice ”.

23.4

If alternative measures have been taken or are in use to comply with a
relevant duty, a duty to make and keep a written record containing the
following information—

23.4.a

the applicable measures in a code of practice that have not been taken or are
not in use,

23.4.b

the alternative measures that have been taken or are in use,

23.4.c

how those alternative measures amount to compliance with the duty in question,
and

23.4.d

how the provider has complied with section 49(5) (freedom of expression and
privacy).

23.5

If alternative measures have been taken or are in use to comply with a duty
set out in section 10 (2)  or  (3)  or 12 (2)  or  (3) , the record required
under subsection  (4)  of this section must also indicate whether such
measures have been taken or are in use in every area listed in section 10 (4)
or 12 (8)  (as the case may be) in relation to which there are applicable
measures in a code of practice.

23.6

A duty to review compliance with the relevant duties in relation to a service—

23.6.a

regularly, and

23.6.b

as soon as reasonably practicable after making any significant change to any
aspect of the design or operation of the service.

23.7

OFCOM may provide that particular descriptions of providers of user-to-user
services are exempt from any or all of the duties set out in this section, and
may revoke such an exemption.

23.8

OFCOM must publish details of any exemption or revocation under subsection
(7) , including reasons for the revocation of an exemption.

######### Additional duties for Category 1 services

23.9

A duty to make and keep a written record, in an easily understandable form, of
all aspects of every assessment under section 14 (assessments related to the
adult user empowerment duty set out in section 15(2)), including details about
how the assessment was carried out and its findings.

23.10

As soon as reasonably practicable after making a record of an assessment as
required by subsection (2) or  (9) , or revising such a record, a duty to
supply OFCOM with a copy of the record (in full).

######### Interpretation

23.11

In this section—

      “ alternative measures ” means measures other than measures which are
(in relation to the provider and the service in question) applicable measures
in a code of practice;           “ code of practice ” means a code of practice
published under section 46;           “ relevant duties ” means the duties set
out in—         section 10 (illegal content),           section 12 (children’s
online safety),           section 15 (user empowerment),           section 17
(content of democratic importance),           section 19 (journalistic
content),           section 20 (content reporting), and           section 21
(complaints procedures),         and for the purposes of subsection (6), also
includes the duties set out in sections 18 (news publisher content), 71 and 72
(duties about terms of service), and 75 (deceased child users).

#### Providers of search services: duties of care

##### Search services: which duties apply, and scope of duties

###### Providers of search services: duties of care

24

24.1

Subsections  (2)  to  (4)  apply to determine which of the duties set out in
this Chapter must be complied with by providers of regulated search services.

24.2

All providers of regulated search services must comply with the following
duties in relation to each such service which they provide—

24.2.a

the duties about illegal content risk assessments set out in section 26,

24.2.b

the duties about illegal content set out in section 27 (2)  to  (8) ,

24.2.c

the duty about content reporting set out in section 31,

24.2.d

the duties about complaints procedures set out in section 32,

24.2.e

the duties about freedom of expression and privacy set out in section 33, and

24.2.f

the duties about record-keeping and review set out in section 34 (2)  to  (6)
.

24.3

Additional duties must be complied with by providers of particular kinds of
regulated search services, as follows.

24.4

All providers of regulated search services that are likely to be accessed by
children must comply with the following duties in relation to each such
service which they provide—

24.4.a

the duties about children’s risk assessments set out in section 28, and

24.4.b

the duties to protect children’s online safety set out in section 29 (2)  to
(8) .

24.5

All providers of regulated search services that are Category 2A services must
comply with the following duties in relation to each such service which they
provide—

24.5.a

the duty about illegal content risk assessments set out in section 27 (9) ,

24.5.b

the duty about children’s risk assessments set out in section 29 (9) , and

24.5.c

the duty about record-keeping set out in section 34 (9) .

24.6

For the meaning of “likely to be accessed by children”, see section 37.

24.7

For the meaning of “Category 2A service”, see section 95 (register of
categories of services).

###### Scope of duties of care

25

25.1

A duty set out in this Chapter which must be complied with in relation to a
search service extends only to—

25.1.a

the search content of the service,

25.1.b

the design, operation and use of the search engine in the United Kingdom, and

25.1.c

in the case of a duty that is expressed to apply in relation to users of a
service, the design, operation and use of the search engine as it affects
United Kingdom users of the service.

25.2

For the purposes of the application of this Chapter in relation to the search
engine of a combined service (see section 7 (6) )—

25.2.a

a duty set out in this Chapter which requires a matter to be included in a
publicly available statement may be satisfied by including the matter in the
terms of service;

25.2.b

references in this Chapter (except in section 24) to a search service are to
be read as references to the search engine;

25.2.c

references in this Chapter (except in section 24) to the provider of a search
service are to be read as references to the provider of the combined service.

##### Illegal content duties for search services

###### Illegal content risk assessment duties

26

26.1

This section sets out the duties about risk assessments which apply in
relation to all regulated search services.

26.2

A duty to carry out a suitable and sufficient illegal content risk assessment
at a time set out in, or as provided by, Schedule 3.

26.3

A duty to take appropriate steps to keep an illegal content risk assessment up
to date, including when OFCOM make any significant change to a risk profile
that relates to services of the kind in question.

26.4

Before making any significant change to any aspect of a service’s design or
operation, a duty to carry out a further suitable and sufficient illegal
content risk assessment relating to the impacts of that proposed change.

26.5

An “illegal content risk assessment” of a service of a particular kind means
an assessment of the following matters, taking into account the risk profile
that relates to services of that kind—

26.5.a

the level of risk of individuals who are users of the service encountering
search content of the following kinds—

26.5.a.i

each kind of priority illegal content (with each kind separately assessed),
and

26.5.a.ii

other illegal content,

taking into account (in particular) risks presented by algorithms used by the
service, and the way that the service indexes, organises and presents search
results;

26.5.b

the level of risk of functionalities of the service facilitating individuals
encountering search content that is illegal content, identifying and assessing
those functionalities that present higher levels of risk;

26.5.c

the nature, and severity, of the harm that might be suffered by individuals
from the matters identified in accordance with paragraphs (a) and (b);

26.5.d

how the design and operation of the service (including the business model,
governance, use of proactive technology, measures to promote users’ media
literacy and safe use of the service, and other systems and processes) may
reduce or increase the risks identified.

26.6

In this section references to risk profiles are to the risk profiles for the
time being published under section 98 which relate to the risk of harm to
individuals presented by illegal content.

26.7

See also—

26.7.a

section 34 (2)  and  (9)  (records of risk assessments), and

26.7.b

Schedule 3 (timing of providers’ assessments).

###### Safety duties about illegal content

27

27.1

This section sets out the duties about illegal content which apply in relation
to regulated search services (as indicated by the headings).

######### All services

27.2

A duty, in relation to a service, to take or use proportionate measures
relating to the design or operation of the service to effectively mitigate and
manage the risks of harm to individuals, as identified in the most recent
illegal content risk assessment of the service (see section 26(5)(c)).

27.3

A duty to operate a service using proportionate systems and processes designed
to minimise the risk of individuals encountering search content of the
following kinds—

27.3.a

priority illegal content;

27.3.b

other illegal content that the provider knows about (having been alerted to it
by another person or become aware of it in any other way).

27.4

The duties set out in subsections  (2)  and  (3)  apply across all areas of a
service, including the way the search engine is designed, operated and used as
well as search content of the service, and (among other things) require the
provider of a service to take or use measures in the following areas, if it is
proportionate to do so—

27.4.a

regulatory compliance and risk management arrangements,

27.4.b

design of functionalities, algorithms and other features relating to the
search engine,

27.4.c

functionalities allowing users to control the content they encounter in search
results,

27.4.d

content prioritisation,

27.4.e

user support measures, and

27.4.f

staff policies and practices.

27.5

A duty to include provisions in a publicly available statement specifying how
individuals are to be protected from search content that is illegal content.

27.6

A duty to apply the provisions of the statement referred to in subsection  (5)
consistently.

27.7

A duty to include provisions in a publicly available statement giving
information about any proactive technology used by a service for the purpose
of compliance with a duty set out in subsection  (2)  or  (3)  (including the
kind of technology, when it is used, and how it works).

27.8

A duty to ensure that the provisions of the publicly available statement
referred to in subsections  (5)  and  (7)  are clear and accessible.

######### Additional duty for Category 2A services

27.9

A duty to summarise in a publicly available statement the findings of the most
recent illegal content risk assessment of a service (including as to levels of
risk and as to nature, and severity, of potential harm to individuals).

######### Interpretation

27.10

In determining what is proportionate for the purposes of this section, the
following factors, in particular, are relevant—

27.10.a

all the findings of the most recent illegal content risk assessment (including
as to levels of risk and as to nature, and severity, of potential harm to
individuals), and

27.10.b

the size and capacity of the provider of a service.

27.11

In this section “ illegal content risk assessment ” has the meaning given by
section 26.

27.12

See also, in relation to duties set out in this section, section 33 (duties
about freedom of expression and privacy).

##### Search services likely to be accessed by children

###### Children’s risk assessment duties

28

28.1

This section sets out the duties about risk assessments which apply in
relation to regulated search services that are likely to be accessed by
children (in addition to the duties about risk assessments set out in section
26).

28.2

A duty to carry out a suitable and sufficient children’s risk assessment at a
time set out in, or as provided by, Schedule 3.

28.3

A duty to take appropriate steps to keep a children’s risk assessment up to
date, including when OFCOM make any significant change to a risk profile that
relates to services of the kind in question.

28.4

Before making any significant change to any aspect of a service’s design or
operation, a duty to carry out a further suitable and sufficient children’s
risk assessment relating to the impacts of that proposed change.

28.5

A “children’s risk assessment” of a service of a particular kind means an
assessment of the following matters, taking into account the risk profile that
relates to services of that kind—

28.5.a

the level of risk of children who are users of the service encountering search
content of the following kinds—

28.5.a.i

each kind of primary priority content that is harmful to children (with each
kind separately assessed),

28.5.a.ii

each kind of priority content that is harmful to children (with each kind
separately assessed), and

28.5.a.iii

non-designated content that is harmful to children,

giving separate consideration to children in different age groups, and taking
into account (in particular) risks presented by algorithms used by the service
and the way that the service indexes, organises and presents search results;

28.5.b

the level of risk of children who are users of the service encountering search
content that is harmful to children which particularly affects individuals
with a certain characteristic or members of a certain group;

28.5.c

the extent to which the design of the service, in particular its
functionalities, affects the level of risk of harm that might be suffered by
children, identifying and assessing those functionalities that present higher
levels of risk, including a functionality that makes suggestions relating to
users’ search requests (predictive search functionality);

28.5.d

the different ways in which the service is used, including functionalities or
other features of the service that affect how much children use the service,
and the impact of such use on the level of risk of harm that might be suffered
by children;

28.5.e

the nature, and severity, of the harm that might be suffered by children from
the matters identified in accordance with paragraphs  (a)  to  (d) , giving
separate consideration to children in different age groups;

28.5.f

how the design and operation of the service (including the business model,
governance, use of proactive technology, measures to promote users’ media
literacy and safe use of the service, and other systems and processes) may
reduce or increase the risks identified.

28.6

In this section references to risk profiles are to the risk profiles for the
time being published under section 98 which relate to the risk of harm to
children presented by content that is harmful to children.

28.7

See also—

28.7.a

section 34 (2)  and  (9)  (records of risk assessments), and

28.7.b

Schedule 3 (timing of providers’ assessments).

###### Safety duties protecting children

29

29.1

This section sets out the duties to protect children’s online safety which
apply in relation to regulated search services that are likely to be accessed
by children (as indicated by the headings).

######### All services

29.2

A duty, in relation to a service, to take or use proportionate measures
relating to the design or operation of the service to effectively—

29.2.a

mitigate and manage the risks of harm to children in different age groups, as
identified in the most recent children’s risk assessment of the service (see
section 28 (5)(e) ), and

29.2.b

mitigate the impact of harm to children in different age groups presented by
search content that is harmful to children.

29.3

A duty to operate a service using proportionate systems and processes designed
to—

29.3.a

minimise the risk of children of any age encountering search content that is
primary priority content that is harmful to children;

29.3.b

minimise the risk of children in age groups judged to be at risk of harm from
