other content that is harmful to children (or from a particular kind of such
content) encountering search content of that kind.

29.4

The duties set out in subsections  (2)  and  (3)  apply across all areas of a
service, including the way the search engine is designed, operated and used as
well as search content of the service, and (among other things) require the
provider of a service to take or use measures in the following areas, if it is
proportionate to do so—

29.4.a

regulatory compliance and risk management arrangements,

29.4.b

design of functionalities, algorithms and other features relating to the
search engine,

29.4.c

functionalities allowing for control over content that is encountered in
search results, especially by children,

29.4.d

content prioritisation,

29.4.e

user support measures, and

29.4.f

staff policies and practices.

29.5

A duty to include provisions in a publicly available statement specifying how
children are to be protected from search content of the following kinds—

29.5.a

primary priority content that is harmful to children (with each kind of
primary priority content separately covered),

29.5.b

priority content that is harmful to children (with each kind of priority
content separately covered), and

29.5.c

non-designated content that is harmful to children.

29.6

A duty to apply the provisions of the statement referred to in subsection  (5)
consistently.

29.7

A duty to include provisions in a publicly available statement giving
information about any proactive technology used by a service for the purpose
of compliance with a duty set out in subsection  (2)  or  (3)  (including the
kind of technology, when it is used, and how it works).

29.8

A duty to ensure that the provisions of the publicly available statement
referred to in subsections  (5)  and  (7)  are clear and accessible.

######### Additional duty for Category 2A services

29.9

A duty to summarise in a publicly available statement the findings of the most
recent children’s risk assessment of a service (including as to levels of risk
and as to nature, and severity, of potential harm to children).

###### Safety duties protecting children: interpretation

30

30.1

In determining what is proportionate for the purposes of section 29, the
following factors, in particular, are relevant—

30.1.a

all the findings of the most recent children’s risk assessment (including as
to levels of risk and as to nature, and severity, of potential harm to
children), and

30.1.b

the size and capacity of the provider of a service.

30.2

So far as a duty set out in section 29 relates to non-designated content that
is harmful to children, the duty is to be taken to extend only to addressing
risks of harm from the kinds of such content that have been identified in the
most recent children’s risk assessment (if any have been identified).

30.3

The reference in section 29 (3)(b)  to children in age groups judged to be at
risk of harm from content that is harmful to children is a reference to
children in age groups judged to be at risk of such harm as assessed by the
provider of a service in the most recent children’s risk assessment of the
service.

30.4

The duties set out in section 29 (3)  are to be taken to extend only to
content that is harmful to children where the risk of harm is presented by the
nature of the content (rather than the fact of its dissemination).

30.5

The duties set out in section 29 extend only to such parts of a service as it
is possible for children to access.

30.6

For the purposes of subsection  (5) , a provider is only entitled to conclude
that it is not possible for children to access a service, or a part of it, if
age verification or age estimation is used on the service with the result that
children are not normally able to access the service or that part of it.

30.7

In section 29 and this section “ children’s risk assessment ” has the meaning
given by section 28.

30.8

See also, in relation to duties set out in section 29, section 33 (duties
about freedom of expression and privacy).

##### Duties about content reporting and complaints procedures

###### Duty about content reporting

31

31.1

This section sets out the duty about content reporting which applies in
relation to all regulated search services.

31.2

A duty to operate a service using systems and processes that allow users and
affected persons to easily report search content which they consider to be
content of a kind specified below (with the duty extending to content that is
harmful to children depending on the kind of service, as indicated by the
headings).

######### All services

31.3

Illegal content.

######### Services likely to be accessed by children

31.4

Content that is harmful to children.

######### Interpretation

31.5

In this section “ affected person ” means a person, other than a user of the
service in question, who is in the United Kingdom and who is—

31.5.a

the subject of the content,

31.5.b

a member of a class or group of people with a certain characteristic targeted
by the content,

31.5.c

a parent of, or other adult with responsibility for, a child who is a user of
the service or is the subject of the content, or

31.5.d

an adult providing assistance in using the service to another adult who
requires such assistance, where that other adult is a user of the service or
is the subject of the content.

31.6

See also, in relation to the duty set out in this section, section 33 (duties
about freedom of expression and privacy).

###### Duties about complaints procedures

32

32.1

This section sets out the duties about complaints procedures which apply in
relation to all regulated search services.

32.2

A duty to operate a complaints procedure in relation to a service that—

32.2.a

allows for relevant kinds of complaint to be made (as set out under the
headings below),

32.2.b

provides for appropriate action to be taken by the provider of the service in
response to complaints of a relevant kind, and

32.2.c

is easy to access, easy to use (including by children) and transparent.

32.3

A duty to make the policies and processes that govern the handling and
resolution of complaints of a relevant kind publicly available and easily
accessible (including to children).

######### All services

32.4

The following kinds of complaint are relevant for all services—

32.4.a

complaints by users and affected persons about search content which they
consider to be illegal content;

32.4.b

complaints by users and affected persons if they consider that the provider is
not complying with a duty set out in—

32.4.b.i

section 27 (illegal content),

32.4.b.ii

section 31 (content reporting), or

32.4.b.iii

section 33 (freedom of expression and privacy);

32.4.c

complaints by an interested person if the provider of a search service takes
or uses measures in order to comply with a duty set out in section 27 that
result in content relating to that interested person no longer appearing in
search results or being given a lower priority in search results;

32.4.d

complaints by an interested person if—

32.4.d.i

the use of proactive technology on a search service results in content
relating to that interested person no longer appearing in search results or
being given a lower priority in search results, and

32.4.d.ii

the interested person considers that the proactive technology has been used in
a way not contemplated by, or in breach of, the provider’s policies on its use
(for example, by affecting content not of a kind specified in those policies
as a kind of content in relation to which the technology would operate).

######### Services likely to be accessed by children

32.5

The following kinds of complaint are relevant for services that are likely to
be accessed by children—

32.5.a

complaints by users and affected persons about search content which they
consider to be content that is harmful to children;

32.5.b

complaints by users and affected persons if they consider that the provider is
not complying with a duty set out in section 29 (children’s online safety);

32.5.c

complaints by an interested person if the provider of a search service takes
or uses measures in order to comply with a duty set out in section 29 that
result in content relating to that interested person no longer appearing in
search results or being given a lower priority in search results;

32.5.d

complaints by a user who is unable to access content because measures used to
comply with a duty set out in section 29 (2)  or  (3)  have resulted in an
incorrect assessment of the user’s age.

######### Interpretation

32.6

In this section—

      “ affected person ” has the meaning given by section 31;           “
interested person ” has the meaning given by section 227(7).

32.7

See also, in relation to duties set out in this section, section 33 (duties
about freedom of expression and privacy).

##### Cross-cutting duties

###### Duties about freedom of expression and privacy

33

33.1

This section sets out the duties about freedom of expression and privacy which
apply in relation to all regulated search services.

33.2

When deciding on, and implementing, safety measures and policies, a duty to
have particular regard to the importance of protecting the rights of users and
interested persons to freedom of expression within the law.

33.3

When deciding on, and implementing, safety measures and policies, a duty to
have particular regard to the importance of protecting users from a breach of
any statutory provision or rule of law concerning privacy that is relevant to
the use or operation of a search service (including, but not limited to, any
such provision or rule concerning the processing of personal data).

33.4

In this section—

      “ interested person ” has the meaning given by section 227 (7) ;
“ safety measures and policies ” means measures and policies designed to
secure compliance with any of the duties set out in—         section 27
(illegal content),           section 29 (children’s online safety),
section 31 (content reporting), or           section 32 (complaints
procedures).

###### Record-keeping and review duties

34

34.1

This section sets out the record-keeping and review duties which apply in
relation to regulated search services (as indicated by the headings).

######### All services

34.2

A duty to make and keep a written record, in an easily understandable form, of
all aspects of every risk assessment under section 26 or 28, including details
about how the assessment was carried out and its findings.

34.3

A duty to make and keep a written record of any measures taken or in use to
comply with a relevant duty which—

34.3.a

are described in a code of practice and recommended for the purpose of
compliance with the duty in question, and

34.3.b

apply in relation to the provider and the service in question.

In this section such measures are referred to as “ applicable measures in a
code of practice ”.

34.4

If alternative measures have been taken or are in use to comply with a
relevant duty, a duty to make and keep a written record containing the
following information—

34.4.a

the applicable measures in a code of practice that have not been taken or are
not in use,

34.4.b

the alternative measures that have been taken or are in use,

34.4.c

how those alternative measures amount to compliance with the duty in question,
and

34.4.d

how the provider has complied with section 49(5) (freedom of expression and
privacy).

34.5

If alternative measures have been taken or are in use to comply with a duty
set out in section 27 (2)  or  (3)  or 29 (2)  or  (3) , the record required
under subsection  (4)  of this section must also indicate whether such
measures have been taken or are in use in every area listed in subsection  (4)
of those sections in relation to which there are applicable measures in a code
of practice.

34.6

A duty to review compliance with the relevant duties in relation to a service—

34.6.a

regularly, and

34.6.b

as soon as reasonably practicable after making any significant change to any
aspect of the design or operation of the service.

34.7

OFCOM may provide that particular descriptions of providers of search services
are exempt from any or all of the duties set out in this section, and may
revoke such an exemption.

34.8

OFCOM must publish details of any exemption or revocation under subsection
(7) , including reasons for the revocation of an exemption.

######### Additional duty for Category 2A services

34.9

As soon as reasonably practicable after making a record of a risk assessment
as required by subsection  (2) , or revising such a record, a duty to supply
OFCOM with a copy of the record (in full).

######### Interpretation

34.10

In this section—

      “ alternative measures ” means measures other than measures which are
(in relation to the provider and the service in question) applicable measures
in a code of practice;           “ code of practice ” means a code of practice
published under section 46;           “ relevant duties ” means the duties set
out in—         section 27 (illegal content),           section 29 (children’s
online safety),           section 31 (content reporting), and
section 32 (complaints procedures),

and for the purposes of subsection (6), also includes the duties set out in
section 75 (deceased child users).

#### Children's access assessments

##### Children’s access assessments

35

35.1

In this Part, a “ children’s access assessment ” means an assessment of a Part
3 service—

35.1.a

to determine whether it is possible for children to access the service or a
part of the service, and

35.1.b

if it is possible for children to access the service or a part of the service,
to determine whether the child user condition is met in relation to the
service or a part of the service.

35.2

A provider is only entitled to conclude that it is not possible for children
to access a service, or a part of it, if age verification or age estimation is
used on the service with the result that children are not normally able to
access the service or that part of it.

35.3

The “child user condition” is met in relation to a service, or a part of a
service, if—

35.3.a

there is a significant number of children who are users of the service or of
that part of it, or

35.3.b

the service, or that part of it, is of a kind likely to attract a significant
number of users who are children.

35.4

For the purposes of subsection  (3) —

35.4.a

the reference to a “significant” number includes a reference to a number which
is significant in proportion to the total number of United Kingdom users of a
service or (as the case may be) a part of a service;

35.4.b

whether the test in paragraph (a) of that subsection is met is to be based on
evidence about who actually uses a service, rather than who the intended users
of the service are.

35.5

In this Chapter—

35.5.a

references to children are to children in the United Kingdom;

35.5.b

references to a part of a service do not include any part of a service that is
not, or is not included in, a user-to-user part of a service or a search
engine.

##### Duties about children’s access assessments

36

36.1

A provider of a Part 3 service must carry out the first children’s access
assessment at a time set out in, or as provided by, Schedule 3.

36.2

Subsections  (3)  and  (4)  apply to a provider of a Part 3 service during any
period when the service is not treated as likely to be accessed by children
(see section 37).

36.3

The provider must carry out children’s access assessments of the service not
more than one year apart.

36.4

The provider must carry out a children’s access assessment of the service—

36.4.a

before making any significant change to any aspect of the service’s design or
operation to which such an assessment is relevant,

36.4.b

in response to evidence about reduced effectiveness of age verification or age
estimation that is used on the service as mentioned in section 35(2), or

36.4.c

in response to evidence about a significant increase in the number of children
using the service.

36.5

If a person is the provider of more than one Part 3 service, children’s access
assessments must be carried out for each service separately.

36.6

Children’s access assessments must be suitable and sufficient for the purposes
of this Part.

36.7

A provider must make and keep a written record, in an easily understandable
form, of every children’s access assessment.

##### Meaning of “likely to be accessed by children”

37

37.1

For the purposes of this Part, a Part 3 service is to be treated as “likely to
be accessed by children” in the following three cases (with the result that
the duties set out in sections 11 and 12, or (as the case may be) sections 28
and 29, apply in relation to the service).

37.2

The first case is where a children’s access assessment carried out by the
provider of the service concludes that—

37.2.a

it is possible for children to access the service or a part of it, and

37.2.b

the child user condition is met in relation to—

37.2.b.i

the service, or

37.2.b.ii

a part of the service that it is possible for children to access.

This subsection is to be interpreted consistently with section 35.

37.3

In that case, the service is to be treated as likely to be accessed by
children from the date on which the children’s access assessment is completed.

37.4

The second case is where the provider of the service fails to carry out the
first children’s access assessment as required by section 36 (1) .

37.5

In that case—

37.5.a

the service is to be treated as likely to be accessed by children from the
date by which the first children’s access assessment was required to have been
completed (see Part 1 of Schedule 3), and

37.5.b

the service is to continue to be treated as likely to be accessed by children
by reason of subsection  (4)  until such time as the provider completes the
first children’s access assessment of the service.

37.6

The third case is where, following an investigation into a failure to comply
with a duty set out in section 36, OFCOM determine that a service should be
treated as likely to be accessed by children: see section 135 (4)  and  (5) .

37.7

In that case, the service is to be treated as likely to be accessed by
children from the date of, or specified in, the confirmation decision given to
the provider of the service (as the case may be: see section 135 (5) ).

#### Duties about fraudulent advertising

##### Duties about fraudulent advertising: Category 1 services

38

38.1

A provider of a Category 1 service must operate the service using
proportionate systems and processes designed to—

38.1.a

prevent individuals from encountering content consisting of fraudulent
advertisements by means of the service;

38.1.b

minimise the length of time for which any such content is present;

38.1.c

where the provider is alerted by a person to the presence of such content, or
becomes aware of it in any other way, swiftly take down such content.

38.2

A provider of a Category 1 service must include clear and accessible
provisions in the terms of service giving information about any proactive
technology used by the service for the purpose of compliance with the duty set
out in subsection  (1)  (including the kind of technology, when it is used,
and how it works).

38.3

In relation to a Category 1 service, an advertisement is a “fraudulent
advertisement” if—

38.3.a

it is a paid-for advertisement (see section 236),

38.3.b

it amounts to an offence specified in section 40 (construed in accordance with
section 59: see subsections  (3) ,  (11)  and  (12)  of that section), and

38.3.c

it is not regulated user-generated content (see section 55) in relation to the
service.

38.4

If a person is the provider of more than one Category 1 service, the duties
set out in this section apply in relation to each such service.

38.5

In determining what is proportionate for the purposes of this section, the
following factors, in particular, are relevant—

38.5.a

the nature, and severity, of potential harm to individuals presented by
different kinds of fraudulent advertisement, and

38.5.b

the degree of control a provider has in relation to the placement of
advertisements on the service.

38.6

In the case of a Category 1 service which is a combined service, the duties
set out in this section do not extend to—

38.6.a

fraudulent advertisements that may be encountered in search results of the
service or, following a search request, as a result of subsequent interactions
with internet services, or

38.6.b

anything relating to the design, operation or use of the search engine.

But if the service is also a Category 2A service, the duties set out in
section 39 apply as well as the duties set out in this section.

38.7

The duties set out in this section extend only to the design, operation and
use of a Category 1 service in the United Kingdom.

38.8

For the meaning of “Category 1 service”, see section 95 (register of
categories of services).

##### Duties about fraudulent advertising: Category 2A services

39

39.1

A provider of a Category 2A service must operate the service using
proportionate systems and processes designed to—

39.1.a

prevent individuals from encountering content consisting of fraudulent
advertisements in or via search results of the service;

39.1.b

if any such content may be encountered in or via search results of the
service, minimise the length of time that that is the case;

39.1.c

where the provider is alerted by a person to the fact that such content may be
so encountered, or becomes aware of that fact in any other way, swiftly ensure
that individuals are no longer able to encounter such content in or via search
results of the service.

39.2

A provider of a Category 2A service must include clear and accessible
provisions in a publicly available statement giving information about any
proactive technology used by the service for the purpose of compliance with
the duty set out in subsection  (1)  (including the kind of technology, when
it is used, and how it works).

39.3

In relation to a Category 2A service, an advertisement is a “fraudulent
advertisement” if—

39.3.a

it is a paid-for advertisement (see section 236), and

39.3.b

it amounts to an offence specified in section 40 (construed in accordance with
section 59: see subsections  (3) , (11) and (12) of that section).

39.4

The references to encountering fraudulent advertisements “in or via search
results” of a search service—

39.4.a

are references to encountering fraudulent advertisements—

39.4.a.i

in search results of the service, or

39.4.a.ii

as a result of interacting with a paid-for advertisement in search results of
the service (for example, by clicking on it);

39.4.b

do not include references to encountering fraudulent advertisements as a
result of any subsequent interactions with an internet service other than the
search service.

39.5

If a person is the provider of more than one Category 2A service, the duties
set out in this section apply in relation to each such service.

39.6

In determining what is proportionate for the purposes of this section, the
following factors, in particular, are relevant—

39.6.a

the nature, and severity, of potential harm to individuals presented by
different kinds of fraudulent advertisement, and

39.6.b

the degree of control a provider has in relation to the placement of
advertisements on the service.

39.7

The duties set out in this section extend only to the design, operation and
use of a Category 2A service in the United Kingdom.

39.8

For the meaning of “Category 2A service”, see section 95 (register of
categories of services).

##### Fraud etc offences

40

40.1

This section specifies offences for the purposes of this Chapter (see sections
38 (3)(b)  and 39 (3)(b) ).

40.2

An offence under any of the following provisions of the Financial Services and
Markets Act 2000—

40.2.a

section 23 (contravention of prohibition on carrying on regulated activity
unless authorised or exempt);

40.2.b

section 24 (false claims to be authorised or exempt);

40.2.c

section 25 (contravention of restrictions on financial promotion).

40.3

An offence under any of the following provisions of the Fraud Act 2006—

40.3.a

section 2 (fraud by false representation);

40.3.b

section 4 (fraud by abuse of position);

40.3.c

section 7 (making or supplying articles for use in frauds);

40.3.d

section 9 (participating in fraudulent business carried on by sole trader
etc).

40.4

An offence under any of the following provisions of the Financial Services Act
2012—

40.4.a

section 89 (misleading statements);

40.4.b

section 90 (misleading impressions).

40.5

An offence of attempting or conspiring to commit an offence specified in
subsection  (2) ,  (3)  or  (4) .

40.6

An offence under Part 2 of the Serious Crime Act 2007 (encouraging or
assisting) in relation to an offence specified in subsection  (2) ,  (3)  or
(4) , or (in Scotland) inciting a person to commit such an offence.

40.7

An offence of aiding, abetting, counselling or procuring the commission of an
offence specified in subsection  (2) ,  (3)  or  (4) , or (in Scotland) being
involved art and part in the commission of such an offence.

#### Codes of practice and guidance

##### Codes of practice

###### Codes of practice about duties

41

41.1

OFCOM must prepare and issue a code of practice for providers of Part 3
services describing measures recommended for the purpose of compliance with
duties set out in section 10 or 27 (illegal content) so far as relating to
terrorism content or offences within Schedule 5 (terrorism offences).

41.2

OFCOM must prepare and issue a code of practice for providers of Part 3
services describing measures recommended for the purpose of compliance with
duties set out in section 10 or 27 (illegal content) so far as relating to
CSEA content or offences within Schedule 6 (child sexual exploitation and
abuse offences).

41.3

OFCOM must prepare and issue one or more codes of practice for providers of
Part 3 services describing measures recommended for the purpose of compliance
with the relevant duties (except to the extent that measures for the purpose
of compliance with such duties are described in a code of practice prepared
under subsection  (1)  or  (2) ).

41.4

OFCOM must prepare and issue a code of practice for providers of Category 1
services and providers of Category 2A services describing measures recommended
for the purpose of compliance with the duties set out in Chapter 5 (fraudulent
advertising).

41.5

Where a code of practice under this section is in force, OFCOM may—

41.5.a

prepare a draft of amendments of the code of practice;

41.5.b

prepare a draft of a code of practice under subsection  (1) ,  (2) ,  (3)  or
(4)  as a replacement for a code of practice previously issued under the
subsection in question;

41.5.c

withdraw the code of practice.

41.6

In the course of preparing a draft of a code of practice or amendments of a
code of practice under this section, OFCOM must consult—

41.6.a

the Secretary of State,

41.6.b

persons who appear to OFCOM to represent providers of Part 3 services,

41.6.c

persons who appear to OFCOM to represent the interests of United Kingdom users
of Part 3 services,

41.6.d

persons who appear to OFCOM to represent the interests of children (generally
or with particular reference to online safety matters),

41.6.e

persons who appear to OFCOM to represent the interests of persons who have
suffered harm as a result of matters to which the code of practice is
relevant,

41.6.f

persons whom OFCOM consider to have relevant expertise in equality issues and
human rights, in particular—

41.6.f.i

the right to freedom of expression set out in Article 10 of the Convention,
and

41.6.f.ii

the right to respect for a person’s private and family life, home and
correspondence set out in Article 8 of the Convention,

41.6.g

the Information Commissioner,

41.6.h

the Children’s Commissioner,

41.6.i

the Commissioner for Victims and Witnesses,

41.6.j

the Domestic Abuse Commissioner,

41.6.k

persons whom OFCOM consider to have expertise in public health, science or
medicine that is relevant to online safety matters,

41.6.l

persons whom OFCOM consider to have expertise in innovation, or emerging
technology, that is relevant to online safety matters, and

41.6.m

such other persons as OFCOM consider appropriate.

41.7

In the course of preparing a draft of a code of practice or amendments to
which this subsection applies, OFCOM must also consult persons whom OFCOM
consider to have expertise in the enforcement of the criminal law and the
protection of national security that is relevant to online safety matters.

41.8

Subsection  (7)  applies to—

41.8.a

a code of practice under subsection  (1)  and amendments of such a code,

41.8.b

a code of practice under subsection  (2)  and amendments of such a code,

41.8.c

a code of practice under subsection  (3)  that describes measures recommended
for the purpose of compliance with duties set out in section 10 or 27 (illegal
content),

41.8.d

amendments of a code of practice under subsection  (3) , if and to the extent
that those amendments relate to measures recommended for the purpose of
compliance with duties set out in section 10 or 27, and

41.8.e

a code of practice under subsection  (4)  and amendments of such a code.

41.9

Subsections  (6)  and  (7)  are subject to section 48 (minor amendments of
code of practice).

41.10

In this section “ the relevant duties ” means the duties set out in—

41.10.a

sections 10 and 27 (illegal content),

41.10.b

sections 12 and 29 (children’s online safety),

41.10.c

section 15 (user empowerment),

41.10.d

section 17 (content of democratic importance),

41.10.e

section 19 (journalistic content),

41.10.f

sections 20 and 31 (content reporting), and

41.10.g

sections 21 and 32 (complaints procedures).

###### Codes of practice: principles, objectives, content

42

Schedule 4 contains—

42.a

provision about the principles OFCOM must consider when preparing codes of
practice under section 41,

42.b

the online safety objectives (and a power for the Secretary of State by
regulations to revise those objectives),

42.c

provision about the measures that may be described in codes of practice
(including, in particular, constraints on the recommendation of the use of
proactive technology), and

42.d

other provision related to codes of practice.

###### Procedure for issuing codes of practice

43

43.1

Where OFCOM have prepared a draft of a code of practice under section 41, they
must submit the draft to the Secretary of State.

43.2

Unless the Secretary of State intends to give a direction to OFCOM under
section 44 (1) ,  (2)  or  (3)  in relation to the draft, the Secretary of
State must, as soon as reasonably practicable, lay the draft before
Parliament.

43.3

If, within the 40-day period, either House of Parliament resolves not to
approve the draft—

43.3.a

OFCOM must not issue the code of practice in the form of that draft, and

43.3.b

OFCOM must prepare another draft of the code of practice under section 41.

43.4

If no such resolution is made within that period—

43.4.a

OFCOM must issue the code of practice in the form of the draft laid before
Parliament, and

43.4.b

the code of practice comes into force at the end of the period of 21 days
beginning with the day on which it is issued.

43.5

“The 40-day period” is the period of 40 days beginning with the day on which
the draft is laid before Parliament (or, if it is not laid before each House
of Parliament on the same day, the later of the days on which it is laid).

43.6

In calculating the 40-day period, no account is to be taken of any period
during which Parliament is dissolved or prorogued or during which both Houses
are adjourned for more than 4 days.

43.7

Subsections  (1)  to  (6)  apply in relation to a draft of amendments of a
code of practice prepared under section 41 as they apply in relation to a
draft of a code of practice prepared under that section.

43.8

This section is subject to section 48 (minor amendments of codes of practice).

43.9

Subsection  (11)  applies to—

43.9.a

a draft of the first code of practice prepared under section 41(1) (terrorism
code of practice);

43.9.b

a draft of the first code of practice prepared under section 41(2) (CSEA code
of practice);

43.9.c

a draft of the first code of practice prepared under section 41(3) relating to
a duty set out in section 10 or 27 (illegal content);

43.9.d

a draft of the first code of practice prepared under section 41(3) relating to
a duty set out in section 12 or 29 (children’s online safety);

43.9.e

a draft of the first code of practice prepared under section 41(3) relating to
a duty set out in section 20 or 31 (content reporting);

43.9.f

a draft of the first code of practice prepared under section 41(3) relating
to—

43.9.f.i

a duty set out in section 21 (complaints procedures) that concerns complaints
of a kind mentioned in subsection (4) or (5) of that section, or

43.9.f.ii

a duty set out in section 32 (complaints procedures).

43.10

For the purposes of paragraphs  (c)  to (f) of subsection  (9)  a draft of a
code of practice is a draft of the first code of practice relating to a duty
if—

43.10.a

it describes measures recommended for the purpose of compliance with the duty,
and

43.10.b

it is a draft of the first code of practice prepared under section 41(3) that
describes measures for that purpose.

43.11

OFCOM must submit a draft to which this subsection applies to the Secretary of
State under subsection (1) within the period of 18 months beginning with the
day on which this Act is passed.

43.12

If OFCOM consider that it is necessary to extend the period mentioned in
subsection  (11)  in relation to a draft mentioned in any of paragraphs  (a)
to (f) of subsection  (9) , OFCOM may extend the period in relation to that
draft by up to 12 months by making and publishing a statement.

But this is subject to subsection (15).

43.13

A statement under subsection  (12)  must set out—

43.13.a

the reasons why OFCOM consider that it is necessary to extend the period
mentioned in subsection  (11)  in relation to the draft concerned, and

43.13.b

the period of extension.

43.14

A statement under subsection (12) may be published at the same time as (or
incorporate) a statement under section 194 (3)  (extension of time to prepare
certain guidance).

43.15

But a statement under subsection (12) may not be made in relation to a draft
mentioned in a particular paragraph of subsection (9) if—

43.15.a

a statement has previously been made under subsection (12) (whether in
relation to a draft mentioned in the same or a different paragraph of
subsection (9)), or

43.15.b

a statement has previously been made under section 194 (3) .

###### Secretary of State’s powers of direction

44

44.1

The Secretary of State may direct OFCOM to modify a draft of a code of
practice submitted under section 43(1) if the Secretary of State believes that
modifications are required for the purpose of securing compliance with an
international obligation of the United Kingdom.

44.2

The Secretary of State may direct OFCOM to modify a draft of a code of
practice, other than a terrorism or CSEA code of practice, submitted under
section 43(1) if the Secretary of State believes that modifications are
required for exceptional reasons relating to—

44.2.a

national security,

44.2.b

public safety,

44.2.c

public health, or

44.2.d

relations with the government of a country outside the United Kingdom.

44.3

The Secretary of State may direct OFCOM to modify a draft of a terrorism or
CSEA code of practice submitted under section 43 (1)  if the Secretary of
State believes that modifications are required—

44.3.a

for reasons of national security or public safety, or

44.3.b

for exceptional reasons relating to public health or relations with the
government of a country outside the United Kingdom.

44.4

But if a draft of a terrorism or CSEA code of practice is submitted under
section 43 (1)  following a review under section 47 (2) , the Secretary of
State may only direct OFCOM to modify the draft if the Secretary of State
believes that modifications are required for reasons of national security or
public safety.

44.5

If, following a review of a terrorism or CSEA code of practice under section
47 (2) , OFCOM submit a statement to the Secretary of State under section 47
(3)(b)  (“OFCOM’s review statement”), the Secretary of State may direct OFCOM
to modify the code of practice if the Secretary of State believes that
modifications are required for reasons of national security or public safety.

44.6

A direction given under subsection  (5) —

44.6.a

must be given within the period of 45 days beginning with the day on which
OFCOM’s review statement is submitted to the Secretary of State, and

44.6.b

must make particular reference to OFCOM’s review statement.

44.7

A direction given under this section—

44.7.a

may not require OFCOM to include in a code of practice provision about a
particular measure recommended to be taken or used by providers of Part 3
services,

44.7.b

must set out the Secretary of State’s reasons for requiring modifications,
except in a case where the Secretary of State considers that doing so would be
against the interests of national security, public safety or relations with
the government of a country outside the United Kingdom, and

44.7.c

must, as soon as reasonably practicable, be published and laid before
Parliament.

44.8

If the Secretary of State considers that publishing and laying before
Parliament a direction given under this section would be against the interests
of national security, public safety or relations with the government of a
country outside the United Kingdom—

44.8.a

subsection (7)(c) does not apply in relation to the direction, and

44.8.b

the Secretary of State must, as soon as reasonably practicable, publish and
lay before Parliament a document stating—

44.8.b.i

that a direction has been given,

44.8.b.ii

the kind of code of practice to which it relates, and

44.8.b.iii

the reasons for not publishing it.

44.9

If the Secretary of State gives a direction under this section, OFCOM must, as
soon as reasonably practicable—

44.9.a

comply with the direction,

44.9.b

submit to the Secretary of State a draft of the code of practice modified in
accordance with the direction,

44.9.c

submit to the Secretary of State a document containing—

44.9.c.i

(except in a case mentioned in subsection  (7)(b) ) details of the direction,
and

44.9.c.ii

details about how the draft has been revised in response to the direction,

44.9.d

publish the document, and

44.9.e

inform the Secretary of State about modifications that OFCOM have made to the
draft that are not in response to the direction (if there are any).

44.10

The Secretary of State may give OFCOM one or more further directions requiring
OFCOM to modify the draft of the code of practice.

44.11

Such further directions may only be given for the reasons set out in
subsection  (1) ,  (2) ,  (3) ,  (4)  or  (5)  (as the case may be), and
subsections  (7)  to  (9)  apply again in relation to such further directions.

44.12

When the Secretary of State is satisfied that no further modifications to the
draft are required, the Secretary of State must, as soon as reasonably
practicable, lay before Parliament—

44.12.a

the modified draft,

44.12.b

any document submitted by OFCOM as mentioned in subsection  (9)(c) , and

44.12.c

in the case of a direction under subsection  (5) , OFCOM’s review statement.

44.13

Before laying OFCOM’s review statement before Parliament, the Secretary of
State may, with OFCOM’s agreement, remove or obscure information in the
statement (whether by redaction or otherwise) in order to prevent the
disclosure of matters that the Secretary of State considers would be against
the interests of national security, public safety or relations with the
government of a country outside the United Kingdom.

44.14

This section applies in relation to a draft of amendments of a code of
practice submitted under section 43 (1)  as it applies in relation to a draft
of a code of practice submitted under that provision.

44.15

In this section “ terrorism or CSEA code of practice ” means a code of
practice under section 41 (1)  or  (2) .

###### Procedure for issuing codes of practice following direction under section 44

45

45.1

This section sets out the procedure that applies where a draft of a code of
practice is laid before Parliament under section 44 (12) .

45.2

If the draft contains modifications made following a direction given under
section 44 (1) ,  (2)  or  (3)(b) , the affirmative procedure applies.

45.3

If the draft contains modifications made following a direction given under
section 44 (3)(a) ,  (4)  or  (5) , the negative procedure applies.

45.4

The “affirmative procedure” is as follows—

45.4.a

a code of practice in the form of the draft laid before Parliament must not be
issued by OFCOM unless the draft has been approved by a resolution of each
House of Parliament;

45.4.b

if the draft is so approved, the code of practice comes into force at the end
of the period of 21 days beginning with the day on which it is issued;

45.4.c

if the draft is not so approved, OFCOM must prepare another draft of the code
of practice under section 41.

45.5

The “negative procedure” is as follows—

45.5.a

if, within the 40-day period, either House of Parliament resolves not to
approve the draft—

45.5.a.i

OFCOM must not issue the code of practice in the form of that draft, and

45.5.a.ii

OFCOM must prepare another draft of the code of practice under section 41;

45.5.b

if no such resolution is made within that period—

45.5.b.i

OFCOM must issue the code of practice in the form of the draft laid before
Parliament, and

45.5.b.ii

the code of practice comes into force at the end of the period of 21 days
beginning with the day on which it is issued.

45.6

“ The 40-day period ” has the same meaning as in section 43 (see subsections
(5)  and  (6)  of that section).

45.7

This section applies in relation to a draft of amendments of a code of
practice laid before Parliament under section 44 (12)  as it applies in
relation to a draft of a code of practice laid under that provision.

###### Publication of codes of practice

46

46.1

OFCOM must publish each code of practice issued under section 43 or 45 within
the period of three days beginning with the day on which it is issued.

46.2

Where amendments of a code of practice are issued under either of those
sections, OFCOM must publish the amended code of practice within the period of
three days beginning with the day on which the amendments are issued.

46.3

Where a code of practice is withdrawn, OFCOM must publish a notice to that
effect.

###### Review of codes of practice

47

47.1

OFCOM must keep under review each code of practice published under section 46.

47.2

The Secretary of State may require OFCOM to review a terrorism or CSEA code of
practice published under section 46 if the Secretary of State considers a
review to be necessary for reasons of national security or public safety (and
the Secretary of State must notify OFCOM whether the reasons fall into the
category of national security or public safety).

47.3

OFCOM must carry out a review of the code of practice under subsection  (2)
as soon as reasonably practicable, and when it is completed—

47.3.a

if OFCOM consider that changes are required, they must prepare a draft of
amendments to the code of practice or a draft of a replacement code of
practice under section 41, or

47.3.b

if OFCOM consider that no changes are required, they must submit to the
Secretary of State a statement which explains the reasons for that conclusion.

47.4

Subsection  (5)  applies if—

47.4.a

OFCOM submit a statement under subsection  (3)(b)  to the Secretary of State,

47.4.b

the period of 45 days beginning with the day on which the statement was
submitted has elapsed, and

47.4.c

the Secretary of State has not given a direction under section 44 (5) .

47.5

OFCOM must publish the statement as soon as reasonably practicable after the
end of the period mentioned in subsection  (4)(b) , making it clear which code
of practice the statement relates to.

47.6

In advance of publication, the Secretary of State may make representations to
OFCOM about the desirability of removing or obscuring information in the
statement (whether by redaction or otherwise) in order to prevent the
disclosure of matters that the Secretary of State considers would be against
the interests of national security, public safety or relations with the
government of a country outside the United Kingdom (and see also section 116
(3) ).

47.7

In this section “ terrorism or CSEA code of practice ” means a code of
practice under section 41 (1)  or  (2) .

###### Minor amendments of codes of practice

48

48.1

This section applies if—

48.1.a

OFCOM propose to amend a code of practice under section 41, and

48.1.b

OFCOM consider that the minor nature of the proposal means that—

48.1.b.i

consultation is unnecessary, and

48.1.b.ii

the proposed amendments should not be required to be laid before Parliament.

48.2

OFCOM must notify the Secretary of State of the proposed amendments.

48.3

If the Secretary of State agrees with OFCOM that it is appropriate—

48.3.a

the consultation requirements set out in section 41 (6)  and  (7)  do not
apply in relation to the proposed amendments, and

48.3.b

section 43 does not apply to the amendments, once prepared.

48.4

If the Secretary of State agrees with OFCOM as mentioned in subsection  (3) ,
OFCOM may prepare and issue the amendments of the code of practice.

48.5

Amendments of a code of practice issued under this section come into force at
the end of the period of 21 days beginning with the day on which the
amendments are issued.

48.6

Section 46 (2)  applies in relation to amendments of a code of practice issued
under this section as it applies in relation to amendments of a code of
practice issued under section 43 or 45.

###### Relationship between duties and codes of practice

49

######### Duties set out in Chapters 2 and 3

49.1

A provider of a Part 3 service is to be treated as complying with a relevant
duty if the provider takes or uses the measures described in a code of
practice which are recommended for the purpose of compliance with the duty in
question.

49.2

A provider of a user-to-user service—

49.2.a

is to be treated as complying with the duty set out in section 22 (2)
(freedom of expression) if the provider takes or uses such of the relevant
recommended measures as incorporate safeguards to protect users’ right to
freedom of expression within the law;

49.2.b

is to be treated as complying with the duty set out in section 22 (3)
(privacy) if the provider takes or uses such of the relevant recommended
measures as incorporate safeguards to protect the privacy of users.

49.3

A provider of a search service—

49.3.a

is to be treated as complying with the duty set out in section 33 (2)
(freedom of expression) if the provider takes or uses such of the relevant
recommended measures as incorporate safeguards to protect the rights of users
and interested persons to freedom of expression within the law;

49.3.b

is to be treated as complying with the duty set out in section 33 (3)
(privacy) if the provider takes or uses such of the relevant recommended
measures as incorporate safeguards to protect the privacy of users.

######### Duties set out in Chapter 5

49.4

A provider of a Category 1 service or a Category 2A service (or a provider of
a service which is both a Category 1 service and a Category 2A service) is to
be treated as complying with a duty set out in Chapter 5 if the provider takes
or uses the measures described in a fraudulent advertising code of practice
which are recommended for the purpose of compliance with the duty in question.

######### Alternative measures

49.5

A provider of a Part 3 service who seeks to comply with a relevant duty by
acting otherwise than by taking or using a measure described in a code of
practice or a fraudulent advertising code of practice which is recommended for
the purpose of compliance with the duty must have particular regard to the
importance of the following (where relevant)—

49.5.a

protecting the right of users and (in the case of search services) interested
persons to freedom of expression within the law, and

49.5.b

protecting the privacy of users.

49.6

When assessing whether a provider of a Part 3 service is compliant with a
relevant duty where the provider has acted otherwise than by taking or using a
measure described in a code of practice or a fraudulent advertising code of
practice which is recommended for the purpose of compliance with the duty,
OFCOM must consider the extent to which the alternative measures taken or in
use by the provider—

49.6.a

extend across all areas of a service as mentioned in section 10 (4) , 12 (8) ,
27 (4)  or 29 (4)  (if relevant to the duty in question), and

49.6.b

(where appropriate) incorporate safeguards for the protection of the matters
mentioned in subsection  (5)(a)  and  (b) .

######### Interpretation

49.7

In subsections  (1)  to  (4) , references to taking or using measures
recommended for the purpose of compliance with a duty, or to taking or using
relevant recommended measures, are to taking or using such of those measures
as are relevant to the provider and the service in question.

49.8

In this section—

49.8.a

references to protecting the privacy of users are to protecting users from a
breach of any statutory provision or rule of law concerning privacy that is
relevant to the use or operation of a user-to-user service or search service
(including, but not limited to, any such provision or rule concerning the
processing of personal data);

49.8.b

references to a search service include references to a combined service (see
section 7 (6) ).

49.9

In this section—

      “ Chapter 2 safety duty ” means a duty set out in—         section 10
(illegal content), or           section 12 (children’s online safety);
“ Chapter 3 safety duty ” means a duty set out in—         section 27 (illegal
content), or           section 29 (children’s online safety);
“ code of practice ” means a code of practice published under section 46,
except a fraudulent advertising code of practice;           “ fraudulent
advertising code of practice ” means a code of practice prepared under section
41 (4)  and published under section 46;           “ relevant duty ” means—
a Chapter 2 safety duty,           a Chapter 3 safety duty,           a duty
set out in section 15 (user empowerment),           a duty set out in section
17 (content of democratic importance),           a duty set out in section 19
(journalistic content),           a duty set out in section 20 or 31 (content
reporting), or           a duty set out in section 21 or 32 (complaints
procedures);                 “ relevant recommended measures ” means the
measures described in a code of practice which are recommended for the purpose
of compliance with—         in the case of a user-to-user service—         a
Chapter 2 safety duty, or           a duty set out in section 15 (user
empowerment);                 in the case of a search service, a Chapter 3
safety duty.

###### Effects of codes of practice

50

50.1

A failure by a provider of a Part 3 service to act in accordance with a
provision of a code of practice does not of itself make the provider liable to
legal proceedings in a court or tribunal.

50.2

A code of practice is admissible in evidence in legal proceedings.

50.3

In any proceedings in a court or tribunal, the court or tribunal must take
into account a provision of a code of practice in determining a question
arising in the proceedings if—

50.3.a

the question relates to a time when the provision was in force, and

50.3.b

the provision appears to the court or tribunal to be relevant to the question.

50.4

OFCOM must take into account a provision of a code of practice in determining
a question arising in connection with their exercise of any relevant function
if—

50.4.a

the question relates to a time when the provision was in force, and

50.4.b

the provision appears to OFCOM to be relevant to the question.

50.5

In this section—

      “ code of practice ” means a code of practice published under section
46;           “ relevant functions ” means OFCOM’s functions under—
Chapter 4 of Part 7 (information),           Chapter 5 of Part 7 (notices to
deal with terrorism content and CSEA content),           Chapter 6 of Part 7
(enforcement), and           Chapter 2 of Part 8 (super-complaints).

###### Duties and the first codes of practice

51

51.1

A duty mentioned in subsection  (3)  applies to providers of Part 3 services
from the day on which a code of practice prepared under section 41 (3)  that
is the first code of practice relating to that duty comes into force.

51.2

In the case of the duties set out in sections 10 and 27, subsection  (1)  is
subject to subsections  (5)  and  (6) .

51.3

The duties referred to in subsection  (1)  are the duties set out in—

51.3.a

sections 10 and 27 (illegal content),

51.3.b

sections 12 and 29 (children’s online safety),

51.3.c

section 15 (user empowerment),

51.3.d

section 17 (content of democratic importance),

51.3.e

section 19 (journalistic content),

51.3.f

sections 20 and 31 (content reporting), and

51.3.g

sections 21 and 32 (complaints procedures).

51.4

For the purposes of subsection  (1)  a code of practice is the first code of
practice relating to a duty if—

51.4.a

it describes measures recommended for the purpose of compliance with that
duty, and

51.4.b

it is the first code of practice prepared under section 41 (3)  that describes
measures for that purpose.

51.5

The duties set out in sections 10 and 27, so far as relating to terrorism
content or offences within Schedule 5 (terrorism offences), apply to providers
of Part 3 services from the day on which the first code of practice prepared
under section 41 (1)  comes into force.

51.6

The duties set out in sections 10 and 27, so far as relating to CSEA content
or offences within Schedule 6 (child sexual exploitation and abuse offences),
apply to providers of Part 3 services from the day on which the first code of
practice prepared under section 41 (2)  comes into force.

51.7

The duties set out in Chapter 5 (fraudulent advertising) apply to providers of
a Category 1 service and providers of a Category 2A service (and to providers
of a service which is both a Category 1 service and a Category 2A service)
from the day on which the first code of practice prepared under section 41 (4)
comes into force.

51.8

In relation to the provider of a particular Part 3 service, references in this
section to duties applying to providers of Part 3 services (or to providers of
Category 1 services or Category 2A services) are to such duties as apply in
relation to that service in accordance with sections 7 and 24 or (as the case
may be) Chapter 5.

51.9

This section is subject to Part 2 of Schedule 17 (video-sharing platform
services: transitional provision etc).

##### Guidance

###### OFCOM’s guidance about certain duties in Part 3

52

52.1

OFCOM must produce guidance for providers of Category 1 services to assist
them in complying with their duties set out in section 14 (assessments related
to the adult user empowerment duty set out in section 15(2)).

52.2

OFCOM must produce guidance for providers of Category 1 services to assist
them in complying with their duties set out in section 18 (news publisher
content).

52.3

OFCOM must produce guidance for providers of Part 3 services to assist them in
complying with—

52.3.a

their duties set out in section 23 or 34, except the duty set out in section
23(10) or 34(9) (record-keeping and review), and

52.3.b

their duties set out in section 36 (children’s access assessments).

52.4

Before producing guidance under subsection  (1)  or  (3)  (including revised
or replacement guidance), OFCOM must consult the Information Commissioner.

52.5

OFCOM must publish guidance under this section (and any revised or replacement
guidance).

###### OFCOM’s guidance: content that is harmful to children and user empowerment

53

53.1

OFCOM must produce guidance for providers of Part 3 services which contains
examples of content or kinds of content that OFCOM consider to be, or consider
not to be—

53.1.a

primary priority content that is harmful to children, or

53.1.b

priority content that is harmful to children.

53.2

OFCOM must produce guidance for providers of Category 1 services which
contains examples of content or kinds of content that OFCOM consider to be, or
consider not to be, content to which section 15(2) applies (see section 16).

53.3

Before producing any guidance under this section (including revised or
replacement guidance), OFCOM must consult such persons as they consider
appropriate.

53.4

OFCOM must publish guidance under this section (and any revised or replacement
guidance).

###### OFCOM’s guidance about protecting women and girls

54

54.1

OFCOM must produce guidance for providers of Part 3 services which focuses on
content and activity—

54.1.a

in relation to which such providers have duties set out in this Part or Part
4, and

54.1.b

which disproportionately affects women and girls.

54.2

The guidance may, among other things—

54.2.a

contain advice and examples of best practice for assessing risks of harm to
women and girls from content and activity mentioned in subsection (1), and for
reducing such risks;

54.2.b

refer to provisions contained in a code of practice under section 41 which are
particularly relevant to the protection of women and girls from such content
and activity.

54.3

Before producing the guidance (including revised or replacement guidance),
OFCOM must consult—

54.3.a

the Commissioner for Victims and Witnesses,

54.3.b

the Domestic Abuse Commissioner, and

54.3.c

such other persons as OFCOM consider appropriate.

54.4

OFCOM must publish the guidance (and any revised or replacement guidance).

#### Interpretation of Part 3

##### “Regulated user-generated content”, “user-generated content”, “news publisher content”

55

55.1

This section applies for the purposes of this Part.

55.2

“ Regulated user-generated content ”, in relation to a regulated user-to-user
service, means user-generated content, except—

55.2.a

emails,

55.2.b

SMS messages,

55.2.c

MMS messages,

55.2.d

one-to-one live aural communications (see subsection  (5) ),

55.2.e

comments and reviews on provider content (see subsection  (6) ),

55.2.f

identifying content that accompanies content within any of paragraphs (a) to
(e), and

55.2.g

news publisher content (see subsection  (8) ).

55.3

“ User-generated content ”, in relation to a user-to-user service, means
content—

55.3.a

that is—

55.3.a.i

generated directly on the service by a user of the service, or

55.3.a.ii

uploaded to or shared on the service by a user of the service, and

55.3.b

that may be encountered by another user, or other users, of the service by
means of the service.

55.4

For the purposes of subsection  (3) —

55.4.a

the reference to content generated, uploaded or shared by a user includes
content generated, uploaded or shared by means of software or an automated
tool applied by the user;

55.4.b

a bot or other automated tool is to be regarded as a user of a service if—

55.4.b.i

the functions of the bot or tool include interacting with user-generated
content, and

55.4.b.ii

the bot or tool is not controlled by or on behalf of the provider of the
service.

55.5

“ One-to-one live aural communications ”, in relation to a user-to-user
service, means content—

55.5.a

consisting of speech or other sounds conveyed in real time between two users
of the service by means of the service,

55.5.b

that is not a recording, and

55.5.c

that is not accompanied by user-generated content of any other kind, except
identifying content.

55.6

“ Comments and reviews on provider content ”, in relation to a user-to-user
service, means content present on the service consisting of comments or
reviews relating to provider content (together with any further comments on
such comments or reviews).

55.7

In subsection (6) “ provider content ” means content published on a service by
the provider of the service or by a person acting on behalf of the provider,
including where the publication of the content is effected or controlled by
means of—

55.7.a

software or an automated tool or algorithm applied by the provider or by a
person acting on behalf of the provider, or

55.7.b

an automated tool or algorithm made available on the service by the provider
or by a person acting on behalf of the provider.

For the purposes of subsection  (6) , content that is user-generated content
in relation to a service is not to be regarded as provider content in relation
to that service.

55.8

“ News publisher content ”, in relation to a regulated user-to-user service,
means any content present on the service that is within subsection  (9)  or
(10) .

55.9

Content is within this subsection if it was generated directly on the service
by a user of the service that is a recognised news publisher.

55.10

Content is within this subsection if—

55.10.a

the content was uploaded to or shared on the service by a user of the service,
and

55.10.b

the content either—

55.10.b.i

reproduces in full an article or written item that was originally published by
a recognised news publisher (and is not a screenshot or photograph of that
article or item or of part of it),

55.10.b.ii

is video or audio content that was originally published or broadcast by a
recognised news publisher, and is not a clipped or edited form of such content
(unless it is the recognised news publisher who has clipped or edited it), or

55.10.b.iii

is a link to an article or item within sub-paragraph (i) or to content within
sub-paragraph (ii).

55.11

For the meaning of “recognised news publisher”, see section 56.

55.12

In this section—

      “ MMS message ” means a Multimedia Messaging Service message (that may
include images, sounds and short videos) that may be sent between telephone
numbers allocated in accordance with a national or international numbering
plan;           “ SMS message ” means a Short Message Service text message
composed principally of letters or numbers that may be sent between telephone
numbers allocated in accordance with a national or international numbering
plan.

##### “Recognised news publisher”

56

56.1

In this Part, “ recognised news publisher ” means any of the following
entities—

56.1.a

the British Broadcasting Corporation,

56.1.b

Sianel Pedwar Cymru,

56.1.c

the holder of a licence under the Broadcasting Act 1990 or 1996 who publishes
news-related material in connection with the broadcasting activities
authorised under the licence, and

56.1.d

any other entity which—

56.1.d.i

meets all of the conditions in subsection  (2) ,

56.1.d.ii

is not an excluded entity (see subsection  (3) ), and

56.1.d.iii

is not a sanctioned entity (see subsection  (4) ).

56.2

The conditions referred to in subsection  (1)(d)(i)  are that the entity—

56.2.a

has as its principal purpose the publication of news-related material, and
such material—

56.2.a.i

is created by different persons, and

56.2.a.ii

is subject to editorial control,

56.2.b

publishes such material in the course of a business (whether or not carried on
with a view to profit),

56.2.c

is subject to a standards code,

56.2.d

has policies and procedures for handling and resolving complaints,

56.2.e

has a registered office or other business address in the United Kingdom,

56.2.f

is the person with legal responsibility for material published by it in the
United Kingdom, and

56.2.g

publishes—

56.2.g.i

the entity’s name, the address mentioned in paragraph (e) and the entity’s
registered number (if any), and

56.2.g.ii

the name and address of any person who controls the entity (including, where
such a person is an entity, the address of that person’s registered or
principal office and that person’s registered number (if any)).

56.3

An “excluded entity” is an entity—

56.3.a

which is a proscribed organisation under the Terrorism Act 2000 (see section 3
of that Act), or

56.3.b

the purpose of which is to support a proscribed organisation under that Act.

56.4

A “sanctioned entity” is an entity which—

56.4.a

is designated by name under a power contained in regulations under section 1
of the Sanctions and Anti-Money Laundering Act 2018 that authorises the
Secretary of State or the Treasury to designate persons for the purposes of
the regulations or of any provisions of the regulations, or

56.4.b

is a designated person under any provision included in such regulations by
virtue of section 13 of that Act (persons named by or under UN Security
Council Resolutions).

56.5

For the purposes of subsection  (2) —

56.5.a

news-related material is “subject to editorial control” if there is a person
(whether or not the publisher of the material) who has editorial or equivalent
responsibility for the material, including responsibility for how it is
presented and the decision to publish it;

56.5.b

“ control ” has the same meaning as it has in the Broadcasting Act 1990 by
virtue of section 202 of that Act.

56.6

In this section—

      “ news-related material ” means material consisting of—         news or
information about current affairs,           opinion about matters relating to
the news or current affairs, or           gossip about celebrities, other
public figures or other persons in the news;                 “ publish ” means
publish by any means (including by broadcasting), and references to a
publisher and publication are to be construed accordingly;           “
standards code ” means—         a code of standards that regulates the conduct
of publishers, that is published by an independent regulator, or           a
code of standards that regulates the conduct of the entity in question, that
is published by the entity itself.

##### “Search content”, “search results” etc

57

57.1

This section applies for the purposes of this Part.

57.2

“ Search content ” means content that may be encountered in or via search
results of a search service, except—

57.2.a

paid-for advertisements (see section 236),

57.2.b

content on the website of a recognised news publisher (see section 56), and

57.2.c

content that—

57.2.c.i

reproduces in full an article or written item that was originally published by
a recognised news publisher (and is not a screenshot or photograph of that
article or item or of part of it),

57.2.c.ii

is video or audio content that was originally published or broadcast by a
recognised news publisher, and is not a clipped or edited form of such content
(unless it is the recognised news publisher who has clipped or edited it), or

57.2.c.iii

is a link to an article or item within sub-paragraph (i) or to content within
sub-paragraph (ii).

57.3

“ Search results ”, in relation to a search service, means content presented
to a user of the service by operation of the search engine in response to a
search request made by the user.

57.4

“ Search ” means search by any means, including by input of text or images or
by speech, and references to a search request are to be construed accordingly.

57.5

In subsection (2), the reference to encountering content “via search results”—

57.5.a

is to encountering content as a result of interacting with search results (for
example, by clicking on them);

57.5.b

does not include a reference to encountering content as a result of subsequent
interactions with an internet service other than the search service.

57.6

In this section references to a search service include references to a user-
to-user service that includes a search engine.

##### Restricting users’ access to content

58

58.1

This section applies for the purposes of this Part.

58.2

References to restricting users’ access to content, and related references,
include any case where a provider takes or uses a measure which has the effect
that—

58.2.a

a user is unable to access content without taking a prior step (whether or not
taking that step might result in access being denied), or

58.2.b

content is temporarily hidden from a user.

58.3

But such references do not include any case where—

58.3.a

the effect mentioned in subsection (2) results from the voluntary use or
application by a user of features, functionalities or settings which a
provider includes in a service (for example, features, functionalities or
settings included in compliance with the duty set out in section 15 (2)  or
(9)  (user empowerment)), or

58.3.b

access to content is controlled by another user, rather than the provider.

58.4

See also section 236 (6) .

##### “Illegal content” etc

59

59.1

This section applies for the purposes of this Part.

59.2

“ Illegal content ” means content that amounts to a relevant offence.

59.3

Content consisting of certain words, images, speech or sounds amounts to a
relevant offence if—

59.3.a

the use of the words, images, speech or sounds amounts to a relevant offence,

59.3.b

the possession, viewing or accessing of the content constitutes a relevant
offence, or

59.3.c

the publication or dissemination of the content constitutes a relevant
offence.

59.4

“ Relevant offence ” means—

59.4.a

a priority offence, or

59.4.b

an offence within subsection (5).

59.5

An offence is within this subsection if—

59.5.a

it is not a priority offence,

59.5.b

the victim or intended victim of the offence is an individual (or
individuals), and

59.5.c

the offence is created by this Act or, before or after this Act is passed, by—

59.5.c.i

another Act,

59.5.c.ii

an Order in Council,

59.5.c.iii

an order, rules or regulations made under an Act by the Secretary of State or
other Minister of the Crown, including such an instrument made jointly with a
devolved authority, or

59.5.c.iv

devolved subordinate legislation made by a devolved authority with the consent
of the Secretary of State or other Minister of the Crown.

59.6

But an offence is not within subsection (5) if—

59.6.a

the offence concerns—

59.6.a.i

the infringement of intellectual property rights,

59.6.a.ii

the safety or quality of goods (as opposed to what kind of goods they are), or

59.6.a.iii

the performance of a service by a person not qualified to perform it; or

59.6.b

it is an offence under the Consumer Protection from Unfair Trading Regulations
2008 ( S.I. 2008/1277 ).

59.7

“ Priority offence ” means—

59.7.a

an offence specified in Schedule 5 (terrorism offences),

59.7.b

an offence specified in Schedule 6 (offences related to child sexual
exploitation and abuse), or

59.7.c

an offence specified in Schedule 7 (other priority offences).

59.8

“ Terrorism content ” means content that amounts to an offence specified in
Schedule 5.

59.9

“ CSEA content ” means content that amounts to an offence specified in
Schedule 6.

59.10

“ Priority illegal content ” means—

59.10.a

terrorism content,

59.10.b

CSEA content, and

59.10.c

content that amounts to an offence specified in Schedule 7.

59.11

For the purposes of determining whether content amounts to an offence, no
account is to be taken of whether or not anything done in relation to the
content takes place in any part of the United Kingdom.

59.12

References in subsection (3) to conduct of particular kinds are not to be
taken to prevent content generated by a bot or other automated tool from being
capable of amounting to an offence (see also section 192(7) (providers’
judgements about the status of content)).

59.13

Subsection  (14)  applies in relation to a regulated user-to-user service
(but, in the case of a combined service, does not apply in relation to the
search content of the service).

59.14

References to “illegal content”, “terrorism content”, “CSEA content” and
“priority illegal content” are to be read as—

59.14.a

limited to content within the definition in question that is regulated user-
generated content in relation to the service, and

59.14.b

including material which, if it were present on the service, would be content
within paragraph  (a)  (and this section is to be read with such modifications
as may be necessary for the purpose of this paragraph).

59.15

In this section—

      “ devolved authority ” means—         the Scottish Ministers,
the Welsh Ministers, or           a Northern Ireland department;
“ devolved subordinate legislation ” means—         an instrument made under
an Act of the Scottish Parliament,           an instrument made under an Act
or Measure of Senedd Cymru, or           an instrument made under Northern
Ireland legislation;                 “ Minister of the Crown ” has the meaning
given by section 8 of the Ministers of the Crown Act 1975 and also includes
the Commissioners for His Majesty’s Revenue and Customs;           “ offence ”
means an offence under the law of any part of the United Kingdom.

59.16

See also section 192 (providers’ judgements about the status of content).

##### “Content that is harmful to children”

60

60.1

This section and sections 61 and 62 apply for the purposes of this Part.

60.2

“ Content that is harmful to children ” means—

60.2.a

primary priority content that is harmful to children (see section 61),

60.2.b

priority content that is harmful to children (see section 62), or

60.2.c

content, not within paragraph (a) or (b), of a kind which presents a material
risk of significant harm to an appreciable number of children in the United
Kingdom.

60.3

Content is not to be regarded as within subsection  (2)(c)  if the risk of
harm flows from—

60.3.a

the content’s potential financial impact,

60.3.b

the safety or quality of goods featured in the content, or

60.3.c

the way in which a service featured in the content may be performed (for
example, in the case of the performance of a service by a person not qualified
to perform it).

60.4

“ Non-designated content that is harmful to children ” means content within
subsection  (2)(c) .

60.5

Subsection  (6)  applies in relation to a regulated user-to-user service (but,
in the case of a combined service, does not apply in relation to the search
content of the service).

60.6

References to “primary priority content that is harmful to children”,
“priority content that is harmful to children”, “content that is harmful to
children” and “non-designated content that is harmful to children” are to be
read as—

60.6.a

limited to content within the definition in question that is regulated user-
generated content in relation to the service, and

60.6.b

including material which, if it were present on the service, would be content
within paragraph (a) (and this section and sections 61 and 62 are to be read
with such modifications as may be necessary for the purpose of this
paragraph).

##### “Primary priority content that is harmful to children”

61

61.1

“ Primary priority content that is harmful to children ” means content of any
of the following kinds.

61.2

Pornographic content, other than content within subsection  (6) .

61.3

Content which encourages, promotes or provides instructions for suicide.

61.4

Content which encourages, promotes or provides instructions for an act of
deliberate self-injury.

61.5

Content which encourages, promotes or provides instructions for an eating
disorder or behaviours associated with an eating disorder.

61.6

Content is within this subsection if it—

61.6.a

consists only of text, or

61.6.b

consists only of text accompanied by—

61.6.b.i

identifying content which consists only of text,

61.6.b.ii

other identifying content which is not itself pornographic content,

61.6.b.iii

a GIF which is not itself pornographic content,

61.6.b.iv

an emoji or other symbol, or

61.6.b.v

any combination of content mentioned in sub-paragraphs  (i)  to  (iv) .

61.7

In this section and section 62 “ injury ” includes poisoning.

##### “Priority content that is harmful to children”

62

62.1

“ Priority content that is harmful to children ” means content of any of the
following kinds.

62.2

Content which is abusive and which targets any of the following
characteristics—

62.2.a

race,

62.2.b

religion,

62.2.c

sex,

62.2.d

sexual orientation,

62.2.e

disability, or

62.2.f

gender reassignment.

62.3

Content which incites hatred against people—

62.3.a

of a particular race, religion, sex or sexual orientation,

62.3.b

who have a disability, or

62.3.c

who have the characteristic of gender reassignment.

62.4

Content which encourages, promotes or provides instructions for an act of
serious violence against a person.

62.5

Bullying content.

62.6

Content which—

62.6.a

depicts real or realistic serious violence against a person;

62.6.b

depicts the real or realistic serious injury of a person in graphic detail.

62.7

Content which—

62.7.a

depicts real or realistic serious violence against an animal;

62.7.b

depicts the real or realistic serious injury of an animal in graphic detail;

62.7.c

realistically depicts serious violence against a fictional creature or the
serious injury of a fictional creature in graphic detail.

62.8

Content which encourages, promotes or provides instructions for a challenge or
stunt highly likely to result in serious injury to the person who does it or
to someone else.

62.9

Content which encourages a person to ingest, inject, inhale or in any other
way self-administer—

62.9.a

a physically harmful substance;

62.9.b

a substance in such a quantity as to be physically harmful.

62.10

In subsections (2) and (3)—

62.10.a

“ disability ” means any physical or mental impairment;

62.10.b

“ race ” includes colour, nationality, and ethnic or national origins;

62.10.c

references to religion include references to a lack of religion.

62.11

For the purposes of subsection (3), a person has the characteristic of gender
reassignment if the person is proposing to undergo, is undergoing or has
undergone a process (or part of a process) for the purpose of reassigning the
person’s sex by changing physiological or other attributes of sex, and the
reference to gender reassignment in subsection (2) is to be construed
accordingly.

62.12

For the purposes of subsection  (5)  content may, in particular, be “bullying
content” if it is content targeted against a person which—

62.12.a

conveys a serious threat;

62.12.b

is humiliating or degrading;

62.12.c

forms part of a campaign of mistreatment.

62.13

In subsection  (6)  “person” is not limited to a real person.

62.14

In subsection  (7)  “animal” is not limited to a real animal.

##### Content harmful to children: OFCOM’s review and report

63

63.1

OFCOM must carry out reviews of—

63.1.a

the incidence on regulated user-to-user services of content that is harmful to
children,

63.1.b

the incidence on regulated search services and combined services of search
content that is harmful to children, and

63.1.c

the severity of harm that children in the United Kingdom suffer, or may
suffer, as a result of those kinds of content.

63.2
