OFCOM must produce and publish a report on the outcome of each review.

63.3

The report must include advice as to whether, in OFCOM’s opinion, it is
appropriate to make changes to sections 61 and 62, specifying the changes that
OFCOM recommend.

63.4

The reports must be published not more than three years apart.

63.5

The first report must be published before the end of the period of three years
beginning with the day on which this Act is passed.

63.6

OFCOM must send a copy of each report to the Secretary of State.

### Other duties of providers of regulated user-to-user services and regulated search services

#### User identity verification

##### User identity verification

64

64.1

A provider of a Category 1 service must offer all adult users of the service
the option to verify their identity (if identity verification is not required
for access to the service).

64.2

The verification process may be of any kind (and in particular, it need not
require documentation to be provided).

64.3

A provider of a Category 1 service must include clear and accessible
provisions in the terms of service explaining how the verification process
works.

64.4

If a person is the provider of more than one Category 1 service, the duties
set out in this section apply in relation to each such service.

64.5

The duty set out in subsection  (1)  applies in relation to all adult users,
not just those who begin to use a service after that duty begins to apply.

64.6

The duties set out in this section extend only to—

64.6.a

the user-to-user part of a service, and

64.6.b

the design, operation and use of a service in the United Kingdom.

64.7

For the purposes of this section a person is an “adult user” of a service if
the person is an adult in the United Kingdom who—

64.7.a

is a user of the service, or

64.7.b

seeks to begin to use the service (for example by setting up an account).

64.8

For the meaning of “Category 1 service”, see section 95 (register of
categories of services).

##### OFCOM’s guidance about user identity verification

65

65.1

OFCOM must produce guidance for providers of Category 1 services to assist
them in complying with the duty set out in section 64 (1) .

65.2

In producing the guidance (including revised or replacement guidance), OFCOM
must have particular regard to the desirability of ensuring that providers of
Category 1 services offer users a form of identity verification likely to be
available to vulnerable adult users.

65.3

Before producing the guidance (including revised or replacement guidance),
OFCOM must consult—

65.3.a

the Information Commissioner,

65.3.b

persons whom OFCOM consider to have technological expertise relevant to the
duty set out in section 64 (1) ,

65.3.c

persons who appear to OFCOM to represent the interests of vulnerable adult
users of Category 1 services, and

65.3.d

such other persons as OFCOM consider appropriate.

65.4

OFCOM must publish the guidance (and any revised or replacement guidance).

#### Reporting child sexual exploitation and abuse content

##### Requirement to report CSEA content to the NCA

66

66.1

A UK provider of a regulated user-to-user service must operate the service
using systems and processes which secure (so far as possible) that the
provider reports all detected and unreported CSEA content present on the
service to the NCA.

66.2

A non-UK provider of a regulated user-to-user service must operate the service
using systems and processes which secure (so far as possible) that the
provider reports all detected and unreported UK-linked CSEA content present on
the service to the NCA (and does not report to the NCA CSEA content which is
not UK-linked).

66.3

A UK provider of a regulated search service must operate the service using
systems and processes which secure (so far as possible) that the provider
reports all detected and unreported CSEA content present on websites or
databases capable of being searched by the search engine to the NCA.

66.4

A non-UK provider of a regulated search service must operate the service using
systems and processes which secure (so far as possible) that the provider
reports all detected and unreported UK-linked CSEA content present on websites
or databases capable of being searched by the search engine to the NCA (and
does not report to the NCA CSEA content which is not UK-linked).

66.5

A UK provider of a combined service must comply with the requirement under
subsection  (3)  in relation to the search engine of the service.

66.6

A non-UK provider of a combined service must comply with the requirement under
subsection  (4)  in relation to the search engine of the service.

66.7

Providers’ reports under this section—

66.7.a

must meet the requirements set out in regulations under section 67, and

66.7.b

must be sent to the NCA in the manner, and within the time frames, set out in
those regulations.

66.8

If a person is the provider of more than one regulated user-to-user service or
regulated search service, requirements under this section apply in relation to
each such service.

66.9

Terms used in this section are defined in section 70.

66.10

This section applies only in relation to CSEA content detected on or after the
date on which this section comes into force.

##### Regulations about reports to the NCA

67

67.1

The Secretary of State must make regulations in connection with the reports
that are to be made to the NCA (including by non-UK providers) as required by
section 66.

67.2

The regulations may make provision about—

67.2.a

the information to be included in the reports,

67.2.b

the format of the reports,

67.2.c

the manner in which the reports must be sent to the NCA,

67.2.d

the time frames for sending the reports to the NCA (including provision about
cases of particular urgency),

67.2.e

the records that providers must keep in relation to the reports, or the
details that providers must retain as evidence that they have made the
reports, and

67.2.f

such other matters relating to the reports as the Secretary of State considers
appropriate.

67.3

The regulations may also—

67.3.a

require providers to retain, for a specified period, data of a specified
description associated with a report, and

67.3.b

impose restrictions or requirements in relation to the retention of such data
(including how the data is to be secured or stored or who may access the
data).

67.4

The power to require the retention of data associated with a report includes
power to require the retention of—

67.4.a

content generated, uploaded or shared by any user mentioned in the report (or
metadata relating to such content), and

67.4.b

user data relating to any such person (or metadata relating to such data).

“User data” here has the meaning given by section 231.

67.5

Before making regulations under this section, the Secretary of State must
consult—

67.5.a

the NCA,

67.5.b

OFCOM, and

67.5.c

such other persons as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

##### NCA: information sharing

68

In section 16 of the Crime and Courts Act 2013 (interpretation of Part 1), in
subsection (1), in the definition of “permitted purpose”, after paragraph (o)
insert—

68.oa

the exercise of any function of OFCOM (the Office of Communications) under the
Online Safety Act 2023;

.

##### Offence in relation to CSEA reporting

69

69.1

A person commits an offence if, in purported compliance with a requirement
under section 66—

69.1.a

the person provides information that is false in a material respect, and

69.1.b

at the time the person provides it, the person knows that it is false in a
material respect or is reckless as to whether it is false in a material
respect.

69.2

A person who commits an offence under this section is liable—

69.2.a

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding the general limit in a magistrates’ court or a fine (or both);

69.2.b

on summary conviction in Scotland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 12
months or a fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both);

69.2.c

on summary conviction in Northern Ireland, to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding 6 months or a fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both);

69.2.d

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 2 years
or a fine (or both).

##### Interpretation of this Chapter

70

70.1

This section applies for the purposes of this Chapter.

70.2

A provider of a regulated user-to-user service or a regulated search service
is a “UK provider” of the service if the provider is—

70.2.a

an individual or individuals who are habitually resident in the United
Kingdom, or

70.2.b

an entity incorporated or formed under the law of any part of the United
Kingdom.

70.3

Otherwise, a provider of a regulated user-to-user service or a regulated
search service is a “non-UK provider” of the service.

70.4

CSEA content is “detected” by a provider when the provider becomes aware of
the content, whether by means of the provider’s systems or processes or as a
result of another person alerting the provider.

70.5

CSEA content is “ unreported ”, in relation to a provider, if the reporting of
that content is not covered by arrangements (mandatory or voluntary)—

70.5.a

by which the provider reports content relating to child sexual exploitation or
abuse to a foreign agency, or

70.5.b

by which an entity that is a group undertaking in relation to the provider
reports content relating to child sexual exploitation or abuse to—

70.5.b.i

the NCA, or

70.5.b.ii

a foreign agency.

70.6

CSEA content is “UK-linked” if a provider has evidence of a link between the
content and the United Kingdom, based on any of the following—

70.6.a

the place where the content was published, generated, uploaded or shared;

70.6.b

the nationality of a person suspected of committing the related offence;

70.6.c

the location of a person suspected of committing the related offence;

70.6.d

the location of a child who is a suspected victim of the related offence.

For the purposes of paragraphs  (b) ,  (c)  and  (d)  an offence is “related”
to CSEA content if the content amounts to that offence (construed in
accordance with section 59: see subsections  (3) , (11) and (12) of that
section).

70.7

In this Chapter—

“ CSEA content ” has the same meaning as in Part 3 (see section 59); “ foreign
agency ” means a person exercising functions in a country outside the United
Kingdom which correspond to the NCA’s functions insofar as they relate to
receiving and disseminating reports about CSEA content; “ group undertaking ”
has the meaning given by section 1161(5) of the Companies Act 2006; “ NCA ”
means the National Crime Agency.

70.8

Sections 1161(5) and 1162 of, and Schedule 7 to, the Companies Act 2006—

70.8.a

are to apply in relation to an entity which is not an undertaking (as defined
in section 1161(1) of that Act) as they apply in relation to an undertaking,
and

70.8.b

are to be read with any necessary modifications if applied to an entity formed
under the law of a country outside the United Kingdom.

#### Terms of service: transparency, accountability and freedom of expression

##### Duty not to act against users except in accordance with terms of service

71

71.1

A provider of a Category 1 service must operate the service using
proportionate systems and processes designed to ensure that the provider does
not—

71.1.a

take down regulated user-generated content from the service,

71.1.b

restrict users’ access to regulated user-generated content, or

71.1.c

suspend or ban users from using the service,

except in accordance with the terms of service.

71.2

Nothing in subsection (1) is to be read as preventing a provider from taking
down content from a service or restricting users’ access to it, or suspending
or banning a user, if such an action is taken—

71.2.a

to comply with the duties set out in—

71.2.a.i

section 10(2) or (3) (protecting individuals from illegal content), or

71.2.a.ii

section 12(2) or (3) (protecting children from content that is harmful to
children), or

71.2.b

to avoid criminal or civil liability on the part of the provider that might
reasonably be expected to arise if such an action were not taken.

71.3

In addition, nothing in subsection (1) is to be read as preventing a provider
from—

71.3.a

taking down content from a service or restricting users’ access to it on the
basis that a user has committed an offence in generating, uploading or sharing
it on the service, or

71.3.b

suspending or banning a user on the basis that—

71.3.b.i

the user has committed an offence in generating, uploading or sharing content
on the service, or

71.3.b.ii

the user is responsible for, or has facilitated, the presence or attempted
placement of a fraudulent advertisement on the service.

71.4

The duty set out in subsection (1) does not apply in relation to—

71.4.a

consumer content (see section 74);

71.4.b

terms of service which deal with the treatment of consumer content.

71.5

If a person is the provider of more than one Category 1 service, the duty set
out in subsection (1) applies in relation to each such service.

71.6

The duty set out in subsection (1) extends only to the design, operation and
use of a service in the United Kingdom, and references in this section to
users are to United Kingdom users of a service.

71.7

In this section—

“ criminal or civil liability ” includes such a liability under the law of a
country outside the United Kingdom; “ fraudulent advertisement ” has the
meaning given by section 38; “ offence ” includes an offence under the law of
a country outside the United Kingdom.

71.8

See also section 18 (duties to protect news publisher content).

##### Further duties about terms of service

72

######## All services

72.1

A provider of a regulated user-to-user service must include clear and
accessible provisions in the terms of service informing users about their
right to bring a claim for breach of contract if—

72.1.a

regulated user-generated content which they generate, upload or share is taken
down, or access to it is restricted, in breach of the terms of service, or

72.1.b

they are suspended or banned from using the service in breach of the terms of
service.

######## Category 1 services

72.2

The duties set out in subsections  (3)  to  (7)  apply in relation to a
Category 1 service, and references in subsections  (3)  to  (9)  to “ provider
” and “ service ” are to be read accordingly.

72.3

A provider must operate a service using proportionate systems and processes
designed to ensure that—

72.3.a

if the terms of service indicate (in whatever words) that the presence of a
particular kind of regulated user-generated content is prohibited on the
service, the provider takes down such content;

72.3.b

if the terms of service state that the provider will restrict users’ access to
a particular kind of regulated user-generated content in a specified way, the
provider does restrict users’ access to such content in that way;

72.3.c

if the terms of service state cases in which the provider will suspend or ban
a user from using the service, the provider does suspend or ban the user in
those cases.

72.4

A provider must ensure that—

72.4.a

terms of service which make provision about the provider taking down regulated
user-generated content from the service or restricting users’ access to such
content, or suspending or banning a user from using the service, are—

72.4.a.i

clear and accessible, and

72.4.a.ii

written in sufficient detail to enable users to be reasonably certain whether
the provider would be justified in taking the specified action in a particular
case, and

72.4.b

those terms of service are applied consistently.

72.5

A provider must operate a service using systems and processes that allow users
and affected persons to easily report—

72.5.a

content which they consider to be relevant content (see section 74);

72.5.b

a user who they consider should be suspended or banned from using the service
in accordance with the terms of service.

72.6

A provider must operate a complaints procedure in relation to a service that—

72.6.a

allows for complaints of a kind mentioned in subsection  (8)  to be made,

72.6.b

provides for appropriate action to be taken by the provider of the service in
response to complaints of those kinds, and

72.6.c

is easy to access, easy to use (including by children) and transparent.

72.7

A provider must include in the terms of service provisions which are easily
accessible (including to children) specifying the policies and processes that
govern the handling and resolution of complaints of a kind mentioned in
subsection  (8) .

72.8

The kinds of complaints referred to in subsections  (6)  and  (7)  are—

72.8.a

complaints by users and affected persons about content present on a service
which they consider to be relevant content;

72.8.b

complaints by users and affected persons if they consider that the provider is
not complying with a duty set out in any of subsections  (1)  or  (3)  to  (5)
;

72.8.c

complaints by a user who has generated, uploaded or shared content on a
service if that content is taken down, or access to it is restricted, on the
basis that it is relevant content;

72.8.d

complaints by users who have been suspended or banned from using a service.

72.9

The duties set out in subsections  (3)  and  (4)  do not apply in relation to
terms of service which—

72.9.a

make provision of the kind mentioned in section 10(5) (protecting individuals
from illegal content) or 12 (9)  (protecting children from content that is
harmful to children), or

72.9.b

deal with the treatment of consumer content.

######## Further provision

72.10

If a person is the provider of more than one regulated user-to-user service or
Category 1 service, the duties set out in this section apply in relation to
each such service.

72.11

The duties set out in this section extend only to the design, operation and
use of a service in the United Kingdom, and references to users are to United
Kingdom users of a service.

72.12

See also section 18 (duties to protect news publisher content).

##### OFCOM’s guidance about duties set out in sections 71 and 72

73

73.1

OFCOM must produce guidance for providers of Category 1 services to assist
them in complying with their duties set out in sections 71 and 72 (3)  to  (7)
.

73.2

OFCOM must publish the guidance (and any revised or replacement guidance).

##### Interpretation of this Chapter

74

74.1

This section applies for the purposes of this Chapter.

74.2

“ Regulated user-generated content ” has the same meaning as in Part 3 (see
section 55), and references to such content are to content that is regulated
user-generated content in relation to the service in question.

74.3

“ Consumer content ” means—

74.3.a

regulated user-generated content that constitutes, or is directly connected
with content that constitutes, an offer to sell goods or to supply services,

74.3.b

regulated user-generated content that amounts to an offence under the Consumer
Protection from Unfair Trading Regulations 2008 ( S.I. 2008/1277 ) (construed
in accordance with section 59: see subsections (3), (11) and (12) of that
section), or

74.3.c

any other regulated user-generated content in relation to which an enforcement
authority has functions under those Regulations (see regulation 19 of those
Regulations).

74.4

References to restricting users’ access to content, and related references,
are to be construed in accordance with sections 58 and 236 (6) .

74.5

Content of a particular kind is “relevant content” if—

74.5.a

a term of service, other than a term of service mentioned in section 72 (9) ,
indicates (in whatever words) that the presence of content of that kind is
prohibited on the service or that users’ access to content of that kind is
restricted, and

74.5.b

it is regulated user-generated content.

References to relevant content are to content that is relevant content in
relation to the service in question.

74.6

“ Affected person ” means a person, other than a user of the service in
question, who is in the United Kingdom and who is—

74.6.a

the subject of the content,

74.6.b

a member of a class or group of people with a certain characteristic targeted
by the content,

74.6.c

a parent of, or other adult with responsibility for, a child who is a user of
the service or is the subject of the content, or

74.6.d

an adult providing assistance in using the service to another adult who
requires such assistance, where that other adult is a user of the service or
is the subject of the content.

74.7

In determining what is proportionate for the purposes of sections 71 and 72,
the size and capacity of the provider of a service is, in particular,
relevant.

74.8

For the meaning of “Category 1 service”, see section 95 (register of
categories of services).

#### Deceased Child Users

##### Disclosure of information about use of service by deceased child users

75

75.1

A provider of a relevant service must make it clear in the terms of service
what their policy is about dealing with requests from parents of a deceased
child for information about the child’s use of the service.

75.2

A provider of a relevant service must have a dedicated helpline or section of
the service, or some similar means, by which parents can easily find out what
they need to do to obtain information and updates in those circumstances, and
the terms of service must provide details.

75.3

A provider of a relevant service must include clear and accessible provisions
in the terms of service—

75.3.a

specifying the procedure for parents of a deceased child to request
information about the child’s use of the service,

75.3.b

specifying what evidence (if any) the provider will require about the parent’s
identity or relationship to the child, and

75.3.c

giving sufficient detail to enable child users and their parents to be
reasonably certain about what kinds of information would be disclosed and how
information would be disclosed.

75.4

A provider of a relevant service must respond in a timely manner to requests
from parents of a deceased child for information about the child’s use of the
service or for updates about the progress of such information requests.

75.5

A provider of a relevant service must operate a complaints procedure in
relation to the service that—

75.5.a

allows for complaints to be made by parents of a deceased child who consider
that the provider is not complying with a duty set out in any of subsections
(1) to (4),

75.5.b

provides for appropriate action to be taken by the provider of the service in
response to such complaints, and

75.5.c

is easy to access, easy to use and transparent.

75.6

A provider of a relevant service must include in the terms of service
provisions which are easily accessible specifying the policies and processes
that govern the handling and resolution of such complaints.

75.7

If a person is the provider of more than one relevant service, the duties set
out in this section apply in relation to each such service.

75.8

The duties set out in this section extend only to the design, operation and
use of a service in the United Kingdom, and references in this section to
children are to children in the United Kingdom.

75.9

A “ relevant service ” means—

75.9.a

a Category 1 service (see section 95(10)(a));

75.9.b

a Category 2A service (see section 95(10)(b));

75.9.c

a Category 2B service (see section 95(10)(c)).

75.10

In this section “ parent ”, in relation to a child, includes any person who is
not the child’s parent but who—

75.10.a

has parental responsibility for the child within the meaning of section 3 of
the Children Act 1989 or Article 6 of the Children (Northern Ireland) Order
1995 ( S.I. 1995/755 (N.I. 2) ), or

75.10.b

has parental responsibilities in relation to the child within the meaning of
section 1(3) of the Children (Scotland) Act 1995.

75.11

In the application of this section to a Category 2A service, references to the
terms of service include references to a publicly available statement.

##### OFCOM’s guidance about duties set out in section 75

76

76.1

OFCOM must produce guidance for providers of relevant services to assist them
in complying with their duties set out in section 75.

76.2

OFCOM must publish the guidance (and any revised or replacement guidance).

76.3

In this section “ relevant service ” has the meaning given by section 75.

#### Transparency reporting

##### Transparency reports about certain Part 3 services

77

77.1

Once a year, OFCOM must give every provider of a relevant service a notice
which requires the provider to produce a report about the service (a
“transparency report”).

77.2

If a person is the provider of more than one relevant service, a notice must
be given to the provider in respect of each such service.

77.3

In response to a notice relating to a relevant service, the provider of the
service must produce a transparency report which must—

77.3.a

contain information of a kind specified or described in the notice,

77.3.b

be in the format specified in the notice,

77.3.c

be submitted to OFCOM by the date specified in the notice, and

77.3.d

be published in the manner and by the date specified in the notice.

77.4

A provider must ensure that the information provided in a transparency report
is—

77.4.a

complete, and

77.4.b

accurate in all material respects.

77.5

A “ relevant service ” means—

77.5.a

a Category 1 service (see section 95 (10)(a) );

77.5.b

a Category 2A service (see section 95 (10)(b) );

77.5.c

a Category 2B service (see section 95 (10)(c) ).

77.6

In a notice which relates to a Category 1 service or a Category 2B service,
OFCOM may only specify or describe user-to-user information.

But in the case of a service described in subsection  (9) , that subsection
applies instead.

77.7

In a notice which relates to a regulated search service that is a Category 2A
service, OFCOM may only specify or describe search engine information.

77.8

In a notice which relates to a combined service that is a Category 2A service,
and is not also a Category 1 service or a Category 2B service, OFCOM may only
specify or describe search engine information.

77.9

In a notice which relates to a combined service that is a Category 2A service,
as well as being a Category 1 service or a Category 2B service, OFCOM may
specify or describe user-to-user information or search engine information, or
both those kinds of information.

77.10

In subsections  (6)  to  (9) —

77.10.a

“ user-to-user information ” means information which—

77.10.a.i

is about the matters listed in Part 1 of Schedule 8, and

77.10.a.ii

relates to the user-to-user part of a service;

77.10.b

“ search engine information ” means information which—

77.10.b.i

is about the matters listed in Part 2 of Schedule 8, and

77.10.b.ii

relates to the search engine of a service.

77.11

Part 3 of Schedule 8 makes further provision about transparency reports.

77.12

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend subsection  (1)  so as to
change the frequency of the transparency reporting process.

77.13

The Secretary of State must consult OFCOM before making regulations under
subsection  (12) .

77.14

In this section “ notice ” means a notice under subsection  (1) .

##### OFCOM’s guidance about transparency reports

78

78.1

OFCOM must produce guidance about—

78.1.a

how OFCOM will determine which information they will require transparency
reports under section 77 to contain, including—

78.1.a.i

the principles that they will apply in relation to each of the factors
mentioned in paragraph  37  of Schedule 8, and

78.1.a.ii

the steps that they will take to engage with providers of relevant services
before requiring information in a notice under section 77 (1) ;

78.1.b

how information from transparency reports produced by providers of relevant
services under section 77 will be used to produce OFCOM’s transparency reports
(see section 159); and

78.1.c

any other matter that OFCOM consider to be relevant to the production and
publication of transparency reports under section 77 or 159.

78.2

Before producing the guidance (including revised or replacement guidance),
OFCOM must consult such of the following as they consider appropriate—

78.2.a

providers of regulated user-to-user services, and of regulated search
services,

78.2.b

persons who appear to OFCOM to represent such providers,

78.2.c

persons who appear to OFCOM to represent the interests of children (generally
or with particular reference to online safety matters),

78.2.d

persons whom OFCOM consider to have expertise in equality issues and human
rights, in particular—

78.2.d.i

the right to freedom of expression set out in Article 10 of the Convention,
and

78.2.d.ii

the right to respect for a person’s private and family life, home and
correspondence set out in Article 8 of the Convention,

78.2.e

the Information Commissioner,

78.2.f

persons who appear to OFCOM to represent the interests of those with protected
characteristics (within the meaning of Part 2 of the Equality Act 2010), and

78.2.g

persons whom OFCOM consider to have expertise in the enforcement of the
criminal law and the protection of national security that is relevant to
online safety matters,

and OFCOM must also consult such other persons as OFCOM consider appropriate.

78.3

OFCOM must publish the guidance (and any revised or replacement guidance).

78.4

In exercising their functions under section 77 or 159, OFCOM must have regard
to the guidance for the time being published under this section.

78.5

In this section, “ relevant service ” has the same meaning as in section 77
(see subsection  (5)  of that section).

### Duties of providers of regulated services: certain pornographic content

#### “Provider pornographic content” and “regulated provider pornographic content”

79

79.1

This section applies for the purposes of this Part.

79.2

“ Provider pornographic content ”, in relation to an internet service, means
pornographic content that is published or displayed on the service by the
provider of the service or by a person acting on behalf of the provider,
including pornographic content published or displayed on the service by means
of—

79.2.a

software or an automated tool or algorithm applied by the provider or by a
person acting on behalf of the provider, or

79.2.b

an automated tool or algorithm made available on the service by the provider
or by a person acting on behalf of the provider.

79.3

“ Regulated provider pornographic content ”, in relation to an internet
service, means provider pornographic content other than content within
subsection  (4)  or  (5) .

79.4

Content is within this subsection if it—

79.4.a

consists only of text, or

79.4.b

consists only of text accompanied by—

79.4.b.i

a GIF which is not itself pornographic content,

79.4.b.ii

an emoji or other symbol, or

79.4.b.iii

a combination of content mentioned in sub-paragraphs (i) and (ii).

79.5

Content is within this subsection if it consists of a paid-for advertisement
(see section 236).

79.6

References to pornographic content that is “published or displayed” on a
service—

79.6.a

include, in particular—

79.6.a.i

references to pornographic content that is only visible or audible to users as
a result of interacting with content that is blurred, distorted or obscured
(for example, by clicking on such content), but only where the pornographic
content is present on the service,

79.6.a.ii

references to pornographic content that is embedded on the service, and

79.6.a.iii

references to pornographic content that is generated on the service by means
of an automated tool or algorithm in response to a prompt by a user and is
only visible or audible to that user (no matter for how short a time);

79.6.b

do not include references to pornographic content that appears in search
results of a search service or a combined service.

79.7

Pornographic content that is user-generated content in relation to an internet
service is not to be regarded as provider pornographic content in relation to
that service.

79.8

In this section—

“ search results ” has the meaning given by section 57 (3) ; “ user-generated
content ” has the meaning given by section 55 (see subsections  (3)  and  (4)
of that section).

#### Scope of duties about regulated provider pornographic content

80

80.1

A provider of an internet service within subsection  (2)  must comply with the
duties set out in section 81 in relation to the service.

80.2

An internet service is within this subsection if—

80.2.a

regulated provider pornographic content is published or displayed on the
service,

80.2.b

the service is not exempt, and

80.2.c

the service has links with the United Kingdom.

80.3

A service is “ exempt ” for the purposes of this Part if it is —

80.3.a

a user-to-user service or a search service of a description that is exempt as
provided for by Schedule 1, or

80.3.b

an internet service of a kind described in Schedule 9.

80.4

A service “ has links with the United Kingdom ” for the purposes of this Part
if either of the following conditions is met in relation to the service—

80.4.a

the service has a significant number of United Kingdom users, or

80.4.b

United Kingdom users form one of the target markets for the service (or the
only target market).

80.5

This Part does not apply in relation to a part of a regulated service if—

80.5.a

in the case of a Part 3 service, the conditions in paragraph  7(2)  of
Schedule 1 (internal business service conditions) are met in relation to that
part;

80.5.b

in the case of an internet service other than a Part 3 service, the conditions
in paragraph 1(2) of Schedule 9 (internal business service conditions) are met
in relation to that part.

80.6

This Part does not apply in relation to a part of a regulated service if that
part is an on-demand programme service  or a non-UK on-demand programme
service that is a Tier 1 service    ....

80.6A

In subsection (6), “ on-demand programme service ”, “ non-UK on-demand
programme service ” and “ Tier 1 service ” have the same meaning as in the
Communications Act (see sections 368A,  368AA  and  368HA  of that Act).

80.7

If a person is the provider of more than one internet service within
subsection  (2) , the duties set out in section 81 apply in relation to each
such service.

80.8

The duties set out in section 81 extend only to the design, operation and use
of an internet service in the United Kingdom.

#### Duties about regulated provider pornographic content

81

81.1

This section sets out the duties which apply in relation to internet services
within section 80 (2) .

81.2

A duty to ensure, by the use of age verification or age estimation (or both),
that children are not normally able to encounter content that is regulated
provider pornographic content in relation to the service.

81.3

The age verification or age estimation must be of such a kind, and used in
such a way, that it is highly effective at correctly determining whether or
not a particular user is a child.

81.4

In relation to the duty set out in subsection  (2) , a duty to make and keep a
written record, in an easily understandable form, of—

81.4.a

the kinds of age verification or age estimation used, and how they are used,
and

81.4.b

the way in which the provider, when deciding on the kinds of age verification
or age estimation and how they should be used, has had regard to the
importance of protecting United Kingdom users from a breach of any statutory
provision or rule of law concerning privacy that is relevant to the use or
operation of a regulated service (including, but not limited to, any such
provision or rule concerning the processing of personal data).

81.5

A duty to summarise the written record in a publicly available statement, so
far as the record concerns compliance with the duty set out in subsection (2),
including details about which kinds of age verification or age estimation a
provider is using and how they are used.

#### OFCOM’s guidance about duties set out in section 81

82

82.1

OFCOM must produce guidance for providers of internet services within section
80 (2)  to assist them in complying with their duties set out in section 81.

82.2

The guidance must include—

82.2.a

examples of kinds and uses of age verification and age estimation that are, or
are not, highly effective at correctly determining whether or not a particular
user is a child,

82.2.b

examples of ways in which a provider may have regard to the importance of
protecting users as mentioned in section 81 (4)(b) ,

82.2.c

principles that OFCOM propose to apply when determining whether a provider has
complied with each of the duties set out in section 81, and

82.2.d

examples of circumstances in which OFCOM are likely to consider that a
provider has not complied with each of those duties.

82.3

The guidance may elaborate on the following principles governing the use of
age verification or age estimation for the purpose of compliance with the duty
set out in section 81 (2) —

82.3.a

the principle that age verification or age estimation should be easy to use;

82.3.b

the principle that age verification or age estimation should work effectively
for all users regardless of their characteristics or whether they are members
of a certain group;

82.3.c

the principle of interoperability between different kinds of age verification
or age estimation.

82.4

The guidance may refer to industry or technical standards for age verification
or age estimation (where they exist).

82.5

Before producing the guidance (including revised or replacement guidance),
OFCOM must consult—

82.5.a

the Secretary of State,

82.5.b

persons who appear to OFCOM to represent providers of internet services within
section 80 (2) ,

82.5.c

persons who appear to OFCOM to represent adult users of internet services
within section 80 (2) ,

82.5.d

persons who appear to OFCOM to represent the interests of children (generally
or with particular reference to online safety matters),

82.5.e

the Information Commissioner,

82.5.f

persons whom OFCOM consider to have expertise in innovation, or emerging
technology, that is relevant to online safety matters, and

82.5.g

such other persons as OFCOM consider appropriate.

82.6

But if OFCOM propose to revise the guidance, and consider that the minor
nature of the proposal means that consultation is unnecessary—

82.6.a

OFCOM must notify the Secretary of State of the proposed changes, and

82.6.b

if the Secretary of State agrees that it is appropriate, the consultation
requirements set out in subsection  (5)  do not apply in relation to the
proposed changes.

82.7

OFCOM must keep the guidance under review.

82.8

OFCOM must publish the guidance (and any revised or replacement guidance).

### Duties of providers of regulated services: fees

#### Duty to notify OFCOM

83

83.1

A provider of a regulated service must notify OFCOM in relation to a charging
year which is—

83.1.a

the first fee-paying year in relation to that provider, or

83.1.b

any charging year after the first fee-paying year where—

83.1.b.i

the previous charging year was not a fee-paying year in relation to the
provider, and the charging year in question is a fee-paying year in relation
to the provider, or

83.1.b.ii

the previous charging year was a fee-paying year in relation to the provider,
and the charging year in question is not a fee-paying year in relation to the
provider.

83.2

A “ fee-paying year ”, in relation to a provider, means a charging year where
both of the following conditions apply—

83.2.a

the provider’s qualifying worldwide revenue for the qualifying period that
relates to that charging year is equal to or greater than the threshold figure
that has effect for that charging year (see section 86), and

83.2.b

the provider is not exempt (see subsection  (6) ).

83.3

A notification under subsection  (1)  in relation to a charging year must
include details of all regulated services provided by the provider, and where
it is a notification under subsection  (1)(a)  or  (b)(i) , it must also
include—

83.3.a

details of the provider’s qualifying worldwide revenue for the qualifying
period that relates to that charging year, and

83.3.b

supporting evidence, documents or other information as required by regulations
made by OFCOM under section 85.

83.4

Section 85 confers power on OFCOM to make regulations about the determination
of a provider’s qualifying worldwide revenue, and the meaning of “qualifying
period”, for the purposes of this Part.

83.5

A notification under subsection  (1)  must be provided to OFCOM—

83.5.a

in relation to the initial charging year, within four months of the date on
which the first regulations under section 86 come into force (first threshold
figure);

83.5.b

in relation to subsequent charging years, at least six months before the
beginning of the charging year to which the notification relates.

83.6

OFCOM may provide that particular descriptions of providers of regulated
services are exempt for the purposes of this section and section 84 where—

83.6.a

OFCOM consider that an exemption for such providers is appropriate, and

83.6.b

the Secretary of State approves the exemption.

83.7

OFCOM may revoke such an exemption where they consider that it is no longer
appropriate and the Secretary of State approves the revocation.

83.8

Exemptions, or revocations of exemptions, which are approved by the Secretary
of State are to take effect from the beginning of a particular charging year.

83.9

Details of an exemption or revocation must be published by OFCOM at least six
months before the beginning of the first charging year for which the exemption
or revocation is to have effect.

83.10

But subsection  (9)  does not apply in relation to any exemptions which are to
have effect for the initial charging year.

83.11

For the purposes of this section and section 84, the “provider” of a regulated
service, in relation to a charging year, includes a person who is the provider
of the service for part of that year.

#### Duty to pay fees

84

84.1

OFCOM may require a provider of a regulated service to pay a fee in respect of
a charging year which is a fee-paying year.

84.2

Where OFCOM require a provider of a regulated service to pay a fee in respect
of a charging year, the fee is to be equal to the amount produced by a
computation—

84.2.a

made by reference to—

84.2.a.i

the provider’s qualifying worldwide revenue for the qualifying period relating
to that charging year, and

84.2.a.ii

any other factors that OFCOM consider appropriate, and

84.2.b

made in the manner that OFCOM consider appropriate.

84.3

For the purposes of this section and section 83—

84.3.a

the amount of a provider’s qualifying worldwide revenue for a qualifying
period, or

84.3.b

the amount of a fee to be paid to OFCOM, or of an instalment of such a fee,

is, in the event of a disagreement between the provider and OFCOM, the amount
determined by OFCOM.

84.4

When determining fees payable under this section, OFCOM must do so in
accordance with a statement of principles as mentioned in section 88 (1) .

84.5

Where a person is the provider of a regulated service for part of a charging
year only, OFCOM may refund all or part of a fee paid to OFCOM under this
section by that provider in respect of that year.

84.6

In this section, “ fee-paying year ” has the same meaning as in section 83.

#### Regulations by OFCOM about qualifying worldwide revenue etc

85

85.1

For the purposes of this Part, OFCOM may by regulations make provision—

85.1.a

about how the qualifying worldwide revenue of a provider of a regulated
service is to be determined, and

85.1.b

defining the “ qualifying period ” in relation to a charging year.

85.2

OFCOM may by regulations also make provision specifying or describing
evidence, documents or other information that providers must supply to OFCOM
for the purposes of section 83 (see subsection (3)(b) of that section),
including provision about the way in which providers must supply the evidence,
documents or information.

85.3

Regulations under subsection (1)(a) may provide that the qualifying worldwide
revenue of a provider of a regulated service (P) who is a member of a group
during any part of a qualifying period is to include the qualifying worldwide
revenue of any entity that—

85.3.a

is a group undertaking in relation to P for all or part of that period, and

85.3.b

receives or is due to receive, during that period, any amount referable (to
any degree) to a regulated service provided by P.

85.4

Regulations under subsection (1)(a) may, in particular—

85.4.a

make provision about circumstances in which amounts do, or do not, count as
being referable (to any degree) to a regulated service for the purposes of the
determination of the qualifying worldwide revenue of the provider of the
service or of an entity that is a group undertaking in relation to the
provider;

85.4.b

provide for cases or circumstances in which amounts that—

85.4.b.i

are of a kind specified or described in the regulations, and

85.4.b.ii

are not referable to a regulated service,

are to be brought into account in determining the qualifying worldwide revenue
of the provider of the service or of an entity that is a group undertaking in
relation to the provider.

85.5

Regulations which make provision of a kind mentioned in subsection (3) may
include provision that, in the case of an entity that is a group undertaking
in relation to a provider for part (not all) of a qualifying period, only
amounts relating to the part of the qualifying period for which the entity was
a group undertaking may be brought into account in determining the entity’s
qualifying worldwide revenue.

85.6

Regulations under subsection (1)(a) may make provision corresponding to
paragraph 5(8) of Schedule 13.

85.7

Before making regulations under subsection  (1)  OFCOM must consult—

85.7.a

the Secretary of State,

85.7.b

the Treasury, and

85.7.c

such other persons as OFCOM consider appropriate.

85.8

Before making regulations under subsection  (2)  OFCOM must consult the
Secretary of State.

85.9

Regulations under this section may make provision subject to such exemptions
and exceptions as OFCOM consider appropriate.

85.10

In this section—

      “ group ” means a parent undertaking and its subsidiary undertakings,
reading those terms in accordance with section 1162 of the Companies Act 2006;
“ group undertaking ” has the meaning given by section 1161(5) of that Act.

#### Threshold figure

86

86.1

OFCOM must carry out a consultation to inform the setting of the threshold
figure for the purposes of sections 83 and 84, consulting such persons as they
consider appropriate.

86.2

After the completion of the consultation, and having taken advice from OFCOM,
the Secretary of State must make regulations specifying the threshold figure
for those purposes.

86.3

The Secretary of State must keep the threshold figure under review.

86.4

If the Secretary of State considers that it may be appropriate to revise the
threshold figure, the Secretary of State may request OFCOM to carry out a
further consultation, and subsections  (1)  and  (2)  apply again.

86.5

Regulations must provide that a threshold figure is to take effect from the
beginning of a particular charging year.

86.6

Regulations specifying a threshold figure must be in force at least nine
months before the beginning of the first charging year for which that figure
is to have effect.

86.7

But subsection  (6)  does not apply in relation to the first regulations made
under this section.

#### Secretary of State’s guidance about fees

87

87.1

The Secretary of State must issue guidance to OFCOM about the principles to be
included in a statement of principles that OFCOM propose to apply in
determining fees payable under section 84 (see section 88).

87.2

The Secretary of State must consult OFCOM before issuing, revising or
replacing the guidance.

87.3

The guidance may not be revised or replaced more frequently than once every
three years unless—

87.3.a

the guidance needs to be corrected because of an amendment, repeal or
modification of any provision of this Part, or

87.3.b

the revision or replacement is by agreement between the Secretary of State and
OFCOM.

87.4

The Secretary of State must lay the guidance (including revised or replacement
guidance) before Parliament.

87.5

The Secretary of State must publish the guidance (and any revised or
replacement guidance).

87.6

In exercising any functions under this Part, OFCOM must have regard to the
guidance for the time being published under this section.

#### OFCOM’s fees statements

88

88.1

OFCOM may not require a provider of a regulated service to pay a fee under
section 84 unless there is in force a statement of the principles that OFCOM
propose to apply in determining fees payable under that section.

88.2

Those principles must be such as appear to OFCOM to be likely to secure, on
the basis of such estimates of the likely costs as it is practicable for them
to make—

88.2.a

that on a year by year basis, the aggregate amount of the fees payable to
OFCOM under section 84 is sufficient to meet, but does not exceed, the annual
cost to OFCOM of the exercise of their online safety functions;

88.2.b

that the fees required under section 84 are justifiable and proportionate
having regard to the functions in respect of which they are imposed;

88.2.c

that the relationship between meeting the cost of the exercise of those
functions and the amounts of the fees is transparent.

88.3

A statement of principles mentioned in subsection  (1)  must (among other
things)—

88.3.a

include details relating to the computation model used to calculate fees
payable under section 84, including details of factors mentioned in subsection
(2)(a)(ii)  of that section (if any),

88.3.b

include details about the meaning of “qualifying worldwide revenue” and “
qualifying period ” for the purposes of this Part, and

88.3.c

specify the threshold figure contained in regulations under section 86.

88.4

Before making or revising such a statement of principles, OFCOM must consult
such persons as they consider appropriate.

88.5

Such a statement of principles may make different provision in relation to
different kinds of regulated services.

88.6

OFCOM must publish such a statement of principles (and any revised or
replacement statement).

88.7

As soon as reasonably practicable after the end of each charging year, OFCOM
must publish a statement setting out, in respect of that year—

88.7.a

the aggregate amount of the fees payable under section 84 for that year that
has been received by OFCOM,

88.7.b

the aggregate amount of the fees payable under that section for that year that
remains outstanding and is likely to be paid or recovered, and

88.7.c

the cost to OFCOM of the exercise of their online safety functions.

88.8

Any deficit or surplus shown (after applying this subsection for all previous
years) by a statement under subsection  (7)  must be carried forward and taken
into account in determining what is required to satisfy the requirement
imposed by virtue of subsection  (2)(a)  in relation to the following year.

88.9

For the purposes of this section OFCOM’s costs of the exercise of their online
safety functions during a charging year include the costs of preparations for
the exercise of their online safety functions incurred during that year.

#### Recovery of OFCOM’s initial costs

89

Schedule 10 makes provision about fees chargeable to providers of regulated
services in connection with OFCOM’s recovery of costs incurred before the
first day of the initial charging year.

#### Meaning of “charging year” and “initial charging year”

90

In this Part—

      “ charging year ” means any period of 12 months beginning with 1 April,
except such a period that falls before the initial charging year;           “
initial charging year ” means the period of 12 months beginning with 1 April
specified by OFCOM in a notice published for the purposes of this Part.

### OFCOM's powers and duties in relation to regulated services

#### General duties

##### General duties of OFCOM under section 3 of the Communications Act

91

91.1

Section 3 of the Communications Act (general duties of OFCOM) is amended in
accordance with subsections  (2)  to  (8) .

91.2

In subsection (2), after paragraph (f) insert—

91.2.g

the adequate protection of citizens from harm presented by content on
regulated services, through the appropriate use by providers of such services
of systems and processes designed to reduce the risk of such harm.

91.3

In subsection (4)(c), at the beginning insert  “(subject to subsection (5A))”
.

91.4

After subsection (4) insert—

91.4.4A

In performing their duties under subsection (1) in relation to matters to
which subsection (2)(g) is relevant, OFCOM must have regard to such of the
following as appear to them to be relevant in the circumstances—

91.4.4A.a

the risk of harm to citizens presented by regulated services;

91.4.4A.b

the need for a higher level of protection for children than for adults;

91.4.4A.c

the need for it to be clear to providers of regulated services how they may
comply with their duties set out in Chapter 2, 3, 4 or 5 of Part 3, Chapter 1,
3 or 4 of Part 4, or Part 5 of the Online Safety Act 2023;

91.4.4A.d

the need to exercise their functions so as to secure that providers of
regulated services may comply with such duties by taking measures, or using
measures, systems or processes, which are (where relevant) proportionate to—

91.4.4A.d.i

the size or capacity of the provider in question, and

91.4.4A.d.ii

the level of risk of harm presented by the service in question, and the
severity of the potential harm;

91.4.4A.e

the desirability of promoting the use by providers of regulated services of
technologies which are designed to reduce the risk of harm to citizens
presented by content on regulated services;

91.4.4A.f

the extent to which providers of regulated services demonstrate, in a way that
is transparent and accountable, that they are complying with their duties set
out in Chapter 2, 3, 4 or 5 of Part 3, Chapter 1, 3 or 4 of Part 4, or Part 5
of the Online Safety Act 2023.

91.5

After subsection (5) insert—

91.5.5A

Subsection (4)(c) does not apply in relation to the carrying out of any of
OFCOM’s online safety functions.

91.6

After subsection (6) insert—

91.6.6ZA

Where it appears to OFCOM, in relation to the carrying out of any of their
online safety functions, that any of their general duties conflict with their
duty under section 24, priority must be given to their duty under that
section.

91.7

In subsection (14), at the appropriate places insert—

      “ content on regulated services ” means—         regulated user-
generated content present on regulated services,           search content of
regulated services,           fraudulent advertisements present on regulated
services, and           regulated provider pornographic content present on
regulated services;

;

      “ online safety functions ” has the meaning given by section 235 of the
Online Safety Act 2023, except that it does not include OFCOM’s general
duties;

.

91.8

After subsection (14) insert—

91.8.15

In this section the following terms have the same meaning as in the Online
Safety Act 2023—

      “ content ” (see section 236 of that Act);           “ fraudulent
advertisement ” (see sections 38 and 39 of that Act);           “ harm ” (see
section 234 of that Act);           “ provider ”, in relation to a regulated
service (see section 226 of that Act);           “ regulated user-generated
content ” (see section 55 of that Act);           “ regulated provider
pornographic content ” (see section 79 of that Act);           “ regulated
service ” (see section 4 of that Act);           “ search content ” (see
section 57 of that Act).

91.9

In section 6 of the Communications Act (duties to review regulatory burdens)—

91.9.a

in subsection (2), after “this section” insert  “(except their online safety
functions)” , and

91.9.b

after subsection (10) insert—

91.9.b.11

In this section “ online safety functions ” has the same meaning as in section
3.

##### Duties in relation to strategic priorities

92

92.1

This section applies where a statement has been designated under section 172
(1)  (Secretary of State’s statement of strategic priorities).

92.2

OFCOM must have regard to the statement when carrying out their online safety
functions.

92.3

Within the period of 40 days beginning with the day on which the statement is
designated, or such longer period as the Secretary of State may allow, OFCOM
must—

92.3.a

explain in writing what they propose to do in consequence of the statement,
and

92.3.b

publish a copy of that explanation.

92.4

OFCOM must, as soon as reasonably practicable after the end of—

92.4.a

the period of 12 months beginning with the day on which the first statement is
designated under section 172 (1) , and

92.4.b

every subsequent period of 12 months,

publish a review of what they have done during the period in question in
consequence of the statement.

##### Duty to carry out impact assessments

93

93.1

Section 7 of the Communications Act (duty to carry out impact assessments) is
amended as follows.

93.2

In subsection (2), at the beginning insert  “Subject to subsection (2A),” .

93.3

After subsection (2) insert—

93.3.2A

A proposal to do any of the following is important for the purposes of this
section—

93.3.2A.a

to prepare a code of practice under section 41 of the Online Safety Act 2023;

93.3.2A.b

to prepare amendments of such a code of practice; or

93.3.2A.c

to prepare a code of practice as a replacement for such a code of practice.

93.4

After subsection (4) insert—

93.4.4A

An assessment under subsection (3)(a) that relates to a proposal mentioned in
subsection (2A) must include an assessment of the likely impact of
implementing the proposal on small businesses and micro businesses.

93.4.4B

An assessment under subsection (3)(a) that relates to a proposal to do
anything else for the purposes of, or in connection with, the carrying out of
OFCOM’s online safety functions (within the meaning of section 235 of the
Online Safety Act 2023) must, so far as the proposal relates to such
functions, include an assessment of the likely impact of implementing the
proposal on small businesses and micro businesses.

#### Register of categories of regulated user-to-user services and regulated search services

##### Meaning of threshold conditions etc

94

94.1

Schedule 11 contains provision about regulations specifying the threshold
conditions that a Part 3 service must meet to be included in the relevant part
of the register established by OFCOM under section 95, and associated
provision about the publication of OFCOM’s advice.

94.2

In this Chapter, “ Category 1 threshold conditions ”, “ Category 2A threshold
conditions ” and “ Category 2B threshold conditions ” have the same meaning as
in Schedule 11 (see paragraph  1(1) ,  (2)  and  (3)  of that Schedule).

94.3

For the purposes of this Chapter—

94.3.a

references to a service meeting the Category 1, Category 2A or Category 2B
threshold conditions are to a service meeting those conditions in a way
specified in regulations under paragraph 1 of Schedule 11 (see paragraph  1(4)
of that Schedule);

94.3.b

a regulated user-to-user service meets the Category 1 threshold conditions if
those conditions are met in relation to the user-to-user part of the service;

94.3.c

a regulated search service or a combined service meets the Category 2A
threshold conditions if those conditions are met in relation to the search
engine of the service;

94.3.d

a regulated user-to-user service meets the Category 2B threshold conditions if
those conditions are met in relation to the user-to-user part of the service;

94.3.e

a regulated user-to-user service meets the conditions in section 97 (2)  if
those conditions are met in relation to the user-to-user part of the service;

94.3.f

references to OFCOM assessing a service (to determine if it meets, or no
longer meets, the relevant threshold conditions or the conditions in section
97 (2) ) are accordingly to be read as references to OFCOM assessing the
relevant part (or parts) of a service.

##### Register of categories of certain Part 3 services

95

95.1

As soon as reasonably practicable after the first regulations under Schedule
11 come into force, OFCOM must comply with subsections  (2)  to  (4) .

95.2

OFCOM must establish a register of particular categories of Part 3 services
with—

95.2.a

one part for regulated user-to-user services meeting the Category 1 threshold
conditions,

95.2.b

one part for regulated search services and combined services meeting the
Category 2A threshold conditions, and

95.2.c

one part for regulated user-to-user services meeting the Category 2B threshold
conditions.

95.3

OFCOM must assess Part 3 services, as follows—

95.3.a

OFCOM must assess each regulated user-to-user service which they consider is
likely to meet the Category 1 threshold conditions, to determine whether the
service does, or does not, meet those conditions;

95.3.b

OFCOM must assess each regulated search service and combined service which
they consider is likely to meet the Category 2A threshold conditions, to
determine whether the service does, or does not, meet those conditions;

95.3.c

OFCOM must assess each regulated user-to-user service which they consider is
likely to meet the Category 2B threshold conditions, to determine whether the
service does, or does not, meet those conditions.

95.4

If OFCOM consider that a service meets the relevant threshold conditions, they
must add entries relating to that service to the relevant part of the register
established under subsection  (2) .

95.5

But—

95.5.a

if OFCOM consider that a regulated user-to-user service meets the Category 1
threshold conditions and the Category 2B threshold conditions (only), entries
relating to that service are to be added to the part of the register
established under subsection  (2)(a)  (only);

95.5.b

if OFCOM consider that a combined service meets the Category 1 threshold
conditions, the Category 2A threshold conditions and the Category 2B threshold
conditions, entries relating to that service are to be added to the parts of
the register established under subsection  (2)(a)  and  (b)  (only).

95.6

If OFCOM consider that a combined service—

95.6.a

meets the Category 2A threshold conditions, and

95.6.b

meets either the Category 1 threshold conditions or the Category 2B threshold
conditions (but not both),

entries relating to that service are to be added to the part of the register
established under subsection  (2)(b)  and to the part of the register
established under subsection  (2)(a)  or  (c)  (whichever applies).

95.7

Each part of the register must contain—

95.7.a

the name, and a description, of each service that, in OFCOM’s opinion, meets
the relevant threshold conditions, and

95.7.b

the name of the provider of each such service.

95.8

OFCOM must publish the register.

95.9

When assessing whether a Part 3 service does, or does not, meet the relevant
threshold conditions, OFCOM must take such steps as are reasonably practicable
to obtain or generate information or evidence for the purposes of the
assessment.

95.10

In this Act—

95.10.a

a “ Category 1 service ” means a regulated user-to-user service for the time
being included in the part of the register established under subsection
(2)(a) ;

95.10.b

a “ Category 2A service ” means a regulated search service or a combined
service for the time being included in the part of the register established
under subsection  (2)(b) ;

95.10.c

a “ Category 2B service ” means a regulated user-to-user service for the time
being included in the part of the register established under subsection
(2)(c) .

##### Duty to maintain register

96

96.1

If regulations are made under paragraph  1(1)  of Schedule 11 which amend or
replace regulations previously made under that provision, OFCOM must, as soon
as reasonably practicable after the date on which the amending or replacement
regulations come into force—

96.1.a

assess each regulated user-to-user service which they consider is likely to
meet the new Category 1 threshold conditions, to determine whether the service
does, or does not, meet those conditions, and

96.1.b

make any necessary changes to the register.

96.2

If regulations are made under paragraph  1(2)  of Schedule 11 which amend or
replace regulations previously made under that provision, OFCOM must, as soon
as reasonably practicable after the date on which the amending or replacement
regulations come into force—

96.2.a

assess each regulated search service and combined service which they consider
is likely to meet the new Category 2A threshold conditions, to determine
whether the service does, or does not, meet those conditions, and

96.2.b

make any necessary changes to the register.

96.3

If regulations are made under paragraph  1(3)  of Schedule 11 which amend or
replace regulations previously made under that provision, OFCOM must, as soon
as reasonably practicable after the date on which the amending or replacement
regulations come into force—

96.3.a

assess each regulated user-to-user service which they consider is likely to
meet the new Category 2B threshold conditions, to determine whether the
service does, or does not, meet those conditions, and

96.3.b

make any necessary changes to the register.

96.4

At any other time, if OFCOM consider that a Part 3 service not included in a
particular part of the register is likely to meet the threshold conditions
relevant to that part, OFCOM must—

96.4.a

assess the service accordingly, and

96.4.b

(subject to section 95 (5) ) if they consider that the service meets the
relevant conditions, add entries relating to that service to that part of the
register.

96.5

Nothing in subsection  (3)  or  (4)  requires OFCOM to assess a Category 1
service to determine whether the service meets the Category 2B threshold
conditions.

96.6

A provider of a Part 3 service included in the register may at any time
request OFCOM to remove entries relating to that service from the register, or
from a particular part of the register.

96.7

If OFCOM are satisfied, on the basis of evidence submitted by a provider with
such a request, that since the registration day there has been a change to the
service or to regulations under paragraph 1 of Schedule 11 which appears
likely to be relevant, OFCOM must—

96.7.a

assess the service, and

96.7.b

notify the provider of OFCOM’s decision.

96.8

OFCOM must remove entries relating to a Part 3 service from the relevant part
of the register if, following an assessment of the service, they consider that
it no longer meets the threshold conditions relevant to that part.

96.9

Section 95 (9)  applies to an assessment under this section as it applies to
an assessment under section 95.

96.10

OFCOM must re-publish the register each time a change is made to it.

96.11

See section 167 for provision about appeals against a decision to include a
service in the register (or in a particular part of the register), or not to
remove a service from the register (or from a particular part of the
register).

96.12

In this section—

      “ the register ” means the register established under section 95;
“ the registration day ”, in relation to a Part 3 service, means—         the
day on which entries relating to the service were added to the register, or to
the particular part of the register in question, or           if later, the
day on which OFCOM last completed an assessment of the service under
subsection  (1) ,  (2) ,  (3)  or  (7) .

##### List of emerging Category 1 services

97

97.1

As soon as reasonably practicable after the first regulations under paragraph
1(1) of Schedule 11 come into force (regulations specifying Category 1
threshold conditions), OFCOM must comply with subsections  (2)  and  (3) .

97.2

OFCOM must assess each regulated user-to-user service which does not meet the
Category 1 threshold conditions and which they consider is likely to meet each
of the following conditions, to determine whether the service does, or does
not, meet them—

97.2.a

the first condition is that the number of United Kingdom users of the user-to-
user part of the service is at least 75% of the figure specified in any of the
Category 1 threshold conditions relating to number of users (calculating the
number of users in accordance with the threshold condition in question);

97.2.b

the second condition is that—

97.2.b.i

at least one of the Category 1 threshold conditions relating to
functionalities of the user-to-user part of the service is met, or

97.2.b.ii

if the regulations under paragraph  1(1)  of Schedule 11 specify that a
Category 1 threshold condition relating to a functionality of the user-to-user
part of the service must be met in combination with a Category 1 threshold
condition relating to another characteristic of that part of the service or a
factor relating to that part of the service (see paragraph  1(4)  of Schedule
11), at least one of those combinations of conditions is met.

97.3

OFCOM must prepare a list of regulated user-to-user services which meet the
conditions in subsection  (2) .

97.4

If the regulations under paragraph  1(1)  of Schedule 11 specify that a
service meets the Category 1 threshold conditions if any one condition about
number of users or functionality is met (as mentioned in paragraph  1(4)(a)
of that Schedule)—

97.4.a

subsection  (2)  applies as if paragraph (b) were omitted, and

97.4.b

subsections  (3)  and  (8)  apply as if the reference to the conditions in
subsection  (2)  were to the condition in subsection  (2)(a) .

97.5

The list must contain the following details about a service included in it—

97.5.a

the name of the service,

97.5.b

a description of the service,

97.5.c

the name of the provider of the service, and

97.5.d

a description of the Category 1 threshold conditions by reference to which the
conditions in subsection  (2)  are met.

97.6

OFCOM must take appropriate steps to keep the list up to date, including by
carrying out further assessments of regulated user-to-user services.

97.7

OFCOM must publish the list when it is first prepared and each time it is
revised.

97.8

When assessing whether a service does, or does not, meet the conditions in
subsection  (2) , OFCOM must take such steps as are reasonably practicable to
obtain or generate information or evidence for the purposes of the assessment.

97.9

An assessment for the purposes of this section may be included in an
assessment under section 95 or 96 (as the case may be) or carried out
separately.

#### Risk assessments of regulated user-to-user services and regulated search services

##### OFCOM’s register of risks, and risk profiles, of Part 3 services

98

98.1

OFCOM must carry out risk assessments to identify and assess the following
risks of harm presented by Part 3 services of different kinds—

98.1.a

the risks of harm to individuals in the United Kingdom presented by illegal
content present on regulated user-to-user services and by the use of such
services for the commission or facilitation of priority offences;

98.1.b

the risk of harm to individuals in the United Kingdom presented by search
content of regulated search services that is illegal content;

98.1.c

the risk of harm to children in the United Kingdom, in different age groups,
presented by content that is harmful to children.

98.2

The risk assessments must, among other things, identify characteristics of
different kinds of Part 3 services that are relevant to such risks of harm,
and assess the impact of those kinds of characteristics on such risks.

98.3

OFCOM—

98.3.a

may combine assessment of any or all of the risks of harm mentioned in
subsection  (1) , or may carry out separate assessments of those risks;

98.3.b

in the case of the risk of harm mentioned in subsection (1)(c), may assess
regulated user-to-user services and regulated search services separately or
together.

98.4

The findings of each risk assessment are to be reflected, as soon as
reasonably practicable after completion, in a register of risks of Part 3
services prepared and published by OFCOM.

98.5

As soon as reasonably practicable after completing their assessment of a risk
of harm mentioned in a particular paragraph of subsection  (1) , OFCOM must
prepare risk profiles for Part 3 services which relate to that risk of harm.

98.6

For the purposes of the risk profiles, OFCOM may group Part 3 services
together in whichever way they consider appropriate, taking into account—

98.6.a

the characteristics of the services, and

98.6.b

the risk levels and other matters identified in the relevant risk assessment.

98.7

OFCOM must publish risk profiles prepared under this section.

98.8

OFCOM must from time to time review and revise the risk assessments and risk
profiles so as to keep them up to date.

98.9

References in this section to Part 3 services—

98.9.a

in the case of a risk assessment or risk profiles which relate only to
regulated user-to-user services or to regulated search services, are to be
read as references to the kind of service in question;

98.9.b

in the case of a risk assessment or risk profiles which relate only to the
risk of harm mentioned in subsection (1)(a), are to be read as references to
regulated user-to-user services;

98.9.c

in the case of a risk assessment or risk profiles which relate only to the
risk of harm mentioned in subsection (1)(b), are to be read as references to
regulated search services.

98.10

References in this section to regulated search services include references to
the search engine of combined services.

98.11

In this section the “characteristics” of a service include its
functionalities, user base, business model, governance and other systems and
processes.

98.12

In this section—

      “ content that is harmful to children ” has the same meaning as in Part
3 (see section 60);           “ illegal content ” has the same meaning as in
Part 3 (see section 59);           “ priority offence ” has the same meaning
as in Part 3 (see section 59).

##### OFCOM’s guidance about risk assessments

99

99.1

As soon as reasonably practicable after OFCOM have published the first risk
profiles relating to the illegality risks, OFCOM must produce guidance to
assist providers of regulated user-to-user services in complying with their
duties to carry out illegal content risk assessments under section 9.

99.2

As soon as reasonably practicable after OFCOM have published the first risk
profiles relating to the risk of harm from illegal content, OFCOM must produce
guidance to assist providers of regulated search services in complying with
their duties to carry out illegal content risk assessments under section 26.

99.3

As soon as reasonably practicable after OFCOM have published the first risk
profiles relating to the risk of harm to children, OFCOM must produce guidance
to assist providers of Part 3 services in complying with their duties to carry
out children’s risk assessments under section 11 or 28.

99.4

Before producing any guidance under this section (including revised or
replacement guidance), OFCOM must consult the Information Commissioner.

99.5

OFCOM must revise guidance under this section from time to time in response to
further risk assessments under section 98 or to revisions of the risk
profiles.

99.6

OFCOM must publish guidance under this section (and any revised or replacement
guidance).

99.7

If the risk profiles mentioned in subsection  (3)  relate to regulated user-
to-user services only or to regulated search services only, that subsection is
to be read as requiring the production of guidance relating only to regulated
user-to-user services or to regulated search services, as the case may be.

99.8

References in this section to regulated search services include references to
the search engine of combined services.

99.9

In this section—

      “ illegality risks ” means the risks mentioned in section 98(1)(a);
“ risk of harm from illegal content ” means the risk of harm mentioned in
section 98(1)(b);           “ risk of harm to children ” means the risk of
harm mentioned in section 98 (1)(c) ;           “ risk profiles ” means risk
profiles prepared under section 98.

#### Information

##### Information powers and information notices

###### Power to require information

100

100.1

OFCOM may by notice under this subsection require a person within subsection
(5)  to provide them with any information that they require for the purpose of
exercising, or deciding whether to exercise, any of their online safety
functions.

100.2

The power conferred by subsection  (1)  includes power to require a person
within subsection  (5)  to—

100.2.a

obtain or generate information;

100.2.b

provide information about the use of a service by a named individual.

100.3

The power conferred by subsection  (1)  also includes power to require a
person within any of paragraphs  (a)  to  (d)  of subsection  (5)  to take
steps so that a person authorised by OFCOM is able to view remotely—

100.3.a

information demonstrating in real time the operation of systems, processes or
features, including functionalities and algorithms, used by a service;

100.3.b

information generated by a service in real time by the performance of a test
or demonstration of a kind required by a notice under subsection  (1) .

100.4

But the power conferred by subsection  (1)  must be exercised in a way that is
proportionate to the use to which the information is to be put in the exercise
of OFCOM’s functions.

100.5

The persons within this subsection are—

100.5.a

a provider of a user-to-user service or a search service,

100.5.b

a provider of an internet service on which regulated provider pornographic
content is published or displayed,

100.5.c

a person who provides an ancillary service (within the meaning of section 144)
in relation to a regulated service (see subsections  (11)  and  (12)  of that
section),

100.5.d

a person who provides an access facility (within the meaning of section 146)
in relation to a regulated service (see subsections  (10)  and  (11)  of that
section),

100.5.e

a person who was within any of paragraphs  (a)  to  (d)  at a time to which
the required information relates, and

100.5.f

a person not within any of paragraphs  (a)  to  (e)  who appears to OFCOM to
have, or to be able to generate or obtain, information required by them as
mentioned in subsection  (1) .

100.6

The information that may be required by OFCOM under subsection  (1)  includes,
in particular, information that they require for any one or more of the
following purposes—

100.6.a

the purpose of assessing compliance with—

100.6.a.i

any duty or requirement set out in Chapter 2, 3, 4 or 5 of Part 3,

100.6.a.ii

any duty set out in section 64 (user identity verification),

100.6.a.iii

any requirement under section 66 (reporting CSEA content),

100.6.a.iv

any duty set out in section 71 or 72 (terms of service),

100.6.a.v

any duty set out in section 75 (deceased child users),

100.6.a.vi
