any requirement relating to transparency reporting (see section 77 (3)  and
(4) ), or

100.6.a.vii

any duty set out in section 81 (provider pornographic content);

100.6.b

the purpose of assessing compliance with a requirement under section 83 (duty
to notify OFCOM in relation to the charging of fees);

100.6.c

the purpose of a consultation about a threshold figure as mentioned in section
86 (threshold figure for the purposes of charging fees);

100.6.d

the purpose of ascertaining the amount of a person’s qualifying worldwide
revenue for the purposes of—

100.6.d.i

Part 6 (fees), or

100.6.d.ii

paragraph  4  or  5  of Schedule 13 (amount of penalties etc);

100.6.e

the purpose of assessing compliance with any requirements imposed on a person
by—

100.6.e.i

a notice under section 121 (1)  (notices to deal with terrorism content and
CSEA content), or

100.6.e.ii

a confirmation decision;

100.6.f

the purpose of assessing the accuracy and effectiveness of technology required
to be used by—

100.6.f.i

a notice under section 121 (1) , or

100.6.f.ii

a confirmation decision;

100.6.g

the purpose of assessing whether to give a notice under section 121 (1)
relating to the development or sourcing of technology (see subsections  (2)(b)
and  (3)(b)  of that section);

100.6.h

the purpose of dealing with complaints made to OFCOM under section 169 (super-
complaints);

100.6.i

the purpose of OFCOM’s advice to the Secretary of State about provision to be
made by regulations under paragraph  1  of Schedule 11 (threshold conditions
for categories of Part 3 services);

100.6.j

the purpose of determining whether a Part 3 service meets threshold conditions
specified in regulations under paragraph  1  of Schedule 11;

100.6.k

the purpose of preparing a code of practice under section 41;

100.6.l

the purpose of preparing guidance in relation to online safety matters;

100.6.m

the purpose of carrying out research, or preparing a report, in relation to
online safety matters;

100.6.n

the purpose of complying with OFCOM’s duties under section 11 of the
Communications Act, so far as relating to regulated services (media literacy).

100.7

See also section 103 (power to include a requirement to name a senior
manager).

100.8

The reference in subsection (3) to a person authorised by OFCOM is to a person
authorised by OFCOM in writing for the purposes of notices that impose
requirements of a kind mentioned in that subsection, and such a person must
produce evidence of their identity if requested to do so by a person in
receipt of such a notice.

100.9

The power conferred by subsection  (1)  does not include power to require the
provision of information in respect of which a claim to legal professional
privilege, or (in Scotland) to confidentiality of communications, could be
maintained in legal proceedings.

100.10

In this section—

      “ information ” includes documents, and any reference to providing
information includes a reference to producing a document (and see also section
102 (11) );           “ regulated provider pornographic content ” and “
published or displayed ” have the same meaning as in Part 5 (see section 79).

###### Information in connection with an investigation into the death of a child

101

101.1

OFCOM may by notice under this subsection require a relevant person to provide
them with information for the purpose of—

101.1.a

responding to a notice given by a senior coroner under paragraph 1(2) of
Schedule 5 to the Coroners and Justice Act 2009 in connection with an
investigation into the death of a child, or preparing a report under section
163 in connection with such an investigation;

101.1.b

responding to a request for information in connection with the investigation
of a procurator fiscal into, or an inquiry held or to be held in relation to,
the death of a child, or preparing a report under section 163 in connection
with such an inquiry;

101.1.c

responding to a notice given by a coroner under section 17A(2) of the
Coroners Act (Northern Ireland) 1959 (c. 15 (N.I.))  in connection with—

101.1.c.i

an investigation to determine whether an inquest into the death of a child is
necessary, or

101.1.c.ii

an inquest in relation to the death of a child,

or preparing a report under section 163 in connection with such an
investigation or inquest.

101.2

The power conferred by subsection (1) includes power to require a relevant
person to provide OFCOM with information about the use of a regulated service
by the child whose death is under investigation, including, in particular—

101.2.a

content encountered by the child by means of the service,

101.2.b

how the content came to be encountered by the child (including the role of
algorithms or particular functionalities),

101.2.c

how the child interacted with the content (for example, by viewing, sharing or
storing it or enlarging or pausing on it), and

101.2.d

content generated, uploaded or shared by the child.

101.3

The power conferred by subsection (1) includes power to require a relevant
person to obtain or generate information.

101.4

The power conferred by subsection (1) must be exercised in a way that is
proportionate to the purpose mentioned in that subsection.

101.5

The power conferred by subsection (1) does not include power to require the
provision of information in respect of which a claim to legal professional
privilege, or (in Scotland) to confidentiality of communications, could be
maintained in legal proceedings.

101.6

Nothing in this section limits the power conferred on OFCOM by section 100.

101.7

In this section—

      “ information ” includes documents, and any reference to providing
information includes a reference to producing a document (and see also section
102 (11) );           “ inquiry ” means an inquiry held, or to be held, under
the Inquiries into Fatal Accidents and Sudden Deaths etc. (Scotland) Act  2016
(asp 2) ;           “ relevant person ” means a person within any of
paragraphs (a) to (e) of section 100 (5) .

###### Information notices

102

102.1

A notice given under section 100(1) or 101 (1)  is referred to in this Act as
an information notice.

102.2

An information notice may require information in any form (including in
electronic form).

102.3

An information notice must—

102.3.a

specify or describe the information to be provided,

102.3.b

specify why OFCOM require the information,

102.3.c

specify the form and manner in which it must be provided, and

102.3.d

contain information about the consequences of not complying with the notice.

102.4

An information notice must specify when the information must be provided
(which may be on or by a specified date, within a specified period, or at
specified intervals).

102.5

An information notice requiring a person to take steps of a kind mentioned in
section 100(3) must give the person at least seven days’ notice before the
steps are required to be taken.

102.6

An information notice may specify a place at which, and a person to whom,
information is to be provided.

102.7

A person to whom a document is produced in response to an information notice
may—

102.7.a

take copies of, or extracts from, the document;

102.7.b

require the person producing the document, or a person who is or was an
officer of that person, or (in the case of a partnership) a person who is or
was a partner, to give an explanation of it.

102.8

A person to whom an information notice is given has a duty—

102.8.a

to act in accordance with the requirements of the notice, and

102.8.b

to ensure that the information provided is accurate in all material respects.

102.9

OFCOM may cancel an information notice by notice to the person to whom it was
given.

102.10

In this section—

      “ information ” includes documents, and any reference to providing
information includes a reference to producing a document;           “ officer
”, in relation to an entity, includes a director, a manager, an associate, a
secretary or, where the affairs of the entity are managed by its members, a
member.

102.11

In relation to information recorded otherwise than in a legible form,
references in this section to producing a document are to producing a copy of
the information—

102.11.a

in a legible form, or

102.11.b

in a form from which it can readily be produced in a legible form.

###### Requirement to name a senior manager

103

103.1

This section applies where—

103.1.a

OFCOM give a provider of a regulated service an information notice, and

103.1.b

the provider is an entity.

103.2

OFCOM may include in the information notice a requirement that the provider
must name, in their response to the notice, an individual who the provider
considers to be a senior manager of the entity and who may reasonably be
expected to be in a position to ensure compliance with the requirements of the
notice.

103.3

If OFCOM impose a requirement to name an individual, the information notice
must—

103.3.a

require the provider to inform such an individual, and

103.3.b

include information about the consequences for such an individual of the
entity’s failure to comply with the requirements of the notice (see section
110).

103.4

An individual is a “senior manager” of an entity if the individual plays a
significant role in—

103.4.a

the making of decisions about how the entity’s relevant activities are to be
managed or organised, or

103.4.b

the actual managing or organising of the entity’s relevant activities.

103.5

An entity’s “relevant activities” are activities relating to the entity’s
compliance with the regulatory requirements imposed by this Act in connection
with the regulated service to which the information notice in question
relates.

##### Skilled persons' reports

###### Reports by skilled persons

104

104.1

OFCOM may exercise the powers in this section where they consider that it is
necessary to do so for either of the following purposes—

104.1.a

assisting OFCOM in identifying and assessing a failure, or possible failure,
by a provider of a regulated service to comply with a relevant requirement, or

104.1.b

developing OFCOM’s understanding of—

104.1.b.i

the nature and level of risk of a provider of a regulated service failing to
comply with a relevant requirement, and

104.1.b.ii

ways to mitigate such a risk.

104.2

But the powers in this section may be exercised for a purpose mentioned in
subsection (1)(b) only where OFCOM consider that the provider in question may
be at risk of failing to comply with a relevant requirement.

104.3

Section 122 requires OFCOM to exercise the power in subsection  (4)  for the
purpose of assisting OFCOM in connection with a notice under section 121 (1) .

104.4

OFCOM may appoint a skilled person to provide them with a report about matters
relevant to the purpose for which the powers under this section are exercised
(“the relevant matters”), and, where OFCOM make such an appointment, they must
notify the provider about the appointment and the relevant matters to be
explored in the report.

104.5

Alternatively, OFCOM may give a notice to the provider—

104.5.a

requiring the provider to appoint a skilled person to provide OFCOM with a
report in such form as may be specified in the notice, and

104.5.b

specifying the relevant matters to be explored in the report.

104.6

References in this section to a skilled person are to a person—

104.6.a

appearing to OFCOM to have the skills necessary to prepare a report about the
relevant matters, and

104.6.b

where the appointment is to be made by the provider, nominated or approved by
OFCOM.

104.7

It is the duty of—

104.7.a

the provider of the service (“ P ”),

104.7.b

any person who works for (or used to work for) P, or is providing (or used to
provide) services to P related to the relevant matters, and

104.7.c

other providers of internet services,

to give the skilled person all such assistance as the skilled person may
reasonably require to prepare the report.

104.8

The provider of the service is liable for the payment, directly to the skilled
person, of the skilled person’s remuneration and expenses relating to the
preparation of the report.

104.9

Subsections  (10)  to  (12)  apply in relation to an amount due to a skilled
person under subsection  (8) .

104.10

In England and Wales, such an amount is recoverable—

104.10.a

if the county court so orders, as if it were payable under an order of that
court;

104.10.b

if the High Court so orders, as if it were payable under an order of that
court.

104.11

In Scotland, such an amount may be enforced in the same manner as an extract
registered decree arbitral bearing a warrant for execution issued by the
sheriff court of any sheriffdom in Scotland.

104.12

In Northern Ireland, such an amount is recoverable—

104.12.a

if a county court so orders, as if it were payable under an order of that
court;

104.12.b

if the High Court so orders, as if it were payable under an order of that
court.

104.13

In this section “ relevant requirement ” means—

104.13.a

a duty or requirement set out in any of the following—

104.13.a.i

section 9, 11, 26 or 28 (risk assessments);

104.13.a.ii

section 10 or 27 (illegal content);

104.13.a.iii

section 12 or 29 (children’s online safety);

104.13.a.iv

section 14 (assessments related to the adult user empowerment duty set out in
section 15(2));

104.13.a.v

section 15 (user empowerment);

104.13.a.vi

section 20 or 31 (content reporting);

104.13.a.vii

section 21 or 32 (complaints procedures);

104.13.a.viii

section 23 or 34 (record-keeping and review);

104.13.a.ix

section 36 (children’s access assessments);

104.13.a.x

section 38 or 39 (fraudulent advertising);

104.13.a.xi

section 64 (user identity verification);

104.13.a.xii

section 66 (reporting CSEA content);

104.13.a.xiii

section 71 or 72 (terms of service);

104.13.a.xiv

section 75 (deceased child users);

104.13.a.xv

section 77 (3)  or  (4)  (transparency reports);

104.13.a.xvi

section 81(2) (children’s access to pornographic content);

104.13.b

a requirement under section 83 to notify OFCOM in connection with the charging
of fees (see subsections  (1) ,  (3)  and  (5)  of that section); or

104.13.c

a requirement imposed by a notice under section 121 (1)  (notices to deal with
terrorism content and CSEA content).

##### Investigations and interviews

###### Investigations

105

105.1

If OFCOM open an investigation into whether a provider of a regulated service
has failed, or is failing, to comply with any requirement mentioned in
subsection  (2) , the provider must co-operate fully with the investigation.

105.2

The requirements are—

105.2.a

a requirement imposed by a notice under section 121 (1)  (notices to deal with
terrorism content and CSEA content), and

105.2.b

an enforceable requirement as defined in section 131 (except the requirement
in subsection  (1)  of this section).

###### Power to require interviews

106

106.1

The power conferred by this section is exercisable by OFCOM for the purposes
of an investigation that they are carrying out into the failure, or possible
failure, of a provider of a regulated service to comply with a relevant
requirement.

106.2

OFCOM may give an individual within subsection  (4)  a notice requiring the
individual—

106.2.a

to attend at a time and place specified in the notice, and

106.2.b

to answer questions and provide explanations about any matter relevant to the
investigation.

106.3

A notice under this section must—

106.3.a

indicate the subject matter and purpose of the interview, and

106.3.b

contain information about the consequences of not complying with the notice.

106.4

The individuals within this subsection are—

106.4.a

if the provider of the service is an individual or individuals, that
individual or those individuals,

106.4.b

an officer of the provider of the service,

106.4.c

if the provider of the service is a partnership, a partner,

106.4.d

an employee of the provider of the service, and

106.4.e

an individual who was within any of paragraphs  (a)  to  (d)  at a time to
which the required information or explanation relates.

106.5

If OFCOM give a notice to an individual within subsection  (4)(b) ,  (c)  or
(d) , they must give a copy of the notice to the provider of the service.

106.6

An individual is not required under this section to disclose information in
respect of which a claim to legal professional privilege, or (in Scotland) to
confidentiality of communications, could be maintained in legal proceedings.

106.7

In this section—

      “ officer ”, in relation to an entity, includes a director, a manager,
an associate, a secretary or, where the affairs of the entity are managed by
its members, a member;           “ relevant requirement ” has the meaning
given by section 104(13).

##### Powers of entry, inspection and audit

###### Powers of entry, inspection and audit

107

Schedule 12 makes provision about—

107.a

OFCOM’s powers of entry and inspection, and

107.b

the carrying out of audits by OFCOM.

###### Amendment of Criminal Justice and Police Act 2001

108

108.1

The Criminal Justice and Police Act 2001 is amended as follows.

108.2

In section 57(1) (retention of seized items), after paragraph (t) insert—

108.2.u

paragraph 8 of Schedule 12 to the Online Safety Act 2023.

108.3

In section 65 (meaning of “ legal privilege ”)—

108.3.a

after subsection (8B) insert—

108.3.a.8C

An item which is, or is comprised in, property which has been seized in
exercise or purported exercise of the power of seizure conferred by paragraph
7(f), (j) or (k) of Schedule 12 to the Online Safety Act 2023 is to be taken
for the purposes of this Part to be an item subject to legal privilege if, and
only if, the seizure of that item was in contravention of paragraph 17(3) of
that Schedule (privileged information or documents).

;

108.3.b

in subsection (9)—

108.3.b.i

at the end of paragraph (d) omit “or”;

108.3.b.ii

at the end of paragraph (e) insert  “or” ;

108.3.b.iii

before the closing words insert—

108.3.b.iii.g

paragraph 7(f), (j) or (k) of Schedule 12 to the Online Safety Act 2023.

108.4

In Part 1 of Schedule 1 (powers of seizure to which section 50 of the Act
applies), after paragraph 73U insert—

############ Online Safety Act 2023

108.4.73V

Each of the powers of seizure conferred by paragraph 7(f), (j) and (k) of
Schedule 12 to the Online Safety Act 2023.

##### Information offences and penalties

###### Offences in connection with information notices

109

109.1

A person commits an offence if the person fails to comply with a requirement
of an information notice.

109.2

It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under subsection  (1)  to
show that—

109.2.a

it was not reasonably practicable to comply with the requirements of the
information notice at the time required by the notice, but

109.2.b

the person has subsequently taken all reasonable steps to comply with those
requirements.

109.3

A person commits an offence if, in response to an information notice—

109.3.a

the person provides information that is false in a material respect, and

109.3.b

at the time the person provides it, the person knows that it is false in a
material respect or is reckless as to whether it is false in a material
respect.

109.4

A person commits an offence if, in response to an information notice, the
person—

109.4.a

provides information which is encrypted such that it is not possible for OFCOM
to understand it, or produces a document which is encrypted such that it is
not possible for OFCOM to understand the information it contains, and

109.4.b

the person’s intention was to prevent OFCOM from understanding such
information.

109.5

A person commits an offence if—

109.5.a

the person suppresses, destroys or alters, or causes or permits the
suppression, destruction or alteration of, any information required to be
provided, or document required to be produced, by an information notice, and

109.5.b

the person’s intention was to prevent OFCOM from being provided with the
information or document or (as the case may be) from being provided with it as
it was before the alteration.

109.6

The reference in subsection  (5)  to suppressing information or a document
includes a reference to destroying the means of reproducing information
recorded otherwise than in a legible form.

109.7

Offences under this section may be committed only in relation to an
information notice which—

109.7.a

relates to—

109.7.a.i

a user-to-user service,

109.7.a.ii

a search service, or

109.7.a.iii

an internet service on which regulated provider pornographic content is
published or displayed; and

109.7.b

is given to the provider of that service.

109.8

If a person is convicted of an offence under this section, the court may, on
an application by the prosecutor, make an order requiring the person to comply
with a requirement of an information notice within such period as may be
specified by the order.

109.9

See also section 201 (supplementary provision about defences).

109.10

In this section, “ regulated provider pornographic content ” and “ published
or displayed ” have the same meaning as in Part 5 (see section 79).

###### Senior managers’ liability: information offences

110

110.1

In this section “ an individual named as a senior manager of an entity ” means
an individual who, as required by an information notice, is named as a senior
manager of an entity in a response to that notice (see section 103).

110.2

An individual named as a senior manager of an entity commits an offence if—

110.2.a

the entity commits an offence under section 109 (1)  (failure to comply with
information notice), and

110.2.b

the individual has failed to take all reasonable steps to prevent that offence
being committed.

110.3

It is a defence for an individual charged with an offence under subsection
(2)  to show that the individual was a senior manager within the meaning of
section 103 for such a short time after the information notice in question was
given that the individual could not reasonably have been expected to take
steps to prevent that offence being committed.

110.4

An individual named as a senior manager of an entity commits an offence if—

110.4.a

the entity commits an offence under section 109 (3)  (false information), and

110.4.b

the individual has failed to take all reasonable steps to prevent that offence
being committed.

110.5

An individual named as a senior manager of an entity commits an offence if—

110.5.a

the entity commits an offence under section 109 (4)  (encrypted information),
and

110.5.b

the individual has failed to take all reasonable steps to prevent that offence
being committed.

110.6

An individual named as a senior manager of an entity commits an offence if—

110.6.a

the entity commits an offence under section 109 (5)  (destruction etc of
information), and

110.6.b

the individual has failed to take all reasonable steps to prevent that offence
being committed.

110.7

It is a defence for an individual charged with an offence under subsection
(4) ,  (5)  or  (6)  to show that the individual was not a senior manager
within the meaning of section 103 at the time at which the act constituting
the offence occurred.

110.8

It is a defence for an individual charged with an offence under this section
to show that the individual had no knowledge of being named as a senior
manager in a response to the information notice in question.

110.9

See also section 201 (supplementary provision about defences).

###### Offences in connection with notices under Schedule 12

111

111.1

A person commits an offence if the person fails without reasonable excuse to
comply with a requirement of an audit notice.

111.2

A person commits an offence if, in response to an audit notice—

111.2.a

the person provides information that is false in a material respect, and

111.2.b

at the time the person provides it, the person knows that it is false in a
material respect or is reckless as to whether it is false in a material
respect.

111.3

A person commits an offence if—

111.3.a

the person suppresses, destroys or alters, or causes or permits the
suppression, destruction or alteration of, any information required to be
provided, or document required to be produced, by a notice to which this
subsection applies, and

111.3.b

the person’s intention was to prevent OFCOM from being provided with the
information or document or (as the case may be) from being provided with it as
it was before the alteration.

111.4

The reference in subsection  (3)  to suppressing information or a document
includes a reference to destroying the means of reproducing information
recorded otherwise than in a legible form.

111.5

Subsection  (3)  applies to—

111.5.a

a notice under paragraph  3  of Schedule 12 (information required for
inspection), and

111.5.b

an audit notice (see paragraph  4  of that Schedule).

111.6

If a person is convicted of an offence under this section, the court may, on
an application by the prosecutor, make an order requiring the person, within
such period as may be specified by the order, to comply with a requirement of
a notice under paragraph  3  of Schedule 12 or an audit notice (as the case
may be).

###### Other information offences

112

112.1

A person commits an offence if the person intentionally obstructs or delays a
person in the exercise of the power conferred by section 102 (7)(a)  (copying
a document etc).

112.2

A person commits an offence if the person fails without reasonable excuse to
comply with a requirement under section 106 (interviews).

112.3

A person commits an offence if, in purported compliance with a requirement
under section 106—

112.3.a

the person provides information that is false in a material respect, and

112.3.b

at the time the person provides it, the person knows that it is false in a
material respect or is reckless as to whether it is false in a material
respect.

112.4

If a person is convicted of an offence under this section, the court may, on
an application by the prosecutor, make an order requiring the person, within
such period as may be specified by the order, to permit the making of a copy
of a document, or to comply with a requirement under section 106 (as the case
may be).

###### Penalties for information offences

113

113.1

A person who commits an offence under section 109 (1) , 110 (2)  or 111 (1)
is liable—

113.1.a

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to a fine;

113.1.b

on summary conviction in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding
the statutory maximum;

113.1.c

on conviction on indictment, to a fine.

113.2

A person who commits an offence under section 109 (3) ,  (4)  or  (5) , 110
(4) ,  (5)  or  (6) , 111 (2)  or  (3)  or 112 (1)  is liable—

113.2.a

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding the general limit in a magistrates’ court or a fine (or both);

113.2.b

on summary conviction in Scotland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 12
months or a fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both);

113.2.c

on summary conviction in Northern Ireland, to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding 6 months or a fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both);

113.2.d

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 2 years
or a fine (or both).

113.3

A person who commits an offence under section 112 (2)  or  (3)  is liable—

113.3.a

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to a fine;

113.3.b

on summary conviction in Scotland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale;

113.3.c

on summary conviction in Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on
the standard scale.

##### Disclosure of information

###### Co-operation and disclosure of information: overseas regulators

114

114.1

OFCOM may co-operate with an overseas regulator, including by disclosing
online safety information to that regulator, for the purposes of—

114.1.a

facilitating the exercise by the overseas regulator of any of that regulator’s
online regulatory functions, or

114.1.b

criminal investigations or proceedings relating to a matter to which the
overseas regulator’s online regulatory functions relate.

114.2

The power conferred by subsection  (1)  applies only in relation to an
overseas regulator for the time being specified in regulations made by the
Secretary of State.

114.3

Where information is disclosed to a person in reliance on subsection  (1) ,
the person may not—

114.3.a

use the information for a purpose other than the purpose for which it was
disclosed, or

114.3.b

further disclose the information,

except with OFCOM’s consent (which may be general or specific) or in
accordance with an order of a court or tribunal.

114.4

Except as provided by subsection  (5) , a disclosure of information under
subsection  (1)  does not breach—

114.4.a

any obligation of confidence owed by the person making the disclosure, or

114.4.b

any other restriction on the disclosure of information (however imposed).

114.5

Subsection  (1)  does not authorise a disclosure of information that—

114.5.a

would contravene the restriction imposed by section 116 (intelligence service
information),

114.5.b

would contravene the data protection legislation (but in determining whether a
disclosure would do so, the power conferred by that subsection is to be taken
into account), or

114.5.c

is prohibited by any of Parts 1 to 7 or Chapter 1 of Part 9 of the
Investigatory Powers Act 2016.

114.6

Section 18 of the Anti-terrorism, Crime and Security Act 2001 (restriction on
disclosure of information for overseas purposes) has effect in relation to a
disclosure authorised by subsection  (1)(b)  as it has effect in relation to a
disclosure authorised by any of the provisions to which section 17 of that Act
applies.

114.7

In this section—

      “ online regulatory functions ”, in relation to an overseas regulator,
means functions of that regulator which correspond to OFCOM’s online safety
functions;           “ online safety information ” means information held by
OFCOM in connection with any of OFCOM’s online safety functions;           “
overseas regulator ” means a person exercising functions in a country outside
the United Kingdom which correspond to any of OFCOM’s online safety functions;
“ the data protection legislation ” has the same meaning as in the Data
Protection Act 2018 (see section 3 of that Act).

###### Disclosure of information

115

115.1

Section 393 of the Communications Act (general restrictions on disclosure of
information) is amended as follows.

115.2

In subsection (1)—

115.2.a

at the end of paragraph (c) omit “or”,

115.2.b

at the end of paragraph (d) insert  “or” , and

115.2.c

after paragraph (d) insert—

115.2.c.e

the Online Safety Act 2023,

.

115.3

In subsection (2)(e), after “this Act” insert  “or the Online Safety Act 2023”
.

115.4

In subsection (3), after paragraph (h) insert—

115.4.ha

a person appointed under—

115.4.ha.i

paragraph 1 of Schedule 3 to the Coroners and Justice Act 2009, or

115.4.ha.ii

section 2 of the  Coroners Act (Northern Ireland) 1959 (c. 15 (N.I.)) ;

115.4.hb

the procurator fiscal, within the meaning of the enactment mentioned in
subsection (5)(s);

.

115.5

In subsection (5)—

115.5.a

before paragraph (d) insert—

115.5.a.ca

the Coroners Act (Northern Ireland) 1959;

,

115.5.b

after paragraph (na) insert—

115.5.b.nb

Part 1 of the Coroners and Justice Act 2009;

, and

115.5.c

after paragraph (r) insert—

115.5.c.s

the Inquiries into Fatal Accidents and Sudden Deaths etc. (Scotland) Act  2016
(asp 2) .

115.6

In subsection (6)(a), after “390” insert  “, or under section 149 of or
Schedule 11 to the Online Safety Act 2023” .

115.7

In subsection (6)(b), at the end insert  “or the Online Safety Act 2023” .

###### Intelligence service information

116

116.1

OFCOM may not disclose information received (directly or indirectly) from, or
that relates to, an intelligence service unless the intelligence service
consents to the disclosure.

116.2

If OFCOM have disclosed information described in subsection  (1)  to a person,
the person must not further disclose the information unless the intelligence
service consents to the disclosure.

116.3

If OFCOM would contravene subsection  (1)  by publishing in its entirety—

116.3.a

a statement required to be published by section 47 (5) , or

116.3.b

a report mentioned in section 164 (5) ,

OFCOM must, before publication, remove or obscure the information which by
reason of subsection  (1)  they must not disclose.

116.4

In this section—

      “ information ” means information held by OFCOM in connection with an
online safety matter;           “ intelligence service ” means—         the
Security Service,           the Secret Intelligence Service, or           the
Government Communications Headquarters.

###### Provision of information to the Secretary of State

117

117.1

Section 24B of the Communications Act (provision of information to assist in
formulation of policy) is amended as follows.

117.2

In subsection (2)—

117.2.a

at the end of paragraph (d) omit “or”,

117.2.b

at the end of paragraph (e) insert  “or” , and

117.2.c

after paragraph (e) insert—

117.2.c.f

the Online Safety Act 2023,

.

117.3

After subsection (3) insert—

117.3.4

Subsection (2) does not apply to information—

117.3.4.a

obtained by OFCOM—

117.3.4.a.i

in the exercise of a power conferred by section 100 of the Online Safety Act
2023 for the purpose mentioned in subsection  (6)(c)  of that section
(information in connection with a consultation about a threshold figure for
the purposes of charging fees under that Act), or

117.3.4.a.ii

in the exercise of a power conferred by section 175(5) of that Act
(information in connection with circumstances presenting a threat), and

117.3.4.b

reasonably required by the Secretary of State.

      Online Safety Act 2023.

Section 26 of the Communications Act (publication of information and advice

119.2

.

119.3.7

In this section the following terms have the same meaning as in the Online

      “ regulated service ” (see section 4 of that Act);           “ United

###### Admissibility of statements

120

120.1

An explanation given, or information provided, by a person in response to a
requirement imposed under or by virtue of section 100, 101 or 106 or paragraph
2(4)(e)  or  (f) , 3(2),  4(2)(i)  or  (j)  or  7(d)  of Schedule 12, may, in
criminal proceedings, only be used in evidence against that person—

120.1.a

on a prosecution for an offence under a provision listed in subsection  (2) ,
or

120.1.b

on a prosecution for any other offence where—

120.1.b.i

in giving evidence that person makes a statement inconsistent with that
explanation or information, and

120.1.b.ii

evidence relating to that explanation or information is adduced, or a question
relating to it is asked, by that person or on that person’s behalf.

120.2

Those provisions are—

120.2.a

section 69 (1) ,

120.2.b

section 109 (3) ,

120.2.c

section 110 (4) ,

120.2.d

section 111 (2) ,

120.2.e

section 112 (3) ,

120.2.f

paragraph  18 (1)(c) of Schedule 12,

120.2.g

section 5 of the Perjury Act 1911 (false statements made otherwise than on
oath),

120.2.h

section 44(2) of the Criminal Law (Consolidation) (Scotland) Act 1995 (false
statements made otherwise than on oath), and

120.2.i

Article 10 of the Perjury (Northern Ireland) Order 1979 ( S.I. 1979/1714 (N.I.
19) ) (false statutory declarations and other false unsworn statements).

#### Regulated user-to-user services and regulated search services: notices to deal with terrorism content and CSEA content

##### Notices to deal with terrorism content or CSEA content (or both)

121

121.1

If OFCOM consider that it is necessary and proportionate to do so, they may
give a notice described in subsection (2), (3) or (4) relating to a regulated
user-to-user service or a regulated search service to the provider of the
service.

121.2

A notice under subsection (1) that relates to a regulated user-to-user service
is a notice requiring the provider of the service—

121.2.a

to do any or all of the following—

121.2.a.i

use accredited technology to identify terrorism content communicated publicly
by means of the service and to swiftly take down that content;

121.2.a.ii

use accredited technology to prevent individuals from encountering terrorism
content communicated publicly by means of the service;

121.2.a.iii

use accredited technology to identify CSEA content, whether communicated
publicly or privately by means of the service, and to swiftly take down that
content;

121.2.a.iv

use accredited technology to prevent individuals from encountering CSEA
content, whether communicated publicly or privately, by means of the service;
or

121.2.b

to use the provider’s best endeavours to develop or source technology for use
on or in relation to the service or part of the service, which—

121.2.b.i

achieves the purpose mentioned in paragraph (a)(iii) or (iv), and

121.2.b.ii

meets the standards published by the Secretary of State (see section 125(13)).

121.3

A notice under subsection (1) that relates to a regulated search service is a
notice requiring the provider of the service—

121.3.a

to do either or both of the following—

121.3.a.i

use accredited technology to identify search content of the service that is
terrorism content and to swiftly take measures designed to secure, so far as
possible, that search content of the service no longer includes terrorism
content identified by the technology;

121.3.a.ii

use accredited technology to identify search content of the service that is
CSEA content and to swiftly take measures designed to secure, so far as
possible, that search content of the service no longer includes CSEA content
identified by the technology; or

121.3.b

to use the provider’s best endeavours to develop or source technology for use
on or in relation to the service which—

121.3.b.i

achieves the purpose mentioned in paragraph (a)(ii), and

121.3.b.ii

meets the standards published by the Secretary of State (see section 125(13)).

121.4

A notice under subsection (1) that relates to a combined service is a notice
requiring the provider of the service—

121.4.a

to do any or all of the things described in subsection (2)(a) in relation to
the user-to-user part of the service, or to use best endeavours to develop or
source technology as described in subsection (2)(b) for use on or in relation
to that part of the service;

121.4.b

to do either or both of the things described in subsection (3)(a) in relation
to the search engine of the service, or to use best endeavours to develop or
source technology as described in subsection (3)(b) for use on or in relation
to the search engine of the service;

121.4.c

to do any or all of the things described in subsection (2)(a) in relation to
the user-to-user part of the service and either or both of the things
described in subsection (3)(a) in relation to the search engine of the
service; or

121.4.d

to use best endeavours to develop or source—

121.4.d.i

technology as described in subsection (2)(b) for use on or in relation to the
user-to-user part of the service, and

121.4.d.ii

technology as described in subsection (3)(b) for use on or in relation to the
search engine of the service.

121.5

For the purposes of subsections (2) and (3), a requirement to use accredited
technology may be complied with by the use of the technology alone or by means
of the technology together with the use of human moderators.

121.6

See—

121.6.a

section 122, which requires OFCOM to obtain a skilled person’s report before
giving a notice under subsection (1),

121.6.b

section 123, which requires OFCOM to give a warning notice before giving a
notice under subsection (1), and

121.6.c

section 124 for provision about matters which OFCOM must consider before
giving a notice under subsection (1).

121.7

A notice under subsection  (1)  that relates to a user-to-user service (or to
the user-to-user part of a combined service) and requires the use of
technology in relation to terrorism content must identify the content, or
parts of the service that include content, that OFCOM consider is communicated
publicly on that service (see section 232).

121.8

For the meaning of “accredited” technology, see section 125 (12)  and  (13) .

##### Requirement to obtain skilled person’s report

122

122.1

OFCOM may give a notice under section 121 (1)  to a provider only after
obtaining a report from a skilled person appointed by OFCOM under section 104
(4) .

122.2

The purpose of the report is to assist OFCOM in deciding whether to give a
notice under section 121 (1) , and to advise about the requirements that might
be imposed by such a notice if it were to be given.

##### Warning notices

123

123.1

OFCOM may give a notice under section 121(1) to a provider relating to a
service or part of a service only after giving a warning notice to the
provider that they intend to give such a notice relating to that service or
that part of it.

123.2

A warning notice under subsection (1) relating to the use of accredited
technology (see section 121(2)(a) and (3)(a)) must—

123.2.a

contain a summary of the report obtained by OFCOM under section 122,

123.2.b

contain details of the technology that OFCOM are considering requiring the
provider to use,

123.2.c

specify whether the technology is to be required in relation to terrorism
content or CSEA content (or both),

123.2.d

specify any other requirements that OFCOM are considering imposing (see
section 125(2) to (4)),

123.2.e

specify the period for which OFCOM are considering imposing the requirements
(see section 125(7)),

123.2.f

state that the provider may make representations to OFCOM (with any supporting
evidence), and

123.2.g

specify the period within which representations may be made.

123.3

A warning notice under subsection (1) relating to the development or sourcing
of technology (see section 121 (2)(b) and  (3)(b) ) must—

123.3.a

contain a summary of the report obtained by OFCOM under section 122,

123.3.b

describe the proposed purpose for which the technology must be developed or
sourced (see section 121 (2)(a)(iii)  and  (iv)  and (3)(a)(ii)),

123.3.c

specify steps that OFCOM consider the provider needs to take in order to
comply with the requirement described in section 121(2)(b) or (3)(b), or both
those requirements (as the case may be),

123.3.d

specify the proposed period within which the provider must take each of those
steps,

123.3.e

specify any other requirements that OFCOM are considering imposing,

123.3.f

state that the provider may make representations to OFCOM (with any supporting
evidence), and

123.3.g

specify the period within which representations may be made.

123.4

A notice under section 121 (1)  that relates to both the user-to-user part of
a combined service and the search engine of the service (as described in
section 121 (4)(c)  or  (d) ) may be given to the provider of the service only
if—

123.4.a

two separate warning notices have been given to the provider (one relating to
the user-to-user part of the service and the other relating to the search
engine), or

123.4.b

a single warning notice relating to both the user-to-user part of the service
and the search engine has been given to the provider.

123.5

A notice under section 121 (1)  may not be given to a provider until the
period allowed by the warning notice for the provider to make representations
has expired.

##### Matters relevant to a decision to give a notice under section 121

124

124.1

This section specifies the matters which OFCOM must particularly consider in
deciding whether it is necessary and proportionate to give a notice under
section 121 (1)  relating to a Part 3 service to the provider of the service.

124.2

In the case of a notice requiring the use of accredited technology, the
matters are as follows—

124.2.a

the kind of service it is;

124.2.b

the functionalities of the service;

124.2.c

the user base of the service;

124.2.d

in the case of a notice relating to a user-to-user service (or to the user-to-
user part of a combined service), the prevalence of relevant content on the
service, and the extent of its dissemination by means of the service;

124.2.e

in the case of a notice relating to a search service (or to the search engine
of a combined service), the prevalence of search content of the service that
is relevant content;

124.2.f

the level of risk of harm to individuals in the United Kingdom presented by
relevant content, and the severity of that harm;

124.2.g

the systems and processes used by the service which are designed to identify
and remove relevant content;

124.2.h

the contents of the skilled person’s report obtained as required by section
122;

124.2.i

the extent to which the use of the specified technology would or might result
in interference with users’ right to freedom of expression within the law;

124.2.j

the level of risk of the use of the specified technology resulting in a breach
of any statutory provision or rule of law concerning privacy that is relevant
to the use or operation of the service (including, but not limited to, any
such provision or rule concerning the processing of personal data);

124.2.k

in the case of a notice relating to a user-to-user service (or to the user-to-
user part of a combined service), the extent to which the use of the specified
technology would or might—

124.2.k.i

have an adverse impact on the availability of journalistic content on the
service, or

124.2.k.ii

result in a breach of the confidentiality of journalistic sources;

124.2.l

whether the use of any less intrusive measures than the specified technology
would be likely to achieve a significant reduction in the amount of relevant
content.

124.3

The references to relevant content in subsection  (2)(f) , (g) and  (l)  are
to—

124.3.a

in the case of a user-to-user service (or the user-to-user part of a combined
service), relevant content present on the service;

124.3.b

in the case of a search service (or the search engine of a combined service),
search content of the service that is relevant content.

124.4

In the case of a notice relating to the development or sourcing of technology,
subsection (2) applies—

124.4.a

as if references to relevant content were to CSEA content, and

124.4.b

with the omission of paragraphs  (i) ,  (j) ,  (k)  and  (l) .

124.5

In this section—

      “ journalistic content ” has the meaning given by section 19;
“ relevant content ” means terrorism content or CSEA content or both those
kinds of content (depending on the kind, or kinds, of content in relation to
which the specified technology is to operate);           “ specified
technology ” means the technology to be specified in the notice under section
121 (1) .

##### Notices under section 121

125

125.1

In this section “ a notice ” means a notice under section 121 (1)  (including
a further notice under that provision).

125.2

If a provider is already using accredited technology in relation to the
service in question, a notice may require the provider to use it more
effectively (specifying the ways in which that must be done).

125.3

A notice relating to a user-to-user service (or to the user-to-user part of a
combined service) may also require a provider to operate an effective
complaints procedure allowing for United Kingdom users to challenge the
provider for taking down content which they have generated, uploaded or shared
on the service.

125.4

A notice relating to a search service (or to the search engine of a combined
service) may also require a provider to operate an effective complaints
procedure allowing for an interested person (see section 227 (7) ) to
challenge measures taken or in use by the provider that result in content
relating to that interested person no longer appearing in search results of
the service.

125.5

A notice given to a provider of a Part 3 service requiring the use of
accredited technology is to be taken to require the provider to make such
changes to the design or operation of the service as are necessary for the
technology to be used effectively.

125.6

A notice requiring the use of accredited technology must—

125.6.a

give OFCOM’s reasons for their decision to give the notice,

125.6.b

contain details of the requirements imposed by the notice,

125.6.c

contain details of the technology to be used,

125.6.d

contain details about the manner in which the technology is to be implemented,

125.6.e

specify a reasonable period for compliance with the notice,

125.6.f

specify the period for which the notice is to have effect,

125.6.g

contain details of the rights of appeal under section 168,

125.6.h

contain information about when OFCOM intend to review the notice (see section
126), and

125.6.i

contain information about the consequences of not complying with the notice
(including information about the further kinds of enforcement action that it
would be open to OFCOM to take).

125.7

A notice requiring the use of accredited technology may impose requirements
for a period of up to 36 months beginning with the last day of the period
specified in the notice in accordance with subsection  (6)(e) .

125.8

A notice relating to the development or sourcing of technology must—

125.8.a

give OFCOM’s reasons for their decision to give the notice,

125.8.b

describe the purpose for which technology is required to be developed or
sourced (see section 121 (2)(a)(iii)  and  (iv)  and  (3)(a)(ii) ,

125.8.c

specify steps that the provider is required to take (including steps relating
to the use of a system or process) in order to comply with the requirement
described in section 121 (2)(b)  or  (3)(b) , or both those requirements (as
the case may be),

125.8.d

specify a reasonable period within which each of the steps specified in the
notice must be taken,

125.8.e

contain details of any other requirements imposed by the notice,

125.8.f

contain details of the rights of appeal under section 168,

125.8.g

contain information about when OFCOM intend to review the notice (see section
126), and

125.8.h

contain information about the consequences of not complying with the notice
(including information about the further kinds of enforcement action that it
would be open to OFCOM to take).

125.9

In deciding what period or periods to specify for steps to be taken in
accordance with subsection (8)(d), OFCOM must, in particular, consider—

125.9.a

the size and capacity of the provider, and

125.9.b

the state of development of technology capable of achieving the purpose
described in the notice in accordance with subsection (8)(b).

125.10

A notice may impose requirements only in relation to the design and operation
of a Part 3 service—

125.10.a

in the United Kingdom, or

125.10.b

as it affects United Kingdom users of the service.

125.11

OFCOM may vary or revoke a notice given to a provider by notifying the
provider to that effect.

125.12

For the purposes of this Chapter, technology is “accredited” if it is
accredited (by OFCOM or another person appointed by OFCOM) as meeting minimum
standards of accuracy in the detection of terrorism content or CSEA content
(as the case may be).

125.13

Those minimum standards of accuracy must be such standards as are for the time
being approved and published by the Secretary of State, following advice from
OFCOM.

##### Review and further notice under section 121

126

126.1

This section applies where OFCOM have given a provider of a Part 3 service a
notice under section 121 (1) .

126.2

The power conferred by section 125 (11)  includes power to revoke the notice
if there are reasonable grounds for believing that the provider is failing to
comply with it.

126.3

If a notice is revoked as mentioned in subsection  (2) , OFCOM may give the
provider a further notice under section 121 (1)  if they consider that it is
necessary and proportionate to do so (taking into account the matters
mentioned in section 124).

126.4

Except where a notice under section 121 (1)  is revoked as mentioned in
subsection  (2) , OFCOM must carry out a review of the provider’s compliance
with the notice—

126.4.a

in the case of a notice requiring the use of accredited technology, before the
end of the period for which the notice has effect;

126.4.b

in the case of a notice relating to the development or sourcing of technology,
before the last date by which any step specified in the notice is required to
be taken.

126.5

In the case of a notice requiring the use of accredited technology, the review
must consider—

126.5.a

the extent to which the technology specified in the notice has been used, and

126.5.b

the effectiveness of its use.

126.6

Following the review, and after consultation with the provider, OFCOM may give
the provider a further notice under section 121 (1)  if they consider that it
is necessary and proportionate to do so (taking into account the matters
mentioned in section 124).

126.7

If a further notice under section 121 (1)  is given, subsections  (3)  to  (6)
apply again.

126.8

A further notice under section 121 (1)  may impose different requirements from
an earlier notice under that provision.

126.9

Sections 122 (skilled person’s report) and 123 (warning notices) do not apply
in relation to a further notice under section 121 (1) .

##### OFCOM’s guidance about functions under this Chapter

127

127.1

OFCOM must produce guidance for providers of Part 3 services about how OFCOM
propose to exercise their functions under this Chapter.

127.2

Before producing the guidance (including revised or replacement guidance),
OFCOM must consult the Information Commissioner.

127.3

OFCOM must keep the guidance under review.

127.4

OFCOM must publish the guidance (and any revised or replacement guidance).

127.5

In exercising their functions under this Chapter, or deciding whether to
exercise them, OFCOM must have regard to the guidance for the time being
published under this section.

##### OFCOM’s annual report

128

128.1

OFCOM must produce and publish an annual report about—

128.1.a

the exercise of their functions under this Chapter, and

128.1.b

technology which meets, or is in the process of development so as to meet,
minimum standards of accuracy (see subsections  (12)  and  (13)  of section
125) for the purposes of this Chapter.

128.2

OFCOM must send a copy of the report to the Secretary of State, and the
Secretary of State must lay it before Parliament.

128.3

For further provision about reports under this section, see section 164.

##### Interpretation of this Chapter

129

In this Chapter—

      “ search content ” has the same meaning as in Part 3 (see section 57);
“ search results ” has the meaning given by section 57 (3) ;           “
terrorism content ” and “ CSEA content ” have the same meaning as in Part 3
(see section 59).

#### Enforcement powers

##### Provisional notices and confirmation decisions

###### Provisional notice of contravention

130

130.1

OFCOM may give a notice under this section (a “provisional notice of
contravention”) relating to a regulated service to the provider of the service
if they consider that there are reasonable grounds for believing that the
provider has failed, or is failing, to comply with any enforceable requirement
(see section 131) that applies in relation to the service.

130.2

OFCOM may also give a provisional notice of contravention to a person on
either of the grounds in subsection  (3) .

130.3

The grounds are that—

130.3.a

the person has been given an information notice and OFCOM consider that there
are reasonable grounds for believing that the person has failed, or is
failing, to comply with either of the duties set out in section 102 (8)
(duties in relation to information notices), or

130.3.b

the person is required by a skilled person appointed under section 104 to give
assistance to the skilled person, and OFCOM consider that there are reasonable
grounds for believing that the person has failed, or is failing, to comply
with the duty set out in subsection  (7)  of that section to give such
assistance.

130.4

A provisional notice of contravention given to a person must—

130.4.a

specify the duty or requirement with which (in OFCOM’s opinion) the person has
failed, or is failing, to comply, and

130.4.b

give OFCOM’s reasons for their opinion that the person has failed, or is
failing, to comply with it.

130.5

A provisional notice of contravention may also contain details as mentioned in
subsection  (6)  or  (7) , or both.

130.6

A provisional notice of contravention may specify steps that OFCOM consider
the person needs to take in order to—

130.6.a

comply with the duty or requirement, or

130.6.b

remedy the failure to comply with it.

130.7

A provisional notice of contravention may state that OFCOM propose to impose a
penalty on the person, and in such a case the notice must—

130.7.a

state the reasons why OFCOM propose to impose a penalty,

130.7.b

state whether OFCOM propose to impose a penalty of a single amount, a penalty
calculated by reference to a daily rate, or both penalties (see section 137
(1) ),

130.7.c

indicate the amount of a penalty that OFCOM propose to impose, including (in
relation to a penalty calculated by reference to a daily rate) the daily rate
and how the penalty would be calculated,

130.7.d

in relation to a penalty calculated by reference to a daily rate, specify or
describe the period for which OFCOM propose that the penalty should be
payable, and

130.7.e

state the reasons for proposing a penalty of that amount, including any
aggravating or mitigating factors that OFCOM propose to take into account.

130.8

A provisional notice of contravention given to a person must—

130.8.a

state that the person may make representations to OFCOM (with any supporting
evidence) about the matters contained in the notice, and

130.8.b

specify the period within which such representations may be made.

130.9

A provisional notice of contravention may be given in respect of a failure to
comply with more than one enforceable requirement.

130.10

Where a provisional notice of contravention is given in respect of a
continuing failure, the notice may be given in respect of any period during
which the failure has continued, and must specify that period.

130.11

Where a provisional notice of contravention is given to a person in respect of
a failure to comply with a duty or requirement (“the first notice”), a further
provisional notice of contravention in respect of a failure to comply with
that same duty or requirement may be given to the person only—

130.11.a

in respect of a separate instance of the failure after the first notice was
given,

130.11.b

where a period was specified in the first notice in accordance with subsection
(10) , in respect of the continuation of the failure after the end of that
period, or

130.11.c

if the first notice has been withdrawn (without a confirmation decision being
given to the person in respect of the failure).

###### Requirements enforceable by OFCOM against providers of regulated services

131

131.1

References in this Chapter to “enforceable requirements” are to—

131.1.a

the duties or requirements set out in the provisions of this Act specified in
the table in subsection  (2) , and

131.1.b

the requirements mentioned in subsection  (3) .

131.2

Here is the table—

        Provision Subject matter   Section 9 Illegal content risk assessments
Section 10 Illegal content Section 11 Children’s risk assessments Section 12
Children’s online safety Section 14 Assessments related to duty in section
15(2) Section 15 User empowerment Section 17 Content of democratic importance
Section 18 News publisher content Section 19 Journalistic content Section 20
Content reporting Section 21 Complaints procedures Section 22 Freedom of
expression and privacy Section 23 Record-keeping and review Section 26 Illegal
content risk assessments Section 27 Illegal content Section 28 Children’s risk
assessments Section 29 Children’s online safety Section 31 Content reporting
Section 32 Complaints procedures Section 33 Freedom of expression and privacy
Section 34 Record-keeping and review Section 36 Children’s access assessments
Section 38 Fraudulent advertising Section 39 Fraudulent advertising Section 64
User identity verification Section 66 Reporting CSEA content to NCA Section 71
Acting against users only in accordance with terms of service Section 72 Terms
of service Section 75 Information about use of service by deceased child users
Section 77 (3)  and  (4) Transparency reports Section 81 Provider pornographic
content Section 83 Fees: notification of OFCOM  Section 102 (8) Information
notices Section 104 (7) Assistance to skilled person Section 105 (1) Co-
operation with investigation

131.3

The requirements referred to in subsection  (1)(b)  are—

131.3.a

requirements of a notice under section 104 (5)(a)  to appoint a skilled
person;

131.3.b

requirements of a notice given by virtue of section 175 (3)  (duty to make
public statement);

131.3.c

requirements of a notice under section 175 (5)  (information in connection
with circumstances presenting a threat);

131.3.d

requirements imposed by a person acting—

131.3.d.i

in the exercise of powers conferred by paragraph  2  of Schedule 12 (entry and
inspection without warrant), or

131.3.d.ii

in the execution of a warrant issued under paragraph  5  of that Schedule.

###### Confirmation decisions

132

132.1

This section applies if—

132.1.a

OFCOM have given a provisional notice of contravention to a person in relation
to a failure to comply with a duty or requirement (or with duties or
requirements), and

132.1.b

the period allowed for representations has expired.

A duty or requirement to which the provisional notice of contravention relates
is referred to in this section as a “ notified requirement ”.

132.2

If, after considering any representations and evidence, OFCOM decide not to
give the person a notice under this section, they must inform the person of
that fact.

132.3

If OFCOM are satisfied that the person has failed, or has been failing, to
comply with a notified requirement, OFCOM may give the person a notice under
this section (a “confirmation decision”) confirming that that is OFCOM’s
opinion.

132.4

A confirmation decision and a notice under section 121 (1)  may be given in
respect of the same failure.

132.5

A confirmation decision given to a person may—

132.5.a

require the person to take steps as mentioned in section 133;

132.5.b

require the person to pay a penalty as mentioned in section 137;

132.5.c

require the person to do both those things (or neither of them).

132.6

See sections 134 and 135 for further provision which a confirmation decision
may include in cases of failure to comply with duties about risk assessments
or children’s access assessments.

###### Confirmation decisions: requirements to take steps

133

133.1

A confirmation decision may require the person to whom it is given to take
such steps as OFCOM consider appropriate (including steps relating to the use
of a system or process) for either or both of the following purposes—

133.1.a

complying with a notified requirement;

133.1.b

remedying the failure to comply with a notified requirement.

133.2

But see section 136 in relation to OFCOM’s power to include in a confirmation
decision requirements as described in subsection  (1)  relating to the use of
proactive technology.

133.3

A confirmation decision may impose requirements as described in subsection
(1)  only in relation to the design or operation of a regulated service—

133.3.a

in the United Kingdom, or

133.3.b

as it affects United Kingdom users of the service.

133.4

A confirmation decision that includes requirements as described in subsection
(1)  must—

133.4.a

specify the steps that are required,

133.4.b

give OFCOM’s reasons for their decision to impose those requirements,

133.4.c

specify which of those requirements (if any) have been designated as CSEA
requirements (see subsections  (6)  and  (7) ),

133.4.d

specify each notified requirement to which the steps relate,

133.4.e

specify the period during which the failure to comply with a notified
requirement has occurred, and whether the failure is continuing,

133.4.f

specify a reasonable period within which each of the steps specified in the
decision must be taken or, if a step requires the use of a system or process,
a reasonable period within which the system or process must begin to be used
(but see subsection  (5)  in relation to information duties),

133.4.g

(if relevant) specify the period for which a system or process must be used,

133.4.h

contain details of the rights of appeal under section 168, and

133.4.i

contain information about the consequences of not complying with the
requirements included in the decision (including information about the further
kinds of enforcement action that it would be open to OFCOM to take).

133.5

A confirmation decision that requires a person to take steps for the purpose
of complying with an information duty may require the person to take those
steps immediately.

133.6

If the condition in subsection  (7)  is met in relation to a requirement
imposed by a confirmation decision which is of a kind described in subsection
(1), OFCOM must designate the requirement as a “ CSEA requirement ” for the
purposes of section 138(3) (offence of failure to comply with confirmation
decision).

133.7

The condition referred to in subsection  (6)  is that the requirement is
imposed (whether or not exclusively) in relation to either or both of the
following—

133.7.a

a failure to comply with section 10(2)(a) or (3)(a) in respect of CSEA
content, or in respect of priority illegal content which includes CSEA
content;

133.7.b

a failure to comply with section 10(2)(b) in respect of an offence specified
in Schedule 6 (CSEA offences), or in respect of priority offences which
include such an offence.

133.8

A person to whom a confirmation decision is given has a duty to comply with
requirements included in the decision which are of a kind described in
subsection  (1) .

133.9

The duty under subsection  (8)  is enforceable in civil proceedings by OFCOM—

133.9.a

for an injunction,

133.9.b

for specific performance of a statutory duty under section 45 of the Court of
Session Act 1988, or

133.9.c

for any other appropriate remedy or relief.

133.10

In this section—

      “ CSEA content ”, “ priority illegal content ” and “ priority offence ”
have the same meaning as in Part 3 (see section 59);           “ information
duty ” means a duty set out in section 102 (8) ;           “ notified
requirement ” has the meaning given by section 132.

###### Confirmation decisions: risk assessments

134

134.1

This section applies if—

134.1.a

OFCOM are satisfied that a provider of a Part 3 service has failed to comply
with a risk assessment duty,

134.1.b

based on evidence resulting from OFCOM’s investigation into that failure,
OFCOM have identified a risk of serious harm to individuals in the United
Kingdom arising from a particular aspect of the service (“the identified
risk”), and

134.1.c

OFCOM consider that the identified risk is not effectively mitigated or
managed.

134.2

A confirmation decision given to the provider of the service—

134.2.a

if the identified risk relates to matters required to be covered by an illegal
content risk assessment, may include a determination that the duty set out in
section 10 (2) (b) or (c) or 27 (2)  (as the case may be) applies as if an
illegal content risk assessment carried out by the provider had identified
that risk;

134.2.b

if the identified risk relates to matters required to be covered by a
children’s risk assessment, may include a determination that the duty set out
in section 12 (2)(a)  or 29 (2)(a)  (as the case may be) applies as if a
children’s risk assessment carried out by the provider had identified that
risk.

134.3

A confirmation decision which includes a determination as mentioned in
subsection  (2)  must—

134.3.a

give details of the identified risk,

134.3.b

specify the duty to which the determination relates, and

134.3.c

specify the date by which measures (at the provider’s discretion) to comply
with that duty must be taken or must begin to be used.

134.4

A determination as mentioned in subsection  (2)  ceases to have effect on the
date on which the provider of the service complies with the risk assessment
duty with which the provider had previously failed to comply (and accordingly,
from that date the duty to which the determination relates applies without the
modification mentioned in that subsection).

134.5

In this section—

      “ children’s risk assessment ” has the meaning given by section 11 or 28
(as the case may be);           “ illegal content risk assessment ” has the
meaning given by section 9 or 26 (as the case may be);           “ risk
assessment duty ” means a duty set out in—         section 9,
section 11,           section 26, or           section 28.

###### Confirmation decisions: children’s access assessments

135

135.1

This section applies if OFCOM are satisfied that a provider of a Part 3
service has failed to comply with a duty set out in section 36 (duties about
children’s access assessments).

135.2

If OFCOM include in a confirmation decision a requirement to take steps
relating to the carrying out of a children’s access assessment of a service,
they must require that assessment to be completed within three months of the
date of the confirmation decision.

135.3

OFCOM may vary a confirmation decision which includes a requirement as
mentioned in subsection  (2)  to extend the deadline for completion of a
children’s access assessment.

135.4

Subsection  (5)  applies if, based on evidence that OFCOM have about a service
resulting from their investigation into compliance with a duty set out in
section 36, OFCOM consider that—

135.4.a

it is possible for children to access the service or a part of it, and

135.4.b

the child user condition is met in relation to—

135.4.b.i

the service, or

135.4.b.ii

a part of the service that it is possible for children to access.

135.5

OFCOM may include in the confirmation decision given to the provider of the
service—

135.5.a

a determination that the duties set out in sections 11 and 12, or (as the case
may be) sections 28 and 29, must be complied with—

135.5.a.i

from the date of the confirmation decision, or

135.5.a.ii

from a later date specified in that decision;

135.5.b

provision about the circumstances in which that determination may be treated
as no longer applying in relation to the service.

135.6

Subsection  (4)  is to be interpreted consistently with section 35.

135.7

In this section, “ children’s access assessment ” has the meaning given by
section 35.

###### Confirmation decisions: proactive technology

136

136.1

This section sets out what powers OFCOM have to include in a confirmation
decision a requirement to take steps to use a kind, or one of the kinds, of
proactive technology specified in the decision (a “proactive technology
requirement”).

136.2

A proactive technology requirement may be imposed in a confirmation decision
if—

136.2.a

the decision is given to the provider of an internet service within section
80(2), and

136.2.b

the decision is imposed for the purpose of complying with, or remedying the
failure to comply with, the duty set out in section 81(2) (provider
pornographic content).

136.3

The following provisions of this section set out constraints on OFCOM’s power
to include a proactive technology requirement in a confirmation decision in
any case not within subsection  (2) .

136.4

A proactive technology requirement may be imposed in a confirmation decision
only if the decision is given to the provider of a Part 3 service.

136.5

A proactive technology requirement may be imposed in a confirmation decision
only for the purpose of complying with, or remedying the failure to comply
with, any of the duties set out in—

136.5.a

section 10 (2)  or  (3)  (illegal content),

136.5.b

section 12 (2)  or  (3)  (children’s online safety),

136.5.c

section 27 (2)  or  (3)  (illegal content),

136.5.d

section 29 (2)  or  (3)  (children’s online safety), or

136.5.e

section 38 (1)  or 39 (1)  (fraudulent advertising).

136.6

Proactive technology may be required to be used on or in relation to any Part
3 service or any part of such a service, but if and to the extent that the
technology operates (or may operate) by analysing content that is user-
generated content in relation to the service, or metadata relating to such
content, the technology may not be required to be used except to analyse—

136.6.a

user-generated content communicated publicly, and

136.6.b

metadata relating to user-generated content communicated publicly.

136.7

Before imposing a proactive technology requirement in relation to a service in
a confirmation decision, OFCOM must particularly consider the matters
mentioned in subsection  (8) , so far as they are relevant.

136.8

The matters are as follows—

136.8.a

the kind of service it is;

136.8.b

the functionalities of the service;

136.8.c

the user base of the service;

136.8.d

the prevalence of relevant content on the service and the extent of its
dissemination by means of the service, or (as the case may be) the prevalence
of search content of the service that is relevant content;

136.8.e

the level of risk of harm to individuals in the United Kingdom presented by
relevant content present on the service, or (as the case may be) search
content of the service that is relevant content, and the severity of that
harm;

136.8.f

the degree of accuracy, effectiveness and lack of bias achieved by the kind of
technology specified in the decision;

136.8.g

the extent to which the use of the kind of proactive technology specified in
the decision would or might result in interference with users’ right to
freedom of expression within the law;

136.8.h

the level of risk of the use of the kind of proactive technology specified in
the decision resulting in a breach of any statutory provision or rule of law
concerning privacy that is relevant to the use or operation of the service
(including, but not limited to, any such provision or rule concerning the
processing of personal data);

136.8.i

whether the use of any less intrusive measures than the proactive technology
specified in the decision would be likely to result in compliance with, or
would be likely to effectively remedy the failure to comply with, the duty in
question.

136.9

A confirmation decision that imposes a proactive technology requirement on a
provider may also impose requirements about review of the technology by the
provider.

136.10

A confirmation decision relating to a service which requires the use of
technology of a kind mentioned in subsection  (6)  must identify the content,
or parts of the service that include content, that OFCOM consider is
communicated publicly on that service (see section 232).

136.11

In this section—

      “ content that is harmful to children ” has the same meaning as in Part
3 (see section 60);           “ fraudulent advertisement ” has the meaning
given by section 38 or 39 (depending on the kind of service in question);
“ illegal content ” has the same meaning as in Part 3 (see section 59);
“ relevant content ” means illegal content, content that is harmful to
children or content consisting of fraudulent advertisements, or any or all of
those kinds of content (depending on the duties (as mentioned in subsection
(5) ) for the purposes of which the proactive technology requirement is
imposed);           “ search content ” has the same meaning as in Part 3 (see
section 57);           “ user-generated content ” has the meaning given by
section 55 (see subsections (3) and (4) of that section).

###### Confirmation decisions: penalties

137

137.1

A confirmation decision may require the person to whom it is given to do
either or both of the following, depending on what was proposed in the
provisional notice of contravention (see paragraph 3 of Schedule 13)—

137.1.a

pay to OFCOM a penalty of a single amount in sterling determined by OFCOM (a
“single penalty”) and specified in the confirmation decision;

137.1.b

if the confirmation decision includes a requirement of the kind described in
section 133 (1)(a)  in respect of a continuous failure to comply with a
notified requirement, pay a daily rate penalty to OFCOM if that same failure
continues after the compliance date.

137.2

A “ daily rate penalty ” means a penalty of an amount in sterling determined
by OFCOM and calculated by reference to a daily rate.

137.3

A confirmation decision may impose separate single penalties for failure to
comply with separate notified requirements specified in the decision.

137.4

Where a provisional notice of contravention is given in respect of a period of
continuing failure to comply with a notified requirement, no more than one
single penalty may be imposed by a confirmation decision in respect of the
period of failure specified in the provisional notice of contravention.

137.5

A confirmation decision that imposes a penalty must—

137.5.a

give OFCOM’s reasons for their decision to impose the penalty,

137.5.b

specify each notified requirement to which the penalty relates,

137.5.c

specify the period during which the failure to comply with a notified
requirement has occurred, and whether the failure is continuing,

137.5.d

state the reasons for the amount of the penalty, including any aggravating or
mitigating factors that OFCOM have taken into account,

137.5.e

specify a reasonable period within which the penalty must be paid,

137.5.f

contain details of the rights of appeal under section 168, and

137.5.g

contain information about the consequences of not paying the penalty
(including information about the further kinds of enforcement action that it
would be open to OFCOM to take).

137.6

The period specified under subsection  (5)(e)  for the payment of a single
penalty must be at least 28 days beginning with the day on which the
confirmation decision is given.

137.7

If a confirmation decision imposes a single penalty and a daily rate penalty,
the information mentioned in subsection  (5)(a) ,  (b) ,  (d)  and  (e)  must
be given in respect of each kind of penalty.

137.8

As well as containing the information mentioned in subsection  (5) , a
confirmation decision that imposes a daily rate penalty in respect of a
continuous failure to comply with a notified requirement must—

137.8.a

state the daily rate of the penalty and how the penalty is calculated;

137.8.b

state that the person will be liable to pay the penalty if that same failure
continues after the compliance date;

137.8.c

state the date from which the penalty begins to be payable, which must not be
earlier than the day after the compliance date;

137.8.d

provide for the penalty to continue to be payable at the daily rate until—

137.8.d.i

the date on which the notified requirement is complied with,

137.8.d.ii

if the penalty is imposed in respect of a failure to comply with more than one
notified requirement, the date on which the last of those requirements is
complied with, or

137.8.d.iii

an earlier date specified in the confirmation decision.

137.9

In this section—
