      “ compliance date ”, in relation to a notified requirement, means—
in a case where the confirmation decision requires steps to be taken
immediately to comply with that requirement (see section 133 (5) ), the date
of the confirmation decision;           in any other case, the last day of the
period specified in the confirmation decision in accordance with section 133
(4)(f)  for compliance with that requirement;                 “ notified
requirement ” has the meaning given by section 132.

###### Confirmation decisions: offences

138

138.1

A person to whom a confirmation decision is given commits an offence if,
without reasonable excuse, the person fails to comply with a requirement
imposed by the decision which—

138.1.a

is of a kind described in section 133(1), and

138.1.b

is imposed (whether or not exclusively) in relation to a failure to comply
with a children’s online safety duty.

138.2

A “ children’s online safety duty ” means a duty set out in—

138.2.a

section 12(3)(a),

138.2.b

section 12(3)(b),

138.2.c

section 81(2), or

138.2.d

section 81 (4) .

138.3

A person to whom a confirmation decision is given commits an offence if,
without reasonable excuse, the person fails to comply with a CSEA requirement
imposed by the decision (see section 133(6) and (7)).

138.4

A person who commits an offence under this section is liable—

138.4.a

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding the general limit in a magistrates’ court or a fine (or both);

138.4.b

on summary conviction in Scotland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 12
months or a fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both);

138.4.c

on summary conviction in Northern Ireland, to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding 6 months or a fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both);

138.4.d

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 2 years
or a fine (or both).

##### Penalty notices etc

###### Penalty for failure to comply with confirmation decision

139

139.1

This section applies if—

139.1.a

OFCOM have given a confirmation decision to a person,

139.1.b

the decision includes requirements of a kind described in section 133 (1)
(requirements to take steps),

139.1.c

OFCOM are satisfied that the person has failed to comply with one or more of
those requirements, and

139.1.d

OFCOM have not imposed a daily rate penalty under section 137 (1)(b)  in
respect of that failure.

139.2

OFCOM may give the person a penalty notice under this section in respect of
the failure to comply with the confirmation decision, requiring the person to
pay to OFCOM a penalty of a single amount in sterling determined by OFCOM.

139.3

But OFCOM may give such a notice to the person only after—

139.3.a

notifying the person that they propose to give a penalty notice under this
section, specifying the reasons for doing so and indicating the amount of the
proposed penalty, and

139.3.b

giving the person an opportunity to make representations (with any supporting
evidence).

139.4

A penalty notice under this section must—

139.4.a

give OFCOM’s reasons for their decision to impose the penalty,

139.4.b

state the amount of the penalty,

139.4.c

state the reasons for the amount of the penalty, including any aggravating or
mitigating factors that OFCOM have taken into account,

139.4.d

specify the period within which the penalty must be paid,

139.4.e

contain details of the rights of appeal under section 168, and

139.4.f

contain information about the consequences of not paying the penalty
(including information about the further kinds of enforcement action that it
would be open to OFCOM to take).

139.5

The period specified under subsection  (4)(d)  must be at least 28 days
beginning with the day on which the penalty notice is given.

###### Penalty for failure to comply with notice under section 121

140

140.1

This section applies if—

140.1.a

OFCOM have given a notice under section 121 (1)  relating to a Part 3 service
to the provider of that service (notices to deal with terrorism content and
CSEA content), and

140.1.b

OFCOM are satisfied that the provider has failed, or is failing, to comply
with the notice.

140.2

OFCOM may give the provider a notice under this subsection stating that they
propose to impose a penalty on the provider in respect of that failure.

140.3

The provider may make representations to OFCOM (with any supporting evidence)
about the matters contained in the notice.

140.4

Subsection  (5)  applies if—

140.4.a

the period allowed for representations has expired, and

140.4.b

OFCOM are still satisfied as to the failure mentioned in subsection  (1) .

140.5

OFCOM may give the provider a penalty notice under this subsection requiring
the provider to pay to OFCOM a penalty of an amount in sterling determined by
OFCOM.

140.6

The penalty may consist of any of the following, depending on what was
specified in the notice about the proposed penalty—

140.6.a

a single amount;

140.6.b

an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate;

140.6.c

a combination of a single amount and an amount calculated by reference to a
daily rate.

140.7

See section 142 for information which must be included in notices under this
section.

140.8

Nothing in this section is to be taken to prevent OFCOM from giving the
provider a further notice under section 121 (1)  (see section 126), as well as
giving a penalty notice under subsection  (5) .

###### Non-payment of fee

141

141.1

This section applies if—

141.1.a

the provider of a regulated service is liable to pay a fee to OFCOM under
section 84 or Schedule 10 in respect of the current charging year (within the
meaning of Part 6) or a previous charging year, and

141.1.b

in OFCOM’s opinion, the provider has not paid the full amount of the fee that
the provider is liable to pay.

141.2

OFCOM may give the provider a notice under this subsection specifying—

141.2.a

the outstanding amount of the fee that OFCOM consider the provider is due to
pay to them under section 84 or Schedule 10, and

141.2.b

the period within which the provider must pay it.

141.3

A notice under subsection  (2) —

141.3.a

may be given in respect of liabilities that relate to different charging
years;

141.3.b

may also state that OFCOM propose to impose a penalty on the provider.

141.4

The provider may make representations to OFCOM (with any supporting evidence)
about the matters contained in the notice.

141.5

Subsection  (6)  applies if—

141.5.a

the notice under subsection  (2)  stated that OFCOM propose to impose a
penalty,

141.5.b

the period allowed for representations has expired, and

141.5.c

OFCOM are satisfied that an amount of the fee is still due to them.

141.6

OFCOM may give the provider a penalty notice under this subsection requiring
the provider to pay to OFCOM a penalty of an amount in sterling determined by
OFCOM.

141.7

The penalty may consist of any of the following, depending on what was
specified in the notice about the proposed penalty—

141.7.a

a single amount;

141.7.b

an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate;

141.7.c

a combination of a single amount and an amount calculated by reference to a
daily rate.

141.8

A penalty notice under subsection  (6)  may require the payment of separate
single amounts in respect of liabilities that relate to different charging
years.

141.9

See section 142 for information which must be included in notices under this
section.

141.10

Nothing in this section affects OFCOM’s power to bring proceedings (whether
before or after the imposition of a penalty by a notice under subsection  (6)
) for the recovery of the whole or part of an amount due to OFCOM under
section 84 or Schedule 10.

141.11

But OFCOM may not bring such proceedings unless a provider has first been
given a notice under subsection  (2)  specifying the amount due to OFCOM.

###### Information to be included in notices under sections 140 and 141

142

142.1

Subsection  (2)  applies in relation to—

142.1.a

a notice under section 140 (2) , and

142.1.b

a notice under section 141 (2)  stating that OFCOM propose to impose a
penalty.

142.2

Such a notice must—

142.2.a

state the reasons why OFCOM propose to impose the penalty,

142.2.b

state whether OFCOM propose that the penalty should consist of a single
amount, an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, or a combination of
the two,

142.2.c

indicate the amount of the proposed penalty, including (in relation to an
amount calculated by reference to a daily rate) the daily rate and how the
penalty would be calculated,

142.2.d

in relation to an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, specify or
describe the period for which OFCOM propose that the amount should be payable,

142.2.e

state the reasons for proposing a penalty of that amount, including any
aggravating or mitigating factors that OFCOM propose to take into account, and

142.2.f

specify the period within which representations in relation to the proposed
penalty may be made.

142.3

A penalty notice under section 140 (5)  or 141 (6)  must—

142.3.a

give OFCOM’s reasons for their decision to impose the penalty,

142.3.b

state whether the penalty consists of a single amount, an amount calculated by
reference to a daily rate, or a combination of the two, and how it is
calculated,

142.3.c

in relation to a single amount, state that amount,

142.3.d

in relation to an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, state the
daily rate,

142.3.e

state the reasons for the amount of the penalty, including any aggravating or
mitigating factors that OFCOM have taken into account,

142.3.f

specify a reasonable period within which the penalty must be paid,

142.3.g

contain details of the rights of appeal under section 168, and

142.3.h

contain information about the consequences of not paying the penalty
(including information about the further kinds of enforcement action that it
would be open to OFCOM to take).

142.4

A penalty notice under section 141 (6)  must also specify the amount of the
fee that is (in OFCOM’s opinion) due to be paid to OFCOM.

142.5

The period specified under subsection  (3)(f) for the payment of a single
amount must be at least 28 days beginning with the day on which the penalty
notice is given.

142.6

Subsection  (7)  applies in relation to a penalty notice under section 140 (5)
or 141 (6)  that includes a requirement to pay an amount calculated by
reference to a daily rate.

142.7

Such a notice must—

142.7.a

state the date from which the amount begins to be payable, which must not be
earlier than the day after the day on which the notice is given;

142.7.b

provide for the amount to continue to be payable at the daily rate until—

142.7.b.i

(in the case of a notice under section 140 (5) ) the date on which OFCOM are
satisfied that the provider is complying with the notice under section 121 (1)
, or (in the case of a notice under section 141 (6) ) the date on which the
full amount of the fee (as specified in the penalty notice) has been paid to
OFCOM, or

142.7.b.ii

an earlier date specified in the penalty notice.

##### Amount of penalties etc

###### Amount of penalties etc

143

Schedule 13 contains provision about the amount of penalties that OFCOM may
impose under this Chapter, and makes further provision about such penalties.

##### Business disruption measures

###### Service restriction orders

144

144.1

OFCOM may apply to the court for an order under this section (a “service
restriction order”) in relation to a regulated service where they consider
that—

144.1.a

the grounds in subsection  (3)  apply in relation to the service, or

144.1.b

in the case of a Part 3 service, the grounds in subsection  (4)  apply in
relation to the service.

144.2

A service restriction order is an order imposing requirements on one or more
persons who provide an ancillary service (whether from within or outside the
United Kingdom) in relation to a regulated service (see subsection  (11) ).

144.3

The grounds mentioned in subsection  (1)(a)  are that—

144.3.a

the provider of the regulated service has failed to comply with an enforceable
requirement that applies in relation to the regulated service,

144.3.b

the failure is continuing, and

144.3.c

any of the following applies—

144.3.c.i

the provider has failed to comply with a requirement imposed by a confirmation
decision that is of a kind described in section 133 (1)  relating to the
failure;

144.3.c.ii

the provider has failed to pay a penalty imposed by a confirmation decision
relating to the failure (and the confirmation decision did not impose any
requirements of a kind described in section 133 (1) );

144.3.c.iii

the provider would be likely to fail to comply with requirements imposed by a
confirmation decision if given;

144.3.c.iv

the circumstances of the failure or the risks of harm to individuals in the
United Kingdom are such that it is appropriate to make the application without
having given a provisional notice of contravention, without having given a
confirmation decision, or (having given a confirmation decision imposing
requirements) without waiting to ascertain compliance with those requirements.

144.4

The grounds mentioned in subsection  (1)(b)  are that—

144.4.a

the provider of the Part 3 service has failed to comply with a notice under
section 121 (1)  that relates to the service (notices to deal with terrorism
content and CSEA content), and

144.4.b

the failure is continuing.

144.5

An application by OFCOM for a service restriction order must—

144.5.a

specify the regulated service in relation to which the application is made (“
the relevant service ”),

144.5.b

specify the provider of that service (“the non-compliant provider”),

144.5.c

specify the grounds on which the application is based, and contain evidence
about those grounds,

144.5.d

specify the persons on whom (in OFCOM’s opinion) the requirements of the order
should be imposed,

144.5.e

contain evidence as to why OFCOM consider that the persons mentioned in
paragraph  (d)  provide an ancillary service in relation to the relevant
service, and specify any such ancillary service provided,

144.5.f

specify the requirements which OFCOM consider that the order should impose on
such persons, and

144.5.g

in the case of an application made without notice having been given to the
non-compliant provider, or to the persons mentioned in paragraph  (d) , state
why no notice has been given.

144.6

The court may make a service restriction order imposing requirements on a
person in relation to the relevant service if the court is satisfied—

144.6.a

as to the grounds in subsection  (3)  or the grounds in subsection  (4)  (as
the case may be),

144.6.b

that the person provides an ancillary service in relation to the relevant
service,

144.6.c

that it is appropriate to make the order for the purpose of preventing harm to
individuals in the United Kingdom, and the order is proportionate to the risk
of such harm,

144.6.d

in the case of an application made on the ground in subsection  (3)(c)(iii)
or  (iv) , that it is appropriate to make the order before a provisional
notice of contravention or confirmation decision has been given, or before
compliance with requirements imposed by a confirmation decision has been
ascertained (as the case may be), and

144.6.e

if no notice of the application has been given to the non-compliant provider,
or to the persons on whom requirements are being imposed, that it is
appropriate to make the order without notice.

144.7

When considering whether to make a service restriction order in relation to
the relevant service, and when considering what provision it should contain,
the court must take into account (among other things) the rights and
obligations of all relevant parties, including those of—

144.7.a

the non-compliant provider,

144.7.b

the person or persons on whom the court is considering imposing the
requirements, and

144.7.c

United Kingdom users of the relevant service.

144.8

A service restriction order made in relation to the relevant service must—

144.8.a

identify the non-compliant provider,

144.8.b

identify the persons on whom the requirements are imposed, and any ancillary
service to which the requirements relate,

144.8.c

require such persons to take the steps specified in the order, or to put in
place arrangements, that have the effect of withdrawing the ancillary service
to the extent that it relates to the relevant service (or part of it), or
preventing the ancillary service from promoting or displaying content that
relates to the relevant service (or part of it) in any way,

144.8.d

specify the date by which the requirements in the order must be complied with,
and

144.8.e

specify the date on which the order expires, or the period for which the order
has effect.

144.9

The steps that may be specified or arrangements that may be required to be put
in place—

144.9.a

include steps or arrangements that will or may require the termination of an
agreement (whether or not made before the coming into force of this section),
or the prohibition of the performance of such an agreement, and

144.9.b

are limited, so far as that is possible, to steps or arrangements relating to
the operation of the relevant service as it affects United Kingdom users.

144.10

OFCOM must inform the Secretary of State as soon as reasonably practicable
after a service restriction order has been made.

144.11

For the purposes of this section, a service is an “ ancillary service ” in
relation to a regulated service if the service facilitates the provision of
the regulated service (or part of it), whether directly or indirectly, or
displays or promotes content relating to the regulated service (or to part of
it).

144.12

Examples of ancillary services include—

144.12.a

services, provided (directly or indirectly) in the course of a business, which
enable funds to be transferred in relation to a regulated service,

144.12.b

search engines which generate search results displaying or promoting content
relating to a regulated service,

144.12.c

user-to-user services which make content relating to a regulated service
available to users, and

144.12.d

services which use technology to facilitate the display of advertising on a
regulated service (for example, an ad server or an ad network).

144.13

In this section “ the court ” means—

144.13.a

in England and Wales, the High Court or the county court,

144.13.b

in Scotland, the Court of Session or a sheriff, and

144.13.c

in Northern Ireland, the High Court or a county court.

###### Interim service restriction orders

145

145.1

OFCOM may apply to the court for an interim order under this section (an
“interim service restriction order”) in relation to a regulated service where
they consider that—

145.1.a

the grounds in subsection  (3)  apply in relation to the service, or

145.1.b

in the case of a Part 3 service, the grounds in subsection  (4)  apply in
relation to the service.

145.2

An interim service restriction order is an interim order imposing requirements
on one or more persons who provide an ancillary service (whether from within
or outside the United Kingdom) in relation to a regulated service (see
subsection  (9) ).

145.3

The grounds mentioned in subsection  (1)(a)  are that—

145.3.a

it is likely that the provider of the regulated service is failing to comply
with an enforceable requirement that applies in relation to the regulated
service, and

145.3.b

the level of risk of harm to individuals in the United Kingdom relating to the
likely failure, and the nature and severity of that harm, are such that it
would not be appropriate to wait to establish the failure before applying for
the order.

145.4

The grounds mentioned in subsection  (1)(b)  are that—

145.4.a

it is likely that the provider of the Part 3 service is failing to comply with
a notice under section 121 (1)  that relates to the service (notices to deal
with terrorism content and CSEA content), and

145.4.b

the level of risk of harm to individuals in the United Kingdom relating to the
likely failure, and the nature and severity of that harm, are such that it
would not be appropriate to wait to establish the failure before applying for
the order.

145.5

An application by OFCOM for an interim service restriction order must—

145.5.a

specify the regulated service in relation to which the application is made (“
the relevant service ”),

145.5.b

specify the provider of that service (“the non-compliant provider”),

145.5.c

specify the grounds on which the application is based, and contain evidence
about those grounds,

145.5.d

specify the persons on whom (in OFCOM’s opinion) the requirements of the order
should be imposed,

145.5.e

contain evidence as to why OFCOM consider that the persons mentioned in
paragraph  (d)  provide an ancillary service in relation to the relevant
service, and specify any such ancillary service provided,

145.5.f

specify the requirements which OFCOM consider that the order should impose on
such persons, and

145.5.g

in the case of an application made without notice having been given to the
non-compliant provider, or to the persons mentioned in paragraph  (d) , state
why no notice has been given.

145.6

The court may make an interim service restriction order imposing requirements
on a person in relation to the relevant service if the court is satisfied—

145.6.a

as to the ground in subsection  (3) (a)  or the ground in subsection  (4) (a)
(as the case may be),

145.6.b

that the person provides an ancillary service in relation to the relevant
service,

145.6.c

that there are prima facie grounds to suggest that an application for a
service restriction order under section 144 would be successful,

145.6.d

that the level of risk of harm to individuals in the United Kingdom relating
to the likely failure mentioned in subsection  (3)(a)  or  (4)(a)  (whichever
applies), and the nature and severity of that harm, are such that it is not
appropriate to wait for the failure to be established before making the order,
and

145.6.e

if no notice of the application has been given to the non-compliant provider,
or to the persons on whom requirements are being imposed, that it is
appropriate to make the order without notice.

145.7

An interim service restriction order ceases to have effect on the earlier of—

145.7.a

the date specified in the order, or the date on which the period specified in
the order expires (as the case may be), and

145.7.b

the date on which the court makes a service restriction order under section
144 in relation to the relevant service that imposes requirements on the same
persons on whom requirements are imposed by the interim order, or dismisses
the application for such an order.

145.8

Subsections  (7)  to  (10)  of section 144 apply in relation to an interim
service restriction order under this section as they apply in relation to a
service restriction order under that section.

145.9

In this section, “ ancillary service ” and “ the court ” have the same meaning
as in section 144 (see subsections  (11) ,  (12)  and  (13)  of that section).

###### Access restriction orders

146

146.1

OFCOM may apply to the court for an order under this section (an “access
restriction order”) in relation to a regulated service where they consider
that—

146.1.a

the grounds in section 144 (3)  or  (4)  apply in relation to the service, and

146.1.b

either—

146.1.b.i

a service restriction order under section 144 or an interim service
restriction order under section 145 has been made in relation to the failure,
and it was not sufficient to prevent significant harm arising to individuals
in the United Kingdom as a result of the failure, or

146.1.b.ii

the likely consequences of the failure are such that if a service restriction
order or an interim service restriction order were to be made, it would be
unlikely to be sufficient to prevent significant harm arising to individuals
in the United Kingdom as a result of the failure,

and in this paragraph, “ the failure ” means the failure mentioned in section
144 (3)(a)  or  (4)(a)  (as the case may be).

146.2

An access restriction order is an order imposing requirements on one or more
persons who provide an access facility (whether from within or outside the
United Kingdom) in relation to a regulated service (see subsection  (10) ).

146.3

An application by OFCOM for an access restriction order must—

146.3.a

specify the regulated service in relation to which the application is made (“
the relevant service ”),

146.3.b

specify the provider of that service (“the non-compliant provider”),

146.3.c

specify the grounds on which the application is based, and contain evidence
about those grounds,

146.3.d

specify the persons on whom (in OFCOM’s opinion) the requirements of the order
should be imposed,

146.3.e

contain evidence as to why OFCOM consider that the persons mentioned in
paragraph  (d)  provide an access facility in relation to the relevant
service, and specify any such access facility provided,

146.3.f

specify the requirements which OFCOM consider that the order should impose on
such persons, and

146.3.g

in the case of an application made without notice having been given to the
non-compliant provider, or to the persons mentioned in paragraph  (d) , state
why no notice has been given.

146.4

The court may make an access restriction order imposing requirements on a
person in relation to the relevant service if the court is satisfied—

146.4.a

as to the grounds in subsection  (1) ,

146.4.b

that the person provides an access facility in relation to the relevant
service,

146.4.c

that it is appropriate to make the order for the purpose of preventing
significant harm to individuals in the United Kingdom, and the order is
proportionate to the risk of such harm,

146.4.d

in the case of an application made on the ground in subsection  (3)(c)(iii)
or  (iv)  of section 144 (by virtue of subsection (1)(a)), that it is
appropriate to make the order before a provisional notice of contravention or
confirmation decision has been given, or before compliance with requirements
imposed by a confirmation decision has been ascertained (as the case may be),
and

146.4.e

if no notice of the application has been given to the non-compliant provider,
or to the persons on whom requirements are being imposed, that it is
appropriate to make the order without notice.

146.5

When considering whether to make an access restriction order in relation to
the relevant service, and when considering what provision it should contain,
the court must take into account (among other things) the rights and
obligations of all relevant parties, including those of—

146.5.a

the non-compliant provider,

146.5.b

the person or persons on whom the court is considering imposing the
requirements, and

146.5.c

United Kingdom users of the relevant service.

146.6

An access restriction order made in relation to the relevant service must—

146.6.a

identify the non-compliant provider,

146.6.b

identify the persons on whom the requirements are imposed, and any access
facility to which the requirements relate,

146.6.c

require such persons to take the steps specified in the order, or to put in
place arrangements, to withdraw, adapt or manipulate the access facility in
order to impede users’ access (by means of that facility) to the relevant
service (or to part of it),

146.6.d

specify the date by which the requirements in the order must be complied with,
and

146.6.e

specify the date on which the order expires, or the period for which the order
has effect.

146.7

The steps that may be specified or arrangements that may be required to be put
in place—

146.7.a

include steps or arrangements that will or may require the termination of an
agreement (whether or not made before the coming into force of this section),
or the prohibition of the performance of such an agreement,

146.7.b

are limited, so far as that is possible, to steps or arrangements that impede
the access of United Kingdom users, and

146.7.c

are limited, so far as that is possible, to steps or arrangements that do not
affect such users’ ability to access any other internet services.

146.8

OFCOM must inform the Secretary of State as soon as reasonably practicable
after an access restriction order has been made.

146.9

Where a person who provides an access facility takes steps or puts in place
arrangements required by an access restriction order, OFCOM may, by notice,
require that person to (where possible) notify persons in the United Kingdom
who attempt to access the relevant service via that facility of the access
restriction order (and where a confirmation decision has been given to the
non-compliant provider, the notification must refer to that decision).

146.10

For the purposes of this section, a facility is an “ access facility ” in
relation to a regulated service if the person who provides the facility is
able to withdraw, adapt or manipulate it in such a way as to impede access (by
means of that facility) to the regulated service (or to part of it) by United
Kingdom users of that service.

146.11

Examples of access facilities include—

146.11.a

internet access services by means of which a regulated service is made
available, and

146.11.b

app stores through which a mobile app for a regulated service may be
downloaded or otherwise accessed.

146.12

In this section—

      “ the court ” means—         in England and Wales, the High Court or the
county court,           in Scotland, the Court of Session or a sheriff, and
in Northern Ireland, the High Court or a county court;                 “
facility ” means any kind of service, infrastructure or apparatus enabling
users of a regulated service to access the regulated service;           “
internet access service ” means a service that provides access to virtually
all (or just some) of the end points of the internet.

###### Interim access restriction orders

147

147.1

OFCOM may apply to the court for an interim order under this section (an
“interim access restriction order”) in relation to a regulated service where
they consider that—

147.1.a

the grounds in section 145 (3)  or  (4)  apply in relation to the service, and

147.1.b

either—

147.1.b.i

a service restriction order under section 144 or an interim service
restriction order under section 145 has been made in relation to the likely
failure, and it was not sufficient to prevent significant harm arising to
individuals in the United Kingdom as a result of the failure, or

147.1.b.ii

the likely consequences of such a failure would be such that if a service
restriction order or an interim service restriction order were to be made, it
would be unlikely to be sufficient to prevent significant harm arising to
individuals in the United Kingdom as a result of the failure,

and in this section, “ the likely failure ” means the likely failure mentioned
in section 145 (3)(a)  or  (4)(a)  (as the case may be).

147.2

An interim access restriction order is an interim order imposing requirements
on one or more persons who provide an access facility (whether from within or
outside the United Kingdom) in relation to a regulated service (see subsection
(8) ).

147.3

An application by OFCOM for an interim access restriction order must—

147.3.a

specify the regulated service in relation to which the application is made (“
the relevant service ”),

147.3.b

specify the provider of that service (“the non-compliant provider”),

147.3.c

specify the grounds on which the application is based, and contain evidence
about those grounds,

147.3.d

specify the persons on whom (in OFCOM’s opinion) the requirements of the order
should be imposed,

147.3.e

contain evidence as to why OFCOM consider that the persons mentioned in
paragraph  (d)  provide an access facility in relation to the relevant
service, and specify any such access facility provided,

147.3.f

specify the requirements which OFCOM consider that the order should impose on
such persons, and

147.3.g

in the case of an application made without notice having been given to the
non-compliant provider, or to the persons mentioned in paragraph  (d) , state
why no notice has been given.

147.4

The court may make an interim access restriction order imposing requirements
on a person in relation to the relevant service if the court is satisfied—

147.4.a

that the ground in section 145 (3)(a)  or  (4)(a)  (as the case may be)
applies in relation to the service,

147.4.b

as to the ground in subsection  (1)(b)(i)  or  (ii) ,

147.4.c

that the person provides an access facility in relation to the relevant
service,

147.4.d

that there are prima facie grounds to suggest that an application for an
access restriction order under section 146 would be successful,

147.4.e

that the level of risk of harm to individuals in the United Kingdom relating
to the likely failure, and the nature and severity of that harm, are such that
it is not appropriate to wait for the failure to be established before making
the order, and

147.4.f

if no notice of the application has been given to the non-compliant provider,
or to the persons on whom requirements are being imposed, that it is
appropriate to make the order without notice.

147.5

An interim access restriction order ceases to have effect on the earlier of—

147.5.a

the date specified in the order, or the date on which the period specified in
the order expires (as the case may be), and

147.5.b

the date on which the court makes an access restriction order under section
146 in relation to the relevant service that imposes requirements on the same
persons on whom requirements are imposed by the interim order, or dismisses an
application for such an order.

147.6

Subsections  (5)  to  (8)  of section 146 apply in relation to an interim
access restriction order under this section as they apply in relation to an
access restriction order under that section.

147.7

Where a person who provides an access facility takes steps or puts in place
arrangements required by an interim access restriction order, OFCOM may, by
notice, require that person to (where possible) notify persons in the United
Kingdom who attempt to access the relevant service via that facility of the
interim access restriction order.

147.8

In this section, “ access facility ” and “ the court ” have the same meaning
as in section 146 (see subsections  (10) ,  (11)  and  (12)  of that section).

###### Interaction with other action by OFCOM

148

148.1

Where OFCOM apply for a business disruption order in respect of a failure by a
provider of a regulated service to comply with an enforceable requirement,
nothing in sections 144 to 147 is to be taken to prevent OFCOM also giving the
provider—

148.1.a

a confirmation decision in respect of the failure, or

148.1.b

a penalty notice under section 139 in relation to a confirmation decision in
respect of the failure.

148.2

Where OFCOM apply for a business disruption order in respect of a failure by a
provider of a Part 3 service to comply with a notice under section 121 (1)
(notices to deal with terrorism content and CSEA content), nothing in sections
144 to 147 is to be taken to prevent OFCOM also giving the provider either or
both of the following—

148.2.a

a further notice under section 121 (1)  (see section 126);

148.2.b

a penalty notice under section 140 (5) .

148.3

In this section, a “ business disruption order ” means—

148.3.a

a service restriction order under section 144,

148.3.b

an interim service restriction order under section 145,

148.3.c

an access restriction order under section 146, or

148.3.d

an interim access restriction order under section 147.

##### Publication of enforcement action

###### Publication by OFCOM of details of enforcement action

149

149.1

Subsections  (2)  and  (3)  apply where OFCOM have given a person (and not
withdrawn) any of the following—

149.1.a

a confirmation decision;

149.1.b

a penalty notice under section 139;

149.1.c

a penalty notice under section 140 (5) ;

149.1.d

a penalty notice under section 141 (6) .

149.2

OFCOM must publish details identifying the person and describing—

149.2.a

the failure (or failures) to which the decision or notice relates, and

149.2.b

OFCOM’s response.

149.3

But OFCOM may not publish anything that, in OFCOM’s opinion—

149.3.a

is confidential in accordance with subsections  (4)  and  (5) , or

149.3.b

is otherwise not appropriate for publication.

149.4

A matter is confidential under this subsection if—

149.4.a

it relates specifically to the affairs of a particular body, and

149.4.b

publication of that matter would or might, in OFCOM’s opinion, seriously and
prejudicially affect the interests of that body.

149.5

A matter is confidential under this subsection if—

149.5.a

it relates to the private affairs of an individual, and

149.5.b

publication of that matter would or might, in OFCOM’s opinion, seriously and
prejudicially affect the interests of that individual.

149.6

Where OFCOM have given a person a provisional notice of contravention but have
not given the person a confirmation decision, OFCOM may publish details
identifying the person and describing the reasons for the provisional notice.

149.7

OFCOM must notify the person concerned that information has been published
under this section.

###### Publication by providers of details of enforcement action

150

150.1

This section applies where—

150.1.a

OFCOM have given a person (and not withdrawn) any of the following—

150.1.a.i

a confirmation decision;

150.1.a.ii

a penalty notice under section 139;

150.1.a.iii

a penalty notice under section 140(5);

150.1.a.iv

a penalty notice under section 141(6), and

150.1.b

the appeal period in relation to the decision or notice has ended.

150.2

OFCOM may give to the person a notice (a “publication notice”) requiring the
person to—

150.2.a

publish details describing—

150.2.a.i

the failure (or failures) to which the decision or notice mentioned in
subsection  (1)(a)  relates, and

150.2.a.ii

OFCOM’s response, or

150.2.b

otherwise notify users of the service to which the decision or notice
mentioned in subsection  (1)(a)  relates of those details.

150.3

A publication notice may require a person to publish details under subsection
(2)(a)  or give notification of details under subsection  (2)(b)  or both.

150.4

A publication notice must—

150.4.a

specify the decision or notice mentioned in subsection  (1)(a)  to which it
relates,

150.4.b

specify or describe the details that must be published or notified,

150.4.c

specify the form and manner in which the details must be published or
notified,

150.4.d

specify a date by which the details must be published or notified, and

150.4.e

contain information about the consequences of not complying with the notice.

150.5

Where a publication notice requires a person to publish details under
subsection  (2)(a)  the notice may also specify a period during which
publication in the specified form and manner must continue.

150.6

Where a publication notice requires a person to give notification of details
under subsection  (2)(b)  the notice may only require that notification to be
given to United Kingdom users of the service (see section 227).

150.7

A publication notice may not require a person to publish or give notification
of anything that, in OFCOM’s opinion—

150.7.a

is confidential in accordance with subsections  (8)  and  (9) , or

150.7.b

is otherwise not appropriate for publication or notification.

150.8

A matter is confidential under this subsection if—

150.8.a

it relates specifically to the affairs of a particular body, and

150.8.b

publication or notification of that matter would or might, in OFCOM’s opinion,
seriously and prejudicially affect the interests of that body.

150.9

A matter is confidential under this subsection if—

150.9.a

it relates to the private affairs of an individual, and

150.9.b

publication or notification of that matter would or might, in OFCOM’s opinion,
seriously and prejudicially affect the interests of that individual.

150.10

A person to whom a publication notice is given has a duty to comply with it.

150.11

The duty under subsection  (10)  is enforceable in civil proceedings by OFCOM—

150.11.a

for an injunction,

150.11.b

for specific performance of a statutory duty under section 45 of the Court of
Session Act 1988, or

150.11.c

for any other appropriate remedy or relief.

150.12

For the purposes of subsection  (1)(b)  “ the appeal period ”, in relation to
a decision or notice mentioned in subsection  (1)(a) , means—

150.12.a

the period during which any appeal relating to the decision or notice may be
made, or

150.12.b

where such an appeal has been made, the period ending with the determination
or withdrawal of that appeal.

##### Guidance

###### OFCOM’s guidance about enforcement action

151

151.1

OFCOM must produce guidance for providers of regulated services about how
OFCOM propose to exercise their functions under this Chapter.

151.2

The guidance must, in particular, give information about the factors that
OFCOM would consider it appropriate to take into account when taking, or
considering taking, enforcement action relating to a person’s failure to
comply with different kinds of enforceable requirements.

151.3

In relation to any enforcement action by OFCOM which relates to a failure by a
provider of a regulated service to comply with a relevant duty, the guidance
must include provision explaining how OFCOM will take into account the impact
(or possible impact) of such a failure on children.

151.4

Before producing the guidance (including revised or replacement guidance),
OFCOM must consult—

151.4.a

the Secretary of State,

151.4.b

the Information Commissioner, and

151.4.c

such other persons as OFCOM consider appropriate.

151.5

OFCOM must publish the guidance (and any revised or replacement guidance).

151.6

Guidelines prepared by OFCOM under section 392 of the Communications Act
(amount of penalties) may, so far as relating to penalties imposed under this
Chapter, be included in the same document as guidance under this section.

151.7

In exercising their functions under this Chapter, or deciding whether to
exercise them, OFCOM must have regard to the guidance for the time being
published under this section.

151.8

In this section, a “ relevant duty ” means—

151.8.a

a duty set out in section 10 or 27 (illegal content),

151.8.b

a duty set out in section 12 or 29 (children’s online safety), or

151.8.c

a duty set out in section 81 (2)  (children’s access to provider pornographic
content).

#### Committees, research and reports

##### Advisory committee on disinformation and misinformation

152

152.1

OFCOM must, in accordance with the following provisions of this section,
exercise their powers under paragraph 14 of the Schedule to the Office of
Communications Act 2002 (committees of OFCOM) to establish and maintain a
committee to provide the advice specified in this section.

152.2

The committee is to consist of—

152.2.a

a chairman appointed by OFCOM, and

152.2.b

such number of other members appointed by OFCOM as OFCOM consider appropriate.

152.3

In appointing persons to be members of the committee, OFCOM must have regard
to the desirability of ensuring that the members of the committee include—

152.3.a

persons representing the interests of United Kingdom users of regulated
services,

152.3.b

persons representing providers of regulated services, and

152.3.c

persons with expertise in the prevention and handling of disinformation and
misinformation online.

152.4

The function of the committee is to provide advice to OFCOM (including other
committees established by OFCOM) about—

152.4.a

how providers of regulated services should deal with disinformation and
misinformation on such services,

152.4.b

OFCOM’s exercise of the power conferred by section 77 to require information
about a matter listed in Part 1 or 2 of Schedule 8, so far as relating to
disinformation and misinformation, and

152.4.c

OFCOM’s exercise of their functions under section 11 of the Communications Act
(duties to promote media literacy) in relation to countering disinformation
and misinformation on regulated services.

152.5

The committee must publish a report within the period of 18 months after being
established, and after that must publish periodic reports.
