##### OFCOM’s statement about freedom of expression and privacy

156

OFCOM’s report under paragraph 12 of the Schedule to the Office of
Communications Act 2002 for each financial year must contain a statement by
OFCOM about the steps they have taken, and the processes they operate, to
ensure that their online safety functions have been exercised in that year
compatibly with Articles 8 and 10 of the Convention (so far as relevant).

##### OFCOM’s reports about use of age assurance

157

157.1

OFCOM must produce and publish a report assessing—

157.1.a

how providers of regulated services have used age assurance for the purpose of
compliance with their duties set out in this Act,

157.1.b

how effective the use of age assurance has been for that purpose, and

157.1.c

whether there are factors that have prevented or hindered the effective use of
age assurance, or a particular kind of age assurance, for that purpose,

(and in this section, references to a report are to a report described in this
subsection).

157.2

A report must, in particular, consider whether the following have prevented or
hindered the effective use of age assurance—

157.2.a

the costs to providers of using it, and

157.2.b

the need to protect users from a breach of any statutory provision or rule of
law concerning privacy that is relevant to the use or operation of a regulated
service (including, but not limited to, any such provision or rule concerning
the processing of personal data).

157.3

Unless the Secretary of State requires the production of a further report (see
subsection  (6) ), the requirement in subsection  (1)  is met by producing and
publishing one report within the period of 18 months beginning with the day on
which sections 12 and 81(2) come into force (or if those provisions come into
force on different days, the period of 18 months beginning with the later of
those days).

157.4

In preparing a report, OFCOM must consult—

157.4.a

the Information Commissioner, and

157.4.b

such other persons as OFCOM consider appropriate.

157.5

OFCOM must send a copy of a report to the Secretary of State, and the
Secretary of State must lay it before Parliament.

157.6

The Secretary of State may require OFCOM to produce and publish a further
report in response to—

157.6.a

the development of age assurance technology, or

157.6.b

evidence of the reduced effectiveness of such technology.

157.7

But such a requirement may not be imposed—

157.7.a

within the period of three years beginning with the date on which the first
report is published, or

157.7.b

more frequently than once every three years.

157.8

For further provision about reports under this section, see section 164.

157.9

In this section “ age assurance ” means age verification or age estimation.

##### OFCOM’s reports about news publisher content and journalistic content

158

158.1

OFCOM must produce and publish a report assessing the impact of the regulatory
framework provided for in this Act on the availability and treatment of news
publisher content and journalistic content on Category 1 services (and in this
section, references to a report are to a report described in this subsection).

158.2

Unless the Secretary of State requires the production of a further report (see
subsection  (6) ), the requirement in subsection  (1)  is met by producing and
publishing one report within the period of two years beginning with the day on
which sections 18 and 19 come into force (or if those sections come into force
on different days, the period of two years beginning with the later of those
days).

158.3

A report must, in particular, consider how effective the duties to protect
such content set out in sections 18 and 19 are at protecting it.

158.4

In preparing a report, OFCOM must consult—

158.4.a

persons who represent recognised news publishers,

158.4.b

persons who appear to OFCOM to represent creators of journalistic content,

158.4.c

persons who appear to OFCOM to represent providers of Category 1 services, and

158.4.d

such other persons as OFCOM consider appropriate.

158.5

OFCOM must send a copy of a report to the Secretary of State, and the
Secretary of State must lay it before Parliament.

158.6

The Secretary of State may require OFCOM to produce and publish a further
report if the Secretary of State considers that the regulatory framework
provided for in this Act is, or may be, having a detrimental effect on the
availability and treatment of news publisher content or journalistic content
on Category 1 services.

158.7

But such a requirement may not be imposed—

158.7.a

within the period of three years beginning with the date on which the first
report is published, or

158.7.b

more frequently than once every three years.

158.8

For further provision about reports under this section, see section 164.

158.9

In this section—

      “ journalistic content ” has the meaning given by section 19;
“ news publisher content ” has the meaning given by section 55;           “
recognised news publisher ” has the meaning given by section 56.

158.10

For the meaning of “Category 1 service”, see section 95 (register of
categories of services).

##### OFCOM’s transparency reports

159

159.1

OFCOM must produce transparency reports based on information contained in the
transparency reports produced by providers of Part 3 services under section
77.

159.2

OFCOM’s transparency reports must contain—

159.2.a

a summary of conclusions drawn from the transparency reports produced under
section 77 regarding patterns or trends which OFCOM have identified in such
reports,

159.2.b

a summary of measures mentioned in such transparency reports which OFCOM
consider to be good industry practice, and

159.2.c

any other information from such transparency reports which OFCOM consider it
appropriate to include.

159.3

OFCOM’s first transparency report must be published by the end of the period
of one year beginning with—

159.3.a

the day on which the first report under section 77 is published by a provider
of a Part 3 service (see subsection  (3)(d)  of that section), or

159.3.b

if later, the earliest date specified by OFCOM for submission of a report
under section 77 in a notice given to a provider (see subsection  (3)(c)  of
that section).

159.4

OFCOM must publish a transparency report at least once a year after the
publication of their first transparency report.

159.5

For further provision about reports under this section, see section 164.

##### OFCOM’s report about reporting and complaints procedures

160

160.1

OFCOM must produce a report assessing the measures taken or in use by
providers of Part 3 services to enable users and others to—

160.1.a

report particular kinds of content present on such services, and

160.1.b

make complaints to providers of such services.

160.2

OFCOM’s report must take into account the experiences of users and others in
reporting content and making complaints to providers of Part 3 services,
including—

160.2.a

how clear the procedures are for reporting content and making complaints,

160.2.b

how easy it is to do those things, and

160.2.c

whether providers are taking appropriate and timely action in response to
reports and complaints that are made.

160.3

The report must include advice from OFCOM about whether they consider that the
Secretary of State should make regulations under section 217 (duty about
alternative dispute resolution procedure).

160.4

In the report, OFCOM may make recommendations that they consider would improve
the experiences of users and others in reporting content or making complaints
to providers of Part 3 services, or would deliver better outcomes in relation
to reports or complaints that are made.

160.5

In preparing the report under this section, OFCOM must consult—

160.5.a

the Secretary of State,

160.5.b

persons who appear to OFCOM to represent the interests of United Kingdom users
of Part 3 services,

160.5.c

persons who appear to OFCOM to represent the interests of children (generally
or with particular reference to online safety matters),

160.5.d

the Information Commissioner, and

160.5.e

such other persons as OFCOM consider appropriate.

160.6

The report may draw on OFCOM’s research under section 14 of the Communications
Act (see subsection (6B) of that section).

160.7

The report is not required to address any matters which are the subject of a
report by OFCOM under section 158 (report about the availability and treatment
of news publisher content and journalistic content).

160.8

OFCOM must publish the report within the period of two years beginning with
the day on which this section comes into force.

160.9

OFCOM must send a copy of the report to the Secretary of State, and the
Secretary of State must lay it before Parliament.

160.10

The Secretary of State must publish a statement responding to the report
within the period of three months beginning with the day on which the report
is published, and the statement must include a response to OFCOM’s advice
about whether to make regulations under section 217.

160.11

The statement must be published in such manner as the Secretary of State
considers appropriate for bringing it to the attention of persons who may be
affected by it.

160.12

For further provision about the report under this section, see section 164.

160.13

References in this section to “users and others” are to United Kingdom users
and individuals in the United Kingdom.

##### OFCOM’s report about use of app stores by children

161

161.1

OFCOM must produce a report about the use of app stores by children.

161.2

In particular, the report must—

161.2.a

assess what role app stores play in children encountering content that is
harmful to children, search content that is harmful to children or regulated
provider pornographic content by means of regulated apps which the app stores
make available,

161.2.b

assess the extent to which age assurance is currently used by providers of app
stores, and how effective it is, and

161.2.c

explore whether children’s online safety would be better protected by the
greater use of age assurance or particular kinds of age assurance by such
providers, or by other measures.

161.3

OFCOM must publish the report during the period beginning two years, and
ending three years, after the day on which sections 12 and 29 come into force
(or if those sections come into force on different days, the later of those
days).

161.4

For further provision about the report under this section, see section 164.

161.5

In this section—

      “ age assurance ” means age verification or age estimation;           “
app ” includes an app for use on any kind of device, and “app store” is to be
read accordingly;           “ content that is harmful to children ” has the
same meaning as in Part 3 (see section 60);           “ regulated app ” means
an app for a regulated service;           “ regulated provider pornographic
content ” has the same meaning as in Part 5 (see section 79);           “
search content ” has the same meaning as in Part 3 (see section 57).

161.6

In this section references to children are to children in the United Kingdom.

##### OFCOM’s report about researchers’ access to information

162

162.1

OFCOM must produce a report—

162.1.a

describing how, and to what extent, persons carrying out independent research
into online safety matters are currently able to obtain information from
providers of regulated services to inform their research,

162.1.b

exploring the legal and other issues which currently constrain the sharing of
information for such purposes, and

162.1.c

assessing the extent to which greater access to information for such purposes
might be achieved.

162.2

For the purposes of this section a person carries out “independent research”
if the person carries out research on behalf of a person other than a provider
of a regulated service.

162.3

In preparing the report, OFCOM must consult—

162.3.a

the Information Commissioner,

162.3.b

the Centre for Data Ethics and Innovation,

162.3.c

United Kingdom Research and Innovation,

162.3.d

persons who appear to OFCOM to represent providers of regulated services, and

162.3.e

such other persons as OFCOM consider appropriate.

162.4

OFCOM must publish the report within the period of 18 months beginning with
the day on which this section comes into force.

162.5

OFCOM must send a copy of the report to the Secretary of State, and the
Secretary of State must lay it before Parliament.

162.6

For further provision about the report under this section, see section 164.

162.7

OFCOM must produce guidance about the matters dealt with by the report for
providers of regulated services and persons carrying out independent research
into online safety matters.

162.8

Before producing the guidance (including revised guidance) OFCOM must consult
the persons mentioned in subsection  (3) .

162.9

OFCOM must publish the guidance (and any revised guidance).

162.10

OFCOM must include in each transparency report under section 159 an assessment
of the effectiveness of the guidance.

##### OFCOM’s report in connection with investigation into a death

163

163.1

Subsection (2) applies if OFCOM receive—

163.1.a

a notice from a senior coroner under paragraph 1(2) of Schedule 5 to the
Coroners and Justice Act 2009 in connection with an investigation into the
death of a person;

163.1.b

a request for information in connection with the investigation of a procurator
fiscal into, or an inquiry held or to be held in relation to, the death of a
person;

163.1.c

a notice from a coroner under section 17A(2) of the  Coroners Act (Northern
Ireland) 1959 (c. 15 (N.I.))  in connection with—

163.1.c.i

an investigation to determine whether an inquest into the death of a person is
necessary, or

163.1.c.ii

an inquest in relation to the death of a person.

163.2

OFCOM may produce a report for use by the coroner or procurator fiscal,
dealing with any matters that they consider may be relevant.

163.3

In subsection (1)(b) “ inquiry ” means an inquiry held, or to be held, under
the Inquiries into Fatal Accidents and Sudden Deaths etc. (Scotland) Act  2016
(asp 2) .

##### OFCOM’s reports

164

164.1

OFCOM may from time to time produce and publish reports about online safety
matters.

164.2

In publishing a report mentioned in subsection  (5) , OFCOM must have regard
to the need to exclude from publication, so far as that is practicable, the
matters which are confidential in accordance with subsections  (3)  and  (4) .

164.3

A matter is confidential under this subsection if—

164.3.a

it relates specifically to the affairs of a particular body, and

164.3.b

publication of that matter would or might, in OFCOM’s opinion, seriously and
prejudicially affect the interests of that body.

164.4

A matter is confidential under this subsection if—

164.4.a

it relates to the private affairs of an individual, and

164.4.b

publication of that matter would or might, in OFCOM’s opinion, seriously and
prejudicially affect the interests of that individual.

164.5

The reports referred to in subsection  (2)  are—

164.5.a

a report under section 128 (report in connection with notices to deal with
terrorism content and CSEA content),

164.5.b

a report under section 157 (report about use of age assurance),

164.5.c

a report under section 158 (report about news publisher content and
journalistic content),

164.5.d

a report under section 159 (transparency report),

164.5.e

a report under section 160 (report about reporting and complaints procedures),

164.5.f

a report under section 161 (report about use of app stores by children),

164.5.g

a report under section 162 (report about researchers’ access to information),
and

164.5.h

a report produced under this section.

164.6

See also section 116 (3)  (restriction on publishing intelligence service
information).

#### Media literacy

##### Media literacy

165

165.1

Section 11 of the Communications Act is amended in accordance with subsections
(2)  to  (5) .

165.2

Before subsection (1) insert—

165.2.A1

In this section—

165.2.A1.a

subsection (1) imposes duties on OFCOM which apply in relation to material
published by means of the electronic media (including by means of regulated
services), and

165.2.A1.b

subsections (1A) to (1E) expand on those duties, and impose further duties on
OFCOM, in relation to regulated services only.

165.3

After subsection (1) insert—

165.3.1A

OFCOM must take such steps, and enter into such arrangements, as they consider
most likely to be effective in heightening the public’s awareness and
understanding of ways in which they can protect themselves and others when
using regulated services, in particular by helping them to—

165.3.1A.a

understand the nature and impact of harmful content and the harmful ways in
which regulated services may be used, especially content and activity
disproportionately affecting particular groups, including women and girls;

165.3.1A.b

reduce their and others’ exposure to harmful content and to the use of
regulated services in harmful ways, especially content and activity
disproportionately affecting particular groups, including women and girls;

165.3.1A.c

use or apply—

165.3.1A.c.i

features included in a regulated service, including features mentioned in
section 15(2) of the Online Safety Act 2023, and

165.3.1A.c.ii

tools or apps, including tools such as browser extensions,

so as to mitigate the harms mentioned in paragraph (b);

165.3.1A.d

establish the reliability, accuracy and authenticity of content;

165.3.1A.e

understand the nature and impact of disinformation and misinformation, and
reduce their and others’ exposure to it;

165.3.1A.f

understand how their personal information may be protected.

165.3.1B

OFCOM must take such steps, and enter into such arrangements, as they consider
most likely to encourage the development and use of technologies and systems
for supporting users of regulated services to protect themselves and others as
mentioned in paragraph (a), (b), (c), (d) or (e) of subsection (1A), including
technologies and systems which—

165.3.1B.a

provide further context to users about content they encounter;

165.3.1B.b

help users to identify, and provide further context about, content of
democratic importance present on regulated user-to-user services;

165.3.1B.c

signpost users to resources, tools or information raising awareness about how
to use regulated services so as to mitigate the harms mentioned in subsection
(1A)(b).

165.3.1C

OFCOM’s duty under subsection (1A) is to be performed in the following ways
(among others)—

165.3.1C.a

pursuing activities and initiatives,

165.3.1C.b

commissioning others to pursue activities and initiatives,

165.3.1C.c

taking steps designed to encourage others to pursue activities and
initiatives, and

165.3.1C.d

making arrangements for the carrying out of research (see section 14(6)(a)).

165.3.1D

OFCOM must draw up, and from time to time review and revise, a statement
recommending ways in which others, including providers of regulated services,
might develop, pursue and evaluate activities or initiatives relevant to media
literacy in relation to regulated services.

165.3.1E

OFCOM must publish the statement and any revised statement in such manner as
they consider appropriate for bringing it to the attention of the persons who,
in their opinion, are likely to be affected by it.

165.4

After subsection (2) insert—

165.4.3

In this section and in section 11A, “ regulated service ” means—

165.4.3.a

a regulated user-to-user service, or

165.4.3.b

a regulated search service.

“ Regulated user-to-user service ” and “ regulated search service ” have the
same meaning as in the Online Safety Act 2023 (see section 4 of that Act).

165.4.4

In this section—

165.4.4.a

“ content ”, in relation to regulated services, means regulated user-generated
content, search content or fraudulent advertisements;

165.4.4.b

the following terms have the same meaning as in the Online Safety Act 2023—

      “ content of democratic importance ” (see section 17 of that Act);
“ fraudulent advertisement ” (see sections 38 and 39 of that Act);           “
harm ” (see section 234 of that Act) (and “harmful” is to be interpreted
consistently with that section);           “ provider ” (see section 226 of
that Act);           “ regulated user-generated content ” (see section 55 of
that Act);           “ search content ” (see section 57 of that Act).

165.5

In the heading, for “Duty” substitute  “Duties” .

165.6

In section 14 of the Communications Act (consumer research), in subsection
(6)(a), after “11(1)” insert  “, (1A) and (1B)” .

##### Media literacy strategy and media literacy statement

166

After section 11 of the Communications Act insert—

######### Regulated services: media literacy strategy and media literacy statement

166.11A

166.11A.1

OFCOM must prepare and publish a media literacy strategy within the period of
one year beginning with the day on which the Online Safety Act 2023 is passed.

166.11A.2

A media literacy strategy is a plan setting out how OFCOM propose to exercise
their functions under section 11 in the period covered by the plan, which must
be not more than three years.

166.11A.3

In particular, a media literacy strategy must state OFCOM’s objectives and
priorities for the period it covers.

166.11A.4

Before the end of the period covered by a media literacy strategy, OFCOM must
prepare and publish a media literacy strategy for a further period, ensuring
that each successive strategy covers a period beginning immediately after the
end of the last one.

166.11A.5

In preparing or revising a media literacy strategy, OFCOM must consult such
persons as they consider appropriate.

166.11A.6

OFCOM’s annual report must contain a media literacy statement.

166.11A.7

A media literacy statement is a statement by OFCOM—

166.11A.7.a

summarising what they have done in the financial year to which the report
relates in the exercise of their functions under section 11, and

166.11A.7.b

assessing what progress has been made towards achieving the objectives and
priorities set out in their media literacy strategy in that year.

166.11A.8

A media literacy statement must include a summary and an evaluation of the
activities and initiatives pursued or commissioned by OFCOM in the exercise of
their functions under section 11 in the financial year to which the report
relates.

166.11A.9

The first annual report that is required to contain a media literacy statement
is the report for the financial year during which OFCOM’s first media literacy
strategy is published, and that first statement is to relate to the period
from publication day until the end of that financial year.

166.11A.10

But if OFCOM’s first media literacy strategy is published during the second
half of a financial year—

166.11A.10.a

the first annual report that is required to contain a media literacy statement
is the report for the next financial year, and

166.11A.10.b

that first statement is to relate to the period from publication day until the
end of that financial year.

166.11A.11

References in this section to OFCOM’s functions under section 11 are to those
functions so far as they relate to regulated services.

166.11A.12

In this section—

      “ annual report ” means OFCOM’s annual report under paragraph 12 of the
Schedule to the Office of Communications Act 2002;           “ financial year
” means a year ending with 31 March.

### Appeals and super-complaints

#### Appeals

##### Appeals against OFCOM decisions relating to the register under section 95

167

167.1

This section applies to the following decisions of OFCOM—

167.1.a

a decision to include a regulated user-to-user service in the part of the
register referred to in section 95 (2)(a)  (Category 1 services);

167.1.b

a decision not to remove a regulated user-to-user service from that part of
the register;

167.1.c

a decision to include a regulated search service or a combined service in the
part of the register referred to in section 95 (2)(b)  (Category 2A services);

167.1.d

a decision not to remove a regulated search service or a combined service from
that part of the register;

167.1.e

a decision to include a regulated user-to-user service in the part of the
register referred to in section 95 (2)(c)  (Category 2B services);

167.1.f

a decision not to remove a regulated user-to-user service from that part of
the register.

167.2

The provider of the service to which the decision relates may appeal to the
Upper Tribunal against the decision.

167.3

Where an appeal is made under subsection  (1)(a) ,  (c)  or  (e) , any special
requirements need not be complied with until the determination or withdrawal
of the appeal.

167.4

“ Special requirement ” means—

167.4.a

in the case of an appeal against a decision mentioned in subsection  (1)(a) —

167.4.a.i

any duty or requirement of this Act that applies in relation to Category 1
services but not in relation to any other regulated services, or

167.4.a.ii

any duty or requirement of this Act that applies in relation to Category 1
services, Category 2A services and Category 2B services but not in relation to
any other regulated services;

167.4.b

in the case of an appeal against a decision mentioned in subsection  (1)(c) —

167.4.b.i

any duty or requirement of this Act that applies in relation to Category 2A
services but not in relation to any other regulated services, or

167.4.b.ii

any duty or requirement of this Act that applies in relation to Category 1
services, Category 2A services and Category 2B services but not in relation to
any other regulated services;

167.4.c

in the case of an appeal against a decision mentioned in subsection  (1)(e) ,
any duty or requirement of this Act that applies in relation to Category 1
services, Category 2A services and Category 2B services but not in relation to
any other regulated services.

167.5

The Upper Tribunal must decide the appeal by applying the same principles as
would be applied—

167.5.a

by the High Court on an application for judicial review, or

167.5.b

in Scotland, on an application to the supervisory jurisdiction of the Court of
Session.

167.6

On an appeal under this section, the Upper Tribunal may—

167.6.a

dismiss the appeal, or

167.6.b

quash the decision being challenged.

167.7

Where a decision is quashed, the Upper Tribunal must remit the decision to
OFCOM for reconsideration with such directions (if any) as the Tribunal
considers appropriate.

##### Appeals against OFCOM notices

168

168.1

An appeal to the Upper Tribunal against OFCOM’s decision to give to a person—

168.1.a

a notice under section 121 (1)  (notices to deal with terrorism content and
CSEA content),

168.1.b

a confirmation decision, or

168.1.c

a penalty notice,

may be brought by any person with a sufficient interest in the decision.

168.2

An appeal under subsection  (1)  by a person other than the person given the
notice or decision in question may be brought only with the permission (or
leave) of the Upper Tribunal.

168.3

The Upper Tribunal must decide the appeal by applying the same principles as
would be applied—

168.3.a

by the High Court on an application for judicial review, or

168.3.b

in Scotland, on an application to the supervisory jurisdiction of the Court of
Session.

168.4

On an appeal under this section, the Upper Tribunal may—

168.4.a

dismiss the appeal, or

168.4.b

quash the decision being challenged.

168.5

Where a decision is quashed, the Upper Tribunal must remit the decision to
OFCOM for reconsideration with such directions (if any) as the Tribunal
considers appropriate.

168.6

In this section “ penalty notice ” means a penalty notice under section 139,
140 (5)  or 141 (6) .

#### Super-complaints

##### Power to make super-complaints

169

169.1

An eligible entity may make a complaint to OFCOM that any feature of one or
more regulated services, or any conduct of one or more providers of such
services, or any combination of such features and such conduct is, appears to
be, or presents a material risk of—

169.1.a

causing significant harm to users of the services or members of the public, or
a particular group of such users or members of the public;

169.1.b

significantly adversely affecting the right to freedom of expression within
the law of users of the services or members of the public, or of a particular
group of such users or members of the public; or

169.1.c

otherwise having a significant adverse impact on users of the services or
members of the public, or on a particular group of such users or members of
the public.

169.2

But a complaint under subsection  (1)  that relates to a single regulated
service or that relates to a single provider of one or more regulated services
is only admissible if OFCOM consider that—

169.2.a

the complaint is of particular importance, or

169.2.b

the complaint relates to the impacts on a particularly large number of users
of the service or members of the public.

169.3

An entity is an “eligible entity” if the entity meets criteria specified in
regulations made by the Secretary of State.

169.4

Regulations under subsection  (3)  must specify as one of the criteria that
the entity must be a body representing the interests of users of regulated
services, or members of the public, or a particular group of such users or
members of the public.

169.5

Before making regulations under subsection  (3) , the Secretary of State must
consult—

169.5.a

OFCOM, and

169.5.b

such other persons as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

169.6

In this section—

      “ conduct ” includes acts and omissions;           “ users ” means
United Kingdom users (see section 227), except in subsection  (1)(a)  where “
users ” means individuals in the United Kingdom who are users of a service.

##### Procedure for super-complaints

170

170.1

The Secretary of State must make regulations containing provision about
procedural matters relating to complaints under section 169.

170.2

Such regulations may, in particular, include provision about the following
matters—

170.2.a

notification to OFCOM of an intention to make a complaint under section 169;

170.2.b

the form and manner of such a complaint, including requirements for supporting
evidence in relation to—

170.2.b.i

matters mentioned in subsections  (1)  and  (2)  of section 169, and

170.2.b.ii

criteria specified in regulations under subsection  (3)  of that section;

170.2.c

steps that OFCOM must take in relation to such a complaint, including
requirements for publication of responses;

170.2.d

time limits for taking steps in relation to such a complaint (or provision
about how such time limits are to be determined) including time limits in
relation to the determination of—

170.2.d.i

whether a complaint is a complaint that is within section 169 (1) ,

170.2.d.ii

where applicable, whether a complaint is admissible under section 169 (2) ,
and

170.2.d.iii

whether an entity is an eligible entity (see section 169 (3) ).

170.3

Before making regulations under subsection  (1) , the Secretary of State must
consult—

170.3.a

OFCOM, and

170.3.b

such other persons as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

##### OFCOM’s guidance about super-complaints

171

171.1

OFCOM must produce guidance about complaints under section 169, which must
include guidance about—

171.1.a

the criteria specified in regulations under section 169 (3) ,

171.1.b

procedural matters relating to such complaints, and

171.1.c

any other aspect of such complaints that OFCOM consider it appropriate to
include.

171.2

OFCOM must publish the guidance (and any revised or replacement guidance).

### Secretary of State's functions in relation to regulated services

#### Strategic priorities

##### Statement of strategic priorities

172

172.1

The Secretary of State may designate a statement for the purposes of this
section if the requirements set out in section 173 (consultation and
parliamentary procedure) are satisfied.

172.2

The statement is a statement prepared by the Secretary of State that sets out
strategic priorities of His Majesty’s Government in the United Kingdom
relating to online safety matters.

172.3

The statement may, among other things, set out particular outcomes identified
with a view to achieving the strategic priorities.

172.4

This section does not restrict the Secretary of State’s powers under any other
provision of this Act or any other enactment.

172.5

A statement designated under subsection  (1)  must be published in such manner
as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

172.6

A statement designated under subsection  (1)  may be amended (including by
replacing the whole or a part of the statement with new material) by a
subsequent statement designated under that subsection, and this section and
sections 92 and 173 apply in relation to any such subsequent statement as they
apply in relation to the original statement.

172.7

Except as provided by subsection  (8) , no amendment may be made under
subsection  (6)  within the period of five years beginning with the day on
which a statement was most recently designated under subsection  (1) .

172.8

An earlier amendment may be made under subsection  (6)  if—

172.8.a

since that day—

172.8.a.i

a Parliamentary general election has taken place, or

172.8.a.ii

there has been a significant change in the policy of His Majesty’s Government
affecting online safety matters, or

172.8.b

the Secretary of State considers that the statement, or any part of it,
conflicts with any of OFCOM’s general duties (within the meaning of section 3
of the Communications Act).

##### Consultation and parliamentary procedure

173

173.1

This section sets out the requirements that must be satisfied in relation to a
statement before the Secretary of State may designate it under section 172.

173.2

The Secretary of State must consult—

173.2.a

OFCOM, and

173.2.b

such other persons as the Secretary of State considers appropriate,

on a draft of the statement.

173.3

The Secretary of State must allow OFCOM a period of at least 40 days to
respond to any consultation under subsection  (2)(a) .

173.4

After that period has ended the Secretary of State—

173.4.a

must make any changes to the draft that appear to the Secretary of State to be
necessary in view of responses to the consultation, and

173.4.b

must then lay the draft before Parliament.

173.5

The Secretary of State must then wait until the end of the 40-day period and
may not designate the statement if, within that period, either House of
Parliament resolves not to approve it.

173.6

“The 40-day period” is the period of 40 days beginning with the day on which
the draft is laid before Parliament (or, if it is not laid before each House
on the same day, the later of the days on which it is laid).

173.7

In calculating the 40-day period, no account is to be taken of any period
during which Parliament is dissolved or prorogued or during which both Houses
are adjourned for more than 4 days.

#### Directions to OFCOM

##### Directions about advisory committees

174

174.1

The Secretary of State may give OFCOM a direction requiring OFCOM to establish
a committee to provide them with advice about online safety matters of a kind
specified in the direction.

174.2

The Secretary of State must consult OFCOM before giving or varying such a
direction.

174.3

A committee required to be established by a direction is to consist of the
following members, unless the direction specifies otherwise—

174.3.a

a chairman appointed by OFCOM, and

174.3.b

such number of other members appointed by OFCOM as OFCOM consider appropriate.

174.4

A committee required to be established by a direction must, unless the
direction specifies otherwise, publish a report within the period of 18 months
after being established, and after that must publish periodic reports.

174.5

The Secretary of State may vary or revoke a direction given under this
section.

##### Directions in special circumstances

175

175.1

The Secretary of State may give a direction to OFCOM under subsection  (2)  or
(3)  if the Secretary of State has reasonable grounds for believing that
circumstances exist that present a threat—

175.1.a

to the health or safety of the public, or

175.1.b

to national security.

175.2

A direction under this subsection is a direction requiring OFCOM, in
exercising their media literacy functions, to give priority for a specified
period to specified objectives designed to address the threat presented by the
circumstances mentioned in subsection  (1) .

175.3

A direction under this subsection is a direction requiring OFCOM to give a
public statement notice to—

175.3.a

a specified provider of a regulated service, or

175.3.b

providers of regulated services generally.

175.4

A “public statement notice” is a notice requiring a provider of a regulated
service to make a publicly available statement, by a date specified in the
notice, about steps the provider is taking in response to the threat presented
by the circumstances mentioned in subsection  (1) .

175.5

OFCOM may, by a public statement notice or a subsequent notice, require a
provider of a regulated service to provide OFCOM with such information as they
may require for the purpose of responding to that threat.

175.6

If a direction under subsection  (2)  or  (3)  is given on the ground
mentioned in subsection  (1)(a) , the Secretary of State must publish the
reasons for giving the direction.

175.7

The Secretary of State may vary or revoke a direction given under subsection
(2)  or  (3) .

175.8

If the Secretary of State varies or revokes a direction given under subsection
(3) , OFCOM may, in consequence, vary or revoke a public statement notice that
they have given by virtue of the direction.

175.9

In subsection  (2)  “ media literacy functions ” means OFCOM’s functions under
section 11 of the Communications Act (duties to promote media literacy), so
far as functions under that section relate to regulated services.

175.10

In subsections  (2)  and  (3)  “ specified ” means specified in a direction
under this section.

#### Guidance

##### Secretary of State’s guidance

176

176.1

The Secretary of State may issue guidance to OFCOM about—

176.1.a

OFCOM’s exercise of their functions under this Act,

176.1.b

OFCOM’s exercise of their powers under section 1(3) of the Communications Act
(functions and general powers of OFCOM) to carry out research in connection
with online safety matters or to arrange for others to carry out research in
connection with such matters, and

176.1.c

OFCOM’s exercise of their functions under section 11 of the Communications Act
(media literacy) in relation to regulated services.

176.2

In the rest of this section, “ the guidance ” means any such guidance as is
mentioned in subsection (1), except that it does not include guidance under
section 87 (guidance to OFCOM about fees).

176.3

The Secretary of State must consult OFCOM before issuing, revising or
replacing the guidance.

176.4

The guidance may not be revised or replaced more frequently than once every
three years unless—

176.4.a

the guidance needs to be corrected because of an amendment, repeal or
modification of any provision of this Act or of section 11 of the
Communications Act, or

176.4.b

the revision or replacement is by agreement between the Secretary of State and
OFCOM.

176.5

The guidance must be issued as one document.

176.6

The Secretary of State must lay the guidance (including revised or replacement
guidance) before Parliament.

176.7

The Secretary of State must publish the guidance (and any revised or
replacement guidance).

176.8

In exercising any functions to which the guidance relates, or deciding whether
to exercise them, OFCOM must have regard to the guidance for the time being
published under this section.

#### Annual report

##### Annual report on the Secretary of State’s functions

177

In section 390 of the Communications Act (annual report on the Secretary of
State’s functions), in subsection (2), after paragraph (e) insert—

177.f

the Online Safety Act 2023.

#### Review

##### Review

178

178.1

The Secretary of State must review the operation of—

178.1.a

the regulatory framework provided for in this Act, and

178.1.b

section 11 of the Communications Act, to the extent that that section relates
to regulated services.

178.2

The review—

178.2.a

must not be carried out before the end of the period of two years beginning
with the day on which the last of the provisions of Part 3 comes into force,
but

178.2.b

must be carried out before the end of the period of five years beginning with
that day.

178.3

The review must, in particular, consider how effective the regulatory
framework provided for in this Act is at—

178.3.a

securing that regulated services are operated using systems and processes
that, so far as relevant—

178.3.a.i

minimise the risk of harm to individuals in the United Kingdom presented by
content on regulated services,

178.3.a.ii

provide higher levels of protection for children than for adults,

178.3.a.iii

provide transparency and accountability to users in relation to actions taken
to comply with duties set out in Chapter 2, 3, 4 or 5 of Part 3, Chapter 1, 3
or 4 of Part 4, or Part 5,

178.3.a.iv

protect the right of users and (in the case of search services or combined
services) interested persons to freedom of expression within the law, and

178.3.a.v

protect users from a breach of any statutory provision or rule of law
concerning privacy that is relevant to the use or operation of a regulated
service (including, but not limited to, any such provision or rule concerning
the processing of personal data); and

178.3.b

ensuring that regulation of services is proportionate, having regard to the
level of risk of harm presented by regulated services of different kinds and
to the size and capacity of providers.

178.4

The review must also, in particular, consider—

178.4.a

the effectiveness of—

178.4.a.i

the information gathering and information sharing powers available to OFCOM,
and

178.4.a.ii

the enforcement powers available to OFCOM; and

178.4.b

the extent to which OFCOM have had regard to the desirability of encouraging
innovation by providers of regulated services.

178.5

In carrying out the review, the Secretary of State must consult—

178.5.a

OFCOM, and

178.5.b

such other persons as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

178.6

In carrying out the review, the Secretary of State must take into account any
report published by OFCOM under section 158 (reports about news publisher
content and journalistic content).

178.7

The Secretary of State must produce and publish a report on the outcome of the
review.

178.8

The report must be laid before Parliament.

178.9

In subsection  (3)  “ content on regulated services ” means—

178.9.a

regulated user-generated content present on regulated services,

178.9.b

search content of regulated services,

178.9.c

fraudulent advertisements present on regulated services, and

178.9.d

regulated provider pornographic content published or displayed on regulated
services.

178.10

In subsection  (9) —

      “ fraudulent advertisement ” has the meaning given by section 38 or 39
(depending on the kind of service in question);           “ regulated user-
generated content ” has the same meaning as in Part 3 (see section 55);
“ regulated provider pornographic content ” and “ published or displayed ”
have the same meaning as in Part 5 (see section 79);           “ search
content ” has the same meaning as in Part 3 (see section 57).

### Communications offences

#### False and threatening communications offences

##### False communications offence

179

179.1

A person commits an offence if—

179.1.a

the person sends a message (see section 182),

179.1.b

the message conveys information that the person knows to be false,

179.1.c

at the time of sending it, the person intended the message, or the information
in it, to cause non-trivial psychological or physical harm to a likely
audience, and

179.1.d

the person has no reasonable excuse for sending the message.

179.2

For the purposes of this offence an individual is a “likely audience” of a
message if, at the time the message is sent, it is reasonably foreseeable that
the individual—

179.2.a

would encounter the message, or

179.2.b

in the online context, would encounter a subsequent message forwarding or
sharing the content of the message.

179.3

In a case where several or many individuals are a likely audience, it is not
necessary for the purposes of subsection  (1)(c)  that the person intended to
cause harm to any one of them in particular (or to all of them).

179.4

See section 180 for exemptions from the offence under this section.

179.5

A person who commits an offence under this section is liable—

179.5.a

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding the maximum term for summary offences or a fine (or both);

179.5.b

on summary conviction in Northern Ireland, to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding 6 months or a fine not exceeding level 5 on the standard scale (or
both).

179.6

In subsection  (5)(a)  “ the maximum term for summary offences ” means—

179.6.a

if the offence is committed before the time when section 281(5) of the
Criminal Justice Act 2003 comes into force, 6 months;

179.6.b

if the offence is committed after that time, 51 weeks.

179.7

Proceedings for an offence under this section may be brought within the period
of 6 months beginning with the date on which evidence sufficient in the
opinion of the prosecutor to justify the proceedings comes to the prosecutor’s
knowledge.

179.8

But such proceedings may not be brought by virtue of subsection  (7)  more
than 3 years after the commission of the offence.

179.9

A certificate signed by the prosecutor as to the date on which the evidence in
question came to the prosecutor’s knowledge is conclusive evidence of the date
on which it did so; and a certificate to that effect and purporting to be so
signed is to be treated as being so signed unless the contrary is proved.

##### Exemptions from offence under section 179

180

180.1

A recognised news publisher cannot commit an offence under section 179.

180.2

An offence under section 179 cannot be committed by the holder of a licence
under the Broadcasting Act 1990 or 1996 in connection with anything done under
the authority of the licence.

180.3

An offence under section 179 cannot be committed by the holder of a multiplex
licence in connection with anything done under the authority of the licence.

180.4

An offence under section 179 cannot be committed by the provider of an on-
demand programme service in connection with anything done in the course of
providing such a service.

180.5

An offence under section 179 cannot be committed in connection with the
showing of a film made for cinema to members of the public.

##### Threatening communications offence

181

181.1

A person commits an offence if—

181.1.a

the person sends a message (see section 182),

181.1.b

the message conveys a threat of death or serious harm, and

181.1.c

at the time of sending it, the person—

181.1.c.i

intended an individual encountering the message to fear that the threat would
be carried out (whether or not by the person sending the message), or

181.1.c.ii

was reckless as to whether an individual encountering the message would fear
that the threat would be carried out (whether or not by the person sending the
message).

181.2

“ Serious harm ” means—

181.2.a

serious injury amounting to grievous bodily harm within the meaning of the
Offences against the Person Act 1861,

181.2.b

rape,

181.2.c

assault by penetration within the meaning of section 2 of the Sexual Offences
Act 2003, or

181.2.d

serious financial loss.

181.3

In proceedings for an offence under this section relating to a threat of
serious financial loss, it is a defence for the person to show that—

181.3.a

the threat was used to reinforce a reasonable demand, and

181.3.b

the person reasonably believed that the use of the threat was a proper means
of reinforcing the demand.

181.4

If evidence is adduced which is sufficient to raise an issue with respect to
the defence under subsection  (3) , the court must assume that the defence is
satisfied unless the prosecution proves beyond reasonable doubt that it is
not.

181.5

A person who commits an offence under this section is liable—

181.5.a

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding the general limit in a magistrates’ court or a fine (or both);

181.5.b

on summary conviction in Northern Ireland, to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding 6 months or a fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both);

181.5.c

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 5 years
or a fine (or both).

##### Interpretation of sections 179 to 181

182

182.1

This section applies for the purposes of sections 179 to 181, and references
in this section to an offence are to an offence under section 179 or 181.

182.2

A person “sends a message” if the person—

182.2.a

sends, transmits or publishes a communication (including an oral
communication) by electronic means, or

182.2.b

sends, or gives to an individual, a letter or a thing of any other
description,

and references to a message are to be read accordingly.

182.3

A person also “sends a message” if the person—

182.3.a

causes a communication (including an oral communication) to be sent,
transmitted or published by electronic means, or

182.3.b

causes a letter or a thing of any other description to be—

182.3.b.i

sent, or

182.3.b.ii

given to an individual.

182.4

But a provider of an internet service by means of which a communication is
sent, transmitted or published is not to be regarded as a person who sends a
message.

182.5

“ Encounter ”, in relation to a message, means read, view, hear or otherwise
experience the message.

182.6

It does not matter whether the content of a message is created by the person
who sends it (so for example, in the online context, an offence may be
committed by a person who forwards another person’s direct message or shares
another person’s post).

182.7

In the application of sections 179 to 181 to the sending by electronic means
of a message consisting of or including a hyperlink to other content—

182.7.a

references to the message are to be read as including references to content
accessed directly via the hyperlink, and

182.7.b

an individual who is a likely audience in relation to the hyperlink for the
purposes of section 179 is to be assumed to be a likely audience in relation
to the linked content.

182.8

In the application of sections 179 to 181 to the sending of an item on which
data is stored electronically, references to the message are to be read as
including content accessed by means of the item to which the recipient is
specifically directed by the sender (and in this subsection “ sending ”
includes “giving”, and “sender” is to be read accordingly).

182.9

In the online context, the date on which a person commits an offence in
relation to a message is the date on which the message is first sent by the
person.

182.10

“ Recognised news publisher ” has the meaning given by section 56.

182.11

“ Multiplex licence ” means a licence under section 8 of the Wireless
Telegraphy Act 2006 which authorises the provision of a multiplex service
within the meaning of section 42(6) of that Act.

182.12

“ On-demand programme service ” has the same meaning as in the Communications
Act (see section 368A of that Act), and a person is the “provider” of an on-
demand programme service if the person has given notification of the person’s
intention to provide that service in accordance with section 368BA of that
Act.

#### Offences of sending or showing flashing images

##### Offences of sending or showing flashing images electronically

183

183.1

A person (A) commits an offence if—

183.1.a

A sends a communication by electronic means which consists of or includes
flashing images (see subsection  (13) ),

183.1.b

either condition 1 or condition 2 is met, and

183.1.c

A has no reasonable excuse for sending the communication.

183.2

Condition 1 is that—

183.2.a

at the time the communication is sent, it is reasonably foreseeable that an
individual with epilepsy would be among the individuals who would view it, and

183.2.b

A sends the communication with the intention that such an individual will
suffer harm as a result of viewing the flashing images.

183.3

Condition 2 is that, when sending the communication—

183.3.a

A believes that an individual (B)—

183.3.a.i

whom A knows to be an individual with epilepsy, or

183.3.a.ii

whom A suspects to be an individual with epilepsy,

will, or might, view it, and

183.3.b

A intends that B will suffer harm as a result of viewing the flashing images.

183.4

In subsections (2)(a) and (3)(a), references to viewing the communication are
to be read as including references to viewing a subsequent communication
forwarding or sharing the content of the communication.

183.5

The exemptions contained in section 180 apply to an offence under subsection
(1) as they apply to an offence under section 179.

183.6

For the purposes of subsection (1), a provider of an internet service by means
of which a communication is sent is not to be regarded as a person who sends a
communication.

183.7

In the application of subsection (1) to a communication consisting of or
including a hyperlink to other content, references to the communication are to
be read as including references to content accessed directly via the
hyperlink.

183.8

A person (A) commits an offence if—

183.8.a

A shows an individual (B) flashing images by means of an electronic
communications device,

183.8.b

when showing the images—

183.8.b.i

A knows that B is an individual with epilepsy, or

183.8.b.ii

A suspects that B is an individual with epilepsy,

183.8.c

when showing the images, A intends that B will suffer harm as a result of
viewing them, and

183.8.d

A has no reasonable excuse for showing the images.

183.9

An offence under subsection (1) or (8) cannot be committed by a healthcare
professional acting in that capacity.

183.10

A person who commits an offence under subsection (1) or (8) is liable—

183.10.a

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding the general limit in a magistrates’ court or a fine (or both);

183.10.b

on summary conviction in Northern Ireland, to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding 6 months or a fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both);

183.10.c

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 5 years
or a fine (or both).

183.11

It does not matter for the purposes of this section whether flashing images
may be viewed at once (for example, a GIF that plays automatically) or only
after some action is performed (for example, pressing play).

183.12

In this section—

183.12.a

references to sending a communication include references to causing a
communication to be sent;

183.12.b

references to showing flashing images include references to causing flashing
images to be shown.

183.13

In this section—

      “ electronic communications device ” means equipment or a device that is
capable of transmitting images by electronic means;           “ flashing
images ” means images which carry a risk that an individual with
photosensitive epilepsy who viewed them would suffer a seizure as a result;
“ harm ” means—         a seizure, or           alarm or distress;
“ individual with epilepsy ” includes, but is not limited to, an individual
with photosensitive epilepsy;           “ send ” includes transmit and publish
(and related expressions are to be read accordingly).

#### Offence of encouraging or assisting serious self-harm

##### Offence of encouraging or assisting serious self-harm

184

184.1

A person (D) commits an offence if—

184.1.a

D does a relevant act capable of encouraging or assisting the serious self-
harm of another person, and

184.1.b

D’s act was intended to encourage or assist the serious self-harm of another
person.

184.2

D “does a relevant act” if D—

184.2.a

communicates in person,

184.2.b

sends, transmits or publishes a communication by electronic means,

184.2.c

shows a person such a communication,

184.2.d

publishes material by any means other than electronic means,

184.2.e

sends, gives, shows or makes available to a person—

184.2.e.i

material published as mentioned in paragraph (d), or

184.2.e.ii

any form of correspondence, or

184.2.f

sends, gives or makes available to a person an item on which data is stored
electronically.

184.3

“ Serious self-harm ” means self-harm amounting to—

184.3.a

in England and Wales and Northern Ireland, grievous bodily harm within the
meaning of the Offences Against the Person Act 1861, and

184.3.b

in Scotland, severe injury,

and includes successive acts of self-harm which cumulatively reach that
threshold.

184.4

The person referred to in subsection (1)(a) and (b) need not be a specific
person (or class of persons) known to, or identified by, D.

184.5

D may commit an offence under this section whether or not serious self-harm
occurs.

184.6

If a person (D1) arranges for a person (D2) to do an act that is capable of
encouraging or assisting the serious self-harm of another person and D2 does
that act, D1 is to be treated as also having done it.

184.7

In the application of subsection (1) to an act by D involving an electronic
communication or a publication in physical form, it does not matter whether
the content of the communication or publication is created by D (so for
example, in the online context, the offence under this section may be
committed by forwarding another person’s direct message or sharing another
person’s post).

184.8

In the application of subsection (1) to the sending, transmission or
publication by electronic means of a communication consisting of or including
a hyperlink to other content, the reference in subsection (2)(b) to the
communication is to be read as including a reference to content accessed
directly via the hyperlink.

184.9

In the application of subsection (1) to an act by D involving an item on which
data is stored electronically, the reference in subsection (2)(f) to the item
is to be read as including a reference to content accessed by means of the
item to which the person in receipt of the item is specifically directed by D.

184.10

A provider of an internet service by means of which a communication is sent,
transmitted or published is not to be regarded as a person who sends,
transmits or publishes it.

184.11

Any reference in this section to doing an act that is capable of encouraging
the serious self-harm of another person includes a reference to doing so by
threatening another person or otherwise putting pressure on another person to
seriously self-harm.

“Seriously self-harm” is to be interpreted consistently with subsection (3).

184.12

Any reference to an act in this section, except in subsection (3), includes a
reference to a course of conduct, and references to doing an act are to be
read accordingly.

184.13

In subsection (3) “ act ” includes omission.

184.14

A person who commits an offence under this section is liable—

184.14.a

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding the general limit in a magistrates’ court or a fine (or both);

184.14.b

on summary conviction in Scotland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 12
months or a fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both);

184.14.c

on summary conviction in Northern Ireland, to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding 6 months or a fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both);

184.14.d

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 5 years
or a fine (or both).

#### Further provision

##### Extra-territorial application and jurisdiction

185

185.1

Sections 179(1), 181(1) and 183 (1)  apply to an act done outside the United
Kingdom, but only if the act is done by a person within subsection  (2) .

185.2

A person is within this subsection if the person is—

185.2.a

an individual who is habitually resident in England and Wales or Northern
Ireland, or

185.2.b

a body incorporated or constituted under the law of England and Wales or
Northern Ireland.

185.3

Section 184 (1)  applies to an act done outside the United Kingdom, but only
if the act is done by a person within subsection  (4) .

185.4

A person is within this subsection if the person is—

185.4.a

an individual who is habitually resident in the United Kingdom, or

185.4.b

a body incorporated or constituted under the law of any part of the United
Kingdom.

185.5

Proceedings for an offence committed under section 179, 181 or 183 (1)
outside the United Kingdom may be taken, and the offence may for incidental
purposes be treated as having been committed, at any place in England and
Wales or Northern Ireland.

185.6

Proceedings for an offence committed under section 184 outside the United
Kingdom may be taken, and the offence may for incidental purposes be treated
as having been committed, at any place in the United Kingdom.

185.7

In the application of subsection  (6)  to Scotland, any such proceedings
against a person may be taken, and the offence may for incidental purposes be
treated as having been committed—

185.7.a

in any sheriff court district in which the person is apprehended or is in
custody, or

185.7.b

in such sheriff court district as the Lord Advocate may determine.

185.8

In subsection  (7)  “ sheriff court district ” is to be construed in
accordance with the Criminal Procedure (Scotland) Act 1995 (see section 307(1)
of that Act).

##### Liability of corporate officers

186

186.1

If an offence under section 179, 181, 183 or 184 is committed by a body
corporate and it is proved that the offence—

186.1.a

has been committed with the consent or connivance of an officer of the body
corporate, or

186.1.b

is attributable to any neglect on the part of an officer of the body
corporate,

the officer (as well as the body corporate) commits the offence and is liable
to be proceeded against and punished accordingly.

186.2

“ Officer ”, in relation to a body corporate, means—

186.2.a

a director, manager, associate, secretary or other similar officer, or

186.2.b

a person purporting to act in any such capacity.

In paragraph  (a)  “ director ”, in relation to a body corporate whose affairs
are managed by its members, means a member of the body corporate.

186.3

If an offence under section 184 is committed by a Scottish partnership and it
is proved that the offence—

186.3.a

has been committed with the consent or connivance of a partner of the
partnership, or

186.3.b

is attributable to any neglect on the part of a partner of the partnership,

the partner (as well as the partnership) commits the offence and is liable to
be proceeded against and punished accordingly.

186.4

“ Partner ”, in relation to a Scottish partnership, includes any person who
was purporting to act as a partner.

#### Offences to be inserted into Sexual Offences Act 2003

##### Sending etc photograph or film of genitals

187

In the Sexual Offences Act 2003, after section 66 insert—

######### Sending etc photograph or film of genitals

187.66A

187.66A.1

A person (A) who intentionally sends or gives a photograph or film of any
person’s genitals to another person (B) commits an offence if—

187.66A.1.a

A intends that B will see the genitals and be caused alarm, distress or
humiliation, or

187.66A.1.b

A sends or gives such a photograph or film for the purpose of obtaining sexual
gratification and is reckless as to whether B will be caused alarm, distress
or humiliation.

187.66A.2

References to sending or giving such a photograph or film to another person
include, in particular—

187.66A.2.a

sending it to another person by any means, electronically or otherwise,

187.66A.2.b

showing it to another person, and

187.66A.2.c

placing it for a particular person to find.

187.66A.3

“ Photograph ” includes the negative as well as the positive version.

187.66A.4

“ Film ” means a moving image.

187.66A.5

References to a photograph or film also include—

187.66A.5.a

an image, whether made or altered by computer graphics or in any other way,
which appears to be a photograph or film,

187.66A.5.b

a copy of a photograph, film or image within paragraph (a), and

187.66A.5.c

data stored by any means which is capable of conversion into a photograph,
film or image within paragraph (a).

187.66A.6

A person who commits an offence under this section is liable—

187.66A.6.a

on summary conviction, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the general
limit in a magistrates’ court or a fine (or both);

187.66A.6.b

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years.

##### Sharing or threatening to share intimate photograph or film

188

In the Sexual Offences Act 2003, after section 66A (inserted by section 187),
insert—

######### Sharing or threatening to share intimate photograph or film

188.66B

188.66B.1

A person (A) commits an offence if—

188.66B.1.a

A intentionally shares a photograph or film which shows, or appears to show,
another person (B) in an intimate state,

188.66B.1.b

B does not consent to the sharing of the photograph or film, and

188.66B.1.c

A does not reasonably believe that B consents.

188.66B.2

A person (A) commits an offence if—

188.66B.2.a

A intentionally shares a photograph or film which shows, or appears to show,
another person (B) in an intimate state,

188.66B.2.b

A does so with the intention of causing B alarm, distress or humiliation, and

188.66B.2.c

B does not consent to the sharing of the photograph or film.

188.66B.3

A person (A) commits an offence if—

188.66B.3.a

A intentionally shares a photograph or film which shows, or appears to show,
another person (B) in an intimate state,

188.66B.3.b

A does so for the purpose of A or another person obtaining sexual
gratification,

188.66B.3.c

B does not consent to the sharing of the photograph or film, and

188.66B.3.d

A does not reasonably believe that B consents.

188.66B.4

A person (A) commits an offence if—

188.66B.4.a

A threatens to share a photograph or film which shows, or appears to show,
another person (B) in an intimate state, and

188.66B.4.b

A does so—

188.66B.4.b.i

with the intention that B or another person who knows B will fear that the
threat will be carried out, or

188.66B.4.b.ii

being reckless as to whether B or another person who knows B will fear that
the threat will be carried out.

188.66B.5

Subsections  (1)  to  (4)  are subject to section  66C  (exemptions).

188.66B.6

For the purposes of subsections  (1)  to  (3)  and section  66C (3)(b) —

188.66B.6.a

“consent” to the sharing of a photograph or film includes general consent
covering the particular act of sharing as well as specific consent to the
particular act of sharing, and

188.66B.6.b

whether a belief is reasonable is to be determined having regard to all the
circumstances including any steps A has taken to ascertain whether B consents.

188.66B.7

Where a person is charged with an offence under subsection  (4) , it is not
necessary for the prosecution to prove—

188.66B.7.a

that the photograph or film mentioned in the threat exists, or

188.66B.7.b

if it does exist, that it is in fact a photograph or film which shows or
appears to show a person in an intimate state.

188.66B.8

It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under subsection  (1)  to
prove that the person had a reasonable excuse for sharing the photograph or
film.

188.66B.9

A person who commits an offence under subsection  (1)  is liable on summary
conviction to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the maximum term for
summary offences or a fine (or both).

188.66B.10

A person who commits an offence under subsection  (2) ,  (3)  or  (4)  is
liable—

188.66B.10.a

on summary conviction, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the general
limit in a magistrates’ court or a fine (or both);

188.66B.10.b

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 2 years.

188.66B.11

In subsection  (9)  “ the maximum term for summary offences ” means—

188.66B.11.a

if the offence is committed before the time when section 281(5) of the
Criminal Justice Act 2003 comes into force, six months;

188.66B.11.b

if the offence is committed after that time, 51 weeks.

188.66B.12

If on the trial of a person charged with an offence under subsection  (2)  or
(3)  a magistrates’ court or jury finds the person not guilty of the offence
charged, the magistrates’ court or jury may find the person guilty of an
offence under subsection  (1) .

188.66B.13

The Crown Court has the same powers and duties in relation to a person who is
by virtue of subsection  (12)  convicted before it of an offence under
subsection  (1)  as a magistrates’ court would have on convicting the person
of the offence.

######### Sharing or threatening to share intimate photograph or film: exemptions

188.66C

188.66C.1

A person (A) who shares a photograph or film which shows, or appears to show,
another person (B) in an intimate state does not commit an offence under
section  66B (1) ,  (2)  or  (3)  if—

188.66C.1.a

the photograph or film was taken in a place to which the public or a section
of the public had or were permitted to have access (whether on payment or
otherwise),

188.66C.1.b

B had no reasonable expectation of privacy from the photograph or film being
taken, and

188.66C.1.c

B was, or A reasonably believes that B was, in the intimate state voluntarily.

188.66C.2

For the purposes of subsection  (1)(b) , whether a person had a reasonable
expectation of privacy from a photograph or film being taken is to be
determined by reference to the circumstances that the person sharing the
photograph or film reasonably believes to have existed at the time the
photograph or film was taken.

188.66C.3

A person (A) who shares a photograph or film which shows, or appears to show,
another person (B) in an intimate state does not commit an offence under
section  66B (1) ,  (2)  or  (3)  if—

188.66C.3.a

the photograph or film had, or A reasonably believes that the photograph or
film had, been previously publicly shared, and

188.66C.3.b

B had, or A reasonably believes that B had, consented to the previous sharing.

188.66C.4

A person (A) who shares a photograph or film which shows, or appears to show,
another person (B) in an intimate state does not commit an offence under
section  66B (1)  if—

188.66C.4.a

B is a person under 16,

188.66C.4.b

B lacks, or A reasonably believes that B lacks, capacity to consent to the
sharing of the photograph or film, and

188.66C.4.c

the photograph or film is shared—

188.66C.4.c.i

with a healthcare professional acting in that capacity, or

188.66C.4.c.ii

otherwise in connection with the care or treatment of B by a healthcare
professional.

188.66C.5

A person who shares a photograph or film which shows, or appears to show, a
child in an intimate state does not commit an offence under section  66B (1)
if the photograph or film is of a kind ordinarily shared between family and
friends.

188.66C.6

A person who threatens to share a photograph or film which shows, or appears
to show, another person in an intimate state does not commit an offence under
section  66B (4)  if, by reason of this section, the person would not commit
an offence under section  66B (1) ,  (2)  or  (3)  by sharing the photograph
or film in the circumstances conveyed by the threat.

######### Sharing or threatening to share intimate photograph or film: interpretation

188.66D

188.66D.1

This section applies for the purposes of sections  66B  and  66C .

188.66D.2

A person “shares” something if the person, by any means, gives or shows it to
another person or makes it available to another person.

188.66D.3

But a provider of an internet service by means of which a photograph or film
is shared is not to be regarded as a person who shares it.

188.66D.4

“ Photograph ” and “ film ” have the same meaning as in section 66A (see
subsections (3) to (5) of that section).

188.66D.5

Except where a photograph or film falls within subsection  (8) , a photograph
or film shows, or appears to show, another person in an intimate state if it
shows or appears to show—

188.66D.5.a

the person participating or engaging in an act which a reasonable person would
consider to be a sexual act,

188.66D.5.b

the person doing a thing which a reasonable person would consider to be
sexual,

188.66D.5.c

all or part of the person’s exposed genitals, buttocks or breasts,

188.66D.5.d

the person in an act of urination or defecation, or

188.66D.5.e

the person carrying out an act of personal care associated with the person’s
urination, defecation or genital or anal discharge.

188.66D.6

For the purposes of subsection  (5)(c)  the reference to all or part of a
person’s “exposed” genitals, buttocks or breasts includes—

188.66D.6.a

a reference to all or part of the person’s genitals, buttocks or breasts
visible through wet or otherwise transparent clothing,

188.66D.6.b

the case where all or part of the person’s genitals, buttocks or breasts would
be exposed but for the fact that they are covered only with underwear, and

188.66D.6.c

the case where all or part of the person’s genitals, buttocks or breasts would
be exposed but for the fact that they are obscured, provided that the area
obscured is similar to or smaller than an area that would typically be covered
by underwear worn to cover a person’s genitals, buttocks or breasts (as the
case may be).

188.66D.7

In subsection  (6)(c)  “ obscured ” means obscured by any means, other than by
clothing that a person is wearing, including, in particular, by an object, by
part of a person’s body or by digital alteration.

188.66D.8

A photograph or film falls within this subsection if (so far as it shows or
appears to show a person in an intimate state) it shows or appears to show
something, other than breastfeeding, that is of a kind ordinarily seen in
public.

188.66D.9

For the purposes of subsection  (8)  “ breastfeeding ” includes the
rearranging of clothing in the course of preparing to breastfeed or having
just finished breastfeeding.

189.2.a

189.2.b

section 1(1)(a)(iii), and

189.2.c

section 1(2).

189.3

Order 1988 ( S.I. 1988/1849 (N.I. 18) ) are repealed—

189.3.a

189.3.b

Article 3(1)(a)(iii), and

189.3.c

Article 3(2).
