### Supplementary and general

#### Providers' judgements about the status of content

##### Providers’ judgements about the status of content

192

192.1

This section sets out the approach to be taken where—

192.1.a

a system or process operated or used by a provider of a Part 3 service for the
purpose of compliance with relevant requirements,

192.1.b

a risk assessment required to be carried out by Part 3, or

192.1.c

an assessment required to be carried out by section 14,

involves a judgement by a provider about whether content is content of a
particular kind.

192.2

Such judgements are to be made on the basis of all relevant information that
is reasonably available to a provider.

192.3

In construing the reference to information that is reasonably available to a
provider, the following factors, in particular, are relevant—

192.3.a

the size and capacity of the provider, and

192.3.b

whether a judgement is made by human moderators, by means of automated systems
or processes or by means of automated systems or processes together with human
moderators.

192.4

Subsections (5) to (7) apply (as well as subsection (2)) in relation to
judgements by providers about whether content is—

192.4.a

illegal content, or illegal content of a particular kind, or

192.4.b

a fraudulent advertisement.

192.5

In making such judgements, the approach to be followed is whether a provider
has reasonable grounds to infer that content is content of the kind in
question (and a provider must treat content as content of the kind in question
if reasonable grounds for that inference exist).

192.6

Reasonable grounds for that inference exist in relation to content and an
offence if, following the approach in subsection (2), a provider—

192.6.a

has reasonable grounds to infer that all elements necessary for the commission
of the offence, including mental elements, are present or satisfied, and

192.6.b

does not have reasonable grounds to infer that a defence to the offence may be
successfully relied upon.

192.7

In the case of content generated by a bot or other automated tool, the tests
mentioned in subsection (6)(a) and (b) are to be applied in relation to the
conduct or mental state of a person who may be assumed to control the bot or
tool (or, depending what a provider knows in a particular case, the actual
person who controls the bot or tool).

192.8

In considering a provider’s compliance with relevant requirements to which
this section is relevant, OFCOM may take into account whether providers’
judgements follow the approaches set out in this section (including judgements
made by means of automated systems or processes, alone or together with human
moderators).

192.9

In this section—

      “ fraudulent advertisement ” has the meaning given by section 38 or 39
(depending on the kind of service in question);           “ illegal content ”
has the same meaning as in Part 3 (see section 59);           “ relevant
requirements ” means—         duties and requirements under this Act, and
requirements of a notice given by OFCOM under this Act.

##### OFCOM’s guidance about illegal content judgements

193

193.1

OFCOM must produce guidance for providers of Part 3 services about the matters
dealt with in section 192 so far as relating to illegal content judgements.

193.2

“ Illegal content judgements ” means—

193.2.a

judgements of a kind mentioned in subsection (4) of that section, and

193.2.b

judgements by providers about whether news publisher content amounts to a
relevant offence (see section 18 (5)  and  (10) ).

193.3

Before producing the guidance (including revised or replacement guidance),
OFCOM must consult such persons as they consider appropriate.

193.4

OFCOM must publish the guidance (and any revised or replacement guidance).

#### Time-limits for first guidance

##### Time for publishing first guidance under certain provisions of this Act

194

194.1

OFCOM must publish guidance to which this section applies within the period of
18 months beginning with the day on which this Act is passed.

194.2

This section applies to—

194.2.a

the first guidance under section 52 (3)(a)  (record-keeping and review);

194.2.b

the first guidance under section 52 (3)(b)  (children’s access assessments);

194.2.c

the first guidance under section 53(1) (content harmful to children);

194.2.d

the first guidance under section 82 (provider pornographic content);

194.2.e

the first guidance under section 99(1) (illegal content risk assessments under
section 9);

194.2.f

the first guidance under section 99(2) (illegal content risk assessments under
section 26);

194.2.g

the first guidance under section 99(3) (children’s risk assessments);

194.2.h

the first guidance under section 151 (enforcement);

194.2.i

the first guidance under section 193 relating to illegal content judgements
within the meaning of subsection (2)(a) of that section (illegal content and
fraudulent advertisements).

194.3

If OFCOM consider that it is necessary to extend the period mentioned in
subsection (1) in relation to guidance mentioned in any of paragraphs  (a)  to
(i)  of subsection  (2) , OFCOM may extend the period in relation to that
guidance by up to 12 months by making and publishing a statement.

But this is subject to subsection (6).

194.4

A statement under subsection  (3)  must set out—

194.4.a

the reasons why OFCOM consider that it is necessary to extend the period
mentioned in subsection (1) in relation to the guidance concerned, and

194.4.b

the period of extension.

194.5

A statement under subsection (3) may be published at the same time as (or
incorporate) a statement under section 43(12) (extension of time to prepare
certain codes of practice).

194.6

But a statement under subsection (3) may not be made in relation to guidance
mentioned in a particular paragraph of subsection (2) if—

194.6.a

a statement has previously been made under subsection (3) (whether in relation
to guidance mentioned in the same or a different paragraph of subsection (2)),
or

194.6.b

a statement has previously been made under section 43(12).

#### Liability of providers etc

##### Providers that are not legal persons

195

195.1

In this section a “ relevant entity ” means an entity that—

195.1.a

is the provider of a regulated service, and

195.1.b

is not a legal person under the law under which it is formed.

195.2

If a penalty notice is given to a relevant entity (in the name of the entity),
the penalty must be paid out of the entity’s funds.

195.3

If a notice is given by OFCOM to a relevant entity (in the name of the entity)
under any provision of this Act, the notice continues to have effect despite a
change in the membership of the entity.

195.4

If a penalty notice is given jointly to two or more officers or members of a
relevant entity, those individuals are jointly and severally liable to pay the
penalty under it.

195.5

In subsection  (4)  the reference to officers or members of a relevant entity
includes a reference to employees of such an entity or any other individuals
associated with such an entity.

195.6

In this section a “ penalty notice ” means—

195.6.a

a confirmation decision that imposes a penalty (see sections 132 (5)(b)  and
137),

195.6.b

a penalty notice under section 139,

195.6.c

a penalty notice under section 140 (5) , or

195.6.d

a penalty notice under section 141 (6) .

##### Individuals providing regulated services: liability

196

196.1

This section applies in relation to two or more individuals who together are
the provider of a regulated service (see section 226 (3) ,  (5) ,  (7) ,  (9)
and  (11) ).

196.2

Any duty or requirement imposed on such a provider under any of the provisions
specified in subsection  (3) , or any liability of such a provider to pay a
fee under section 84 or Schedule 10, is to be taken to be imposed on, or to be
a liability of, all the individuals jointly and severally.

196.3

The provisions are—

196.3.a

Chapter 2 of Part 3 (providers of user-to-user services: duties of care);

196.3.b

Chapter 3 of Part 3 (providers of search services: duties of care);

196.3.c

Chapter 4 of Part 3 (children’s access assessments);

196.3.d

Chapter 5 of Part 3 (duties about fraudulent advertising);

196.3.e

Chapter 1 of Part 4 (user identity verification);

196.3.f

Chapter 2 of Part 4 (reporting CSEA content);

196.3.g

Chapter 3 of Part 4 (terms of service: transparency, accountability and
freedom of expression);

196.3.h

Chapter 4 of Part 4 (deceased child users);

196.3.i

Chapter 5 of Part 4 (transparency reporting);

196.3.j

section 81 (provider pornographic content);

196.3.k

section 83 (duty to notify OFCOM).

196.4

A notice in respect of a matter that may or must be given by OFCOM under any
provision of this Act may be given—

196.4.a

to only one of the individuals,

196.4.b

jointly to two or more of them, or

196.4.c

jointly to all of them,

but a separate notice may not be given to each of the individuals in respect
of the matter.

196.5

If a penalty notice is given jointly to two or more individuals, those
individuals are jointly and severally liable to pay the penalty under it.

196.6

In subsection  (5)  a “ penalty notice ” means—

196.6.a

a confirmation decision that imposes a penalty (see sections 132 (5)(b)  and
137),

196.6.b

a penalty notice under section 139,

196.6.c

a penalty notice under section 140 (5) , or

196.6.d

a penalty notice under section 141 (6) .

##### Liability of parent entities etc

197

Schedule 15 contains provision about—

197.a

the giving of joint provisional notices of contravention to parent entities
etc,

197.b

the liability of parent entities for failures by subsidiary entities,

197.c

the liability of subsidiary entities for failures by parent entities,

197.d

the liability of fellow subsidiary entities for failures by subsidiary
entities, and

197.e

the liability of controlling individuals for failures by entities.

##### Former providers of regulated services

198

198.1

A power conferred by Chapter 6 of Part 7 (enforcement powers) to give a notice
to a provider of a regulated service is to be read as including power to give
a notice to a person who was, at the relevant time, a provider of such a
service but who has ceased to be a provider of such a service (and that
Chapter and Schedules 13 and 15 are to be read accordingly).

198.2

“ The relevant time ” means—

198.2.a

the time of the failure to which the notice relates, or

198.2.b

in the case of a notice which relates to the requirement in section 105(1) to
co-operate with an investigation, the time of the failure or possible failure
to which the investigation relates.

#### Offences

##### Information offences: supplementary

199

199.1

Proceedings against a person for an offence under section 109 (1)  or
paragraph  18(1)(b)  of Schedule 12 may be brought only if—

199.1.a

OFCOM have given the person a provisional notice of contravention in respect
of the failure to comply with the requirements of an information notice or the
requirements imposed by a person acting under Schedule 12 (as the case may
be),

199.1.b

OFCOM have given the person a confirmation decision in respect of that failure
imposing requirements of a kind described in section 133 (1)  and the time
allowed for compliance with the decision has expired without those
requirements having been complied with,

199.1.c

OFCOM have not imposed a penalty on the person in respect of that failure,

199.1.d

a service restriction order under section 144 has not been made in relation to
a regulated service provided by the person in respect of that failure, and

199.1.e

an access restriction order under section 146 has not been made in relation to
a regulated service provided by the person in respect of that failure.

199.2

Proceedings for an offence under section 110 (2)  (failure by named senior
manager to prevent offence under section 109 (1) ) may be brought only if the
conditions in subsection  (1)  are met in respect of the offence under section
109 (1) .

199.3

Where a penalty has been imposed on a person in respect of an act or omission
constituting an offence under section 69 or 109 or paragraph  18  of Schedule
12, no proceedings may be brought against the person for that offence.

199.4

Where a penalty has been imposed on an entity in respect of an act or omission
constituting an offence under section 109, no proceedings for an offence under
section 110 may be brought against an individual in respect of a failure to
prevent that offence.

199.5

A penalty may not be imposed on a person in respect of an act or omission
constituting an offence under section 69 or 109 or paragraph  18  of Schedule
12 if—

199.5.a

proceedings for the offence have been brought against the person but have not
been concluded, or

199.5.b

the person has been convicted of the offence.

199.6

In this section “ penalty ” means a penalty imposed by—

199.6.a

a confirmation decision (see sections 132 (5)(b)  and 137), or

199.6.b

a penalty notice under section 139.

##### Offence of failure to comply with confirmation decision: supplementary

200

200.1

Where a penalty has been imposed on a person by a penalty notice under section
139 in respect of a failure constituting an offence under section 138 (failure
to comply with certain requirements of a confirmation decision), no
proceedings may be brought against the person for that offence.

200.2

A penalty may not be imposed on a person by a penalty notice under section 139
in respect of a failure constituting an offence under section 138 if—

200.2.a

proceedings for the offence have been brought against the person but have not
been concluded, or

200.2.b

the person has been convicted of the offence.

200.3

Where a service restriction order under section 144 or an access restriction
order under section 146 has been made in relation to a regulated service
provided by a person in respect of a failure constituting an offence under
section 138, no proceedings may be brought against the person for that
offence.

##### Defences

201

201.1

Subsection (2) applies where a person relies on a defence under section 109 or
110.

201.2

If evidence is adduced which is sufficient to raise an issue with respect to
the defence, the court must assume that the defence is satisfied unless the
prosecution proves beyond reasonable doubt that it is not.

##### Liability of corporate officers for offences

202

202.1

In this section a “ relevant entity ” means an entity that is—

202.1.a

the provider of a regulated service, and

202.1.b

a legal person under the law under which it is formed.

202.2

If an offence is committed by a relevant entity and it is proved that the
offence—

202.2.a

has been committed with the consent or connivance of an officer of the entity,
or

202.2.b

is attributable to any neglect on the part of an officer of the entity,

the officer (as well as the entity) commits the offence and (subject to
section 199 (1) ) is liable to be proceeded against and punished accordingly.

202.3

In relation to an entity which is a body corporate, “ officer ” means—

202.3.a

a director, manager, associate, secretary or other similar officer, or

202.3.b

a person purporting to act in any such capacity.

In paragraph  (a)  “ director ”, in relation to a body corporate whose affairs
are managed by its members, means a member of the body corporate.

202.4

In relation to a partnership which is not regarded as a body corporate under
the law under which it is formed, “ officer ” means—

202.4.a

a partner, or

202.4.b

a person purporting to act as a partner.

202.5

In this section—

      “ body corporate ” includes an entity incorporated outside the United
Kingdom;           “ offence ” means an offence under this Act, except under
Part 10.

##### Application of offences to providers that are not legal persons

203

203.1

In this section a “ relevant entity ” means an entity that—

203.1.a

is the provider of a regulated service, and

203.1.b

is not a legal person under the law under which it is formed.

203.2

Proceedings for an offence alleged to have been committed by a relevant entity
must be brought against the entity in its own name (and not in that of any of
its officers or members).

203.3

For the purposes of such proceedings—

203.3.a

rules of court relating to the service of documents have effect as if the
entity were a body corporate; and

203.3.b

the following provisions apply as they apply in relation to a body corporate—

203.3.b.i

section 33 of the Criminal Justice Act 1925 and Schedule 3 to the Magistrates’
Courts Act 1980;

203.3.b.ii

section 18 of the  Criminal Justice Act (Northern Ireland) 1945 (c. 15 (N.I.))
and Article 166 of, and Schedule 4 to, the Magistrates’ Courts (Northern
Ireland) Order 1981 ( S.I. 1981/1675 (N.I. 26) ).

203.4

A fine imposed on a relevant entity on its conviction of an offence must be
paid out of the entity’s funds.

203.5

If an offence is committed by a relevant entity and it is proved that the
offence—

203.5.a

has been committed with the consent or connivance of an officer of the entity,
or

203.5.b

is attributable to any neglect on the part of an officer of the entity,

the officer (as well as the entity) commits the offence and (subject to
section 199 (1) ) is liable to be proceeded against and punished accordingly.

203.6

In relation to a partnership, “ officer ” means—

203.6.a

a partner, or

203.6.b

a person purporting to act as a partner.

203.7

In relation to a relevant entity other than a partnership, “ officer ” means—

203.7.a

an officer of the entity or a person concerned in the management or control of
the entity, or

203.7.b

a person purporting to act in such a capacity.

203.8

Subsection  (2)  is not to be read as prejudicing any liability of an officer
under subsection  (5) .

203.9

In this section “ offence ” means an offence under this Act, except under Part
10.

#### Extra-territorial application

##### Extra-territorial application

204

204.1

References in this Act to an internet service, a user-to-user service or a
search service include such a service provided from outside the United Kingdom
(as well as such a service provided from within the United Kingdom).

204.2

The power to require the production of documents by an information notice
includes power to require the production of documents held outside the United
Kingdom.

204.3

The power conferred by section 106 includes power to require the attendance
for interview of an individual who is outside the United Kingdom.

204.4

Sections 133(9) and 150(11) (requirements enforceable in civil proceedings
against a person) apply whether or not the person is in the United Kingdom.

##### Offences: extra-territorial application and jurisdiction

205

205.1

Sections 69, 109 and 112 apply to acts done by a person in the United Kingdom
or elsewhere (information offences).

205.2

Section 110 applies to acts done by an individual in the United Kingdom or
elsewhere (offences by senior managers of providers of regulated services).

205.3

Section 138 applies to acts done by a person in the United Kingdom or
elsewhere (offence of failure to comply with confirmation decision).

205.4

Sections 202 (2)  and 203 (5) , so far as relating to an offence under a
section specified in subsection  (1)  or  (3)  of this section, apply to acts
done by an individual in the United Kingdom or elsewhere (liability of
directors etc of providers of regulated services).

205.5

In the case of an offence under section 69, 109, 110, 112 or 138 which is
committed outside the United Kingdom—

205.5.a

proceedings for the offence may be taken at any place in the United Kingdom,
and

205.5.b

the offence may for all incidental purposes be treated as having been
committed at any such place.

205.6

In the application of subsection  (5)  to Scotland, any such proceedings
against a person may be taken—

205.6.a

in any sheriff court district in which the person is apprehended or is in
custody, or

205.6.b

in such sheriff court district as the Lord Advocate may determine.

205.7

In this section—

      “ act ” includes a failure to act;           “ sheriff court district ”
is to be construed in accordance with the Criminal Procedure (Scotland) Act
1995 (see section 307(1) of that Act).

#### Payment of sums into Consolidated Fund

##### Payment of sums into the Consolidated Fund

206

206.1

Section 400 of the Communications Act (destination of penalties etc) is
amended as follows.

206.2

In subsection (1), after paragraph (i) insert—

206.2.j

an amount paid to OFCOM in respect of a penalty imposed by them under Chapter
6 of Part 7 of the Online Safety Act 2023;

206.2.k

an amount paid to OFCOM in respect of an additional fee charged under Schedule
10 to the Online Safety Act 2023.

206.3

In subsection (2), after “applies” insert  “(except an amount mentioned in
subsection (1)(j) or (k))” .

206.4

After subsection (3) insert—

206.4.3A

Where OFCOM receive an amount mentioned in subsection (1)(j) or (k), it must
be paid into the Consolidated Fund of the United Kingdom.

206.5

In the heading, omit “licence”.

#### Publication by OFCOM

##### Publication by OFCOM

207

Anything required by this Act to be published by OFCOM must be published in
such manner as OFCOM consider appropriate for bringing it to the attention of
the persons who, in their opinion, are likely to be affected by it.

#### Service of notices

##### Service of notices

208

208.1

This section applies in relation to a notice that may or must be given by
OFCOM to a person under any provision of this Act.

208.2

OFCOM may give a notice to a person by—

208.2.a

delivering it by hand to the person,

208.2.b

leaving it at the person’s proper address,

208.2.c

sending it by post to the person at that address, or

208.2.d

sending it by email to the person’s email address.

208.3

A notice to a body corporate may be given to any officer of that body.

208.4

A notice to a partnership may be given to any partner or to a person who has
the control or management of the partnership business.

208.5

A notice to an entity that is not a legal person under the law under which it
is formed (other than a partnership) may be given to any member of the
governing body of the entity.

208.6

In the case of a notice given to a person who is a provider of a regulated
service, the person’s proper address for the purposes of paragraphs  (b)  and
(c)  of subsection  (2) , and section 7 of the Interpretation Act 1978 in its
application to those paragraphs, is any address (within or outside the United
Kingdom) at which OFCOM believe, on reasonable grounds, that the notice will
come to the attention of the person or (where the person is an entity) any
director or other officer of that entity.

208.7

In the case of a notice given to a person other than a provider of a regulated
service, a person’s proper address for the purposes of paragraphs  (b)  and
(c)  of subsection  (2) , and section 7 of the Interpretation Act 1978 in its
application to those paragraphs, is—

208.7.a

in the case of an entity, the address of the entity’s registered or principal
office;

208.7.b

in any other case, the person’s last known address.

208.8

In the case of an entity registered or carrying on business outside the United
Kingdom, or with offices outside the United Kingdom, the reference in
subsection  (7)  to its principal office includes its principal office in the
United Kingdom or, if the entity has no office in the United Kingdom, any
place in the United Kingdom at which OFCOM believe, on reasonable grounds,
that the notice will come to the attention of any director or other officer of
that entity.

208.9

In the case of a notice given to an individual under section 106 (interviews),
the reference in subsection  (7)  to the person’s last known address is to the
individual’s home address or, if the individual is currently connected with a
provider of a regulated service, the address of the provider’s registered or
principal office.

208.10

For the purposes of subsection  (2)(d) , a person’s email address is—

208.10.a

any email address published for the time being by that person as an address
for contacting that person, or

208.10.b

if there is no such published address, any email address by means of which
OFCOM believe, on reasonable grounds, that the notice will come to the
attention of that person or (where that person is an entity) any director or
other officer of that entity.

208.11

A notice sent by email is treated as given 48 hours after it was sent, unless
the contrary is proved.

208.12

In this section—

      “ director ” includes any person occupying the position of a director,
by whatever name called;           “ officer ”, in relation to an entity,
includes a director, a manager, a partner, an associate, a secretary or, where
the affairs of the entity are managed by its members, a member.

that Part);

211.1.b

in connection with the repeal of Part 4B of the Communications Act.

211.2

211.3

211.3.b

Schedule 17.

211.4

or engaged by OFCOM, or assisting OFCOM in the exercise of any of their online
safety functions (within the meaning of section 235 of the Online Safety Act
2023), and

213.2.5A.b

the person published the article for the purposes of OFCOM’s exercise of any
