#### Power to amend Act to regulate app stores

##### Power to regulate app stores

215

215.1

Subject to the following provisions of this section and section 216, the
Secretary of State may by regulations amend any provision of this Act to make
provision for or in connection with the regulation of internet services that
are app stores.

215.2

Regulations under this section may not be made before OFCOM have published a
report under section 161 (report about use of app stores by children).

215.3

Regulations under this section may be made only if the Secretary of State,
having considered that report, considers that there is a material risk of
significant harm to an appreciable number of children presented by either of
the following, or by both taken together—

215.3.a

harmful content present on app stores, or

215.3.b

harmful content encountered by means of regulated apps available in app
stores.

215.4

Before making regulations under this section the Secretary of State must
consult—

215.4.a

persons who appear to the Secretary of State to represent providers of app
stores,

215.4.b

persons who appear to the Secretary of State to represent the interests of
children (generally or with particular reference to online safety matters),

215.4.c

OFCOM,

215.4.d

the Information Commissioner,

215.4.e

the Children’s Commissioner, and

215.4.f

such other persons as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

215.5

In this section and in section 216—

      “ amend ” includes repeal and apply (with or without modifications);
“ app ” includes an app for use on any kind of device, and “app store” is to
be read accordingly;           “ content that is harmful to children ” has the
same meaning as in Part 3 (see section 60);           “ harmful content ”
means—         content that is harmful to children,           search content
that is harmful to children, and           regulated provider pornographic
content;                 “ regulated app ” means an app for a regulated
service;           “ regulated provider pornographic content ” has the same
meaning as in Part 5 (see section 79);           “ search content ” has the
same meaning as in Part 3 (see section 57).

215.6

In this section and in section 216 references to children are to children in
the United Kingdom.

##### Power to regulate app stores: supplementary

216

216.1

In this section (except in subsection  (4)(c) ) “ regulations ” means
regulations under section 215(1).

216.2

Provision may be made by regulations only for or in connection with the
purposes of minimising or mitigating the risks of harm to children presented
by harmful content as mentioned in section 215(3)(a) and (b).

216.3

Regulations may not have the effect that any body other than OFCOM is the
regulator in relation to app stores.

216.4

Regulations may—

216.4.a

make provision exempting specified descriptions of app stores from regulation
under this Act;

216.4.b

make provision amending Part 2, section 55 or Schedule 1 in connection with
provision mentioned in paragraph  (a) ;

216.4.c

make provision corresponding or similar to provision which may be made by
regulations under paragraph 1 of Schedule 11 (“threshold conditions”), with
the effect that only app stores which meet specified conditions are regulated
by this Act.

216.5

Regulations may make provision having the effect that app stores provided from
outside the United Kingdom are regulated by this Act (as well as app stores
provided from within the United Kingdom), but, if they do so, must contain
provision corresponding or similar to section 4(5) and (6) (UK links).

216.6

The provision that may be made by regulations includes provision—

216.6.a

imposing on providers of app stores duties corresponding or similar to duties
imposed on providers of Part 3 services by—

216.6.a.i

section 11 or 12 (children’s online safety: user-to-user services) or any of
sections 20 to 23 so far as relating to section 11 or 12;

216.6.a.ii

section 28 or 29 (children’s online safety: search services) or any of
sections 31 to 34 so far as relating to section 28 or 29;

216.6.b

imposing on providers of app stores duties corresponding or similar to duties
imposed on providers of internet services within section 80(2) by section 81
(duties about regulated provider pornographic content);

216.6.c

imposing on providers of app stores requirements corresponding or similar to
requirements imposed on providers of regulated services by, or by OFCOM under,
Part 6 (fees);

216.6.d

imposing on OFCOM duties in relation to app stores corresponding or similar to
duties imposed in relation to Part 3 services by Chapter 3 of Part 7 (OFCOM’s
register of risks, and risk profiles);

216.6.e

conferring on OFCOM functions in relation to app stores corresponding or
similar to the functions that OFCOM have in relation to regulated services
under—

216.6.e.i

Chapter 4 of Part 7 (information), or

216.6.e.ii

Chapter 6 of Part 7 (enforcement), including provisions of that Chapter
conferring power for OFCOM to impose monetary penalties;

216.6.f

about OFCOM’s production of guidance or a code of practice relating to any
aspect of the regulation of app stores that is included in the regulations.

216.7

The provision that may be made by regulations includes provision having the
effect that app stores fall within the definition of “Part 3 service” or “
regulated service ” for the purposes of specified provisions of this Act (with
the effect that specified provisions of this Act which apply in relation to
Part 3 services or regulated services, or to providers of Part 3 services or
regulated services, also apply in relation to app stores or to providers of
app stores).

216.8

Regulations may not amend or make provision corresponding or similar to—

216.8.a

Chapter 2 of Part 4 (reporting CSEA content),

216.8.b

Chapter 5 of Part 7 (notices to deal with terrorism content and CSEA content),
or

216.8.c

Part 10 (communications offences).

216.9

Regulations may make different provision with regard to app stores of
different kinds.

216.10

In this section “ specified ” means specified in regulations.

#### Power to amend Act: alternative dispute resolution

##### Power to impose duty about alternative dispute resolution procedure

217

217.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend this Act for or in connection
with the imposition on providers of Category 1 services of an ADR duty.

217.2

An “ADR duty”—

217.2.a

is a duty requiring providers of Category 1 services to arrange for and engage
in an alternative dispute resolution procedure in specified circumstances for
the resolution of disputes about their handling of relevant complaints, and

217.2.b

may include a duty requiring such providers to meet the costs incurred by any
other person in using a dispute resolution procedure which is so arranged.

217.3

Complaints are “ relevant ” for the purposes of subsection (2)(a) if they—

217.3.a

relate to a Category 1 service,

217.3.b

are of a specified kind, and

217.3.c

are made by persons of a specified kind.

217.4

Regulations under this section may not be made before the publication of a
statement by the Secretary of State responding to OFCOM’s report under section
160 (report about reporting and complaints procedures in use by providers of
Part 3 services: see subsection (10) of that section).

217.5

Before making regulations under this section the Secretary of State must
consult—

217.5.a

OFCOM,

217.5.b

the Information Commissioner, and

217.5.c

such other persons as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

217.6

If the power conferred by subsection (1) is exercised, the first regulations
made under the power must—

217.6.a

require the use of a dispute resolution procedure which is impartial, and

217.6.b

prohibit the use of a dispute resolution procedure which restricts or excludes
the availability of civil proceedings.

217.7

Provision made by regulations under this section may have the effect that the
duties set out in any or all of sections 21, 22 and 23 which apply in relation
to duties imposed by other provisions of Chapter 2 of Part 3 are also to apply
in relation to the ADR duty, and accordingly the regulations may amend—

217.7.a

section 21(6),

217.7.b

the definition of “safety measures and policies” in section 22(8), or

217.7.c

the definition of “relevant duties” in section 23 (11) .

217.8

The provisions of this Act that may be amended by the regulations in
connection with the imposition of the ADR duty include, but are not limited
to, the following provisions (in addition to those mentioned in subsection
(7))—

217.8.a

section 7(5),

217.8.b

section 104 (13)(a) , and

217.8.c

section 131(2).

217.9

If the power conferred by subsection (1) is exercised, the first regulations
made under the power must require OFCOM to—

217.9.a

produce and publish guidance for providers of Category 1 services to assist
them in complying with the ADR duty, and

217.9.b

consult the Secretary of State, the Information Commissioner and such other
persons as OFCOM consider appropriate before producing the guidance.

217.10

Section 204(1) applies for the purposes of the references to Category 1
services in this section.

217.11

In this section “ specified ” means specified in regulations under this
section.

217.12

For the meaning of “Category 1 service”, see section 95 (register of
categories of services).

#### Other powers to amend Act

##### Power to amend section 40

218

218.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend section 40 (fraud etc
offences).

But the power to add an offence to that section is limited by subsections (2)
and (3).

218.2

An offence may be added to section 40 only if the Secretary of State considers
it appropriate to do so because of—

218.2.a

the prevalence on Category 1 services of content (other than regulated user-
generated content) consisting of paid-for advertisements that amount to that
offence, or the prevalence in or via search results of Category 2A services of
paid-for advertisements that amount to that offence,

218.2.b

the risk of harm to individuals in the United Kingdom presented by such
advertisements, and

218.2.c

the severity of that harm.

218.3

An offence may not be added to section 40 if—

218.3.a

the offence concerns—

218.3.a.i

the infringement of intellectual property rights,

218.3.a.ii

the safety or quality of goods (as opposed to what kind of goods they are), or

218.3.a.iii

the performance of a service by a person not qualified to perform it; or

218.3.b

it is an offence under the Consumer Protection from Unfair Trading Regulations
2008 ( S.I. 2008/1277 ).

218.4

In this section—

218.4.a

“ regulated user-generated content ” has the same meaning as in Part 3 (see
section 55);

218.4.b

the words “in or via search results” are to be construed in accordance with
section 39;

218.4.c

references to advertisements that amount to an offence are to be construed in
accordance with section 59 (see subsections (3), (11) and (12) of that
section).

##### Powers to amend sections 61 and 62

219

219.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend—

219.1.a

section 61 (primary priority content that is harmful to children);

219.1.b

section 62 (priority content that is harmful to children).

But the power to add a kind of content is limited by subsections (2) to (4).

219.2

A kind of content may be added to section 61 only if the Secretary of State
considers that, in relation to Part 3 services—

219.2.a

there is a material risk of significant harm to an appreciable number of
children presented by content of that kind that is regulated user-generated
content or search content, and

219.2.b

it is appropriate for the duties set out in sections 12(3)(a) and 29(3)(a)
(duty in relation to children of all ages) to apply in relation to content of
that kind.

219.3

A kind of content may be added to section 62 only if the Secretary of State
considers that, in relation to Part 3 services, there is a material risk of
significant harm to an appreciable number of children presented by content of
that kind that is regulated user-generated content or search content.

219.4

A kind of content may not be added to section 61 or 62 if the risk of harm
presented by content of that kind flows from—

219.4.a

the content’s potential financial impact,

219.4.b

the safety or quality of goods featured in the content, or

219.4.c

the way in which a service featured in the content may be performed (for
example, in the case of the performance of a service by a person not qualified
to perform it).

219.5

The Secretary of State must consult OFCOM before making regulations under this
section.

219.6

In this section references to children are to children in the United Kingdom.

219.7

In this section—

“ regulated user-generated content ” has the same meaning as in Part 3 (see
section 55); “ search content ” has the same meaning as in Part 3 (see section
57).

##### Powers to amend or repeal provisions relating to exempt content or services

220

220.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

220.1.a

amend section 55(5), or

220.1.b

repeal section 55 (2)(d)  and  (5) , and make a consequential amendment of
sections 3(6), 5(2)(a) and 55 (2)(f) ,

if the Secretary of State considers that it is appropriate to do so because of
the risk of harm to individuals in the United Kingdom presented by one-to-one
live aural communications.

220.2

Subject to subsection (3), the Secretary of State may by regulations amend
section 55(2)(e),  (6)  or  (7)  if the Secretary of State considers that it
is appropriate to do so because of the risk of harm to individuals in the
United Kingdom presented by comments and reviews on provider content.

220.3

Regulations under subsection (2) may not have the effect that comments and
reviews on provider content present on a service of which the provider is a
recognised news publisher become regulated user-generated content within the
meaning of Part 3.

220.4

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend Part 1 of Schedule 1 to
provide for a further description of user-to-user service or search service to
be exempt, if the Secretary of State considers that the risk of harm to
individuals in the United Kingdom presented by a service of that description
is low.

220.5

Regulations under subsection  (4)  may amend sections 3, 5 and 55 and Schedule
2 in connection with the amendment of Part 1 of Schedule 1.

220.6

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend Schedule 9 to provide for a
further description of internet service to be included, if the Secretary of
State considers that the risk of harm to children in the United Kingdom
presented by regulated provider pornographic content published or displayed on
a service of that description is low.

220.7

If the condition in subsection  (8)  is met, the Secretary of State may by
regulations amend or repeal either of the following—

220.7.a

paragraph 3 of Schedule 1 (services offering only one-to-one live aural
communications);

220.7.b

any provision of that Schedule added in exercise of the power conferred by
subsection  (4) .

220.8

The condition is that the Secretary of State considers that it is appropriate
to amend or repeal the provision in question (as the case may be) because of
the risk of harm to individuals in the United Kingdom presented by a service
of the description in question.

220.9

Subject to subsection (10), the Secretary of State may by regulations amend
paragraph 4 of Schedule 1 (limited functionality services) if the Secretary of
State considers that it is appropriate because of the risk of harm to
individuals in the United Kingdom presented by a service described in that
paragraph.

220.10

Regulations under subsection (9) may not have the effect that a service
described in paragraph 4 of Schedule 1 of which the provider is a recognised
news publisher is no longer exempt under that paragraph.

220.11

Regulations under subsection  (7)  may amend or repeal a provision of Schedule
2 in connection with the amendment or repeal of a provision of Part 1 of
Schedule 1.

220.12

Regulations under subsection  (7)(b)  may amend or repeal a provision of
sections 3, 5 and 55 in connection with the amendment or repeal of a provision
of Part 1 of Schedule 1.

220.13

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend or repeal any provision of
Schedule 9 added in exercise of the power conferred by subsection  (6) , if
the Secretary of State considers that it is appropriate to do so because of
the risk of harm to children in the United Kingdom presented by regulated
provider pornographic content published or displayed on a service of that
description.

220.14

In this section—

      “comments and reviews on provider content” and “one-to-one live aural
communications” have the meaning given by section 55;           “ recognised
news publisher ” has the meaning given by section 56;           “ regulated
provider pornographic content ” and “ published or displayed ” have the same
meaning as in Part 5 (see section 79).

##### Powers to amend Part 2 of Schedule 1

221

######## England

221.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend the part of the list in Part 2
of Schedule 1 which relates to England—

221.1.a

if there has been an amendment or repeal of legislation, or of a provision of
legislation, by reference to which a description of education or childcare is
framed;

221.1.b

to add a further description of education or childcare, if the Secretary of
State considers that it is appropriate to do so because of the application of
enactments other than this Act, or guidance or requirements (however referred
to) produced under enactments other than this Act, to persons providing
education or childcare of that description;

221.1.c

to omit a description of education or childcare, if the Secretary of State
considers that it is appropriate to do so because of the risk of harm to
individuals in England presented by services provided by persons providing
education or childcare of that description which are provided for the purposes
of such education or childcare (other than a service described in paragraph 7
of Schedule 1).

221.2

In subsection  (1)(b) , “ enactment ” includes an enactment contained in
subordinate legislation (within the meaning of the Interpretation Act 1978).

######## Scotland

221.3

The Scottish Ministers may by regulations amend the part of the list in Part 2
of Schedule 1 which relates to Scotland—

221.3.a

if there has been an amendment or repeal of legislation, or of a provision of
legislation, by reference to which a description of education or childcare is
framed;

221.3.b

to add a further description of education or childcare, if the Scottish
Ministers consider that it is appropriate to do so because of the application
of enactments other than this Act, or guidance or requirements (however
referred to) produced under enactments other than this Act, to persons
providing education or childcare of that description;

221.3.c

to omit a description of education or childcare, if the Scottish Ministers
consider that it is appropriate to do so because of the risk of harm to
individuals in Scotland presented by services provided by persons providing
education or childcare of that description which are provided for the purposes
of such education or childcare (other than a service described in paragraph 7
of Schedule 1).

221.4

In subsection  (3)(b) , “ enactment ” includes an enactment contained in, or
in an instrument made under, an Act of the Scottish Parliament.

######## Wales

221.5

The Welsh Ministers may by regulations made by statutory instrument amend the
part of the list in Part 2 of Schedule 1 which relates to Wales—

221.5.a

if there has been an amendment or repeal of legislation, or of a provision of
legislation, by reference to which a description of education or childcare is
framed;

221.5.b

to add a further description of education or childcare, if the Welsh Ministers
consider that it is appropriate to do so because of the application of
enactments other than this Act, or guidance or requirements (however referred
to) produced under enactments other than this Act, to persons providing
education or childcare of that description;

221.5.c

to omit a description of education or childcare, if the Welsh Ministers
consider that it is appropriate to do so because of the risk of harm to
individuals in Wales presented by services provided by persons providing
education or childcare of that description which are provided for the purposes
of such education or childcare (other than a service described in paragraph 7
of Schedule 1).

221.6

In subsection  (5)(b) , “ enactment ” includes an enactment contained in, or
in an instrument made under, a Measure or Act of Senedd Cymru.

######## Northern Ireland

221.7

The relevant Department may by regulations amend the part of the list in Part
2 of Schedule 1 which relates to Northern Ireland—

221.7.a

if there has been an amendment or repeal of legislation, or of a provision of
legislation, by reference to which a description of education or childcare is
framed;

221.7.b

to add a further description of education or childcare, if the relevant
Department considers that it is appropriate to do so because of the
application of enactments other than this Act, or guidance or requirements
(however referred to) produced under enactments other than this Act, to
persons providing education or childcare of that description;

221.7.c

to omit a description of education or childcare, if the relevant Department
considers that it is appropriate to do so because of the risk of harm to
individuals in Northern Ireland presented by services provided by persons
providing education or childcare of that description which are provided for
the purposes of such education or childcare (other than a service described in
paragraph 7 of Schedule 1).

221.8

In subsection  (7) , “ the relevant Department ” means—

221.8.a

where the amendment relates to childcare, primary education or secondary
education, the Department of Education in Northern Ireland;

221.8.b

where the amendment relates to further education or higher education, the
Department for the Economy in Northern Ireland with the concurrence of the
Department of Agriculture, Environment and Rural Affairs in Northern Ireland,
or the Department of Agriculture, Environment and Rural Affairs in Northern
Ireland with the concurrence of the Department for the Economy in Northern
Ireland;

221.8.c

where the amendment relates to education in agriculture and related subjects,
the Department of Agriculture, Environment and Rural Affairs in Northern
Ireland.

221.9

In subsection  (7)(b) , “ enactment ” includes an enactment contained in, or
in an instrument made under, Northern Ireland legislation.

######## Interpretation

221.10

In this section, the following terms have the same meaning as in Schedule 1—

“childcare”; “education”; “education in agriculture and related subjects”;
“further education”; “higher education”; “primary education”; “secondary
education”.

##### Powers to amend Schedules 5, 6 and 7

222

222.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend—

222.1.a

Schedule 5 (terrorism offences);

222.1.b

Part 1 of Schedule 6 (child sexual exploitation and abuse offences).

222.2

The Scottish Ministers may by regulations amend Part 2 of Schedule 6.

222.3

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend Schedule 7 (priority
offences).

But an offence may be added to that Schedule only on the grounds in subsection
(4) or (5), and subsection (6) limits the power to add an offence.

222.4

The first ground for adding an offence to Schedule 7 is that the Secretary of
State considers it appropriate to do so because of—

222.4.a

the prevalence on regulated user-to-user services of regulated user-generated
content that amounts to that offence, or the prevalence on regulated search
services and combined services of search content that amounts to that offence,

222.4.b

the risk of harm to individuals in the United Kingdom presented by regulated
user-generated content or search content that amounts to that offence, and

222.4.c

the severity of that harm.

222.5

The second ground for adding an offence to Schedule 7 is that the Secretary of
State considers it appropriate to do so because of—

222.5.a

the prevalence of the use of regulated user-to-user services for the
commission or facilitation of that offence,

222.5.b

the risk of harm to individuals in the United Kingdom presented by the use of
such services for the commission or facilitation of that offence, and

222.5.c

the severity of that harm.

222.6

An offence may not be added to Schedule 7 if—

222.6.a

the offence concerns—

222.6.a.i

the infringement of intellectual property rights,

222.6.a.ii

the safety or quality of goods (as opposed to what kind of goods they are), or

222.6.a.iii

the performance of a service by a person not qualified to perform it; or

222.6.b

it is an offence under the Consumer Protection from Unfair Trading Regulations
2008 ( S.I. 2008/1277 ).

222.7

The Secretary of State must consult the Scottish Ministers before making
regulations under subsection (3) which—

222.7.a

add an offence that extends only to Scotland, or

222.7.b

amend or remove an entry specifying an offence that extends only to Scotland.

222.8

The Secretary of State must consult the Department of Justice in Northern
Ireland before making regulations under subsection (3) which—

222.8.a

add an offence that extends only to Northern Ireland, or

222.8.b

amend or remove an entry specifying an offence that extends only to Northern
Ireland.

222.9

In this section—

222.9.a

“ regulated user-generated content ” has the same meaning as in Part 3 (see
section 55);

222.9.b

“ search content ” has the same meaning as in Part 3 (see section 57);

222.9.c

references to content that amounts to an offence are to be construed in
accordance with section 59 (see subsections (3), (11) and (12) of that
section).

#### Regulations

##### Power to make consequential provision

223

223.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision that is consequential
on this Act or regulations under this Act.

223.2

The regulations may—

223.2.a

amend or repeal provision made by the Communications Act;

223.2.b

amend or revoke provision made under that Act.

223.3

The regulations may make transitional, transitory or saving provision.

##### Regulations: general

224

224.1

Regulations under this Act may make different provision for different purposes
and may, in particular—

224.1.a

make different provision with regard to—

224.1.a.i

user-to-user services,

224.1.a.ii

search services, and

224.1.a.iii

internet services, other than regulated user-to-user services or regulated
search services, that are within section 80 (2) ;

224.1.b

make different provision with regard to user-to-user services of different
kinds;

224.1.c

make different provision with regard to search services of different kinds;

224.1.d

make different provision with regard to different kinds of services mentioned
in paragraph  (a)(iii) ;

224.1.e

make different provision with regard to different kinds of internet services
within section 80 (2) .

224.2

A power to make regulations under this Act includes power to make
supplementary, incidental, transitional, transitory or saving provision.

This subsection does not apply to regulations under section 223 (consequential
provision).

224.3

Any power of the Secretary of State or OFCOM under this Act to make
regulations is exercisable by statutory instrument.

224.4

The Statutory Instruments Act 1946 applies in relation to OFCOM’s powers to
make regulations under this Act as if OFCOM were a Minister of the Crown.

224.5

The Documentary Evidence Act 1868 (proof of orders and regulations etc) has
effect as if—

224.5.a

OFCOM were included in the first column of the Schedule to that Act;

224.5.b

OFCOM and persons authorised to act on their behalf were mentioned in the
second column of that Schedule.

224.6

This section does not apply to regulations under section 240 (commencement and
transitional provision).

##### Parliamentary procedure for regulations

225

225.1

A statutory instrument containing (whether alone or with other provision)—

225.1.a

regulations under section 77 (12) ,

225.1.b

regulations under section 85(1),

225.1.c

regulations under section 114 (2) ,

225.1.d

regulations under section 169 (3) ,

225.1.e

regulations under section 211(2),

225.1.f

regulations under section 215(1),

225.1.g

regulations under section 217(1),

225.1.h

regulations under section 218(1),

225.1.i

regulations under section 220(1), (2), (4), (6), (7), (9) or (13),

225.1.j

regulations under section 221(1),

225.1.k

regulations under section 222 (1)  or  (3) ,

225.1.l

regulations under section 223 that amend or repeal provision made by the
Communications Act,

225.1.m

regulations under paragraph  7  of Schedule 4,

225.1.n

regulations under paragraph  38  of Schedule 8,

225.1.o

regulations under paragraph 7 of Schedule 10, or

225.1.p

regulations under paragraph 5(9) of Schedule 13,

may not be made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before, and
approved by a resolution of, each House of Parliament.

225.2

A statutory instrument containing regulations under section 219(1) may not be
made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before, and approved by a
resolution of, each House of Parliament.

225.3

But a statutory instrument mentioned in subsection  (2)  may be made without a
draft of the instrument being laid before, and approved by a resolution of,
each House of Parliament if it contains a declaration that the Secretary of
State is of the opinion that, because of urgency, it is necessary to make the
regulations without a draft being so laid and approved.

225.4

After an instrument is made in accordance with subsection  (3) , it must be
laid before Parliament.

225.5

Regulations contained in an instrument made in accordance with subsection  (3)
cease to have effect at the end of the period of 28 days beginning with the
day on which the instrument is made unless, during that period, the instrument
is approved by a resolution of each House of Parliament.

225.6

In calculating the period of 28 days, no account is to be taken of any whole
days that fall within a period during which—

225.6.a

Parliament is dissolved or prorogued, or

225.6.b

either House of Parliament is adjourned for more than 4 days.

225.7

If regulations cease to have effect as a result of subsection  (5) , that does
not—

225.7.a

affect the validity of anything previously done under or by virtue of the
regulations, or

225.7.b

prevent the making of new regulations.

225.8

A statutory instrument containing the first regulations under paragraph 1(1)
of Schedule 11 (whether alone or with regulations under paragraph 1(2) or (3)
of that Schedule) may not be made unless a draft of the instrument has been
laid before, and approved by a resolution of, each House of Parliament.

225.9

Any other statutory instrument containing regulations under paragraph 1(1) of
Schedule 11 is subject to annulment in pursuance of a resolution of either
House of Parliament.

225.10

A statutory instrument containing—

225.10.a

regulations under section 67 (1) ,

225.10.b

regulations under section 85 (2) ,

225.10.c

regulations under section 86,

225.10.d

regulations under section 170(1),

225.10.e

regulations under section 223 that do not amend or repeal provision made by
the Communications Act,

225.10.f

regulations under paragraph 8(1) of Schedule 3, or

225.10.g

regulations under paragraph  1(2)  or  (3)  of Schedule 11,

is subject to annulment in pursuance of a resolution of either House of
Parliament.

225.11

As soon as a draft of a statutory instrument containing regulations under
section 85 (1)  or paragraph 5(9) of Schedule 13 (whether alone or with
provision under section 85 (2) ) is ready for laying before Parliament, OFCOM
must send the draft to the Secretary of State, and the Secretary of State must
lay the draft before Parliament.

225.12

Immediately after making a statutory instrument containing only regulations
under section 85 (2) , OFCOM must send the instrument to the Secretary of
State, and the Secretary of State must lay it before Parliament.

225.13

Regulations made by the Scottish Ministers under—

225.13.a

section 221 (3) , and

225.13.b

section 222 (2) ,

are subject to the affirmative procedure (see section 29 of the Interpretation
and Legislative Reform (Scotland) Act  2010 (asp 10) ).

225.14

A statutory instrument containing regulations under section 221 (5)  may not
be made by the Welsh Ministers unless a draft of the instrument has been laid
before and approved by a resolution of Senedd Cymru.

225.15

The power of the relevant Department to make regulations under section 221 (7)
is exercisable by statutory rule for the purposes of the Statutory Rules
(Northern Ireland) Order 1979 ( S.I. 1979/1573 (N.I. 12) ).

225.16

Regulations may not be made by the relevant Department under section 221 (7)
unless a draft of the regulations has been laid before and approved by a
resolution of the Northern Ireland Assembly.

225.17

In subsections  (15)  and  (16) , “ the relevant Department ” has the same
meaning as in section 221 (7)  (see subsection  (8)  of that section).

### Interpretation and final provisions

#### Interpretation

##### “Provider” of internet service

226

226.1

This section applies to determine who is the “provider” of an internet service
for the purposes of this Act.

######## User-to-user services (other than combined services)

226.2

The provider of a user-to-user service is to be treated as being the entity
that has control over who can use the user-to-user part of the service (and
that entity alone).

226.3

If no entity has control over who can use the user-to-user part of a user-to-
user service, but an individual or individuals have control over who can use
that part, the provider of the service is to be treated as being that
individual or those individuals.

######## Search services

226.4

The provider of a search service is to be treated as being the entity that has
control over the operations of the search engine (and that entity alone).

226.5

If no entity has control over the operations of the search engine, but an
individual or individuals have control over those operations, the provider of
the search service is to be treated as being that individual or those
individuals.

######## Combined services

226.6

The provider of a combined service is to be treated as being the entity that
has control over both—

226.6.a

who can use the user-to-user part of the service, and

226.6.b

the operations of the search engine,

(and that entity alone).

226.7

If no entity has control over the matters mentioned in paragraphs (a) and (b)
of subsection  (6) , but an individual or individuals have control over both
those matters, the provider of the combined service is to be treated as being
that individual or those individuals.

######## Internet services other than user-to-user services or search services

226.8

The provider of an internet service, other than a user-to-user service or a
search service, is to be treated as being the entity that has control over
which content is published or displayed on the service.

226.9

If no entity has control over which content is published or displayed on such
an internet service, but an individual or individuals have control over which
content is published or displayed, the provider of the service is to be
treated as being that individual or those individuals.

######## Machine-generated services

226.10

The provider of an internet service that is generated by a machine is to be
treated as being the entity that controls the machine (and that entity alone).

226.11

If no entity controls the machine, but an individual or individuals control
it, the provider of the internet service is to be treated as being that
individual or those individuals.

######## Interpretation

226.12

A person who provides an access facility in relation to a user-to-user
service, within the meaning of section 146, is not to be regarded as a person
who has control over who can use the user-to-user part of the service for the
purposes of this section.

226.13

In this section “ operations of the search engine ” means operations which—

226.13.a

enable users of a search service or a combined service to make search
requests, and

226.13.b

generate responses to those requests.

226.14

In this section “ published or displayed ” is to be construed in accordance
with section 79 (6) .

226.15

For the purposes of subsections  (8)  and  (9) , a person who makes available
on a service an automated tool or algorithm by means of which content is
generated is to be regarded as having control over content so generated.

##### “User”, “United Kingdom user” and “interested person”

227

227.1

For the purposes of this Act a user is a “United Kingdom user” of a service
if—

227.1.a

where the user is an individual, the individual is in the United Kingdom;

227.1.b

where the user is an entity, the entity is incorporated or formed under the
law of any part of the United Kingdom.

227.2

For the purposes of references in this Act to a user of a service it does not
matter whether a person is registered to use a service.

227.3

References in this Act to a user of a service do not include references to any
of the following when acting in the course of the provider’s business—

227.3.a

where the provider of the service is an individual or individuals, that
individual or those individuals;

227.3.b

where the provider is an entity, officers of the entity;

227.3.c

persons who work for the provider (including as employees or volunteers);

227.3.d

any other person providing a business service to the provider such as a
contractor, consultant or auditor.

227.4

In subsection  (3)  “ acting in the course of the provider’s business ” means
(as the case may be)—

227.4.a

acting in the course of the provider’s business of providing the service, or

227.4.b

acting in the course of a business, trade, profession or other concern—

227.4.b.i

carried on (whether or not for profit) by the provider of the service, and

227.4.b.ii

for the purposes of which the service is provided.

227.5

In subsections  (1)  to  (4)  “ service ” (except in the term “business
service”) means internet service, user-to-user service or search service.

227.6

In subsection  (3)  “ officer ” includes a director, manager, partner,
associate, secretary or other similar officer.

227.7

In this Act “ interested person ”, in relation to a search service or a
combined service, means a person that is responsible for a website or database
capable of being searched by the search engine, provided that—

227.7.a

in the case of an individual, the individual is in the United Kingdom;

227.7.b

in the case of an entity, the entity is incorporated or formed under the law
of any part of the United Kingdom.

##### “Internet service”

228

228.1

In this Act “ internet service ” means a service that is made available by
means of the internet.

228.2

For the purposes of subsection  (1)  a service is “made available by means of
the internet” even where it is made available by means of a combination of—

228.2.a

the internet, and

228.2.b

an electronic communications service.

228.3

“ Electronic communications service ” has the same meaning as in the
Communications Act (see section 32(2) of that Act).

##### “Search engine”

229

229.1

In this Act “search engine”—

229.1.a

includes a service or functionality which enables a person to search some
websites or databases (as well as a service or functionality which enables a
person to search (in principle) all websites or databases);

229.1.b

does not include a service which enables a person to search just one website
or database.

229.2

For the purposes of this Act, a search engine is not to be taken to be
“included” in an internet service or a user-to-user service if the search
engine is controlled by a person who does not control other parts of the
service.

##### “Age verification” and “age estimation”

230

230.1

This section applies for the purposes of this Act.

230.2

“ Age verification ” means any measure designed to verify the exact age of
users of a regulated service.

230.3

“ Age estimation ” means any measure designed to estimate the age or age-range
of users of a regulated service.

230.4

A measure which requires a user to self-declare their age (without more) is
not to be regarded as age verification or age estimation.

##### “Proactive technology”

231

231.1

In this Act “ proactive technology ” means—

231.1.a

content identification technology,

231.1.b

user profiling technology, or

231.1.c

behaviour identification technology,

but this is subject to subsections  (3)  and  (7) .

231.2

“ Content identification technology ” means technology, such as algorithms,
keyword matching, image matching or image classification, which analyses
content to assess whether it is content of a particular kind (for example,
illegal content).

231.3

But content identification technology is not to be regarded as proactive
technology if it is used in response to a report from a user or other person
about particular content.

231.4

“ User profiling technology ” means technology which analyses (any or all of)—

231.4.a

relevant content,

231.4.b

user data, or

231.4.c

metadata relating to relevant content or user data,

for the purposes of building a profile of a user to assess characteristics
such as age.

231.5

Technology which—

231.5.a

analyses data specifically provided by a user for the purposes of the provider
verifying or estimating the user’s age in order to decide whether to allow the
user to access a service (or part of a service) or particular content, and

231.5.b

does not analyse any other data or content,

is not to be regarded as user profiling technology.

231.6

“ Behaviour identification technology ” means technology which analyses (any
or all of)—

231.6.a

relevant content,

231.6.b

user data, or

231.6.c

metadata relating to relevant content or user data,

to assess a user’s online behaviour or patterns of online behaviour (for
example, to assess whether a user may be involved in, or be the victim of,
illegal activity).

231.7

But behaviour identification technology is not to be regarded as proactive
technology if it is used in response to concerns identified by another person
or an automated tool about a particular user.

231.8

“ Relevant content ” means—

231.8.a

in relation to a user-to-user service, content that is user-generated content
in relation to the service;

231.8.b

in relation to a search service, the content of websites and databases capable
of being searched by the search engine;

231.8.c

in relation to an internet service within section 80(2), content that is
provider pornographic content in relation to the service.

231.9

“ User data ” means—

231.9.a

data provided by users, including personal data (for example, data provided
when a user sets up an account), and

231.9.b

data created, compiled or obtained by providers of regulated services and
relating to users (for example, data relating to when or where users access a
service or how they use it).

231.10

References in this Act to proactive technology include content identification
technology, user profiling technology or behaviour identification technology
which utilises artificial intelligence or machine learning.

231.11

Accredited technology that may be required to be used in relation to the
detection of terrorism content or CSEA content (or both) by a notice under
section 121 (1)  is an example of content identification technology.

231.12

The reference in subsection  (8)(b)  to a search service includes a reference
to the search engine of a combined service.

231.13

In this section—

      “accredited” technology has the same meaning as in Chapter 5 of Part 7
(see section 125 (12) );           “ illegal content ”, “ terrorism content ”
and “ CSEA content ” have the same meaning as in Part 3 (see section 59);
“ user-generated content ” has the meaning given by section 55 (see
subsections (3) and (4) of that section).

##### Content communicated “publicly” or “privately”

232

232.1

This section specifies factors which OFCOM must, in particular, consider when
deciding whether content is communicated “publicly” or “privately” by means of
a user-to-user service for the purposes of—

232.1.a

section 121 (notice to deal with terrorism content),

232.1.b

section 136 (requirement to use proactive technology), or

232.1.c

paragraph 13 (4)  of Schedule 4 (recommendation of proactive technology in
codes of practice).

232.2

The factors are—

232.2.a

the number of individuals in the United Kingdom who are able to access the
content by means of the service;

232.2.b

any restrictions on who may access the content by means of the service (for
example, a requirement for approval or permission from a user, or the
provider, of the service);

232.2.c

the ease with which the content may be forwarded to or shared with—

232.2.c.i

users of the service other than those who originally encounter it, or

232.2.c.ii

users of another internet service.

232.3

The following factors do not count as restrictions on access—

232.3.a

a requirement to log in to or register with a service (or part of a service);

232.3.b

a requirement to make a payment or take out a subscription in order to access
a service (or part of a service) or to access particular content;

232.3.c

inability to access a service (or part of a service) or to access particular
content except by using particular technology or a particular kind of device
(as long as that technology or device is generally available to the public).

##### “Functionality”

233

233.1

In this Act “ functionality ”, in relation to a user-to-user service, includes
any feature that enables interactions of any description between users of the
service by means of the service, and includes any feature enabling a user to
do anything listed in subsection  (2) .

233.2

The things are—

233.2.a

creating a user profile, including an anonymous or pseudonymous profile;

233.2.b

searching within the service for user-generated content or other users of the
service;

233.2.c

forwarding content to, or sharing content with, other users of the service;

233.2.d

sharing content on other internet services;

233.2.e

sending direct messages to or speaking to other users of the service, or
interacting with them in another way (for example by playing a game);

233.2.f

expressing a view on content, including, for example, by—

233.2.f.i

applying a “like” or “dislike” button or other button of that nature,

233.2.f.ii

applying an emoji or symbol of any kind,

233.2.f.iii

engaging in yes/no voting, or

233.2.f.iv

rating or scoring content in any way (including giving star or numerical
ratings);

233.2.g

sharing current or historic location information with other users of the
service, recording a user’s movements, or identifying which other users of the
service are nearby;

233.2.h

following or subscribing to particular kinds of content or particular users of
the service;

233.2.i

creating lists, collections, archives or directories of content or users of
the service;

233.2.j

tagging or labelling content present on the service;

233.2.k

uploading content relating to goods or services;

233.2.l

applying or changing settings on the service which affect the presentation of
user-generated content on the service;

233.2.m

accessing other internet services through content present on the service (for
example through hyperlinks).

233.3

In this Act “ functionality ”, in relation to a search service, includes (in
particular)—

233.3.a

a feature that enables users to search websites or databases;

233.3.b

a feature that makes suggestions relating to users’ search requests
(predictive search functionality).

233.4

In this section “ user-generated content ” has the meaning given by section 55
(see subsections  (3)  and  (4)  of that section).

##### “Harm” etc

234

234.1

This section applies for the purposes of this Act, apart from Part 10
(communications offences).

234.2

“ Harm ” means physical or psychological harm.

234.3

References to harm presented by content, and any other references to harm in
relation to content, include references to harm arising or that may arise from
any one or combination of the following—

234.3.a

the nature of the content;

234.3.b

the fact of its dissemination;

234.3.c

the manner of its dissemination.

234.4

References to harm presented by content, and any other references to harm in
relation to content, include references to cumulative harm arising or that may
arise in the following circumstances—

234.4.a

where content, or content of a particular kind, is repeatedly encountered by
an individual (including, but not limited to, where content, or a kind of
content, is sent to an individual by one user or by different users or
encountered as a result of algorithms used by, or functionalities of, a
service);

234.4.b

where content of a particular kind is encountered by an individual in
combination with content of a different kind (including, but not limited to,
where a kind of content is sent to an individual by one user or by different
users or encountered as a result of algorithms used by, or functionalities of,
a service).

234.5

References to harm presented by content, and any other references to harm in
relation to content, include references to harm arising or that may arise in
the following circumstances—

234.5.a

where, as a result of the content, individuals act in a way that results in
harm to themselves or that increases the likelihood of harm to themselves;

234.5.b

where, as a result of the content, individuals do or say something to another
individual that results in harm to that other individual or that increases the
likelihood of such harm (including, but not limited to, where individuals act
in such a way as a result of content that is related to that other
individual’s characteristics or membership of a group).

234.6

References to a risk of harm in relation to functionalities, and references to
the risk of functionalities facilitating users encountering particular kinds
of content (however expressed), include references to risks arising or that
may arise due to multiple functionalities which, used in combination, increase
the likelihood of harm arising (for example, as mentioned in subsection  (4)
).

234.7

References to a risk of harm, or to potential harm, are to be read in the same
way as references to harm.

234.8

In contexts where harm (or a risk of harm or potential harm) relates to
children, subsections  (4)  to  (5)  are to be read as if they referred to
children instead of individuals.

##### “Online safety functions” and “online safety matters”

235

235.1

In this Act references to OFCOM’s “online safety functions”—

235.1.a

are references to—

235.1.a.i

the functions that OFCOM have under this Act,

235.1.a.ii

the functions that OFCOM have under the provisions of the Communications Act
listed in subsection  (2) , so far as those functions relate to regulated
services or Part 3 services (as the case may be), and

235.1.a.iii

the functions that OFCOM have under section 3 of the Communications Act
(general duties), so far as duties under that section relate to a function
which is an online safety function by reason of sub-paragraph  (i)  or  (ii) ;

235.1.b

include references to OFCOM’s power to do anything appearing to them to be
incidental or conducive to the carrying out of any of their functions within
paragraph  (a)(i)  or  (ii)  (see section 1(3) of the Communications Act).

235.2

These are the provisions of the Communications Act referred to in subsection
(1)(a)(ii) —

235.2.a

section 6 (duties to review regulatory burdens);

235.2.b

section 7 (duty to carry out impact assessments);

235.2.c

section 8 (duty to publish and meet promptness standards);

235.2.d

sections 11 and 11A (duties to promote media literacy);

235.2.e

sections 12 and 13 (Content Board);

235.2.f

section 14(6)(a) (research about media literacy);

235.2.g

section 14(6B) (research about users’ experience of regulated services);

235.2.h

section 16 (consumer consultation);

235.2.i

section 20 (advisory committees for different parts of the United Kingdom);

235.2.j

section 21 (advisory committee on elderly and disabled persons);

235.2.k

section 22 (representation on international and other bodies);

235.2.l

section 26 (publication of information and advice for consumers etc).

235.3

References to OFCOM’s “online safety functions” also include references to
OFCOM’s duty to comply with any of the following, so far as relating to the
use of a regulated service by a person who has died—

235.3.a

a notice from a senior coroner under paragraph 1(2) of Schedule 5 to the
Coroners and Justice Act 2009 in connection with an investigation into a
person’s death;

235.3.b

a request for information in connection with the investigation of a procurator
fiscal into, or an inquiry held or to be held in relation to, a person’s
death;

235.3.c

a notice from a coroner under section 17A(2) of the  Coroners Act (Northern
Ireland) 1959 (c. 15 (N.I.))  in connection with—

235.3.c.i

an investigation to determine whether an inquest into a person’s death is
necessary, or

235.3.c.ii

an inquest in relation to a person’s death.

235.4

In this Act “ online safety matters ” means the matters to which OFCOM’s
online safety functions relate.

235.5

In subsection  (3)(b)  “ inquiry ” means an inquiry held, or to be held, under
the Inquiries into Fatal Accidents and Sudden Deaths etc. (Scotland) Act  2016
(asp 2) .

##### Interpretation: general

236

236.1

In this Act—

      “ adult ” means a person aged 18 or over;           “ audit notice ”
means a notice given under paragraph 4 of Schedule 12;           “ automated
tool ” includes bot;           “capacity”: any reference to the capacity of a
provider of a regulated service is to—         the financial resources of the
provider, and           the level of technical expertise which is available to
the provider, or which it is reasonable to expect would be available to the
provider given its size and financial resources;                 “ child ”
means a person under the age of 18;           “ the Communications Act ” means
the Communications Act 2003;           “ confirmation decision ” means a
notice given under section 132;           “ content ” means anything
communicated by means of an internet service, whether publicly or privately,
including written material or messages, oral communications, photographs,
videos, visual images, music and data of any description;           “ the
Convention ” has the meaning given by section 21(1) of the Human Rights Act
1998;           “ country ” includes territory;           “ document ” means
anything in which information (in whatever form) is recorded;           “
encounter ”, in relation to content, means read, view, hear or otherwise
experience content;           “ entity ” means a body or association of
persons or an organisation, regardless of whether the body, association or
organisation is—         formed under the law of any part of the United
Kingdom or of a country outside the United Kingdom, or           a legal
person under the law under which it is formed;                 “freedom of
expression”: any reference to freedom of expression (except in sections 41
(6)(f)  and 78 (2)(d) ) is to the freedom to receive and impart ideas,
opinions or information (referred to in Article 10(1) of the Convention) by
means of speech, writing or images;           “ identifying content ” means
content the function of which is to identify a user of an internet service
(for example, a user name or profile picture);           “ information notice
” means a notice given under section 100 (1)  or 101(1);           “measure”:
any reference to a measure includes a reference to any system or process
relevant to the operation of an internet service or any step or action which
may be taken by a provider of an internet service to comply with duties or
requirements under this Act;           “ notice ” means notice in writing;
“ notify ” means notify in writing, and “ notification ” is to be construed
accordingly;           “ OFCOM ” means the Office of Communications;
“paid-for advertisement”: an advertisement is a “ paid-for advertisement ” in
relation to an internet service if—         the provider of the service
receives any consideration (monetary or non-monetary) for the advertisement
(whether directly from the advertiser or indirectly from another person), and
the placement of the advertisement is determined by systems or processes that
are agreed between the parties entering into the contract relating to the
advertisement;                 “ person ” includes (in addition to an
individual and a body of persons corporate or unincorporate) any organisation
or association of persons;           “ personal data ” has the meaning given
by section 3(2) of the Data Protection Act 2018;           “ pornographic
content ” means content of such a nature that it is reasonable to assume that
it was produced solely or principally for the purpose of sexual arousal;
“ processing ” has the meaning given by section 3(4) of the Data Protection
Act 2018;           “ provisional notice of contravention ” means a notice
given under section 130;           “ publicly available ” means available to
members of the public in the United Kingdom;           “systems and/or
processes”: any reference to systems and/or processes is to human or automated
systems and/or processes, and accordingly includes technologies;           “
taking down ” (content): any reference to taking down content is to any action
that results in content being removed from a user-to-user service or being
permanently hidden so users of the service cannot encounter it (and related
expressions are to be read accordingly);           “ terms of service ”, in
relation to a user-to-user service, means all documents (whatever they are
called) comprising the contract for use of the service (or of part of it) by
United Kingdom users;           “ user-to-user part ”, in relation to a user-
to-user service, means the part of the service on which content that is user-
generated content in relation to the service is present.

236.2

The definitions of “encounter” and “person” in subsection  (1)  do not apply
for the purposes of Part 10 (for the definition of “encounter” in that Part,
see section 182 (5) ).

236.3

References in this Act to an individual with a certain characteristic include
references to an individual with a combination of characteristics.

236.4

References in this Act to a kind of user-to-user service or search service (or
Part 3 service) include references to user-to-user services or search services
grouped together for the purposes of a risk profile prepared by OFCOM under
section 98 (and references to different kinds of user-to-user services or
search services (or Part 3 services) are to be read accordingly).

236.5

References in this Act to content (or content of a particular kind) present or
prevalent on a user-to-user service (or on a part of it), or to the presence,
incidence or prevalence of content (or content of a particular kind) on a
user-to-user service (or on a part of it), do not include, in the case of a
user-to-user service that includes a search engine—

236.5.a

search content, or

236.5.b

any other content that, following a search request, may be encountered as a
result of subsequent interactions with internet services.

In this subsection “ search content ” and “ search request ” have the same
meaning as in Part 3 (see section 57).

236.6

For the purposes of this Act—

236.6.a

any reference to the use of or access to a service, or to content present,
published or displayed on a service, is to be taken to include use of or
access to the service or content on registering or on the making of a payment
or on subscription;

236.6.b

any reference to content that is made available or that may be accessed,
encountered or shared, is to be taken to include content that is made
available or that may be accessed, encountered or shared for a limited period
of time only;

and references to restrictions on access to a service or to content are to be
read accordingly.

236.7

For the purposes of this Act, content that is user-generated content in
relation to an internet service does not cease to be such content in relation
to the service when published or displayed on the service by means of—

236.7.a

software or an automated tool or algorithm applied by the provider of the
service or by a person acting on behalf of the provider, or

236.7.b

an automated tool or algorithm made available on the service by the provider
or by a person acting on behalf of the provider.

236.8

Nothing in this Act (other than section 212) affects any prohibition or
restriction in relation to pornographic content, or powers in relation to such
content, under another enactment or rule of law.

236.9

In this section, “ user-generated content ” has the meaning given by section
55 (see subsections  (3)  and  (4)  of that section).

and  (4) user-to-user part (of a service) section 236 user-to-user service
section 3 (see also section 204 (1) )

#### Final provisions

##### Financial provisions

238

There is to be paid out of money provided by Parliament—

238.a

any expenditure incurred under or by virtue of this Act by the Secretary of
State, and

238.b

any increase attributable to this Act in the sums payable under any other Act
out of money so provided.

##### Extent

239

239.1

Subject to the following provisions of this section, this Act extends to
England and Wales, Scotland and Northern Ireland.

239.2

The following provisions extend to England and Wales and Northern Ireland—

239.2.a

sections 179 to 183;

239.2.b

section 189 (1) .

239.3

The following provisions extend to England and Wales only—

239.3.a

section 187;

239.3.b

section 188;

239.3.c

section 189(2);

239.3.d

section 190;

239.3.e

section 213;

239.3.f

section 214 (1)  to  (3) .

239.4

Section 214 (4)  to  (6)  extends to Scotland only.

239.5

The following provisions extend to Northern Ireland only—

239.5.a

section 189(3);

239.5.b

section 214 (7)  to  (9) .

239.6

An amendment or repeal made by Schedule 14 has the same extent within the
United Kingdom as the provision amended or repealed.

239.7

His Majesty may by Order in Council provide for any of the provisions of this
Act to extend, with or without modifications, to the Bailiwick of Guernsey or
to the Isle of Man.

239.8

Subsections (1) and (2) of section 224 apply to an Order in Council under
subsection  (7)  as they apply to regulations under this Act.

239.9

The power conferred by section 411(6) of the Communications Act may be
exercised so as to extend to the Bailiwick of Guernsey or the Isle of Man any
amendment or repeal made by or under this Act of any part of that Act (with or
without modifications).

239.10

The power conferred by section 338 of the Criminal Justice Act 2003 may be
exercised so as to extend to the Bailiwick of Guernsey or the Isle of Man the
amendments of provisions of that Act made by paragraph  17  of Schedule 14.

239.11

The power conferred by section 60(6) of the Modern Slavery Act 2015 may be
exercised so as to extend to the Bailiwick of Guernsey or the Isle of Man the
amendments of Schedule 4 to that Act made by paragraph  19  of Schedule 14.

239.12

The power conferred by section 415(1) of the Sentencing Act 2020 may be
exercised so as to extend to the Bailiwick of Guernsey or the Isle of Man the
amendments of Schedule 18 to that Act made by paragraph  20  of Schedule 14.

##### Short title

241

This Act may be cited as the Online Safety Act 2023.

## SCHEDULES

  Exempt user-to-user and search services

Sections 3 and 4

##### Descriptions of services which are exempt

###### Email services

1

A user-to-user service is exempt if emails are the only user-generated content
(other than identifying content) enabled by the service.

###### SMS and MMS services

2

2.1

A user-to-user service is exempt if SMS messages are the only user-generated
content (other than identifying content) enabled by the service.

2.2

A user-to-user service is exempt if MMS messages are the only user-generated
content (other than identifying content) enabled by the service.

2.3

A user-to-user service is exempt if SMS messages and MMS messages are the only
user-generated content (other than identifying content) enabled by the
service.

2.4

“SMS message” and “MMS message” have the meaning given by section 55 (12) .

###### Services offering only one-to-one live aural communications

3

3.1

A user-to-user service is exempt if one-to-one live aural communications are
the only user-generated content (other than identifying content) enabled by
the service.

3.2

“ One-to-one live aural communications ” has the meaning given by section 55
(5) .

###### Limited functionality services

4

4.1

A user-to-user service is exempt if the functionalities of the service are
limited, such that users are able to communicate by means of the service only
in the following ways—

4.1.a

posting comments or reviews relating to provider content;

4.1.b

sharing such comments or reviews on a different internet service;

4.1.c

expressing a view on such comments or reviews, or on provider content, by
means of—

4.1.c.i

applying a “like” or “dislike” button or other button of that nature,

4.1.c.ii

applying an emoji or symbol of any kind,

4.1.c.iii

engaging in yes/no voting, or

4.1.c.iv

rating or scoring the content (or the comments or reviews) in any way
(including giving star or numerical ratings);

4.1.d

producing or displaying identifying content in connection with any of the
activities described in paragraphs (a) to (c).

4.2

In sub-paragraph  (1) , “ provider content ” means content published on a
service by the provider of the service or by a person acting on behalf of the
provider, including where the publication of the content is effected or
controlled by means of—

4.2.a

software or an automated tool or algorithm applied by the provider or by a
person acting on behalf of the provider, or

4.2.b

an automated tool or algorithm made available on the service by the provider
or by a person acting on behalf of the provider.

4.3

For the purposes of this paragraph, content that is user-generated content in
relation to a service is not to be regarded as provider content in relation to
that service.

###### Services which enable combinations of user-generated content

5

A user-to-user service is exempt if the only user-generated content enabled by
the service is content of the following kinds—

5.a

content mentioned in paragraph  1 ,  2  or  3  and related identifying
content;

5.b

content arising in connection with any of the activities described in
paragraph  4(1) .

###### Exception to exemptions in paragraphs 

6

But a a user-to-user service described in any of paragraphs  1  to  5  is not
exempt if—

6.a

regulated provider pornographic content is published or displayed on the
service, and

6.b

the service has links with the United Kingdom within the meaning of section 80
(4) .

###### Internal business services (entire user-to-user service or search service)

7

7.1

A user-to-user service or a search service is exempt if the conditions in sub-
paragraph  (2)  are met in relation to the service.

7.2

The conditions are—

7.2.a

the user-to-user service or search service is an internal resource or tool for
a business, or for more than one business carried on by the same person,

7.2.b

the person carrying on the business (or businesses) (“ P ”) is the provider of
the user-to-user service or search service, and

7.2.c

the user-to-user service or search service is available only to a closed group
of people comprising some or all of the following—

7.2.c.i

where P is an individual or individuals, that individual or those individuals,

7.2.c.ii

where P is an entity, officers of P,

7.2.c.iii

persons who work for P (including as employees or volunteers) for the purposes
of any activities of the business (or any of the businesses) in question, and

7.2.c.iv

any other persons authorised by a person within sub-paragraph (i), (ii) or
(iii) to use the service for the purposes of any activities of the business
(or any of the businesses) in question (for example, a contractor, consultant
or auditor, or in the case of an educational institution, pupils or students).

7.3

In this paragraph—

      “ business ” includes trade, profession, educational institution or
other concern (whether or not carried on for profit);           “ officer ”
includes a director, manager, partner, associate, secretary, governor, trustee
or other similar officer.

###### Internal business services (part of user-to-user service or search service)

8

8.1

A user-to-user service is exempt if—

8.1.a

the conditions in paragraph  7(2)  are met in relation to a part of the
service,

8.1.b

no user-generated content is enabled by the rest of the service, and

8.1.c

no regulated provider pornographic content is published or displayed on the
rest of the service.

8.2

A user-to-user service is also exempt if—

8.2.a

the conditions in paragraph  7(2)  are met in relation to a part of the
service,

8.2.b

the only user-generated content enabled by the rest of the service is—

8.2.b.i

content mentioned in paragraph  1 ,  2  or  3  and related identifying
content, or

8.2.b.ii

content arising in connection with any of the activities described in
paragraph  4(1) , and

8.2.c

no regulated provider pornographic content is published or displayed on the
rest of the service.

8.3

A search service is exempt if—

8.3.a

the conditions in paragraph  7(2)  are met in relation to a part of the
service that is a search engine,

8.3.b

the service does not include a public search engine, and

8.3.c

no regulated provider pornographic content is published or displayed on the
rest of the service.

8.4

In this paragraph—

      “ public search engine ” means a search engine other than one in
relation to which the conditions in paragraph  7(2)  are met;           “ the
rest of the service ” means all parts of the user-to-user service or search
service other than the part in relation to which the conditions in paragraph
7(2)  are met.

###### Services provided by public bodies

9

9.1

A user-to-user service or a search service is exempt if—

9.1.a

both of the following conditions are met in relation to the service—

9.1.a.i

the provider of the service is a public authority within the meaning of
section 6 of the Human Rights Act 1998, and

9.1.a.ii

the service is provided in the exercise of public functions only,

9.1.b

the provider of the service is Parliament, either House of Parliament, the
Scottish Parliament, Senedd Cymru, the Northern Ireland Assembly or a person
acting on behalf of any of those institutions,

9.1.c

the provider of the service is a foreign sovereign power, or

9.1.d

both of the following conditions are met in relation to the service—

9.1.d.i

the provider of the service is an entity formed under the law of a country
outside the United Kingdom, which exercises functions of a public nature, and

9.1.d.ii

the service is provided in the exercise of such functions only.

9.2

But a user-to-user service or a search service is not exempt under this
paragraph if—

9.2.a

the provider of the service is a person providing education or childcare, and

9.2.b

the service is provided for the purposes of that education or childcare.

See paragraph  10  for an exemption for services provided by persons providing
education or childcare of particular descriptions.

9.3

This paragraph is without prejudice to the fact that this Act does not apply
in relation to a user-to-user or search service provided by the Crown.

9.4

In this paragraph, “ public function ” means a function that is a function of
a public nature for the purposes of the Human Rights Act 1998.

###### Services provided by persons providing education or childcare

10

10.1

A user-to-user service or a search service is exempt if—

10.1.a

the provider of the service is—

10.1.a.i

the person with legal responsibility for education or childcare of a
description listed in Part 2 of this Schedule (“the responsible person”), or
where the responsible person is a body, a member of that body, or

10.1.a.ii

a person who is employed or engaged to provide education or childcare of a
description listed in Part 2 of this Schedule, and who is subject to
safeguarding duties which relate to the provision of that education or
childcare, and

10.1.b

the service is provided for the purposes of that education or childcare.

10.2

In sub-paragraph  (1)(a)(ii) , “ safeguarding duties ” means duties or
requirements which are related to the safeguarding of children arising under
enactments other than this Act, under guidance or requirements (however
referred to) produced under enactments other than this Act, or as a result of
contractual arrangements made by the responsible person.

10.3

For the purposes of this paragraph, the person with legal responsibility for
education or childcare of a particular description is the person with legal
responsibility for its day-to-day provision (for example, the person with
legal responsibility for a particular school), rather than any other person
who has a duty to ensure that, in general, education or childcare of that
description (or education or childcare which includes education or childcare
of that description) is provided.

###### Interpretation

11

In Part 1 of this Schedule—

      “ enactment ” includes—         an enactment contained in subordinate
legislation (within the meaning of the Interpretation Act 1978),           an
enactment contained in, or in an instrument made under, an Act of the Scottish
Parliament,           an enactment contained in, or in an instrument made
under, a Measure or Act of Senedd Cymru, and           an enactment contained
in, or in an instrument made under, Northern Ireland legislation;
“ regulated provider pornographic content ” and “ published or displayed ”
have the same meaning as in Part 5 (see section 79);           “ user-
generated content ” has the meaning given by section 55 (see subsections  (3)
and  (4)  of that section).

##### Paragraph 10 exemption: descriptions of education and childcare

###### England

12

Early years childminding by an early years childminder registered under
Chapter 2 of Part 3 of the Childcare Act 2006.

13

Act.

14

3 of Part 3 of that Act.

15

Later years provision by a person registered under Chapter 3 of Part 3 of that
Act.

16

Education or childcare in a maintained nursery school within the meaning of
section 22 of the School Standards and Framework Act 1998.

17

Education or childcare in—

17.a

an Academy school, within the meaning of section 1A of the Academies Act 2010;

17.b

an alternate provision Academy, within the meaning of section 1C of that Act;

17.c

Act 1998 (see section 20(7) of that Act);

17.d

a non-maintained special school, being a school that is approved under section

17.e

an independent educational institution registered on the register maintained
under section 95 of the Education and Skills Act 2008;

17.f

a pupil referral unit, within the meaning of section 19 of the Education Act
1996.

18

Education in—

18.a

an institution in England within the further education sector, within the

that Act);

18.c

and Families Act 2014 (see section 83(2) of that Act).

Education provided by an independent training provider.

Further education for persons under 19 provided by a local authority in
England.

21

In paragraphs  12  to  15 , “ early years childminding ”, “ early years
provision ”, “ later years childminding ” and “ later years provision ” have
the same meaning as in Part 3 of the Childcare Act 2006 (see section 98 of
that Act).

22

In paragraph  19 , “ independent training provider ” means a provider—

22.a

that is a provider of post-16 education or training carried on, or partly
carried on, in England—

22.a.i

to which Chapter 3 of Part 8 of the Education and Inspections Act 2006
(inspection of further education and training etc) applies, and

22.a.ii

which is funded, wholly or partly, by the Secretary of State, a local
authority in England or a combined authority, but

22.b

that is not—

22.b.i

an employer who only provides such education or training to its employees,

22.b.ii

a 16 to 19 Academy (within the meaning of section 1B of the Academies Act
2010),

22.b.iii

a school,

22.b.iv

a local authority in England,

22.b.v

an institution within the further education sector (within the meaning given
by section 91(3) of the Further and Higher Education Act 1992), or

22.b.vi

a higher education provider (within the meaning given by section 83(1) of the
Higher Education and Research Act 2017).

23

In paragraphs  20  and  22 , “ local authority in England ” has the same
meaning as in the Education Act 1996 (see sections 579(1) and 581 of that
Act).

24

In paragraph  22 —

      “ combined authority ” means a combined authority established under
section 103 of the Local Democracy, Economic Development and Construction Act
2009;           “ school ” has the meaning given by section 4(1) of the
Education Act 1996.

###### Scotland

25

Early learning and childcare, within the meaning of Part 6 of the Children and
Young People (Scotland) Act  2014 (asp 8)  (see section 46 of that Act).

26

Child minding, within the meaning of Part 5 of the Public Services Reform
(Scotland) Act  2010 (asp 8)  (see paragraph 12 of Schedule 12 to that Act).

27

Day care of children, within the meaning of Part 5 of that Act (see paragraph
13 of Schedule 12 to that Act).

28

Primary education, secondary education or childcare in—

28.a

a school, or

28.b

a hostel used mainly by pupils attending a school;

and in this paragraph “ school ” has the same meaning as in the Education
(Scotland) Act 1980 (see section 135(1) of that Act).

Further education provided by a body listed under the heading “Institutions
formerly eligible for funding by the Scottish Further Education Funding
Council” or under the heading “Other institutions” in Schedule 2 to the
Further and Higher Education (Scotland) Act  2005 (asp 6) .

30

Further education provided by a college of further education which is assigned
to a regional strategic body by an order made under section 7C(1) of that Act.

###### Wales

31

Child minding by a person who is registered as a child minder under Part 2 of
the  Children and Families (Wales) Measure 2010 (nawm 1) .

32

Day care for children by a person who is registered to provide day care for

33

Primary education, secondary education or childcare in a school in Wales,
within the meaning of the Education Act 1996 as it applies in relation to

Education provided in accordance with section 19A of the Education Act 1996.

35

Any other post-16 education or training in Wales, the facilities for which are

Skills Act 2000, that is funded by the Welsh Ministers or a local authority in
